# Parity matrix

Java file ŌåÆ ported/partial/not-needed/deferred. Populated per PR from Phase 1.
Pinned Lucene version: **10.5.0** (matches OpenSearch `gradle/libs.versions.toml`).

## lucene-util

| Java | Rust | Status |
|---|---|---|
| `util/BitUtil.zigZagEncode/Decode` | `lucene-util/src/zigzag.rs` | ported, fixture-verified |
| `Long.toString/parseLong(_, 36)` (generation Ōåö base-36 filename suffix) | `lucene-util/src/base36.rs` | ported, round-trip tested |
| `util/FixedBitSet` (dense bitset: get/set/clear/cardinality) | `lucene-util/src/fixed_bit_set.rs` | ported (the subset `.liv` reading needs); no `SparseFixedBitSet` (in-memory-only optimization, not a format difference) |

## lucene-analysis

| Java | Rust | Status |
|---|---|---|
| `analysis/Analyzer`/`Tokenizer`/`TokenFilter` pipeline shape | `lucene-analysis/src/lib.rs::{Token, tokenize, LowerCaseFilter, StopFilter, Analyzer}` | **ported, scoped down.** `Token { term, start_offset, end_offset, position_increment, position_length }` is a plain struct standing in for real Lucene's `CharTermAttribute`/`OffsetAttribute`/`PositionIncrementAttribute` trio (no `AttributeSource` reflection machinery). `tokenize()` is a simplified word-boundary tokenizer ŌĆö split on non-alphanumeric boundaries, keep alphanumeric runs as terms, char offsets ŌĆö mirroring the *core algorithm* of real `StandardTokenizer`/`WhitespaceTokenizer`, plus three narrowly-scoped UAX#29-inspired exceptions handled via `is_word_connector`: embedded numeric punctuation (`"3.14"`, `"1,000"` stay one token instead of splitting at the `.`/`,`), acronym-style internal periods (`"U.S.A."` tokenizes as `"U.S.A"` instead of three single-letter tokens), and internal apostrophes (`"don't"`, `"O'Brien"` stay one token instead of splitting at the `'`/`ŌĆÖ`) ŌĆö in each case only when the connector sits strictly between two alphanumeric characters, so a real sentence-ending period or a leading quote mark still splits normally. **Not** a port of full UAX#29 Unicode Text Segmentation (combining marks, locale word-breaking, CJK/complex script segmentation, and full email/URL recognition are out of scope). Note: despite the doc comment calling these "character offsets," `tokenize()` actually emits UTF-8 **byte** offsets (via `char_indices()`); harmless while every fixture/test string was ASCII (byte and char offsets coincide there), but task #64's fixture needed an explicit char-to-byte reconciliation once non-ASCII text was involved ŌĆö see that row below. `LowerCaseFilter` and `StopFilter` are both ported in full, including `StopFilter`'s position-increment-preservation rule: a removed stopword's own increment is carried onto the next surviving token rather than dropped, so position gaps across query slop (`PhraseQuery`/`SpanNear`) survive stopword removal. `Analyzer::standard(stopwords)` composes tokenizer + lowercase + optional stopwords, standing in for `StandardAnalyzer`. **Stopword list completeness audit (revisit, real gap found and fixed)**: `StopFilter` itself always took a caller-supplied `HashSet<String>` -- there was no built-in default English stop list anywhere in the crate, unlike real Lucene's `EnglishAnalyzer.ENGLISH_STOP_WORDS_SET` (a fixed, well-known 33-word list). Added `ENGLISH_STOP_WORDS: &[&str]`/`english_stop_words() -> HashSet<String>` reproducing that exact 33-word list (`a, an, and, are, as, at, be, but, by, for, if, in, into, is, it, no, not, of, on, or, such, that, the, their, then, there, these, they, this, to, was, will, with`), stored lowercase to match `StopFilter`'s exact case-sensitive match against already-lowercased terms. Verified with a test (`english_stop_words_matches_real_lucene_canonical_list`) that independently re-transcribes the canonical 33 words (not copy-pasted from the source list) and checks both directions -- every canonical word present, and no extra/wrong entries -- plus a lowercase-storage check and a false-positive check against representative content words (`search`/`lucene`/`rust`/`document`/`index`/`query`) run through the real `StopFilter`/`Analyzer::standard` pipeline. **Deferred**: any `TokenFilter` besides `AsciiFoldingFilter`/`PorterStemFilter`/`SynonymFilter` (see the rows below), plus per-field analyzer configuration. This crate is a standalone, dependency-free crate below both `lucene-index` and `lucene-search` in the workspace graph; `lucene-search/src/query_parser.rs` (task #62) and `lucene-index/src/indexing_chain.rs::invert_documents` (task #63, in-memory-only builder, see that row in the `lucene-index` section) are now its two real consumers; term-vector fixtures still take already-tokenized terms directly. **Verified against real Lucene**: `crates/lucene-analysis/tests/analysis_fixtures.rs` runs real `StandardAnalyzer` with a real stopword set (`fixtures/src/GenAnalysis.java`) over six cases ŌĆö a stopword mid-sentence, at the very start, at the very end, three consecutive stopwords, an all-stopwords string (empty output), and a mixed-case/punctuation sentence exercising tokenizing, lowercasing, and stopword removal together ("The" is itself a stopword once lowercased) ŌĆö and asserts this port's `Analyzer` produces byte-identical (term, position_increment, start_offset, end_offset) sequences; all six passed on the first real-Lucene run. |
| `analysis/miscellaneous/ASCIIFoldingFilter` | `lucene-analysis/src/lib.rs::{AsciiFoldingFilter, Analyzer::with_ascii_folding}` | **ported (task #64), scoped to a documented character subset, not the full real table.** A fourth `lucene-analysis` filter (alongside `tokenize`/`LowerCaseFilter`/`StopFilter` from task #61), folding each token's `term` to its closest plain-ASCII form. **Covered, itemized**: the full Latin-1 Supplement letter block (U+00C0-U+00DE uppercase / U+00E0-U+00FE lowercase, i.e. ├Ć-├×/├Ā-├Š, skipping the `├Ś`/`├Ę` math symbols at U+00D7/U+00F7), plus a documented Latin Extended-A subset: Polish (─ä/─ģ, ─å/─ć, ─ś/─Ö, ┼ü/┼é, ┼ā/┼ä, ┼Ü/┼ø, ┼╣/┼║, ┼╗/┼╝) and Czech/Slovak/Baltic caron forms (┼Ā/┼Ī, ─ī/─Ź, ┼Į/┼Š, ─Ä/─Å, ┼ż/┼ź, ┼ć/┼ł). `├å`/`├”` and `┼Æ`/`┼ō` fold to **two** ASCII characters (`AE`/`ae`, `OE`/`oe` respectively ŌĆö real Lucene's actual multi-char folding), and `├¤` folds to `ss` (real Lucene's actual special case, not "b"/"beta") ŌĆö both verified against real `ASCIIFoldingFilter` output, not assumed. **Deferred, real follow-on work**: the rest of real Lucene's table (remaining Latin Extended-A/B, Latin Extended Additional such as precomposed Vietnamese, and non-Latin-script folding e.g. fullwidth Latin forms) ŌĆö a character outside this table passes through **unchanged**, never dropped, never a panic. **Offsets are never adjusted for folding-driven length changes**: folding `├”ther` ŌåÆ `aether` grows the term from 5 to 6 characters, but `start_offset`/`end_offset` still denote the *original* source text span, matching real Lucene's `ASCIIFoldingFilter`, which never touches `OffsetAttribute`. **Filter-ordering decision**: `Analyzer::with_ascii_folding()` inserts folding *before* lowercasing (tokenize ŌåÆ fold ŌåÆ lowercase ŌåÆ stopwords) ŌĆö an uppercase accented letter (`├ē`) folds straight to its ASCII form (`E`) and is lowercased in the same subsequent pass as every other token, and stopword matching (last in the chain) always sees the fully folded-and-lowercased form. Folding is **off by default**: `Analyzer::standard(stopwords)` is unchanged, so `query_parser.rs` (task #62) and `indexing_chain.rs` (task #63) keep their exact prior behavior ŌĆö callers opt in via the additive `.with_ascii_folding()` builder method. **Verified against real Lucene**: `fixtures/src/GenAnalysis.java` gained two new cases via a hand-built `Analyzer` subclass wiring real `StandardTokenizer` + `ASCIIFoldingFilter` ŌĆö `fold_only` (fold with no lowercasing, over "caf├® na├»ve M├╝ller c┼ōur stra├¤e") and `fold_then_lower` (the same plus real `LowerCaseFilter`, over "Caf├® Na├»ve ├ēCOLE") ŌĆö and `crates/lucene-analysis/tests/analysis_fixtures.rs` asserts this port's `AsciiFoldingFilter`/`Analyzer::with_ascii_folding()` produce the same (term, position_increment, offset-span) sequences, both passing on the first real-Lucene run. **Offset-unit reconciliation, done explicitly in the test** (`char_offsets_to_byte_offsets`): real Lucene reports `char`/UTF-16-code-unit offsets, while this crate's `tokenize()` emits UTF-8 byte offsets (see the row above); the test converts real Lucene's char offsets to byte offsets via the fixture's own text before comparing ŌĆö the same kind of documented byte-vs-codepoint scope call `fuzzy.rs`/`wildcard.rs` already make elsewhere in this port, not a bug introduced here. Unit tests cover: each Latin-1 spot-check (caf├®/na├»ve/M├╝ller/├▒), the eszett special case, a ligature growing the term's character count while offsets stay put, a plain-ASCII token passing through untouched, mixed diacritic+ASCII in one token, a non-table character (Cyrillic) passing through unchanged, the composed fold-then-lowercase order, and the unchanged no-folding default. Coverage: `lucene-analysis/src/lib.rs` 100% lines. |
| `analysis/en/PorterStemFilter` | `lucene-analysis/src/lib.rs::{PorterStemFilter, Analyzer::with_stemming}` | **ported in full (task #65) -- all five steps of the classic 1980 Porter algorithm, not a subset.** A fifth `lucene-analysis` filter (alongside `tokenize`/`LowerCaseFilter`/`StopFilter`/`AsciiFoldingFilter`), stemming each token's `term` per Martin Porter's original suffix-stripping algorithm. **Steps ported, itemized**: step 1a (`-sses`->`-ss`, `-ies`->`-i`, `-ss`->`-ss` no-op, else trailing `-s`-> delete); step 1b (`-eed`->`-ee` if `m(stem) > 0`; `-ed`/`-ing` deleted only if the stem contains a vowel, followed by `-at`/`-bl`/`-iz`-append, double-consonant-not-l/s/z-drop, or `m==1`-and-CVC-append cleanup); step 1c (trailing `-y`->`-i` if the stem contains a vowel); step 2, `m(stem) > 0` (the full 20-entry suffix-family table, `-ational`->`-ate` through `-biliti`->`-ble`, tried longest/most-specific-suffix-first exactly as the original paper orders them); step 3, `m(stem) > 0` (`-icate`->`-ic`, `-ative`-> delete, `-alize`->`-al`, `-iciti`->`-ic`, `-ical`->`-ic`, `-ful`/`-ness`-> delete); step 4, `m(stem) > 1` (removes `-al`/`-ance`/`-ence`/`-er`/`-ic`/`-able`/`-ible`/`-ant`/`-ement`/`-ment`/`-ent`/`-ion` (only if the stem ends in `s`/`t`)/`-ou`/`-ism`/`-ate`/`-iti`/`-ous`/`-ive`/`-ize`); step 5a (trailing `-e` deleted if `m(stem) > 1`, or if `m(stem) == 1` and the stem is not CVC); step 5b (a trailing double `-ll` collapses to a single `-l` if `m(word) > 1`). Nothing is deferred within the algorithm itself -- this is the complete classic port. **Domain of definition, explicit**: the algorithm (and real Lucene's own port of it) is defined only over lowercase ASCII alphabetic words; a term with any non-ASCII-alphabetic character or uppercase letter passes through **unchanged**, never a panic -- a non-issue in the normal chain since this filter runs after `LowerCaseFilter`. **Filter-ordering decision**: `Analyzer::with_stemming()` inserts stemming *last* (tokenize -> fold -> lowercase -> stopwords -> stem), matching real Lucene's `EnglishAnalyzer` (its stop set holds unstemmed words like `"the"`, so stopword matching must see pre-stem terms). Off by default -- existing callers unaffected; opt in via the additive `.with_stemming()` builder method. **Verification**: direct unit tests against known Porter-algorithm input/output pairs, not a new Java fixture -- this is a purely algorithmic, non-file-format task (no on-disk bytes to decode), and the test vocabulary is drawn from the algorithm's own canonical worked examples (Porter's 1980 paper's step 2-4 illustration list, e.g. `"relational"`->`"relat"`, `"operator"`->`"oper"`, `"triplicate"`->`"triplic"`, plus the paper's separate step 1a/1b/1c illustration list, e.g. `"caresses"`->`"caress"`, `"agreed"`->`"agre"`, `"hopping"`->`"hop"`, `"happy"`->`"happi"`), independently traced step-by-step against this implementation rather than guessed. Unit tests cover: step 1a plurals (caresses/ponies/ties/caress/cats), step 1b's `m`/vowel guards including words that must **not** stem (feed/bled/sing all fail their respective conditions and stay unchanged; agreed->agre, plastered->plaster, motoring->motor do stem) plus each of its three post-deletion cleanup branches individually (`-at`/`-bl`/`-iz`-append via sized->size; double-consonant-drop via hopping->hop/tanned->tan/falling->fall/hissing->hiss/fizzed->fizz; plain deletion via failing->fail/filing->file), step 1c (happy->happi vs. sky->sky, whose vowel guard doesn't fire), the full step 2/3/4 suffix-family table (47 canonical pairs), step 5's final-e/double-l edge cases (`rate` keeps its `e` since `m==1` and it is CVC; `roll` keeps one `l` since `m==1` not `>1`), offsets/position-increment left untouched, non-lowercase-ASCII pass-through (uppercase, accented, empty, digit-only terms), and the composed `Analyzer::with_stemming()` running after `StopFilter`. Coverage: `lucene-analysis/src/lib.rs` 99.11% lines. **Porter2/Snowball parity check (revisit, no code change to the algorithm)**: reread against the Snowball English ("Porter2") algorithm spec to check for R1/R2-region gaps -- confirmed this port's scope target (real Lucene's `EnglishAnalyzer`, which wires up `PorterStemFilter`) genuinely runs the **classic 1980 Porter algorithm** in real Lucene too (`org.tartarus.snowball.ext.PorterStemmer`, generated from Snowball's `porter.sbl`), not Porter2/`english.sbl` -- so there is no missing R1/R2 region computation to add *here*, since R1/R2 belongs to a different algorithm this filter was never scoped to. **Explicitly deferred, real gap**: the Porter2/"Snowball English" stemmer (`org.tartarus.snowball.ext.EnglishStemmer`, exposed in real Lucene only via `SnowballFilter` constructed with the `English` variant -- a *different, non-default* filter `EnglishAnalyzer` does not use) is **not ported at all** -- its own step 0 (apostrophe-suffix removal), R1/R2 region computation threaded through steps 2-5, doubled-consonant undoubling, and per-step exception tables are a separate, sizeable algorithm and a legitimate follow-on task, not a subset or superset of the `PorterStemFilter` row above. A smaller-scoped alternative was also considered and rejected for now, not silently skipped: adding Porter2/Snowball-English as a new, separate, opt-in sibling filter (leaving `PorterStemFilter` untouched) is real and tractable, but its own R1/R2-threading, step 0, doubled-consonant undoubling, and exception table are enough surface area to warrant their own dedicated task rather than a same-task add-on here. One new test, `porter_stem_step1a_step1b_step1c_paper_vocabulary`, closes the step 1a/1b/1c vocabulary-coverage gap that check surfaced; `cargo test -p lucene-analysis`: 54 lib tests pass (up from 53). |
| `analysis/synonym/SynonymFilter`/`SynonymGraphFilter` | `lucene-analysis/src/lib.rs::{SynonymFilter, Analyzer::with_synonyms, Analyzer::with_bidirectional_synonyms}` | **ported (task #66), scoped to single-word-to-single-word synonyms only -- not the full `SynonymGraphFilter`.** A fifth `lucene-analysis` filter (alongside `tokenize`/`LowerCaseFilter`/`StopFilter`/`AsciiFoldingFilter`/`PorterStemFilter`), taking a caller-supplied `HashMap<String, Vec<String>>` and, for each token whose term is a map key, injecting one additional token per configured replacement immediately after the original. **Explicit scope boundary**: real `SynonymGraphFilter` also handles multi-word synonym *phrases* (`"New York"` <-> `"NYC"`) via a graph token stream -- legitimately out-of-scope machinery here; this filter only maps one term to one or more single-word replacement terms. **Positional semantics (the core real-Lucene rule mirrored)**: an injected synonym gets `position_increment == 0` and the exact same `start_offset`/`end_offset` as the original -- it occupies the *same position*, an alternative reading of the same span, not a new one, so `PhraseQuery`/`SpanNear` built against either term still aligns with surrounding words. This is the first token in the crate with `position_increment == 0` (every prior token, including `StopFilter`'s carried-over increments, has been `>= 1`). **Bidirectionality is NOT automatic by default**, matching real Lucene's `SynonymMap`: configuring `"quick" -> ["fast"]` does not also expand `"fast"` to `"quick"` through the original `SynonymFilter::apply`/`Analyzer::with_synonyms` entry points -- unchanged and unaffected by the addition below. **Bidirectional expansion (follow-up task, "SynonymFilter bidirectional expansion")**: a second, purely additive opt-in entry point, `SynonymFilter::apply_bidirectional`/`Analyzer::with_bidirectional_synonyms`, mirrors real Lucene's `SynonymMap.Builder(true)` bidirectional construction mode at this filter's same single-word-to-single-word scope: given the same `HashMap<String, Vec<String>>` config, a `key -> [values]` mapping also expands each `value -> key` -- configuring only `"cat" -> ["feline"]` is enough for analyzing `"feline"` to inject `"cat"` too, without the caller configuring both directions. A private helper, `build_bidirectional_map`, builds the combined forward+reverse map once per `apply_bidirectional` call (not re-derived per token) and dedupes so a term already configured in both directions (e.g. `"cat" -> ["feline"]` and `"feline" -> ["cat"]` both present) is never injected twice. **What this does NOT replicate**: transitive closure (if `"cat" -> ["feline"]` and `"feline" -> ["kitty"]` are both configured, this does not infer `"cat" -> ["kitty"]` -- only the direct reverse of each configured pair is added), multi-word synonym phrases, weighted/scored synonyms, and real Lucene's `includeOrig` flag -- the same carve-outs the unidirectional case already states. **Filter-ordering decision**: `Analyzer::with_synonyms()`/`with_bidirectional_synonyms()` both insert synonym expansion *last* (tokenize -> fold -> lowercase -> stopwords -> stem -> synonyms) -- real Lucene's convention is that synonym expansion runs over already-normalized terms, so the caller's map keys are expected to already be lowercased/stemmed; and running after `StopFilter` means a term that is itself a stopword (and thus removed) never gets its synonym expanded, since expanding a term about to be dropped would produce an orphaned synonym token with no corresponding original. Both entry points off by default -- existing callers unaffected; opt in via `.with_synonyms(map)` (unidirectional) or `.with_bidirectional_synonyms(map)` (bidirectional). **Verification approach**: no new Java fixture -- the `position_increment == 0` injection is new Rust-level control flow over an already cross-engine-verified position system (`StopFilter`'s increment mechanics were differentially verified in task #61), not new byte-format decoding, so unit tests are the appropriate tool. Unit tests cover: one configured synonym produces two tokens (original at its own increment, synonym at increment 0); multiple synonyms produce the original plus all of them, all at increment 0; a token with no configured synonym passes through unchanged; synonym expansion is confirmed NOT automatically bidirectional through the original `apply`; injected-token offsets match the original's exactly; composed with `StopFilter` (a stopword's own synonym is never expanded since the stopword is removed first, and a surviving term's synonym is correctly carried through with the right accumulated `position_increment`); composed with `PorterStemFilter` (the synonym map's key matches the *stemmed* form, proving synonyms see post-stemming terms); a forward-only-configured term expanding both ways under `apply_bidirectional`; both-directions-configured producing no duplicate injection; and bidirectional mode composed with both `StopFilter` and `PorterStemFilter`, mirroring the unidirectional composition tests. `cargo test -p lucene-analysis`: 44 lib tests pass (up from 37). Coverage: new code (`apply_bidirectional`, `build_bidirectional_map`, `with_bidirectional_synonyms`) fully exercised by the new tests. **Multi-word phrase support (follow-up task, "Synonym expansion multi-word phrase support")**: a third, purely additive entry point, `SynonymFilter::apply_multiword(tokens, rules: &[SynonymRule])`, extends matching to multi-token input phrases (e.g. `"wi" "fi" -> "wifi"`) and multi-token output phrases (e.g. `"usa" -> "united" "states" "of" "america"`), including multi-word-to-multi-word. `SynonymRule { input: Vec<String>, outputs: Vec<Vec<String>> }` replaces the single-word `HashMap<String, Vec<String>>` shape for this entry point only (`apply`/`apply_bidirectional` and their `HashMap` config are completely unchanged). Matching requires lookahead across multiple input tokens (buffered via direct indexing into the input `Vec<Token>`, not the prior per-token loop): at each starting position, every candidate rule sharing that position's term as its first input word is tried longest-first (greedy longest match), and a rule only fires when every one of its input words matches the corresponding contiguous following token -- a bare prefix match (`"wi"` not followed by `"fi"`, including `"wi"` as the last token with nothing following) never fires. **`position_length` added to `Token`** (new field, default `1` everywhere else in the crate) to carry real Lucene's `PositionLengthAttribute`: a multi-word-input/single-word-output match emits one token at `position_increment == 0` and `position_length == ` the number of input tokens it replaces; a multi-word output phrase emits one chained token per output word (first at `position_increment == 0`, the rest at `1` each, all at `position_length == 1`). **Scope, stated explicitly**: this is real `SynonymGraphFilter`'s token-stream *shape* (graph-relevant attributes recorded on ordinary `Token`s) proven via direct token-stream inspection, not its full graph `TokenStream`/lattice-traversal API -- there is no graph-aware traversal type, output is still one flat `Vec<Token>`, and a multi-word *output* phrase does not extend the overall position count the way a true lattice would (tokens after the match keep the position they'd have had relative to the original single input position). Consuming this correctly from a real `PhraseQuery`/`SpanQuery` lattice traversal is deferred; not wired into `Analyzer` (no `with_multiword_synonyms` builder method) since the flat-consumer approximation isn't yet proven against a real downstream query consumer. Covered by new unit tests: multi-word input to single-word output (`"wi fi"` -> `"wifi"`, `position_length == 2`), single-word input to multi-word output (`"usa"` -> 4 chained tokens), multi-word-to-multi-word (`"new york"` -> `"big apple"`), a non-matching partial prefix (both mid-stream and at end-of-stream), no-rules passthrough, longest-match preference when a shorter and longer rule could both match the same start, multiple alternative output paths for one input phrase, and a regression test confirming `apply`/`apply_bidirectional`'s existing single-word behavior is byte-identical after this addition. |
| `analysis/ngram/NGramTokenFilter`/`EdgeNGramTokenFilter` | `lucene-analysis/src/lib.rs::{NGramTokenFilter, EdgeNGramTokenFilter, ngrams_for_term, apply_ngram_filter}` | **ported, token-filter form only -- the tokenizer forms (`NGramTokenizer`/`EdgeNGramTokenizer`) are a real, deferred gap, stated explicitly below.** A sixth/seventh `lucene-analysis` filter, gramming each already-tokenized token's `term` into substrings. `NGramTokenFilter::apply(tokens, min_gram, max_gram)` produces every contiguous codepoint substring whose length is in `min_gram..=max_gram`, ordered by increasing start position then increasing length (`"abcde"` with min=2/max=3 -> `"ab","abc","bc","bcd","cd","cde","de"`, confirmed exact order by test). `EdgeNGramTokenFilter::apply` is the same algorithm restricted to grams anchored at codepoint 0 (prefix-only, the autocomplete/prefix-search shape; `"abcde"` with min=2/max=4 -> `"ab","abc","abcd"`). Both share one internal implementation (`ngrams_for_term`/`apply_ngram_filter`) parameterized by an `edge_only` flag, avoiding near-duplicate logic. **Token-filter vs. tokenizer form, the scope decision**: real Lucene has both a tokenizer form (grams raw text directly, ignoring word boundaries) and a token-filter form (grams already-tokenized terms). Only the token-filter form is implemented here, since it composes naturally with this crate's existing `Vec<Token> -> Vec<Token>` filter-chain shape (same as every other filter in the crate) and lets n-gramming run downstream of `tokenize()`'s word-boundary logic. The tokenizer form -- a raw-`&str -> Vec<Token>` entry point that grams straight across whitespace/punctuation -- is **not implemented**; a real, tractable follow-on task, not silently dropped. **Edge cases**: a token shorter than `min_gram` (in codepoints) produces **no output at all** (confirmed real Lucene behavior -- not a truncated/padded gram, not the whole token passed through); `min_gram > max_gram`, and `min_gram`/`max_gram` `<= 0`, are all rejected as `Result::Err` configuration errors (not a panic, not silently swallowed) by a shared `validate_gram_range` helper; a single-character token with `min_gram == 1` yields exactly one gram equal to the whole token; multiple input tokens are grammed fully independently (no gramming across token boundaries). **Unicode handling**: grams are computed by Unicode codepoint (via `chars().collect::<Vec<char>>()`), never by byte, so a multi-byte character (e.g. `├®` in `"caf├®"`) is never split mid-character; a `char_range_to_byte_range` helper then translates the codepoint range back to byte offsets (via `char_indices()`) for the emitted `Token`'s `start_offset`/`end_offset`, consistent with this crate's existing (documented) byte-offset `Token` convention. **Position/offset convention chosen**: the first gram derived from a given input token keeps that token's own `position_increment`; every subsequent gram from the same input token gets `position_increment == 0` (an alternative reading at the same starting position -- the same convention `SynonymFilter` already uses for injected tokens), and every gram's `position_length` stays `1`. Each gram gets its own precise `start_offset`/`end_offset` (the codepoint span it covers within the original term, translated to bytes and added onto the original token's `start_offset`), not the whole original token's span reused for every gram. **Not wired into `Analyzer`**: no `with_ngrams`/`with_edge_ngrams` builder method yet, since n-gram filters are typically used in a dedicated autocomplete/fuzzy-matching analyzer rather than the general-purpose chain this crate's `Analyzer` composes -- callers needing n-grams today call `NGramTokenFilter::apply`/`EdgeNGramTokenFilter::apply` directly on a token stream. Unit tests cover: the exact `"abcde"` min=2/max=3 gram set and order (plain) and min=2/max=4 prefix set (edge), position_increment convention (first gram gets original increment, rest get 0) for both filters, a token shorter than `min_gram` producing empty output for both filters, `min_gram > max_gram` rejected as `Err` for both filters, `min_gram`/`max_gram` `<= 0` (including negative) rejected as `Err` for both filters, a single-character token, a multi-byte Unicode token (`"caf├®"`) confirming codepoint-based gramming and correct byte-offset translation for both filters, and multiple input tokens grammed independently (including that each token's own `position_increment` seeds its own first gram) for both filters. |

| Java | Rust | Status |
|---|---|---|
| `store/DataInput` (vint/vlong/zlong) | `lucene-store/src/data_input.rs` | ported, fixture-verified |
| `util/GroupVIntUtil` | `lucene-store/src/data_input.rs::read_group_vints` | ported, fixture-verified |
| `store/DataInput.readString` | `lucene-store/src/data_input.rs::read_string` | ported |
| `codecs/CodecUtil` (header/index-header/footer, CRC-32) | `lucene-store/src/codec_util.rs` | ported, fixture-verified (incl. corrupted-checksum case) |
| `codecs/CodecUtil.retrieveChecksum` (structural-only footer check, no full-file CRC) | `lucene-store/src/codec_util.rs::retrieve_checksum` | ported, unit-tested |
| `store/Directory`, `FSDirectory` (listing + whole-file read) | `lucene-store/src/directory.rs::{Directory, FsDirectory}` | ported (read-only), fixture-verified |
| `store/MMapDirectory` | `lucene-store/src/directory.rs::MmapDirectory` | ported (read-only), fixture-verified; this crate's only `unsafe` |
| `index/SegmentInfos.getLastCommitGeneration`, `generationFromSegmentsFileName`, `IndexFileNames.fileNameFromGeneration` | `lucene-store/src/directory.rs::{last_commit_generation, generation_from_segments_file_name, segments_file_name, read_latest_commit}` | ported, fixture-verified end-to-end (open dir ŌåÆ find latest commit ŌåÆ parse `segments_N`) |
| `store/IndexInput.slice(sliceDescription, offset, length)` / `.clone()` | `lucene-store/src/data_input.rs::SliceInput::slice_input`, `Clone for SliceInput` | **ported.** `slice_input` returns a new `SliceInput` over `[offset, offset+length)` of the parent's own addressing, cursor reset to 0, independent of the parent's and any sibling's file pointer; `Clone` (already derived) gives the same independent-pointer duplicate Java's `clone()` does, since `SliceInput` is just `(&[u8], usize)`. Slicing a slice is supported (offsets are always relative to the callee). `Directory::open` still returns a whole-file buffer rather than lazily paging a real file ŌĆö that's unchanged and remains fine for this port's read-into-memory/mmap model, since `slice_input` works over either backend's bytes once opened. `crates/lucene-codecs/src/compound_format.rs::open_input` was refactored to return a `SliceInput` via this primitive instead of a hand-rolled `data.get(range)` slice, since it's the same offset/length-into-a-shared-buffer shape and the real caller (segment merging, reading one source segment's sub-range out of a shared `.cfs`) needs an independent cursor, not just a raw byte range. Unit-tested (bounds, zero-length, slice-of-a-slice, interleaved-reads independence) plus a real-on-disk-file test in `directory.rs` |
| `store/DataOutput` (vint/vlong/zlong/string/fixed-width encode) | `lucene-store/src/data_output.rs` | **write path started.** Ported as an in-memory-buffer-only sink (`VecDataOutput`, plus a direct `impl DataOutput for Vec<u8>`); every codec writer built on this (stored fields, field infos, `.si`) still returns an owned `Vec<u8>` rather than targeting `IndexOutput` directly (see the row below for why that's an intentional, low-risk choice, not a gap). Unit-tested by round-tripping every primitive through `DataInput`'s decoders |
| `codecs/CodecUtil.writeHeader/writeIndexHeader/writeFooter` (encode side) | `lucene-store/src/codec_util.rs::{write_header, write_index_header, write_footer}` | ported, unit-tested by round-tripping through this port's own `check_header`/`check_index_header`/`check_footer` |
| `store/IndexOutput`/`OutputStreamIndexOutput` (sequential write to a real on-disk file) | `lucene-store/src/index_output.rs::{IndexOutput, FsIndexOutput}` | **ported.** `FsIndexOutput` wraps a real `std::fs::File` (buffered via `BufWriter`), implements `DataOutput` directly, and tracks `getFilePointer()`/`getChecksum()` (running CRC32) like Java's `OutputStreamIndexOutput`. `DataOutput`'s methods stay infallible by signature (matching `VecDataOutput`, which can never fail ŌĆö making the trait fallible would ripple through every already-committed codec writer for no benefit there): a real file I/O error is latched as a **sticky error** on first failure, every subsequent write becomes a no-op, and the latched error surfaces from `close()`. `close()` flushes to the OS but deliberately does **not** fsync -- durability is `Directory::sync`'s job (next row), matching Java's actual contract that `close()` alone doesn't guarantee durability. The three existing write-path example binaries (`write_stored_fields_fixture`, `write_field_infos_fixture`, `write_segment_info_fixture`) now route their encoded bytes through this real `Directory`/`IndexOutput` instead of `std::fs::write`, and re-running each of their Java verifiers (`VerifyStoredFields`/`VerifyFieldInfos`/`VerifySegmentInfo`) against the resulting files still passes -- proving the primitive produces real, Java-`FSDirectory`-openable files, without needing new Java scaffolding for this slice |
| `store/Directory.createOutput`/`Directory.sync` (real on-disk write + fsync-before-durable contract) | `lucene-store/src/directory.rs::Directory::{create_output, sync}` (shared impl in `index_output.rs`) | **ported** for both `FsDirectory` and `MmapDirectory` (write doesn't need mmap, so both backends share the same real-file logic). `create_output` creates/truncates a file and returns an `FsIndexOutput`; `sync` fsyncs every named file's contents plus, best-effort, the containing directory entry -- mirrors `IndexWriter`'s real requirement to fsync a new segment's files before a `segments_N` commit references them. Unit-tested by round-tripping bytes written through `create_output` back through the existing read-side `Directory::open` (both backends), plus error paths (missing directory, missing file to sync, a write that fails partway through). **Deliberately out of scope for this slice**: `segments_N`/`SegmentInfos.write` (the commit file itself ŌĆö generation numbers, checksum-of-checksums, atomic rename/publish) is a separate, larger piece with its own commit-lifecycle correctness risks, tracked in its own row below; so is `NativeFSLockFactory` (write-lock acquisition, not needed until concurrent-writer support matters) |

## lucene-codecs

| Java | Rust | Status |
|---|---|---|
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90LiveDocsFormat` (`.liv` read) | `lucene-codecs/src/live_docs.rs` | ported (read-only), fixture-verified against a real IndexWriter deletion (2 of 5 docs deleted by term, `NoMergePolicy` to keep the segment intact) |
| ŌĆö `SparseFixedBitSet`/`SparseLiveDocs` in-memory choice | ŌĆö | not applicable to this port: the on-disk bytes are identical dense bits regardless of Java's in-memory representation choice |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90LiveDocsFormat.writeLiveDocs` | `lucene-codecs/src/live_docs.rs::write` | **write path ported, and genuinely complete for this format** -- unlike every other write-side row in this table, there is no scoped-down subset left to defer. The format itself has no sparse/compressed on-disk variant to omit: `.liv` is always one dense bit array regardless of deletion rate (`SparseFixedBitSet`/`IndexedDISI`-style sparse encodings are Java's in-memory-only choice for `readLiveDocs`, made after the same dense bytes are read off disk -- see the row above), so there's no equivalent of doc-values' "dense only, sparse deferred" or points' "single-leaf only, multi-leaf deferred" caveat here. Real Lucene's `writeBits` copies the input `Bits` in 1024-bit batches via `Bits#applyMask` purely as a performance trick over the generic `Bits` interface; since this port's input is always an already-word-addressable `FixedBitSet`, writing `live_docs.words()` directly produces byte-identical output without needing to replicate that batching. Unit-tested by round-tripping through this port's own reader (`parse`): all-live/no-deletions, some-deleted, a doc count not a multiple of 64 (130 docs, exercising the bitset's partial last-word case), the del-count-mismatch rejection path, and a wrong-segment-id rejection. **Verified against real Lucene in the writeŌåÆread direction**: `crates/lucene-codecs/examples/write_live_docs_fixture.rs` writes three `.liv` files (`_0`: 5 docs, no deletions; `_1`: 5 docs, 2 deleted; `_2`: 130 docs, 2 deleted including the last doc in the final partial word) and `fixtures/src/VerifyLiveDocs.java` opens each directly through `Lucene90LiveDocsFormat.readLiveDocs` (hand-built `SegmentInfo`/`SegmentCommitInfo`, no `.si`/`segments_N`/`.fnm` writer needed -- deletions aren't per-field, so unlike every other codec write-side fixture here this one needs no `FieldInfos` at all) and confirms every doc's live/deleted state matches the manifest via real `Bits#get(int)` -- all three segments passed on the first real-Lucene run |
| `codecs/lucene94/Lucene94FieldInfosFormat` (`.fnm` read, incl. `FieldInfo.checkConsistency`) | `lucene-codecs/src/field_infos.rs` | ported (read-only), fixture-verified against a real IndexWriter (7 field shapes + a soft-deletes field introduced by a later DV-update generation) |
| `codecs/lucene94/Lucene94FieldInfosFormat.write` | `lucene-codecs/src/field_infos.rs::write` | **write path ported.** Always emits the current format version (`FORMAT_DOCVALUE_SKIPPER`); does not re-validate `FieldInfo.checkConsistency` on the way in (callers are trusted, matching the parser's own stance), it's exercised via own-reader round-trip unit tests instead. **Verified against real Lucene in the writeŌåÆread direction**: `crates/lucene-codecs/examples/write_field_infos_fixture.rs` writes an `.fnm` file (8 field shapes: plain indexed, term vectors + payloads + an attribute, numeric doc values with a skip index and a gen, sorted doc values, a point field, a KNN vector field, a soft-deletes field, a parent field) and `fixtures/src/VerifyFieldInfos.java` opens it directly through `Lucene94FieldInfosFormat.read` (hand-built `SegmentInfo`, no `.si` writer needed) and confirms every field's properties match the manifest ŌĆö passed on the first real-Lucene run |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90NormsFormat` (`.nvm`/`.nvd` read: empty/dense/sparse) | `lucene-codecs/src/norms.rs` | ported (read-only), fixture-verified against real per-doc norm values from Lucene's own `NormsProducer`, including a real sparse field (some docs missing it entirely) |
| `codecs/lucene90/IndexedDISI` (sparse doc-id-set: SPARSE/DENSE/ALL blocks) | `lucene-codecs/src/indexed_disi.rs` | ported as a **one-shot decode to `Vec<i32>`**, not Java's lazy seekable iterator ŌĆö see the module doc for why (this port isn't in the hot-path-perf phase yet); jump table and DENSE rank bytes are parsed past but never used, since a full sequential decode doesn't need to skip ahead |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90DocValuesFormat`/`Lucene90DocValuesProducer` (`.dvm`/`.dvd` read, **all five doc-values types**) | `lucene-codecs/src/doc_values.rs` | ported (read-only), fixture-verified against a real IndexWriter: numeric plain-varying dense, numeric GCD-compressed dense, numeric sparse (`IndexedDISI`), binary fixed-length dense, binary variable-length dense (`DirectMonotonicReader`), binary variable-length sparse (`IndexedDISI` + `DirectMonotonicReader`), a SORTED field with repeated values (ordinal reuse + terms dictionary), a SORTED_NUMERIC field with 0-3 values/doc, and a SORTED_SET field with 0-2 values/doc sharing a terms dictionary (both exercising the sparse-via-`IndexedDISI` and multi-value-via-`DirectMonotonicReader`-address-range paths together). **Varying-bits-per-value block decode (this row's prior gap): ported.** A NUMERIC field split by `Lucene90DocValuesConsumer.writeValues`'s `doBlocks` path into independently-bit-packed `2^blockShift`-value blocks (on disk: `tableSize < -1` in the meta, `blockShift = -2 - tableSize`, `bitsPerValue` written as a meaningless `0xFF` sentinel) now decodes via `NumericEntry::block_shift`/`decode_value_varying_bpv`: each block's own start offset is looked up directly (O(1), no prior-block scan needed) in the per-field jump table at `value_jump_table_offset + block * 8` (an absolute `.dvd`-file offset per block, written by the real encoder), then that block's own header (`bitsPerValue` byte, `i64` delta/constant, and -- when non-constant -- an `i32` packed-byte length) is read and its values bit-unpacked with the same `direct_reader::get` helper the single-width path already uses, reusing the whole field's `gcd` across every block. Previously this was `Error::UnsupportedVaryingBpvBlocks`; that variant is now gone. Fixture-verified: `fixtures/src/GenDocValuesVaryingBpv.java` writes 32,868 docs (two full 16384-value blocks with sharply different value ranges -- block 0 in `0..49`, block 1 in huge widely-spaced multiples of 1e9 -- plus a trailing partial block) through a real `IndexWriter`, forcing the 10%-savings `doBlocks` heuristic to trip, and `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/doc_values_varying_bpv_fixtures.rs` asserts `block_shift.is_some()` (confirming the fixture actually exercises the split, not a silent single-width fallback) and every one of the 32,868 decoded values against real Lucene's own read-back. Unit-tested for the block-boundary and all-same-value-in-a-block (`bitsPerValue == 0`) shapes with hand-built bytes (`varying_bpv_blocks_decoded_across_two_blocks`, `varying_bpv_block_all_same_value`). **Per-field doc-values skip index decode (task #185, this row's prior gap): ported.** A field whose `FieldInfo` carries a non-`None` `doc_values_skip_index_type` now gets its `.dvm` `DocValuesSkipperEntry` (`Lucene90DocValuesProducer.readDocValueSkipperMeta`: offset/length into `.dvs`, min/max value, doc count, max doc id, max value count) parsed into `DocValuesSkipperMeta` (`DocValuesMeta::skippers`, keyed by field number, orthogonal to the field's doc-values *type*) instead of the previous `Error::UnsupportedSkipIndex` rejection, and `parse_skip_index` decodes the full multi-level per-interval structure out of `.dvs` (`Lucene90DocValuesConsumer.writeLevels`'s inverse: a level-count byte then, per level coarsest-first, `maxDocID`/`minDocID`/`maxValue`/`minValue`/`docCount`) into a `DocValuesSkipIndex`/`Vec<SkipIndexInterval>`, eagerly rather than real Lucene's lazy `advance()`-driven read. **Decode-only, not yet wired into a range-query scan** (`search/doc_value_query.rs::search_numeric_range` still does a full sweep ŌĆö see that row below and the follow-up tracked as "Doc-values skip index in range query scan"); this is a deliberate scope cut, not a gap discovered late. Fixture-verified: `fixtures/src/GenDocValuesSkipIndex.java` writes 36,000 docs to a `NumericDocValuesField.indexedField` field (past both the 4096-doc base-interval size and the 8-interval level-1 grouping threshold, so the fixture has a genuine 2-level interval, not just 1-level rows), and `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/doc_values_skip_index_fixtures.rs` compares the parsed meta and every decoded interval/level against a manifest built by manually walking the same raw `.dvs` bytes in Java (not by re-deriving them from `writeSkipIndex`'s grouping decisions, which this port doesn't reimplement). Unit-tested for truncated/corrupt input: zero and above-`SKIP_INDEX_MAX_LEVEL` level counts, a truncated level body, an out-of-range offset/length, and a `.dvs` header/id mismatch. |
| `util/packed/DirectReader`/`DirectWriter` (bit-packed integer array read + write) | `lucene-codecs/src/direct_reader.rs` | **both directions ported**, as **one generic bit-position formula** each (`get`/`encode`), not Java's thirteen width-specialized `DirectPackedReaderN`/encode-path classes ŌĆö those exist for JIT monomorphism, a concern this port doesn't have yet. `encode`'s output round-trips through `get` for every `DirectWriter`-supported width (unit-tested); `padding_bytes_needed`/`unsigned_bits_required` (`DirectWriter.paddingBytesNeeded`/`unsignedBitsRequired`) are also ported, needed for wire-compatible writer output even though this port's own bounds-checked `get` never needs the padding itself |
| `util/packed/DirectMonotonicReader`/`DirectMonotonicWriter` (monotonic sequence read/write, blocks of min/avg/bit-packed-delta) | `lucene-codecs/src/direct_monotonic.rs` | **both directions ported.** Read side used by BINARY doc values' variable-length address blocks, SORTED_NUMERIC/SORTED_SET's multi-value address ranges, and (structurally, values discarded) by the terms dictionary. Write side (`write`) returns owned `(meta_bytes, data_bytes)` rather than streaming to an `IndexOutput` (no on-disk `IndexOutput` yet); round-trip-tested through the read side for linear, irregular, single-value, and empty sequences, plus one hand-verified case matching Java's exact `flush()` arithmetic |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90DocValuesProducer.TermsDict` (ordinal ŌåÆ term bytes, 64-term LZ4-compressed blocks + prefix compression) | `lucene-codecs/src/terms_dict.rs` | ported as a **decode-once full materialization** (`decode_all_terms` returns every term up front), not Java's lazy seekable `TermsEnum` ŌĆö the block-address array and reverse index exist purely to support random seeking without a full scan, which a one-shot decode doesn't need; both are parsed structurally (to keep the `.dvm` cursor aligned) but their values are discarded, same trade-off as `IndexedDISI` and stored fields. Noted in passing during the doc-values write-side slice: this file's `cargo llvm-cov` **region** coverage sits at 92.15% (below this project's 95% bar), though its **line** coverage (96.27%, the metric the pre-commit gate actually enforces via `--fail-under-lines`) clears it ŌĆö pre-existing, not introduced by that slice; worth closing the region gap in a future pass but not gating anything today. |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90NormsConsumer` (write side) | `lucene-codecs/src/norms.rs::write_single_dense_field` | **write path started -- scoped to exactly one shape: a single norms field, DENSE (every doc `0..maxDoc` has a value, no `IndexedDISI` sparse structure), at most 1 byte per doc** -- the `numDocsWithValue == maxDoc` branch of `addNormsField` feeding `numBytesPerValue`'s `0` (all values equal, `min >= max`, Java's constant-value encoding) and `1` (`Byte.MIN_VALUE..=Byte.MAX_VALUE`) cases only; a range needing 2/4/8 bytes returns `WriteError::RangeTooWide` rather than silently truncating. Returns `(meta_bytes, data_bytes)` ŌĆö norms have no third (`.dvs`-style) file, unlike doc values. **Explicitly deferred, not silently missing**: sparse fields (`IndexedDISI.writeBitSet`, the `numDocsWithValue != maxDoc` branch), 2/4/8-byte-per-doc widths, and multiple fields in one `.nvm`/`.nvd` pair ŌĆö all separate future slices. Unit-tested by round-tripping through this port's own existing reader (`parse_meta`/`norm_value`/`check_data_header_footer`): varying signed-byte values, an all-equal-values (constant-encoding) set, the non-dense-input rejection path (`WriteError::NotDense`), and the range-too-wide rejection path (`WriteError::RangeTooWide`). **Verified against real Lucene in the writeŌåÆread direction**: `crates/lucene-codecs/examples/write_norms_fixture.rs` writes two segments and `fixtures/src/VerifyNorms.java` opens each directly through `Lucene90NormsFormat.normsProducer` (hand-built `SegmentInfo`/`FieldInfos`, no `.si`/`.fnm` writer needed), confirming every doc's value matches the manifest via real `NumericDocValues.nextDoc`/`longValue` iteration: `_0` (varying small signed values, the real `bytesPerNorm == 1` path) and `_1` (all-equal values, the `bytesPerNorm == 0` constant path, added from the start per the doc-values write-side review's finding rather than shipping it unverified against real Lucene) ŌĆö both passed on the first real-Lucene run. **Now wired into `IndexWriter`'s normal indexing chain** (`crates/lucene-index/src/index_writer.rs::set_norms_field`/`build_norms_output`): before this, `write_single_dense_field` was only ever exercised directly by `merge.rs`'s merge-side tests and this module's own unit tests ŌĆö a caller building an index through `IndexWriter::add_document`/`commit()` had no way to get norms written at all. `set_norms_field(Some(field_name))` opts one field (single-field-per-commit, same scope as `set_doc_values_field`) into automatic norm computation: each pending doc's field length is derived from `crate::indexing_chain::invert_documents`'s own per-term occurrence counts (summed across all terms for that doc ŌĆö real Lucene's `FieldInvertState.length`, total token count not distinct-term count), then encoded with `lucene_util::small_float::int_to_byte4` ŌĆö the exact inverse of this port's own existing `lucene_search::similarity::decode_norm` read-side (`byte4_to_int`), not re-derived from Java source. No caller-supplied norm values are involved; `commit()` computes them from actual indexed text. Still scoped: one field per commit (no `add_norms_field` yet), and a doc missing the field gets a `0`-length norm rather than being excluded (the writer's output is always dense). End-to-end proven by `crates/lucene-index/src/index_writer.rs::commit_with_norms_field_writes_readable_length_dependent_norms_for_multiple_docs` ŌĆö three docs with different body-field token counts, added via plain `add_document`/`commit()`, decode to three different, exactly-correct norm bytes through the unmodified reader stack. See `PLAN.md`'s "Wire norms computation into the `IndexWriter` indexing chain" entry for the full gap analysis and what this does/doesn't unblock for postings-writer competitive-impact computation |
| `codecs/lucene90/IndexedDISI.writeBitSet` (sparse norms/doc-values write side) | ŌĆö | deferred to Phase 5 (write path), needed once sparse norms/doc-values write support is scoped |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90DocValuesConsumer` (write side) | `lucene-codecs/src/doc_values.rs::{write_single_dense_numeric_field, write_single_dense_binary_field, write_single_dense_sorted_numeric_field, write_single_dense_sorted_field, write_single_dense_sorted_set_field}` | **write path covers four of the five doc-values kinds now (task #77 added BINARY and SORTED_NUMERIC to task #11's original NUMERIC-only write side, task #99 added SORTED, an earlier task added SORTED_SET) -- all four share the same scope: DENSE only** (every doc `0..maxDoc`/every doc for SORTED_NUMERIC has at least one value, no `IndexedDISI` sparse structure), **no varying-bits-per-value blocks.** `write_single_dense_numeric_field`/`write_numeric_values_body` (this task): the per-value encoding choice (plain delta, GCD-delta, or table compression) now matches `Lucene90DocValuesConsumer.writeValues` exactly -- a running GCD of every value's offset from the first value seen (with Java's own `[i64::MIN/2, i64::MAX/2]` overflow guard), a `<=256`-entry distinct-value set (abandoned past that cap, same as Java's `uniqueValues`), then table compression wins only if it needs strictly fewer bits than GCD/plain-delta (`unsignedBitsRequired(uniqueValues.len() - 1) < unsignedBitsRequired((max - min) / gcd)`); the `min >= max` (all-equal) case is still handled as `bitsPerValue = 0` constant encoding. The on-disk distinguishing fields are exactly Java's: the `tableSize` i32 in the meta (`-1` = no table, `>= 0` = table entry count followed by that many `i64` table values) and the `gcd` i64 right after `bitsPerValue`/`min` (`1` = no GCD scaling, matching plain delta). No new read-side work was needed -- `read_numeric_entry`/`decode_value` already fully decoded both table and GCD entries (ported read-only, real-Lucene-fixture-verified, before this task's write-side work existed). `write_single_dense_binary_field`: fixed-length (`ordinal * length` indexing) and variable-length (a `direct_monotonic::write`-backed end-offset array, `block_shift = 0`, same simplicity-over-ratio choice `term_vectors.rs`/`stored_fields.rs`'s own monotonic writers already made) ŌĆö an empty-length value is a present value, not "no value". `write_single_dense_sorted_numeric_field`: flattens every doc's values into one shared array (reusing the NUMERIC-entry encoder verbatim via the newly-extracted `write_dense_numeric_entry_body` helper) plus a per-doc address range, **except** when every doc has exactly one value, where it must (not may) omit the address array entirely to match what `read_sorted_numeric_entry` infers from `num_docs_with_field == numeric.num_values` ŌĆö that equality isn't a stored flag, so writing addresses when it holds would desync the two sides. All three functions return `(meta_bytes, data_bytes, skip_index_bytes)`, same shape, and always emit a valid (if empty) `.dvs` skip-index file. **SORTED now has a write side too (this task)**: `write_single_dense_sorted_field` builds the sorted, deduplicated distinct-value dictionary from the field's raw per-doc bytes (`Vec<Vec<u8>>` in, `sort_unstable`+`dedup`), maps each doc to its term's ordinal (written as a plain dense NUMERIC entry via the same `write_dense_numeric_entry_body` the other three functions share ŌĆö matches real Lucene's `doAddSortedField`, which always wraps a `SortedDocValues` as a singleton `SortedNumericDocValues` and so never needs an address array), then writes the dictionary itself via a new `write_terms_dict` helper ŌĆö a from-scratch port of `Lucene90DocValuesConsumer.addTermsDict`/`writeTermsIndex` (64-term LZ4-compressed prefix-compressed blocks, a `DirectMonotonicWriter`-backed block-address array, and the coarser every-1024th-ordinal reverse index with `StringHelper.sortKeyLength`-style disambiguating prefixes) that real Lucene shares byte-for-byte between `addSortedField` and `addSortedSetField`, so it's already positioned to serve a future SORTED_SET writer unchanged. `write_terms_dict` uses `lz4::compress` (no preset-dictionary variant, unlike real Lucene's `compressWithDictionary`) on each block's prefix-compressed body alone rather than the first term acting as a preset dictionary ŌĆö still format-compatible, since the decompressor only ever *permits* back-references into the dictionary region, never requires them, and the dictionary bytes are already present verbatim right before the compressed body starts (see `write_terms_dict`'s own doc comment). Both writer's `DirectMonotonicWriter` block shift is fixed at `0` (real Lucene always uses `16`), the same simplicity-over-compression-ratio choice `write_single_dense_binary_field`'s address array already made ŌĆö the format stores `block_shift` per-field, so any value round-trips correctly through this port's own reader. **SORTED_SET now has a write side too (this task)**: `write_single_dense_sorted_set_field` builds the dictionary from every value of every doc (not one value per doc, since a doc can carry more than one), sorted and deduped the same way `write_single_dense_sorted_field` does, then writes each doc's ordinals following `write_single_dense_sorted_numeric_field`'s exact collapse rule: when every doc ends up with exactly one distinct value it writes a plain `SortedEntry` (`multiValued = 0` flag byte, per-doc ordinal via `write_dense_numeric_entry_body`, no address array), otherwise a true multi-valued form (`multiValued = 1`, flattened ordinals plus a `direct_monotonic`-backed address-range array), matching what `read_sorted_set_entry` actually checks (the `multiValued` flag byte, not a count equality like SORTED_NUMERIC's read side uses). The dictionary itself goes through the same `write_terms_dict` helper, unchanged. Docs with zero values are rejected with `WriteError::EmptyMultiValuedDoc`, same contract as SORTED_NUMERIC. **Explicitly still deferred for the four kinds that do have a write side** (see the module's own doc comments): sparse fields (`IndexedDISI`-backed docs-with-value) for BINARY/SORTED/SORTED_NUMERIC/SORTED_SET (NUMERIC sparse writing exists, see below), the varying-bits-per-value block split (`doBlocks`), per-field doc-values skip indexes (`writeSkipIndex`/`.dvs` content), (multiple fields in one `.dvm`/`.dvd`/`.dvs` triple is no longer deferred: `write_dense_fields` writes any number of distinct dense fields, of the same or different DocValuesTypes, into one container, and the five `write_single_dense_*_field` functions are now thin one-field wrappers over it -- see its own doc comment and unit tests in `doc_values.rs`; `IndexWriter::commit()` and `lucene-index/src/merge.rs`'s merge path do not yet call it with more than one field each, a documented follow-up, not a format limitation). GCD compression and table compression are no longer deferred -- both are now chosen automatically by `write_numeric_values_body` (see above). **Now wired into `IndexWriter::commit()` for all five DocValuesTypes -- NUMERIC, BINARY, SORTED, SORTED_NUMERIC, and SORTED_SET** (SORTED wiring added by task #99, SORTED_SET wiring by the following task, BINARY/SORTED_NUMERIC wiring added by this task): `IndexWriter::set_doc_values_field(Some(field_name))` (`crates/lucene-index/src/index_writer.rs`) opts a writer into calling `write_single_dense_numeric_field`/`write_single_dense_binary_field`/`write_single_dense_sorted_field`/`write_single_dense_sorted_numeric_field`/`write_single_dense_sorted_set_field` (dispatched on `DocValuesFieldConfig::doc_values_type`, cached at `set_doc_values_field` time) for exactly one field of every segment `commit()` flushes. NUMERIC sources per-doc `i64` values from `FieldValue::Int`/`FieldValue::Long`; BINARY sources per-doc raw bytes from `FieldValue::String` (UTF-8 bytes) or `FieldValue::Binary`, one value per doc, via the new `build_binary_doc_values_output` (same accepted-value shape as SORTED, but no terms dictionary/dedup/ordinals -- BINARY stores every doc's bytes verbatim); SORTED sources per-doc raw bytes the same way via `build_sorted_doc_values_output`; SORTED_NUMERIC sources per doc *every* `StoredField` entry carrying that field's number as `FieldValue::Int`/`FieldValue::Long` (a doc opts into multiple values by repeating the field), via the new `build_sorted_numeric_doc_values_output`; SORTED_SET sources per doc *every* `StoredField` entry carrying that field's number as raw bytes (same repeated-field convention, real Lucene's own `SortedSetDocValuesField`/`SortedNumericDocValuesField` convention), via `build_sorted_set_doc_values_output`. **All five now dispatch dense vs. sparse per field, per commit (follow-up task)**: each `build_*_doc_values_output` helper collects only the docs that actually supplied a value; if every pending doc has one, it calls the existing dense writer unchanged (byte-for-byte identical output to before this task); if some but not all do, it calls the corresponding `write_single_sparse_*_field` (all five of which already existed in `doc_values.rs` from earlier tasks, just previously unreachable from `IndexWriter`) with only the present `(doc_id, value)` pairs; if none do, it's still `Error::MissingDenseDocValue` (nothing to encode) -- so this is strictly an addition, not a replacement, of the old dense-only behavior. A wrong-typed value still fails the whole commit with `Error::NonNumericDocValue` (NUMERIC/SORTED_NUMERIC) or `Error::NonBinaryDocValue` (BINARY/SORTED/SORTED_SET), same "atomic, not best-effort" contract as before. A doc with an explicit empty/zero value is still present, not absent -- absence means the doc never supplied the field's `StoredField` entry at all. Tested for all five types (`commit_writes_sparse_{numeric,binary,sorted,sorted_numeric,sorted_set}_doc_values_when_a_pending_doc_has_no_value`), each round-tripping the middle of three docs as correctly absent (`None`/empty, not a stale or zero value) through the existing unmodified sparse reader. **Known limitation, pre-existing and unrelated to sparse support**: `doc_values_field` is `Option<DocValuesFieldConfig>` (singular), so a "one field dense, another field on the same docs sparse" mixed-commit scenario isn't expressible yet -- only one doc-values field can be configured per `IndexWriter` at a time. **This task is IndexWriter wiring only, not new codec logic**: `write_single_dense_binary_field`/`write_single_dense_sorted_numeric_field` themselves (the on-disk byte encoding) were already implemented and already had real-Lucene fixture verification from an earlier task (see the `write_doc_values_fixture.rs`/`VerifyDocValues.java` paragraph below, segments `_3`-`_6`) -- this task only adds the `IndexWriter::set_doc_values_field`/`build_doc_values_output` call sites and `IndexWriter`-level tests (add_document/commit/read-back through the existing reader) for those two already-verified write functions; no new real-Lucene fixture was added by this task. **Merge-policy interaction, applied proactively from the postings/term-vector features' own review findings**: `execute_merge`/`merge_stored_only_segments` have no `.dvd`/`.dvm`/`.dvs` awareness either, so `segment_stats()` also excludes any segment whose `.si` lists a `.dvd` file from `find_merges`' candidate pool, covered by `segments_with_doc_values_are_never_automatically_merged_away`. **Postings + term vectors + doc values together, tested and found to work correctly**: all three setters can be configured at once (to different fields in the same commit) -- each builds its own in-memory output before `dir` is touched, and each `.si`-patching helper reads back whatever the others have already written rather than clobbering it, so a segment ends up with all ten files correctly listed; covered by `postings_term_vectors_and_doc_values_configured_together_all_write_correctly`. Required end-to-end proof: `commit_with_doc_values_field_writes_readable_numeric_values_for_multiple_docs`/`commit_with_doc_values_field_writes_readable_binary_values_for_multiple_docs`/`commit_with_doc_values_field_writes_readable_sorted_values_for_multiple_docs`/`commit_with_doc_values_field_writes_readable_sorted_numeric_values_for_multiple_docs`/`commit_with_doc_values_field_writes_readable_sorted_set_values_for_multiple_docs` (`lucene-index/src/index_writer.rs`) add documents via `IndexWriter::add_document`/`commit()` and read the written `.dvm`/`.dvd` back via the existing unmodified `lucene_codecs::doc_values::{parse_meta, numeric_value, binary_value, sorted_ord, sorted_numeric_values}`/`terms_dict::decode_all_terms`, asserting the exact per-document values (SORTED/SORTED_SET: resolved ordinal(s) -> term bytes) come back; `commit_with_doc_values_field_rejects_non_binary_sorted_value`/`commit_with_doc_values_field_rejects_non_binary_binary_value` cover `Error::NonBinaryDocValue`, and `commit_with_doc_values_field_rejects_non_numeric_sorted_numeric_value`/`commit_with_doc_values_field_rejects_doc_with_no_sorted_numeric_values` cover `Error::NonNumericDocValue`/`Error::MissingDenseDocValue` for the SORTED_NUMERIC wiring added by this task. Unit-tested by round-tripping through this port's own existing, unmodified reader (`parse_meta`/`numeric_value`/`binary_value`/`sorted_numeric_values`/`sorted_ord`/`terms_dict::decode_all_terms`/`check_data_header_footer`): NUMERIC -- a mixed-magnitude value set, an all-equal-values (constant-encoding) set, negative/large values, and the non-dense-input rejection path (`WriteError::NotDense`); BINARY -- fixed-length, variable-length (including an empty-string value), and the non-dense-input rejection path; SORTED_NUMERIC -- varying per-doc value counts (1-3 values/doc), the all-single-valued collapse case (confirms no address array gets written), the all-same-value case (confirms the flattened array still gets constant-value encoding), and the empty-per-doc-value rejection path (`WriteError::EmptyMultiValuedDoc`); SORTED (task #99) -- a small dictionary with repeated values (confirms dedup + ordinal reuse), an all-docs-share-one-value set (confirms constant-ordinal encoding), an empty-`Vec<u8>` value (a present, distinct value, not "no value"), a 300-distinct-term dictionary reversed into descending input order (exercises 4 full + 1 partial 64-term LZ4 block; only the first, `ord == 0` reverse-index sample fires at this size), a separate 2200-distinct-term dictionary that crosses two 1024-ordinal reverse-index sample boundaries (exercising both the `sampled_previous` capture and a non-first sample's `common_prefix_len` computation, which the 300-term case doesn't reach), and the non-dense-input rejection path; SORTED_SET (this task) -- a small dictionary shared across docs with varying, overlapping value sets, an all-docs-single-value set (confirms the collapse to a plain `SortedEntry` with no address array), varying per-doc value counts (1-3 values/doc), intra-doc duplicate raw values collapsing to one ordinal reference per doc, a 2200-distinct-term dictionary reversed into descending input order that crosses many 64-term LZ4 blocks and two non-trivial 1024-ordinal reverse-index sample boundaries (matching SORTED's own large-dictionary term count -- a smaller count such as 2000 only reaches the first non-trivial sample, never the second), the empty-per-doc-value rejection path (`WriteError::EmptyMultiValuedDoc`), and the non-dense-input rejection path. **Verified against real Lucene in the writeŌåÆread direction, all five DocValuesTypes now (task #11 covered NUMERIC only; this task extends to BINARY/SORTED_NUMERIC/SORTED/SORTED_SET)**: `crates/lucene-codecs/examples/write_doc_values_fixture.rs` writes **ten** segments and `fixtures/src/VerifyDocValues.java` opens each directly through `Lucene90DocValuesFormat.fieldsProducer` (hand-built `SegmentInfo`/`FieldInfos`, no `.si`/`.fnm` writer needed), dispatching per segment on a `<segment>.type` manifest key to the matching production-facing read API -- `NumericDocValues`, `BinaryDocValues`, `SortedNumericDocValues`, `SortedDocValues`, or `SortedSetDocValues` -- and confirming every doc's value(s) match the manifest: `_0`/`_1`/`_2` are the original NUMERIC segments (mixed values, the min-shift-drop regression case, and the all-equal constant-encoding case); `_3`/`_4` are BINARY (fixed-length direct addressing, and variable-length including an empty value via the `DirectMonotonicReader` address block); `_5`/`_6` are SORTED_NUMERIC (every doc exactly one value, the address-array-collapse case, and 1-3 values/doc forcing the real address-range array); `_7` is SORTED (repeated terms over a 3-term dictionary, exercising both the ordinal decode and the terms-dict decode); `_8`/`_9` are SORTED_SET (every doc one distinct value, the `multiValued = false` collapse case, and 1-2 distinct values/doc sharing a dictionary including a doc whose raw values dedup to one ordinal). All ten passed on the first real-Lucene run. **Scope note**: `_7`'s SORTED and `_8`/`_9`'s SORTED_SET dictionaries are deliberately small (3 terms), so this real-Lucene verification exercises `write_terms_dict`'s single-64-term-block path only -- it does **not** reach the multi-LZ4-block / multi-1024-ordinal-reverse-index-sample paths a large dictionary forces (those remain covered only by the 2200-term unit tests against this port's own reader, described above; no fixture has yet forced real Lucene to open a multi-block dictionary this port wrote). **Sparse NUMERIC write support added (this task)**: `write_single_sparse_numeric_field(field_number, doc_values: &[(doc_id, value)], max_doc, ...)` is the first write-side function in this module that doesn't require every doc to have a value. It builds the `IndexedDISI`-backed docs-with-field structure via the new `indexed_disi::write` (see that module's own doc comment) and reuses the exact same per-rank value encoding (`write_numeric_values_body`, factored out of what was `write_dense_numeric_entry_body`'s tail) that dense NUMERIC already uses -- a sparse field's value array is indexed by rank-among-present-docs, exactly what the pre-existing read side (`numeric_value`'s sparse branch, `indexed_disi::rank_of`) already expects, since that reader has supported sparse NUMERIC/BINARY/SORTED_NUMERIC since task #4/#21. **Scope, deliberately narrow**: NUMERIC only -- BINARY/SORTED/SORTED_NUMERIC/SORTED_SET sparse writing is still deferred (the shared `write_numeric_values_body`/`indexed_disi::write` machinery would extend to them the same way `write_dense_numeric_entry_body` already does for dense, but wiring that up for the other four kinds, plus `IndexWriter` integration, is left for a future task). `write_dense_numeric_entry_body` and all four other write functions are completely unmodified in behavior (`write_single_dense_numeric_field_still_dense_after_sparse_addition` pins its output byte-for-byte identical to before this change). **Block-shape coverage**: `indexed_disi::write` picks a shape per 65536-doc block by density, exactly like real `IndexedDISIBuilder` -- `<= 4095` present docs -> SPARSE (explicit low-16-bit doc ids), `== 65536` -> ALL (no data), otherwise -> DENSE (a 65536-bit bitset); all three are exercised by `write_single_sparse_numeric_field_uses_all_three_block_shapes` (block 0 forced SPARSE with 10 docs, block 1 forced ALL with every doc present, block 2 forced DENSE at 50% density). Deliberately **not** written: the DENSE rank table (`denseRankPower` is always `0xFF`/no-rank, matching every other sparse entry this port already writes) and the trailing jump table -- both pure random-access speedups the existing whole-structure-decode reader doesn't use. Unit-tested by round-tripping through this port's own existing reader (`parse_meta`/`numeric_value`): `write_single_sparse_numeric_field_round_trips_through_own_reader` (200,000 docs, every 3rd present, forcing multiple DENSE blocks) and `write_single_sparse_numeric_field_uses_all_three_block_shapes` (above) both check a stride sample of docs rather than every doc, since `numeric_value` re-decodes the whole `IndexedDISI` structure per call (see `indexed_disi.rs`'s doc comment) and checking all ~200K docs individually would be quadratic; `write_single_sparse_numeric_field_rejects_duplicate_doc_id`/`_rejects_out_of_range_doc_id` cover the two new `WriteError` variants (`DocIdsNotAscending`, `DocIdOutOfRange`). **Verified against real Lucene in the writeŌåÆread direction (follow-up task)**: `crates/lucene-codecs/examples/write_sparse_numeric_doc_values_fixture.rs` writes two segments (`_0`: 20 docs with values missing interspersed throughout, not just trailing; `_1`: 200,000 docs, 1 of every 3 present, the same DENSE-block-shape case the unit test above covers) and `fixtures/src/VerifySparseNumericDocValues.java` opens each directly through real `Lucene90DocValuesFormat.fieldsProducer` (hand-built `SegmentInfo`/`FieldInfos`, same division of labor as `VerifyDocValues.java`), then calls real `NumericDocValues.advanceExact` for every doc id from `0` to `max_doc - 1` -- not just iterating present docs via `nextDoc()` -- confirming docs with a value return the correct value and docs without one correctly report absent. Both segments passed on the first run. This closes the gap the earlier task's note flagged: `write_single_sparse_numeric_field`'s output is now confirmed genuinely valid, real-Lucene-readable NUMERIC sparse doc-values, not just self-consistent with this port's own reader.  **Skip-index scope revisited (this task), deferral confirmed unchanged**: checked whether this session's multi-field `write_dense_fields`/all-five-type merge/NRT doc-values wiring made real per-field skip-index (`Lucene90DocValuesSkipIndex`) write support tractable. It does not change anything -- every `FieldInfo` constructor in `lucene-index` (`segment_writer.rs`, `update_document.rs`, `index_writer.rs`, `merge.rs`, `check_index.rs`) still hardcodes `doc_values_skip_index_type: DocValuesSkipIndexType::None`, so the writer never even decides a field should carry one; `doc_values.rs`'s shared `finish_field_list_and_footers` still emits only an index-header-plus-footer stub for every write path; the read side (task #185, after this note was written) now decodes any field claiming one instead of rejecting it, but nothing in `lucene-index`'s writers ever sets a non-`None` `doc_values_skip_index_type` to begin with, so this port's own writer output never carries one to decode; `doc_value_query.rs`'s `search_numeric_range` still does a full sweep regardless. Implementing real skip-index *write* bytes in isolation would still be dead serialization code with no writer ever requesting it -- the same unconsumed-accessor trap flagged elsewhere this session -- so the write side remains deferred; only the decode side changed. |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90CompoundFormat`/`Lucene90CompoundReader` (`.cfs`/`.cfe` read) | `lucene-codecs/src/compound_format.rs` | ported (read-only), fixture-verified against a real `useCompoundFile=true` IndexWriter segment (12 packed sub-files); preserves Java's exact-version cross-check between `.cfs`/`.cfe` and the total-length-vs-entries-table sanity check |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90CompoundFormat.write` | `lucene-codecs/src/compound_format.rs::write` | **write path ported**, given already-written sub-files as `(stripped_id, complete_bytes)` pairs -- each sub-file must already be a complete standalone codec file (its own `IndexHeader` sharing the segment's id, a body, and its own `Footer`), exactly what this port's other write-side modules (`field_infos::write`, `stored_fields::write_best_speed`, etc.) already produce, so no new file-on-disk plumbing was needed to compose them. Verified precisely against Java rather than assumed simple: `Lucene90CompoundFormat.writeCompoundFile` isn't a bare concatenation -- it (1) packs sub-files smallest-first (`Comparator.comparingLong(length)`), (2) pads each sub-file's start offset up to a 64-byte boundary, and (3) "verifies and copies" each sub-file's header (checking the object id matches) then re-derives its footer from the *verified* checksum rather than copying the footer bytes outright -- but since that checksum is definitionally the value already stored in the sub-file's own footer, the net result is byte-identical to a verified verbatim copy, which is what this port does (validate header id + footer checksum, then copy the whole sub-file). No per-sub-file checksumming beyond that verification step; the `.cfs` file's own footer covers the whole packed blob via a single CRC, same as every other framed format in this port. Unit-tested by round-tripping through this port's own existing reader (`parse_entries`/`check_data_header_footer`/`open_input`) with three differently-sized/differently-codec-named sub-files, confirming ascending-size ordering, 64-byte-aligned offsets, and byte-for-byte sub-file recovery, plus rejection of a wrong segment id, a bad magic number, and a corrupt footer checksum. **Verified against real Lucene in the writeŌåÆread direction**: `crates/lucene-codecs/examples/write_compound_format_fixture.rs` packs a `.fnm` (`field_infos::write`) and a `.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm` triple (`stored_fields::write_best_speed`) -- four distinct sub-files -- into a `_0.cfs`/`_0.cfe` pair, and `fixtures/src/VerifyCompoundFormat.java` opens it through real `Lucene90CompoundFormat.getCompoundReader` with a hand-built `SegmentInfo`, confirms the sub-file list and lengths, then re-decodes the `.fnm` through real `Lucene94FieldInfosFormat` and the `.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm` triple through real `Lucene90StoredFieldsFormat` -- both read *through* the compound reader, not the raw sub-file bytes directly, so a byte-offset bug would fail this check even if the entries table alone looked correct. Passed on the first real-Lucene run. **Wired into the write path (task #38):** `lucene-index/src/segment_writer.rs::flush_stored_only_segment` now actually calls this `write` function when its caller passes `use_compound_file: true`, packing a flushed segment's `.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm`/`.fnm` into `<name>.cfs`/`.cfe` and setting `SegmentInfo.is_compound_file` accordingly, instead of leaving this codec's write half unreferenced by any writer. See that row below for the wiring's own tests. **Write-side edge-case audit (later task):** zero/one/many (200, stressing the `.cfe` entry-count vint's 128-entry width boundary) sub-files, a zero-length sub-file body, unusual/empty/non-ASCII sub-file names, and duplicate-name detection on read were all checked against the actual code -- every case was already handled correctly (no production bug found); only test coverage was missing, now closed by `write_single_sub_file_round_trips`, `write_zero_length_body_sub_file_round_trips`, `write_many_sub_files_stresses_entry_count_vint_boundary`, `write_unusual_sub_file_names_round_trip`, `write_rejects_completely_empty_sub_file_bytes`, and `write_duplicate_sub_file_names_detected_on_read` (see `PLAN.md` for the full per-case writeup). |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90StoredFieldsFormat`/`Lucene90CompressingStoredFieldsReader`/`FieldsIndexReader` (`.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm` read, **both `Mode.BEST_SPEED` and `Mode.BEST_COMPRESSION`**) | `lucene-codecs/src/stored_fields.rs` | ported (read-only), fixture-verified against a real IndexWriter for both modes: BEST_SPEED (6 docs, one field of each of the 6 stored-field types, varying lengths so the chunk uses the bulk multi-doc framing) and BEST_COMPRESSION (same shape, forced via `Lucene104Codec.Mode.BEST_COMPRESSION`, with a long repeated-text field so the DEFLATE dictionary + multi-sub-block path is actually exercised); the mode is detected from the `.fdt` data codec name itself (`...FastData` vs `...HighData`), and `chunk_size` is read from `.fdm` rather than hardcoded, since BEST_COMPRESSION's is ~480KB vs BEST_SPEED's ~80KB |
| `util/compress/LZ4.decompress`/`LZ4.compressWithDictionary` | `lucene-codecs/src/lz4.rs` | decompress ported (read-only, as before) **and a real compressor is now ported** (`lz4::compress`): a scoped-down port of `compressWithDictionary` with a zero-length dictionary only (preset-dictionary compression is a separate, larger piece -- cross-block dictionary reuse -- and remains unported; `decompress`'s dictionary *read* support is unaffected) and always using the simpler `FastCompressionHashTable` match-finding strategy (a single last-occurrence-per-hash table with a fixed hash-table size) rather than `HighCompressionHashTable`'s hash-chain "try a better match" search (`compressHC`, unported) -- every match this compressor emits is a real, verified back-reference within `MAX_DISTANCE`, just not necessarily the longest one available at each position the way Lucene's own search would find. Verified both by round-trip through this port's own `decompress` (empty input, single byte, below-match-threshold-length, highly repetitive input, pseudo-random incompressible input, matches at the very start/end, and long input forcing the extended-length continuation encoding) and cross-engine (see the `stored_fields.rs::write_best_speed` row below) |
| `codecs/lucene90/LZ4WithPresetDictCompressionMode` (dictionary + fixed-size sub-blocks) | `lucene-codecs/src/stored_fields.rs::decompress_unit` | ported as an eager full decode (no partial/lazy read path ŌĆö this port hands back a materialized `Document`, not a streaming reader); every unit's *compressed*-length vint (the dictionary's, then each block's) is batched up front in this format, before any of the actual compressed bytes -- they exist in Java only to support seeking without decompressing everything before it, so they're read here to keep the cursor aligned and discarded |
| `codecs/lucene90/DeflateWithPresetDictCompressionMode` (raw DEFLATE, dictionary + fixed-size sub-blocks) | `lucene-codecs/src/deflate.rs` | decode ported as an eager full decode, same shape as the LZ4 sibling but a real semantic difference caught by a real fixture: DEFLATE isn't self-terminating from an output-length count alone, and (unlike LZ4) each unit's compressed-length vint sits **immediately before its own compressed bytes**, not batched up front -- getting this backwards (by over-generalizing from the LZ4 format) produced a `MalformedVarint` against real Lucene bytes, caught and fixed before commit.
