Built on `miniz_oxide::inflate::core`'s low-level API (raw deflate, no zlib header/Adler-32) rather than its `decompress_to_vec` convenience wrappers, which don't support a preset dictionary; the preset-dictionary trick is the same one `lz4::decompress` uses -- pre-write the dictionary bytes into the output buffer before `d_off` and let back-references look behind it. **A real DEFLATE compressor is now ported too** (`deflate::compress`): unlike LZ4 (no compress-capable crate was already a dependency, so this port hand-wrote a real greedy-match encoder), `miniz_oxide` -- already a dependency for the decode side -- exposes `miniz_oxide::deflate::compress_to_vec`, a real, already-vetted raw-DEFLATE encoder (no zlib wrapper to strip; that's the sibling `compress_to_vec_zlib`), so this port reuses it directly at level 6 rather than hand-writing Huffman+LZ77 from scratch -- only a *correctly decodable* stream is required, not byte-identical output to Java's own `Deflater`. Fixed a real latent bug while wiring this up: `decompress`'s `decompressed_len == 0` fast path returned without consuming `compressed_len` bytes from the shared reader, silently desyncing every subsequent unit in a chunk whenever a dictionary (or sub-block) happens to be zero-length but still has nonzero *compressed* bytes on the wire (a real DEFLATE stream, even of empty content, still emits a final-block marker) -- caught by `write_best_compression`'s own round-trip tests, not a real-Lucene fixture, but the same bug could in principle have hit a real BEST_COMPRESSION file whose dictionary happens to size out to 0 bytes |
| `codecs/lucene90/compressing/StoredFieldsInts` (bulk per-doc field-count/length arrays) | `lucene-codecs/src/stored_fields.rs::read_bulk_ints`/`write_bulk_ints` | **both directions ported**, `Mode.BEST_SPEED` only for the write side so far. Read: exact on-disk transposed-block layout preserved (values decode identically to Java's SIMD-shaped bulk reader), decoded via a plain per-value loop rather than replicating the bulk/SIMD machinery itself. Write: **scalar-tail encoding only** (correct for `values.len() < 128`; the 128-value transposed-block path Java's bulk writer produces for larger chunks isn't implemented yet, so `write_best_speed` asserts chunks stay under that). **Audited 2026-07-17**: only bits-per-value 0/8/16/32 are real -- confirmed against `StoredFieldsInts.java`'s `writeInts`, which only ever emits those four values (constant-fill, or the smallest of 8/16/32 that fits `max`), and whose own `readInts` throws `IOException("Unsupported number of bits per value: " + bpv)` for anything else. This port's `Error::UnsupportedBulkIntWidth` for other byte values is a faithful match of Java's own defensive check, not a gap; left as-is, with `read_bulk_ints_unsupported_width_rejected` widened to sweep the whole invalid space rather than assert a single sentinel value |
| `codecs/lucene90/compressing/Lucene90CompressingStoredFieldsWriter` (write side), `Mode.BEST_SPEED` (LZ4) only | `lucene-codecs/src/stored_fields.rs::write_best_speed` | **write path started ŌĆö first slice of Phase 5, since updated with a real compressor.** Every doc still goes into one single, un-sliced, zero-dictionary chunk (no dictionary/sub-block splitting, no multi-chunk-by-size flush heuristics -- that part of the real writer's behavior remains out of scope) but the chunk's payload is now compressed with **real LZ4 back-reference matching** (`crate::lz4::compress`, see that row above) rather than the original `encode_literal_lz4` literal-only stub -- the empty zero-length dictionary unit that precedes it is still emitted via `encode_literal_lz4` since a real compressor over zero bytes degenerates to the same single token. Numeric field encodes (`write_zint`/`write_zfloat_full`/`write_tlong_full`/`write_zdouble_full`) still always emit the full/worst-case encoding rather than Java's shortest-of-several choice (still correct, just not size-optimal). **Verified against real Lucene in the writeŌåÆread direction** (the reverse of this repo's usual differential-testing pattern): `crates/lucene-codecs/examples/write_stored_fields_fixture.rs` writes a `.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm` triple -- now including a field whose value is a phrase repeated 50 times, specifically to prove genuine compression (the resulting `.fdt` is ~222 bytes for a doc set whose one repeated field alone is 2250 bytes, well under a literal-wrapped size) -- and `fixtures/src/VerifyStoredFields.java` opens it directly through `Lucene90StoredFieldsFormat.fieldsReader` (with a hand-built `SegmentInfo`/`FieldInfos`, so this slice doesn't also need `.si`/`.fnm` writers) and confirms every document's fields, including the repeated-phrase one, match byte-for-byte -- passed on the first real-Lucene run after the compressor was wired in |
| `codecs/lucene90/compressing/Lucene90CompressingStoredFieldsWriter` (write side), `Mode.BEST_COMPRESSION` (DEFLATE) | `lucene-codecs/src/stored_fields.rs::write_best_compression` | **write path ported**, sharing `write_best_speed`'s single-chunk/`docs.len() < 128` scope and `.fdx`/`.fdm` assembly (factored into a shared `write_index_and_meta` helper -- both modes produce an identical index/meta shape, differing only in the recorded `chunkSize`), but with its own `.fdt` payload framing since the two modes' compression-unit shapes genuinely differ (BEST_SPEED: one zero-dictionary LZ4 unit; BEST_COMPRESSION: a dictionary prefix plus several fixed-size DEFLATE sub-blocks, real Lucene's own `dictLength = len/(NUM_SUB_BLOCKS*DICT_SIZE_FACTOR)`/`blockLength = ceil((len-dictLength)/NUM_SUB_BLOCKS)` sizing formula reused verbatim, `NUM_SUB_BLOCKS=10`/`DICT_SIZE_FACTOR=6`) -- sharing one function across both would have needed a mode-branch threaded through the framing itself, so two functions sharing only the common suffix was the more readable split. Each sub-block (and the dictionary prefix) is compressed independently via `deflate::compress` with no cross-unit back-referencing (`miniz_oxide` has no preset-dictionary compress API) -- still a valid decode per `decompress_unit`'s contract, just a smaller compression ratio than real Lucene's writer, not a correctness gap. **Verified against real Lucene in the writeŌåÆread direction**: `crates/lucene-codecs/examples/write_stored_fields_fixture.rs` now writes *two* segments, `_0` (BEST_SPEED, unchanged) and `_1` (BEST_COMPRESSION, one field repeating a phrase ~2000 times, ~90KB, forcing a real dictionary plus several sub-blocks rather than one trivial unit), and `fixtures/src/VerifyStoredFields.java` was extended to loop over both segments (a `segments=_0,_1` manifest key, each with its own `<seg>.mode` attribute value) -- both pass against real Lucene on the same run |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90TermVectorsFormat`/`Lucene90CompressingTermVectorsReader` (`.tvd`/`.tvx`/`.tvm` read) | `lucene-codecs/src/term_vectors.rs` | ported (read-only), fixture-verified against a real IndexWriter (a repeated-term field with positions/offsets/payloads on some occurrences but not others, a multi-field doc, and a doc with no term vectors at all); positions/offsets reset to a fresh delta chain at each **term's** first occurrence rather than one chain per field (reverse-engineered from the reader's exact loop bounds, not its doc comment ŌĆö see the module doc); the LZ4 unit's term-suffix and payload bytes are interleaved **per document** (each doc's suffixes then its payloads, not two global regions), a second reverse-engineered detail the first fixture run caught; uses two more bit-packing conventions alongside `direct_reader`: `packed_ints` (generic MSB-first bitstream, for the distinct-field-numbers array) and `block_packed` (64-value blocks built on `packed_ints`, for the field/term bookkeeping arrays) |
| `util/packed/PackedInts.Format.PACKED`/`BulkOperationPacked` (generic MSB-first bit-packed array, arbitrary width) | `lucene-codecs/src/packed_ints.rs` | **both directions ported.** Read as before; `encode` is the exact bitwise inverse of `get`, any width `0..=64` (this convention has no whitelist of supported widths, unlike `direct_reader`) |
| `util/packed/BlockPackedReaderIterator`/`BlockPackedWriter` (64-value self-describing blocks) | `lucene-codecs/src/block_packed.rs` | **both directions ported.** Read as before (a single `decode_all`, not Java's seekable `next`/`skip` iterator). Write (`encode_all`) always emits `minValue = 0` rather than Java's per-block min-value optimization -- correct, just not minimal, same "worst-case width over minimal width" stance as `stored_fields::write_best_speed` -- and picks each block's `bitsPerValue` as the exact width its own max value needs, not rounded to any fixed set |
| `codecs/lucene90/compressing/Lucene90CompressingTermVectorsWriter` (write side) | `lucene-codecs/src/term_vectors.rs::write_best_speed` | **write path started, scoped down twice over from the real writer.** Single chunk only (`chunk_docs = docs.len()`), same as `stored_fields::write_best_speed`. Feature matrix: **positions, offsets, and payloads are all supported** (task follow-up; originally positions-only, see git history). Offset deltas are patched against a fixed `CHARS_PER_TERM = 1.0` constant for every distinct field number that has OFFSETS in the chunk -- unlike a real flush's analyzer-derived ratio, this constant only needs to be self-consistent with this writer's own inverse math on read, which it is by construction (whatever's subtracted out when writing is exactly added back on decode), so its value doesn't affect round-trip correctness. Payload bytes are appended into the same LZ4 unit as term suffixes, grouped **per document** (all of that doc's fields' suffixes, then that doc's PAYLOADS fields' payloads) to match the read side's decompression slicing. No prefix sharing: every term is written with `prefix_len = 0` (its full text as the "suffix"), unlike a real writer that shares a prefix with the previous term in the field. Every `block_packed`/`direct_reader`/`packed_ints` array uses the exact bit width its own values need (worst case, not minimized across blocks/chunks). LZ4 is the same zero-dictionary, literal-only "compression" as stored fields' write side (`encode_literal_lz4`, a term-vectors-local copy since this format's LZ4 unit has no dict/block-length wrapper to begin with). **Verified against real Lucene in the writeŌåÆread direction**: `crates/lucene-codecs/examples/write_term_vectors_fixture.rs` writes a `.tvd`/`.tvx`/`.tvm` triple (3 docs, a multi-field doc, a doc with no term vectors, repeated terms with multi-occurrence positions) and `fixtures/src/VerifyTermVectors.java` opens it directly through `Lucene90TermVectorsFormat.vectorsReader` (hand-built `SegmentInfo`/`FieldInfos`, no `.si`/`.fnm` writer needed) and confirms every doc's terms/freqs/positions match via real `Terms`/`TermsEnum`/`PostingsEnum` -- passed on the first real-Lucene run. **Two review-pass fixes landed before this slice's commit**, both worth naming durably rather than leaving only in a source comment: (1) `bits_per_field_num` (the bit width `field_nums`/`allFieldNumOffs` are packed at) is floored at 1, never 0 -- a chunk where every field across every doc has `field_number == 0` (an entirely ordinary shape, e.g. any single-field index) previously computed a 0-bit width, which this port's own reader tolerates (an all-zero chunk just decodes as all-zero) but real Lucene's reader does not: it unconditionally indexes `packedBulkOps[bitsPerValue - 1]`, throwing `ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException` on a 0-bit width, independent of Java's `assert` (stripped without `-ea`, the default). The fixture now writes a second segment (`_1`) specifically shaped this way (every field number 0 across two docs) since the primary fixture's mixed field numbers 0/1 never exercised this; both segments pass against real Lucene. (2) the `.tvm` meta stream's `packedIntsVersion` field must be written as `2` (`PackedInts.VERSION_CURRENT`/`VERSION_MONOTONIC_WITHOUT_ZIGZAG`) -- this port's own reader never validates that field (a wrong value round-trips fine through it), but real Lucene's `BlockPackedReaderIterator` does validate it, so this is a genuine cross-engine-only requirement a purely-Rust test suite could never catch. Multi-chunk segments and real LZ4 back-reference compression remain unimplemented on the write side. **Offsets/payloads write support (later follow-up task)**: round-trip proven via direct `TermVectorField` construction + read-back through the unmodified reader (`write_best_speed_offsets_only_round_trips`, `write_best_speed_payloads_only_round_trips`, `write_best_speed_positions_offsets_payloads_round_trips_multi_term_multi_doc`, `write_best_speed_positions_and_offsets_freq_three_round_trips` in `term_vectors.rs`'s own test module) -- **review-confirmed bug fixed before landing**: the offset-delta correction used each occurrence's absolute position instead of the position *delta* the read side actually applies as its own correction input, which only coincidentally agreed for `freq <= 2` or a first occurrence at position 0 (exactly the shape every other test here happens to use) -- silently corrupting the 3rd+ occurrence's decoded start/end offsets for any term repeated 3+ times with positions+offsets both enabled. Fixed to track the same delta-from-previous-occurrence stream `positions_flat` itself encodes; `write_best_speed_positions_and_offsets_freq_three_round_trips` is the regression test (freq 3, non-uniform position gaps) that would have caught it. **Not yet wired end-to-end**: neither `IndexWriter`'s term-vector commit path (`build_term_vectors_output` in `index_writer.rs`) nor `merge.rs`'s merge path constructs a `TermVectorField` with `has_offsets`/`has_payloads` set today, so no real indexing flow exercises the new capability yet; that plumbing (tokenizer offsets/payloads through to `TermVectorField` construction) is a separate follow-up. `merge.rs`'s `Error::TermVectorOffsetsOrPayloadsNotSupported` guard is deliberately left in place even though the writer no longer needs it -- lifting it would require separately verifying the merge path's own field-reprefixing/combination logic handles offsets/payloads correctly, which hasn't been reviewed. **Now wired into `IndexWriter::commit()`** (follow-up task, see PLAN.md): `IndexWriter::set_term_vector_field(Some(field_name))` (`crates/lucene-index/src/index_writer.rs`) opts a writer into calling this function for exactly one field of every segment `commit()` flushes, sourcing per-document `term -> (freq, positions)` data by regrouping `crate::indexing_chain::invert_documents`'s term-keyed inverted index by doc ID (term vectors need the transpose of what the postings writer wants) -- the same single-chunk/positions-only scope above, unchanged, now reachable from a real `IndexWriter::add_document`/`commit()` call. Requires `store_term_vectors == true` on the field's `FieldInfo` (checked, `Error::UnsupportedTermVectorField` otherwise). **Now wired for more than one field per commit too (same follow-up task as `set_postings_field`):** `IndexWriter::add_term_vector_field(field_name)` opts a writer into additional term-vector fields on top of whatever `set_term_vector_field` already established (same "replace, don't accumulate" semantics for `set_term_vector_field` itself). This was a genuine `IndexWriter`-side gap, not a `term_vectors::write_best_speed` limitation -- that function already accepted multiple `TermVectorField` entries per `TermVectorsDocument` before this task; `build_term_vectors_output` simply never built more than one. Now every configured field with content for a given doc contributes its own `TermVectorField` to that doc's `TermVectorsDocument`, all written in one `write_best_speed` call. Proven end-to-end by `crates/lucene-search/tests/index_writer_term_vectors_fixtures.rs::two_distinct_term_vector_fields_in_one_commit_are_both_readable`. **Merge-policy interaction, applied proactively from the postings feature's own review finding**: `execute_merge`/`merge_stored_only_segments` have no `.tvd`/`.tvx`/`.tvm` awareness either, so `segment_stats()` also excludes any segment whose `.si` lists a `.tvd` file from `find_merges`' candidate pool, keeping it permanently un-mergeable rather than mergeable-with-silent-data-loss. Covered by `segments_with_term_vectors_are_never_automatically_merged_away`, mirroring the postings version. **Postings + term vectors together, tested and found to work correctly**: `set_postings_field` and `set_term_vector_field` can both be set (to the same field) in one commit -- each builds its own in-memory output before `dir` is touched, and the `.si`-patching helper for each reads back whatever the other has already written rather than clobbering it, so a segment ends up with all seven files correctly listed; covered by `a_field_with_both_postings_and_term_vectors_configured_together_produces_both_correctly` (`lucene-search`) and its `lucene-index`-side unit-test counterpart. Required end-to-end proof: `crates/lucene-search/tests/index_writer_term_vectors_fixtures.rs::documents_added_via_index_writer_have_readable_term_vectors` adds documents via `IndexWriter::add_document`/`commit()` (not a hand-built fixture) and reads them back via the existing unmodified `lucene_search::term_vector_for_doc`, asserting the exact per-document term/freq/position data. |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90PointsFormat`/`Lucene90PointsReader`/`util/bkd/BKDReader` (`.kdm`/`.kdi`/`.kdd` read, block KD-tree point values -- `IntPoint`, `LongPoint`, `LatLonPoint`, etc.) | `lucene-codecs/src/points.rs` | ported (read-only), fixture-verified against a real IndexWriter (2000 docs, a `LongPoint` field on two-thirds of them so leaves have non-continuous doc ids, forcing several leaves past the default 512-point-per-leaf threshold); only the current on-disk BKD version (10, vectorized BPV24 + BPV21) is accepted, older versions rejected outright rather than replicated. **Decode-fully, no query pruning yet**: the packed index tree is walked in full left-to-right order to recover every leaf's file pointer rather than replicating Java's bounding-box-pruned seek/skip navigation -- the index's `leftNumBytes` skip-ahead hint is read and discarded, since a full recursive left-then-right traversal naturally consumes exactly that many bytes and needs no seeking at all; every `DocIdsWriter` doc-id encoding is now supported, including the legacy vint-delta marker (byte `0`, `LEGACY_DELTA_VINT`): continuous run, bitset, 16/21/24/32-bit delta-packed all fixture-verified against a real writer, plus the legacy delta-vint decode covered by hand-built unit tests only, since no Lucene 10.5.0 writer (real or this port's) can produce that marker -- it predates the 16/21/24/32-bit encodings and real Lucene's own `DocIdsWriter` source comments it as "legacy, should no longer be used in the writing side." Any other marker byte remains a rejected `Error::UnsupportedDocIdsEncoding`. **`num_index_dims != 1` leaf layout bug fixed (task #22)**: `read_leaf_block`'s per-leaf min/max bounding box (present whenever `numIndexDims > 1`) had been decoded in the wrong position relative to the compressed-dimension marker byte -- it read the box *before* the marker, matching real `BKDReader.visitDocValuesNoCardinality`'s (older, no-longer-written) leaf layout instead of `visitDocValuesWithCardinality`'s (the layout every current-version, `VERSION_LOW_CARDINALITY_LEAVES`-and-up tree actually uses), which reads the marker *first* and only reads the box afterward, and only when the marker isn't `-1`. This went unnoticed for a while since the only test ever exercising it was a hand-built unit test (no real multi-dimension tree had ever been read *or* written by this port), and was only caught once this task's new write side produced a real 2-dimension `.kdd`/`.kdi` pair and `fixtures/src/VerifyPoints.java` tried to open it through real `Lucene90PointsFormat` (`CorruptIndexException: Got compressedDim=127`) -- exactly the kind of bug the differential-testing skill's fixture-first rule exists to catch. Fixed in both `read_leaf_block` (order swapped, box now conditioned on `compressed_dim != -1`) and this port's own `write_leaf` (marker written before the box, matching). **Compressed-dimension boundary re-validated, found already correct (task #191)**: cross-checked `read_leaf_block`'s rejection condition (`compressed_dim < -2 || compressed_dim as i32 >= field.num_dims`) and the real-dimension-index (`>= 0`) branch's `compressed_byte_offset = compressed_dim * bytes_per_dim + common_prefix_lengths[compressed_dim]` math against real `BKDReader.readCompressedDim`/`visitDocValuesWithCardinality` (`util/bkd/BKDReader.java` lines ~974-980, ~944-950) -- both match exactly, no off-by-one, no fix needed. The prior gap was fixture coverage, not correctness: the existing `points_index` fixture's single-dimension `val` field can only ever produce `compressedDim == 0` (there's no dimension 1 to pick), so the offset multiplication was previously only ever exercised at its trivial zero case. `fixtures/src/GenPoints.java` now also writes a second, 2-dimension `IntPoint` field (`multi`: dim0 a bijective multiplicative hash of the doc id spread across the full 32-bit range, dim1 only 4 distinct values), engineered so real `BKDWriter` picks dim1 as `sortedDim`/`compressedDim` in every leaf -- a naive sequential dim0 turned out to be the wrong shape (BKDWriter's recursive range-narrowing squeezed dim0's in-leaf cardinality down to 1-2, which tied or beat dim1's fixed <=4 and kept `compressedDim` at 0 in every leaf; verified this was actually happening, not just theorized, via a temporary debug print in `read_leaf_block`). The generator now mechanically confirms `compressedDim >= 1` was really written, independent of this port's own decoder, via `CompressedDimSpy.java` (lives in `org.apache.lucene.util.bkd` to reach `BKDReader`'s package-private fields, and does its own from-scratch walk of the packed index tree and leaf header) and records the observed per-leaf byte in the `multi_leaf_compressed_dims` manifest key; `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/points_fixtures.rs`'s `parses_real_multi_dim_points_and_matches_lucene_values` test asserts on that recorded value directly (so it fails, not just passes vacuously, if a future regeneration stops exercising the branch) and also confirms this port decodes the fixture identically to real Lucene -- proving the nonzero-index offset math against real bytes, not just hand-built ones. |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90PointsWriter`/`util/bkd/BKDWriter` (write side) | `lucene-codecs/src/points.rs::write` | **write path now supports any number of dimensions, any number of leaves** (task #22 extends the prior one-dimension-only, multi-leaf write path to `numDims > 1`, e.g. `LatLonPoint`-shaped 2D fields; `numIndexDims` may be less than `numDims`, i.e. trailing data-only, non-indexed dimensions are supported, e.g. a `LatLonShape`-style bounding box). **Split-dimension selection**: at every recursive split, [`widest_dim`] picks the dimension with the widest value range (`max - min`, computed via unsigned big-endian byte subtraction so it works for any `bytesPerDim`, not just ones that fit a native integer) across the current point subset, ties toward the lowest dimension index -- for `numDims == 1` this always picks dimension 0, so the original single-dimension path/behavior is unchanged. This is a real, deliberately-chosen heuristic, not a wild deviation from real `BKDWriter`: real Lucene's own multi-dimension `build()` picks its split dimension by computing each dimension's cardinality/range at the current node too (see `BKDWriter.build`'s `usedBytes`/cardinality-driven choice for leaf-level dimension selection, and its inner-node `splitDim` selection based on recomputed per-dimension bounds) -- this port's version is a simpler, still-real range comparison rather than replicating the exact cardinality-counting algorithm, documented as a deliberate scope reduction. Because a different dimension can be chosen at every recursion level, `compute_leaf_plan` now consumes and re-sorts an owned `Vec` at each split node (`Vec::split_off`) rather than indexing into one shared, globally-presorted array the way the single-dimension predecessor did -- still no per-node `radix select` the way real `BKDRadixSelector` does, a plain `sort_by` per node is enough at this port's sizes. Real Lucene picks the leaf-split shape via `getNumLeftLeafNodes` (fill the deepest full binary-tree level, half its leaves go left, then push any remainder left too) and `mid = numLeftLeafNodes * maxPointsInLeafNode`; this port's `compute_leaf_plan` uses the exact same two formulas (verified against `BKDWriter.getNumLeftLeafNodes`'s source, not approximated), so the resulting tree shape matches real Lucene's for any point count/leaf-size combination. `packIndex`/`recursePackIndex`'s general case (split descriptor + left/right children + `leftNumBytes` skip-ahead) is implemented (`pack_index`), matching real Lucene's node layout exactly, **now including the split *dimension*, not just the split value**: the packed-index code formula `(firstDiffByteDelta * (1 + bytesPerDim) + prefix) * numIndexDims + splitDim` (already documented from task #21) now genuinely varies `splitDim` per node rather than always encoding `0`, and the split-value delta-coding's `lastSplitValues`/`negativeDeltas` state (`last_split_values`/`negative_deltas` in this port) is now **one array slot per index dimension** (real `BKDWriter.recursePackIndex`'s own per-dimension arrays) instead of a single dimension-0-only pair -- only the dimension a given node actually split on has its slot touched/saved/restored around that node's children, every other dimension's slot is inherited unchanged from the parent, exactly like real Lucene's shared per-dimension arrays. Leaf data now carries all dimensions per point (`numDims * bytesPerDim` bytes), and each leaf also writes its own (tighter-than-field) per-dimension min/max bounding box whenever `numIndexDims != 1`, matching what the read side ([`read_leaf_block`]) already unconditionally decoded in that case (see the read-side row above for the ordering bug this surfaced and fixed). Leaf-encoding choices remain freely made (not replicating real `BKDWriter`'s size-driven heuristics): common-prefix length always 0 per dimension, compressed-dimension marker always `-2` with every run forced to length 1, doc ids `CONTINUOUS_IDS` or plain `BPV_32`. Unit-tested: `widest_dim`/`unsigned_byte_sub` in isolation (widest-range selection, tie-breaking, multi-byte borrow), `compute_leaf_plan`'s point-distribution/balance invariants (now leaf-content-based rather than range-based, since dimension changes at each recursion level, and confirmed no longer a globally-presorted single order), two dedicated multi-dimension `pack_index`/split-value-reconstruction tests (a 3-dimension, 7-leaf tree whose split dimensions are confirmed to vary across nodes, decoded by a generalized `reconstruct_split_values` mirror of real `BKDReader.readNodeData`), and full writeŌåÆread round trips through this module's own reader for a 2D `LatLonPoint`-shaped 100-point/25-leaf tree and a 3D 2-byte-per-dim, non-continuous-doc-id, 8-leaf tree, on top of the pre-existing 1D single/multi-leaf coverage. 99.5%+ line coverage on `points.rs`. **Verified against real Lucene in the writeŌåÆread direction**: `crates/lucene-codecs/examples/write_points_fixture.rs` now writes *three* segments -- `_0` (single-leaf, 1D, unchanged), `_1` (multi-leaf, 1D, unchanged, including its pre-existing narrow-bounding-box pruning query), and **`_2` (new: 2-dimension, `LatLonPoint`-shaped, multi-leaf, with the two dimensions deliberately correlated so a real bounding-box query narrow on both axes actually finds leaves fully `CELL_INSIDE_QUERY`, not just `CELL_CROSSES_QUERY`/`CELL_OUTSIDE_QUERY`)** -- and `fixtures/src/VerifyPoints.java`'s new `verifySegment2D`/`verifyPruningQuery2D` open `_2` directly through real `Lucene90PointsFormat.fieldsReader`, confirm every point via a full-decode `CELL_CROSSES_QUERY`-only pass, **and then run a real two-dimension bounding-box query that prunes across *both* dimensions** (asserting at least one `CELL_OUTSIDE_QUERY` and one `CELL_INSIDE_QUERY` cell actually occur, then checking the returned point set against the manifest) -- all three segments and both pruning queries (1D and 2D) passed against real Lucene, proving real `BKDReader`/`IndexTree` accepts this port's multi-dimension packed-index encoding and correctly reconstructs per-dimension split values/dimensions from it, including under real pruning. **Data-only dimensions now supported (task #192)**: `WritePointsField::num_index_dims` may be less than `num_dims` -- [`widest_dim`]'s split-dimension selection and [`pack_index`]'s prefix-coding/`lastSplitValues`/`negativeDeltas` state are restricted to the first `num_index_dims` dimensions only (matching real `BKDWriter.split`/`recursePackIndex`, which only ever range over `config.numIndexDims()`), while the per-doc packed value written to every leaf, and read back by [`read_leaf_block`], remains the full `num_dims`-wide value including the trailing data-only dims -- `write_field` rejects `num_index_dims` outside `1..=num_dims` (`Error::InvalidNumIndexDims`). **Explicitly deferred, not silently missing**: real query-driven pruning on this port's *own* read side (still decode-fully, see the read-side row) -- multi-dimension write is otherwise no longer a scoped-out gap. **Multi-leaf/multi-dimension edge case audit**: systematically re-checked the max-points-per-leaf boundary (`count == max` stays one leaf, `count == max + 1` splits into exactly 2), the all-points-identical degenerate case (no dimension has variance -- `widest_dim`'s tie-break still returns a valid dimension and the recursion terminates purely by leaf count, never by value variance), the only-the-last-dimension-varies case (`widest_dim` correctly finds it via unsigned-byte-range comparison, not a naive dimension cycle), `num_dims == 1` vs. `>= 2`, exact-multiple-of-max vs. partial-last-leaf point counts, and deep recursion/many-leaf trees -- all already correct with no production bug found; the audit's only gaps were test coverage at the exact boundary/degenerate cases, closed with five new tests in `points.rs` (`write_then_read_exactly_at_max_points_per_leaf_stays_single_leaf`, `write_then_read_one_over_max_points_per_leaf_splits_into_two`, `write_then_read_all_points_identical_degenerate_case`, `widest_dim_picks_last_dim_when_only_it_varies`, `write_then_read_last_dim_only_varies_multi_leaf_round_trips`). `num_index_dims != num_dims` was re-confirmed as a genuine, pre-existing scope boundary at the time of this audit -- since closed by task #192 (see above: `WritePointsField::num_index_dims` now exists and `write_field` validates/uses it instead of hardcoding `num_index_dims = num_dims`). |

| `codecs/lucene104/Lucene104PostingsReader`/`Writer`, `PostingsUtil`, `ForUtil`, `PForUtil` (`.doc`/`.pos`/`.pay` files, `PostingsEnum` in `DOCS`/`DOCS_AND_FREQS`/`DOCS_AND_FREQS_AND_POSITIONS`/`DOCS_AND_FREQS_AND_POSITIONS_AND_OFFSETS`/`DOCS_AND_CUSTOM_FREQS` mode, incl. payloads) | `lucene-codecs/src/postings.rs` (+ `lucene-codecs/src/for_util.rs`) | **ported: sequential decode (a full forward scan, `nextDoc()`-equivalent -- no skip-ahead/`advance()`) of any `docFreq > 1` up to `LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` (32 * `ForUtil.BLOCK_SIZE` = 8192), `IndexOptions::Docs`/`DocsAndFreqs`.** Three writer-side shapes now all decode: `docFreq == 1` is pulsed entirely into the term dictionary (`Lucene104PostingsWriter.finishTerm`, no `.doc` bytes at all -- `postings::singleton_postings` reconstructs `(docID, freq)` purely from `TermMetadata::singleton_doc_id` + `totalTermFreq`); `1 < docFreq < BLOCK_SIZE` takes `PostingsUtil.writeVIntBlock` (group-varint doc-delta/freq-bit packing + a plain-vint tail of freq exceptions, no skip data, no impacts), decoded via `DataInput::read_group_vints` (`postings::read_tail_block`); and **`docFreq >= BLOCK_SIZE`** now decodes one or more full 256-doc blocks (`postings::read_full_block_header` + `postings::decode_full_block_body`) followed by that same tail-block encoding for the `docFreq % BLOCK_SIZE` remainder. Each full block is `ForUtil`/`PForUtil`-bit-packed -- `for_util.rs` is a direct transliteration of `ForUtil.decode1..decode16`/`decodeSlow` (the lane-interleaved-per-byte/halfword SIMD-shaped bit-packing for `bitsPerValue <= 16`, plain 32-bit-wide packing above that) and `PForUtil.decode` (the token byte + up to 7 byte-patched exceptions), independently round-tripped against a hand-written test encoder for every `bits_per_value` in `1..=32` (not just what one fixture term happens to need) -- and the full block's doc-delta section additionally supports the "all-256-consecutive" (`bitsPerValue == 0`) and dense unary bit-set (`bitsPerValue < 0`) encodings the writer picks for storage efficiency (the bit-set path is not a corner case: it's what real Lucene chooses for this port's own dense `big`/"everywhere" fixture term, confirmed by regenerating against the real writer). Also ported (previously skipped by `blocktree.rs`, see that row): the per-term postings-metadata bytes (`Lucene104PostingsReader.decodeTerm`, no-positions subset) -- `postings::decode_term_metadata`, threaded across a `.tim` block's entries exactly like `SegmentTermsEnumFrame` threads `IntBlockTermState`. `blocktree::FieldTerms::postings(term, doc_in)` wires this up end-to-end: `seekExact` -> stats + metadata -> singleton reconstruction or `.doc` decode. **`advance()`: an "advance()-shaped API, not real skip-ahead" shim, landed this slice.** `postings::PostingsCursor` (`next_doc()`/`advance(target)`/`doc_id()`/`freq()`) gives `PostingsEnum`-style interface parity, but it is a binary search over `DocInput::read_postings`'s already-fully-materialized `Postings.docs`/`freqs` `Vec`s -- **not** a lazy on-wire jump using the level-0/level-1 skip pointers (those are still parsed-and-discarded, exactly as before this slice; see the deferred bullet below, unchanged). This was a deliberate scope choice per this slice's own design brief: a real lazy skip-ahead would need a new stateful `DocInput`-like type tracking on-wire position and decoding blocks on demand, which is a materially larger and riskier change than a cursor over data this file already decodes eagerly by design (the same tradeoff every other decoder in this file already made -- `BlockTree`'s `TermsEnum`, `IndexedDISI`, the terms dictionary, `BlockPackedReaderIterator`). Fixture-verified against real `PostingsEnum.advance(target)` output (`fixtures/src/GenBlockTree.java::appendAdvanceManifest`, `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/blocktree_fixtures.rs::{big,body}_field_advance_matches_real_lucene_postings_enum_advance`) for both "big"/"everywhere" (`docFreq == 300`, so some targets cross the full-block/tail-block boundary) and "body"/"cat" (`docFreq == 2`, single tail block), across before-first-doc/exact-match/between-docs/next-doc-after-a-match/last-doc/past-last-doc targets -- matched on the first real-Lucene run, no decode bugs caught (unsurprising, since the shim never touches the wire format at all, only the already-verified decoded `Vec`s). Unit tests (`postings.rs`) additionally cover: advancing to a target at or before the current doc ID (documented no-op, not an error or rewind -- real Lucene's contract technically forbids this, but the shim's binary-search-from-current-position implementation makes a no-op the natural, safe behavior to document rather than leave accidental), advance on empty postings, advance past the last doc (`NO_MORE_DOCS`), and advance immediately followed by `next_doc()` continuing from the landed position. **Deferred** (rejected with `Error::Unsupported`, or in the skip-ahead case simply not implemented as an API): (1) **real lazy skip-ahead** -- the level-0/level-1 skip pointers (`level0NumBytes`/`blockLength`/level-1 header vlongs) are parsed in wire order for correctness but never used to jump forward or to avoid decoding a block; every block between the start and the target is fully decoded by `read_postings`, and `PostingsCursor` only adds a post-hoc binary-search cursor on top of that (see above) -- correct but not fast for a searcher that only wants a subrange (fine for a full-scan/merge consumer, or a conjunction/phrase query over small-enough postings lists that eager decode is cheap); a stateful decode-on-demand `DocInput` that actually jumps past undecoded blocks using the level-0 pointers remains future work; (2) **`docFreq >= LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS`** (8192) -- level-1 skip entries start appearing inline in the `.doc` stream every 32 full blocks, not yet parsed; (3) positions/offsets/payloads (`.pos`/`.pay`, `IndexOptions::DocsAndFreqsAndPositions` and up -- `decode_term_metadata` doesn't even parse the `posStartFP`/`payStartFP`/`lastPosBlockOffset` fields those index options add to the wire; being worked on separately, this slice deliberately did not touch `.pos`/`.pay`); (4) impacts/competitive-scoring metadata (`ImpactsEnum`, `CompetitiveImpactAccumulator`, needed for WAND/MAXSCORE in PLAN.md Phase 3) -- full-block impact bytes are parsed-and-discarded (skipped by length), never surfaced; (5) ~~`IndexOptions::DocsAndCustomFreqs` -- rejected outright, real Lucene never writes it for a normal text field~~ **now ported** (see the read/write postings-codec support note near the end of this row): it's wire-identical to `DocsAndFreqs` (real Lucene derives `indexHasFreq`/`writeFreqs` from `IndexOptions.subsumes(DOCS_AND_FREQS)`, which is `true` for both), so `read_postings`/`lazy_cursor`/`validate_field` now accept it directly alongside `DocsAndFreqs` with no new decode/encode path. **Positions/offsets/payloads are now ported** (`.pos`/`.pay`, `IndexOptions::DocsAndFreqsAndPositions` and `...AndOffsets`), sequential-only (no skip-ahead, same scope as the `.doc` side): `decode_term_metadata` now parses `posStartFP`/`payStartFP`/`lastPosBlockOffset` (`Lucene104PostingsReader.java:237-250`), `read_full_block` parses (but doesn't act on) the extra level-0 pos/pay skip-pointer fields those index options add to a full doc block's header (`Lucene104PostingsReader.java:754-761`), and the new `PosInput`/`PayInput` + `read_positions` decode every position/offset/payload occurrence for a term as **one flat sequence of `totalTermFreq` occurrences** (not one block per doc -- the writer buffers 256 occurrences at a time across doc boundaries, only resetting the position/offset accumulator per doc, `Lucene104PostingsReader.java:1298-1304`) -- full `ForUtil`/`PForUtil` blocks (payload lengths and offset start-deltas/lengths bulk-encoded, payload bytes batched per block) for `totalTermFreq / BLOCK_SIZE` full blocks, then a `refillLastPositionBlock`-style vint tail (payload bytes inlined in `.pos`, lengths only re-written when they change) for the remainder, re-chopped into per-doc groups via `Postings::freqs`. `blocktree::FieldTerms::positions(term, doc_in, pos_in, pay_in)` wires this up end-to-end alongside `postings()`. Fixture-verified against real `PostingsEnum.nextPosition()`/`startOffset()`/`endOffset()`/`getPayload()` output via a new "pos" field in `fixtures/src/GenBlockTree.java` (`DOCS_AND_FREQS_AND_POSITIONS_AND_OFFSETS`, a repeated term across two docs with a payload on only one occurrence, exercising the vint tail's payload-length-change bit) -- matched on the first real-Lucene run, no decode bugs caught this time. **Deferred**: the full-`ForUtil`/`PForUtil`-block position path (`totalTermFreq >= BLOCK_SIZE`) is only unit-tested (`postings::tests::read_positions_exactly_one_full_block_boundary`), not fixture-verified against real Lucene bytes, since reaching it needs 256+ real token occurrences of one term that this port's small hand-built fixtures don't produce; `docFreq >= LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` interacts with positions the same way it does with docs (not supported, same `Error::Unsupported` gate on `read_postings`, which `positions()` also goes through via `postings()`). Fixture-verified against real `PostingsEnum.nextDoc()`/`freq()` output (not just aggregate `docFreq`/`totalTermFreq` stats) via `fixtures/src/GenBlockTree.java`'s extended manifest: "body" (`docFreq == 2` for every term, `.doc` group-varint decode), "id" (`docFreq == 1`, singleton path, no `.doc` access at all), and **"big"/"everywhere" (`docFreq == 300`, one full `PForUtil`-bit-set-encoded block + a 44-doc group-varint tail, added specifically to force the multi-block path past real `Lucene104PostingsWriter`/`IndexWriter`)** -- see `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/blocktree_fixtures.rs`. Hand-built unit tests cover edge cases no small real fixture reaches: `docFreq == BLOCK_SIZE` (256, exactly one full block, no tail bytes at all), `docFreq == BLOCK_SIZE + 1` (257, one full block + a 1-doc tail), the full-block bit-set (unary) doc-delta decode and its too-few-set-bits corruption check, `docFreq == BLOCK_SIZE - 1` (255, the largest size the non-multi-block path supports), all-docs-freq-1 (group-varint bit-packing path with zero trailing freq-exception vints), `docFreq >= LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` rejection, and `decode_term_metadata`'s absolute-vs-delta and docStartFP-delta-vs-singleton-zigzag-delta branches. `for_util.rs`'s own unit tests independently round-trip `bits_per_value` `1..=32` (both the lane-interleaved `<=16` paths and the `decodeSlow` `17..=32` path) and the `PForUtil` all-equal/exceptions fast paths, via test-only encoders mirroring `ForUtil.collapse8/16`+`encode`/`PForUtil.encode`. **Post-landing review fixes**: (a) `decode_term_metadata` now correctly zeroes `doc_start_fp`/`pos_start_fp`/`pay_start_fp` before applying deltas when `absolute` is set (`Lucene104PostingsReader.decodeTerm`'s own reset), instead of basing them on whatever `prev` the caller passed in -- invisible today since every current caller passes a fresh `TermMetadata::EMPTY` as `prev` on `absolute`, but load-bearing once multi-block BlockTree threads `prev_meta` across blocks; covered by `decode_term_metadata_absolute_resets_fps_even_with_stale_prev`; (b) `read_positions`'s per-doc re-chop loop now returns `Error::Store(Corrupted(_))` instead of panicking via out-of-bounds indexing when a corrupted `.doc`/`.tim`/`.tmd` makes `freqs` sum to more or less than `total_term_freq` (covered by two new rejects-mismatch tests); (c) closed two coverage gaps the Ōēź95%-per-file bar didn't catch: the packed (`bitsPerValue > 0`) `.doc` doc-delta branch and the full-`PForUtil`-block position path *with offsets* (as opposed to payloads) were previously exercised by neither the fixture nor a unit test -- both now have dedicated unit tests (`read_full_block_packed_encoding_decodes_bit_packed_deltas`, `read_positions_full_block_with_offsets_no_payloads`), reusing `for_util`'s own test-only bit-packing encoder (later promoted to the production `for_util::for_encode` function, see below, so this cross-module reuse point moved with it) **Real lazy skip-ahead is now ported** (`postings::LazyDocsCursor`, `DocInput::lazy_cursor`, `blocktree::FieldTerms::lazy_postings`): a decode-on-demand `next_doc()`/`advance(target)` iterator that decodes one `.doc` block at a time, replacing the eager whole-term materialization `PostingsCursor` sits on top of (that shim is unchanged and still exists for callers that want the simpler already-decoded path -- see the module doc for which to pick). **The honest boundary of what is actually skipped**: `read_full_block_header` was split out of `read_full_block` (now a thin wrapper over `read_full_block_header` + `decode_full_block_body`) to read a full block's level-0 header (`level0NumBytes`/`docDelta`/`blockLength`/impacts/pos-pay fields) *without* running `ForUtil`/`PForUtil` decode on its body; the header alone gives the block's last doc ID (`prev_doc_id + docDelta`) and its on-wire byte span. When `advance(target)` finds `target > header.last_doc_id`, it `seek()`s straight to the block's end and moves to the next block, skipping the actual bit-unpack entirely -- the expensive part of a block. This works for **every full block a term has, at any `docFreq`, not just `docFreq >= LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS`**: level-0 skip-past-one-block only requires the term to have at least one full 256-doc block (`docFreq >= BLOCK_SIZE`), which is unrelated to the level-1 (8192-doc) threshold -- level-1 exists to skip past *32 full blocks at once* without reading their individual level-0 headers, a coarser optimization this port still does not need since it already reads every level-0 header cheaply one at a time. The **tail block** (the `docFreq % BLOCK_SIZE` remainder, or the whole term when `docFreq < BLOCK_SIZE`) carries no skip data on the wire at all -- reaching it always means decoding it in full, lazy cursor or not, matching real `Lucene104PostingsReader.refillRemainder`. `docFreq >= LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` is still rejected by `lazy_cursor` with the same `Error::Unsupported` as `read_postings` -- unchanged from before this slice; the lazy cursor does not add level-1 support, it only makes level-0 skip actually *used* instead of parsed-and-discarded. Differential-tested against real `PostingsEnum.advance(target)` output for the same target set as `PostingsCursor` (`crates/lucene-codecs/tests/blocktree_fixtures.rs::{big,body}_field_lazy_advance_matches_real_lucene_postings_enum_advance`) plus a full `next_doc()` walk compared against the eager `read_postings` result byte-for-byte (`big_field_lazy_next_doc_matches_eager_read_postings`) -- all three matched on the first real-Lucene run. A hand-built unit test (`lazy_cursor_advance_skips_corrupted_earlier_block_without_decoding_it`) proves the skip is real, not just correct by coincidence: it builds a first full block whose body is deliberately corrupt (a bit-set with fewer than `BLOCK_SIZE` bits set, which `decode_full_block_body` rejects with a `Corrupted` error) followed by a valid second block, and confirms `advance()` to a target in the second block succeeds (the corrupt first block is never decoded) while `advance()` to a target in the first block surfaces the corruption error (confirming the earlier success wasn't accidental). Other unit tests cover sequential multi-block decode matching `read_postings`, the no-op advance-to-current-or-earlier contract, advance past the last doc, and the `docFreq <= 1` rejection mirroring `read_postings`'s own. **`docFreq >= LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` (8192) level-1 skip data is now ported for both paths, closing the last remaining `docFreq` gap** (supersedes the several "rejected with `Error::Unsupported`" / "not yet parsed" mentions of that threshold above, which described the state before this slice). Above `LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` the `.doc` stream interleaves a level-1 skip entry (`postings::read_level1_entry`, the vInt span-last-doc delta + vLong `level1DocEndFP` + `indexHasFreq`-gated `readShort` skip1EndFP/numImpactBytes + impacts bytes + pos/pay sub-fields, reverse-engineered from `Lucene104PostingsReader.skipLevel1To`, `Lucene104PostingsReader.java:674-719`) before every span of `LEVEL1_FACTOR` (32) full level-0 blocks, for as long as at least `LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` docs remain. `read_postings` (eager) consumes each entry's bytes purely to stay byte-aligned and decodes its 32 blocks like any other; `LazyDocsCursor` (lazy) tracks `level1_last_doc_id`/`level1_doc_end_fp`/`level1_doc_count_upto` and, via the new `skip_level1_to` method (mirroring Java's `skipLevel1To`, wired into `advance` exactly like Java's `moveToNextLevel0Block`/`doAdvanceShallow` call it first), `seek()`s straight to `level1_doc_end_fp` to jump a whole 32-block span whose last doc is behind the target -- never reading even the individual level-0 headers of the skipped span, the coarser counterpart to the level-0 skip-past-one-block above. Positions inherit level-1 support automatically, since `positions()` no longer hits a `docFreq` gate. Fixture-verified against real `PostingsEnum` via a new "l1" field in `fixtures/src/GenBlockTree.java` ("l1term" in 8250 docs, one level-1 span + a 58-doc remainder): full `nextDoc()`/`freq()` iteration over all 8250 docs for both eager and lazy paths, plus eager and lazy `advance()` at the exact span boundaries (occurrence 8191 = span's last doc, 8192 = first remainder doc reached only by jumping the whole span, `appendLevel1AdvanceManifest`) -- matched on the first real-Lucene run, no decode bugs caught. Hand-built unit tests cover the level-1 entry decode in isolation (all freq/pos/pay sub-fields + the docs-only short form), an eager span+tail decode, a lazy sequential walk matching eager, and a "provably skipped" test corrupting an entire 32-block span to confirm `advance()` past it never touches the corrupt bytes while a control target into the span still surfaces the corruption. **Impacts/competitive-scoring metadata (`ImpactsEnum`/`CompetitiveImpactAccumulator`) are now decoded, for both level-0 (per-block) and level-1 (per-span) impact byte runs** -- this was the last thing on the postings wire that was parsed-and-discarded purely by length rather than decoded. `postings::Impact { freq: i32, norm: i64 }` (a direct port of `Impact`'s two fields) plus `postings::decode_impacts(bytes)` implement `Lucene104PostingsReader.readImpacts`'s decode exactly: a flat sequence of vint `freqDelta`s (each storing `impact.freq - previous.freq - 1`, i.e. `+1` is added back on decode) whose low bit selects between an implicit `normDelta == 0` (the common "norm only increases by 1" case, zero extra bytes) and an explicit zigzag `normDelta` vlong. `read_full_block_header` (level-0) and `read_level1_entry` (level-1) both now decode their impacts byte run into `FullBlockHeader::impacts`/`Level1Entry::impacts` instead of `skip()`-ing past it -- the length-prefix parsing (vint for level-0, `readShort` for level-1) is unchanged, only the payload is now real. **Exposed on both cursors** (impacts are inherently a "what's coming up from here" query that only makes sense against a position, matching real `ImpactsEnum.getImpacts()` -- both `LazyDocsCursor` and `PostingsCursor` have one): `LazyDocsCursor::level0_impacts()`/`level1_impacts()` for the genuinely lazy, decode-on-demand cursor, `PostingsCursor::level0_impacts()`/`level1_impacts()` for the eager, already-materialized one (a lookup into `Postings::level0_impacts`/`level1_impacts`, see below): `level0_impacts()` returns the current level-0 block's competitive pairs (empty once positioned in the tail block, which carries no level-0 impacts on the wire at all -- deliberately *not* replicating Java's synthetic "everything is competitive" `(Integer.MAX_VALUE, 1)` sentinel for that state, since this port exposes decoded wire data rather than reconstructing `ImpactsEnum`'s full multi-level fallback semantics) and `level1_impacts()` returns the current level-1 span's merged pairs (empty below `LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` docs or past the last span). Differential-tested against real `TermsEnum.impacts(PostingsEnum.FREQS)`/`ImpactsEnum.getImpacts(level)` ground truth (`fixtures/src/GenBlockTree.java::appendImpactsManifest`, `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/blocktree_fixtures.rs::{big,l1}_field_impacts_match_real_lucene_impacts_enum`) for "big"/"everywhere" (level-0 only, three occurrences within its one full block, freq/norm both varying 1..4) and "l1"/"l1term" (level-0 varying across different blocks of the same level-1 span, level-1 merged and identical across all three sampled occurrences since they share one span) -- matched on the first real-Lucene run. Unit tests for `decode_impacts` itself cover: empty input, a single implicit-norm-delta entry, multiple entries mixing implicit and explicit (including a full-width `i64::MAX` norm) deltas via a test-only encoder mirroring `Lucene104PostingsWriter.writeImpacts` exactly, and two truncation/corruption cases (a freqDelta vint missing its continuation byte, an explicit-norm-delta flag with no following zlong). **Impacts are now threaded through the eager path too**: `DocInput::read_postings` captures each level-0 block's and level-1 span's already-decoded impacts (no second decode pass -- it just retains what it was discarding) into `Postings::level0_impacts`/`level1_impacts` (`Vec<(last_doc_id_covered, Impacts)>`, ascending/contiguous so a lookup is a single `partition_point` binary search), and `PostingsCursor::level0_impacts`/`level1_impacts` look up the entry covering `doc_id()` the same way `LazyDocsCursor::level0_impacts`/`level1_impacts` report the block/span covering its own current position -- same query, same empty-cases contract (tail block, below `LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS`, no freqs, not yet/no-longer positioned), just against pre-materialized data instead of decode-on-demand state. Verified against the same real-Lucene ground truth as the lazy path (`crates/lucene-codecs/tests/blocktree_fixtures.rs`'s `big_field_impacts_match_real_lucene_impacts_enum`/`l1_field_impacts_match_real_lucene_impacts_enum`, extended to assert `PostingsCursor`'s new accessors too, not just cross-check against `LazyDocsCursor`). **Still deferred**: no `ImpactsSource`/full `ImpactsEnum` trait hierarchy (`numLevels()`, `getDocIdUpTo()`) is implemented for either cursor, only the two concrete accessors this port actually needs. **Query-execution-side consumer of these impacts (this task)**: `lucene-search/src/similarity.rs::max_score_for_impacts` computes the true upper-bound BM25 score obtainable from any one `(freq, norm)` pair in a block's/span's competitive impacts list (max over entries of `idf * tf_norm`, not just the list's last entry -- freq and decoded field length move the score in opposite directions, so the true max can be an interior entry; see that function's doc comment and its `max_score_for_impacts_takes_the_true_max_not_just_the_last_entry` test). This is deliberately scoped to **the bound computation itself plus a test-only demonstration harness** (`similarity.rs`'s `assert_block_pruning_matches_brute_force`, exercised by `block_pruning_via_max_score_matches_brute_force_top_1`/`_top_2_spans_both_blocks`) that proves, for a synthetic `Postings` list, that skipping a whole level-0 block once its bound can't beat a `TopDocsCollector`'s current worst kept score never changes the top-`n` result -- **not** wired into the production `term_doc_scores`/`search_term_query_scored` path in `lib.rs`. That path calls `DocInput::read_postings` (the eager, whole-term-materializing decode), so every block's docs/freqs are already fully decoded before scoring even starts; real pruning there would additionally need switching that loop onto `LazyDocsCursor`'s decode-on-demand blocks so a skip actually avoids `ForUtil`/`PForUtil` work, not just a re-score. **Full multi-clause WAND/MAXSCORE dynamic pruning across a `BooleanQuery`'s clauses (maintaining a running minimum-competitive-score threshold across clauses) remains substantial, wholly unimplemented future work**, matching PLAN.md's Phase 3 notes -- that earlier task only reached the single-clause, single-block bound-and-prove-safety increment. **`max_score_for_impacts` is now wired into a real, narrow single-clause query-execution path** (a later task): `lucene-search/src/lib.rs::search_term_query_scored_maxscore` is a `TopDocsCollector`-only sibling of `search_term_query_scored` that streams a `TermQuery`'s postings through `LazyDocsCursor` instead of `DocInput::read_postings`'s eager, whole-term materialization, and, once `TopDocsCollector::min_competitive_score()` (new method) reports the collector is holding a full top-`n`, skips a whole level-0 block outright (`advance()`-ing straight past it, never running `ForUtil`/`PForUtil` decode on it) whenever `max_score_for_impacts`'s bound for that block can't beat the threshold -- real MAXSCORE-shaped dynamic pruning at query-execution time, not just the bound proven in isolation. Falls back to calling `search_term_query_scored` verbatim (never a silently different codepath) whenever the fast path isn't available: no `.doc` file opened, `docFreq <= 1` (no `.doc` bytes at all for a singleton, so nothing to stream lazily), or `IndexOptions::None` (the only index option `LazyDocsCursor` doesn't support, now that `DocsAndCustomFreqs` is accepted, see the postings-codec `DocsAndCustomFreqs` support note above). Differential-tested against the checked-in real-Lucene `big`/"everywhere" fixture (`docFreq == 300`, real Java-written impacts, see above) with real per-doc norms opened (`crates/lucene-search/src/lib.rs::tests::maxscore_lazy_path_matches_eager_path_on_real_fixture_and_actually_skips_blocks`) -- deliberately not `norms: None`, since the impacts' bound is only a valid upper bound against the score formula that consumes those same real norm bytes, and comparing it against the unrelated `UNNORMED_FIELD_LENGTH` fallback would be an unproven mix rather than a documented approximation. Asserts byte-for-byte-identical `TopDocsCollector::top_docs()` between the eager and maxscore paths across several `top_n` values, plus a test-only skip counter (`test_only_maxscore_block_skip_counter`, compiled only under `cfg(test)`, incremented at the real skip call site) proving real block skips happened for small `top_n` and proving zero skips happened when `top_n` equals the full `docFreq` (nothing safely skippable there) -- ruling out both a silent correctness change and a vacuously-passing "skip branch never taken" test. **Deliberately not attempted**: multi-clause `BooleanQuery` WAND (unchanged, see above) and any collector besides `TopDocsCollector` (no min-competitive-score threshold exists for a plain `Collector`/other `ScoringCollector` impl, so there is nothing to prune against for those callers). **`for_util.rs` now has real, production (not test-only) encode-side primitives**: `for_util::for_encode` (`ForUtil.encode`, bit-pack 256 already-fit values at a caller-chosen width) and `for_util::pfor_encode` (`PForUtil.encode`, the full histogram-based bit-width search that picks the smallest width keeping at most `MAX_EXCEPTIONS` (7) patched outliers, plus the all-equal vint fast path) -- both are direct ports of the real Java encoders, independently round-tripped in `for_util.rs`'s own tests (exactly-256-entries no-exceptions, all-zero, full-31-bit, few-outliers-with-patched-exceptions, and a direct `pfor_encode`-then-`for_decode` cross-check). **Not yet wired into `postings_writer.rs`**: the writer's `write_single_field`/`write_fields` still reject any term with `docFreq >= BLOCK_SIZE` or `total_term_freq >= BLOCK_SIZE` (`Error::DocFreqTooLarge`/`Error::TotalTermFreqTooLarge`, see that module's own doc comment) -- calling `for_encode`/`pfor_encode` from the writer to actually emit full 256-entry blocks (matching what `postings.rs`'s reader already fully decodes, see above) additionally needs the writer to build the level-0 skip-list metadata (`level0NumBytes`/`blockLength`/impacts bytes) the reader expects to find alongside each full block, which the writer does not build today. That remaining wiring is out of scope for this slice and tracked here rather than silently left unimplemented. |
| `util/fst/FST` (`FST.Arc`/`BytesReader`/`readArc`/`findTargetArc`/`readMetadata` -- on-heap arc-lookup read side) | `lucene-codecs/src/fst.rs` | **ported, scoped to lookup-only.** Lives in `lucene-codecs`, not `lucene-util` as PLAN.md ┬¦1's crate table originally sketched -- FST metadata parsing needs `CodecUtil.checkHeader` (`lucene-store::codec_util`), and per the `architecture` skill's strict downward dependency graph (`util ŌåÉ store ŌåÉ codecs`), `lucene-util` cannot depend on `lucene-store`, so a module needing both belongs in `lucene-codecs`. Ported: `Fst::read` (metadata + on-heap body, `OnHeapFSTStore`'s single-`Vec<u8>` case, copying the body into a freshly-allocated `Vec<u8>`) and `Fst::read_borrowed` (identical metadata parsing, but the body is a zero-copy `&'a [u8]` borrowed straight out of the caller's own buffer via `SliceInput::slice`/`seek`, no allocation for the body at all). **What "off-heap" honestly means here**: this port's `Directory` abstraction already has a real zero-copy backend, `lucene_store::directory::MmapDirectory` -- an actual OS `mmap(2)` via `memmap2`, returning `Input::Mapped` which `Deref`s to `&[u8]` without ever materializing an owned `Vec<u8>` copy of the file. `Fst::read_borrowed` is the missing FST-level plumbing that lets an `Fst<'a>` be constructed directly over such a buffer without `Fst::read`'s unconditional extra copy of the body -- for an `Fst` opened over an `MmapDirectory`-backed `Input`, that reproduces real Lucene's `OffHeapFSTStore` cost model: bytes stay in the OS page cache, faulted in lazily as arcs are actually visited, never doubled in the process heap. This module itself performs no `mmap(2)` call -- that already exists in `lucene-store` -- so the precise framing is "a borrowing/zero-copy FST constructor that composes with this port's existing mmap `Directory` backend," not "this file re-implements memory-mapping." `Fst::read` and `Fst::read_borrowed` are proven to agree on every lookup for the same bytes (`crates/lucene-codecs/src/fst.rs::tests::read_borrowed_matches_read_for_same_bytes`, `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/fst_fixtures.rs::read_borrowed_matches_read_on_real_fixture` against the real Lucene-written fixture), and an end-to-end test opens a real `MmapDirectory`-backed file this way (`read_borrowed_over_a_real_mmap_directory_input`). The reverse `BytesReader` cursor (`ReverseBytesReader`), and `Fst::get` (`Util.get(FST, BytesRef)`-equivalent: walk `findTargetArc` once per key byte, then check `arc.is_final()`). Single output type: `ByteSequenceOutputs` (`Vec<u8>` in Rust) -- the type real Lucene's term index FST actually uses to map term-prefix byte sequences to concatenated block-pointer bytes, confirmed by checking `ByteSequenceOutputs.java` directly rather than assumed. `Fst::read_label` decodes all three `INPUT_TYPE`s (`BYTE1`: raw byte; `BYTE2`: fixed 2-byte value, little-endian from `VERSION_LITTLE_ENDIAN` on and byte-swapped before that, matching `FST.readLabel`'s own version-gated branch; `BYTE4`: `vint`, not a fixed 4-byte value), and `find_target_arc`'s label-domain arithmetic (binary search / direct addressing / continuous dispatch) never assumed a byte-sized alphabet in the first place. `Fst::get`/`Fst::iter` (the `Vec<u8>`-keyed convenience API real Lucene's `BytesRefFSTEnum`/`Util.get(FST, BytesRef)` mirror) still reject non-`BYTE1` FSTs -- not an arbitrary restriction, but because a `u8` key element genuinely cannot represent a UTF-16 code unit (`BYTE2`) or a full Unicode code point (`BYTE4`). `Fst::get_labels`/`Fst::seek_exact_labels` (`Util.get(FST, IntsRef)`-equivalent) and `Fst::iter_labels`/`FstEnum::next_labels`/`seek_ceil_labels`/`seek_floor_labels`/`seek_exact_labels` (`IntsRefFSTEnum`-equivalent full walk/seek, `i32`-keyed) now widen lookup and enumeration to any `INPUT_TYPE`, reusing the exact same `find_target_arc`/`FstEnum` engine `BYTE1` callers already exercise -- `FstEnum`'s internal `labels`/`target` storage widened from `u8` to `i32` to stop truncating labels outside a byte's range; the existing byte-keyed public methods narrow back to `u8` only at their own boundary, which `Fst::iter`'s `BYTE1`-only guard makes lossless. **Verified against real Lucene-written `BYTE2`/`BYTE4` fixtures, not just hand-built ones**: `fixtures/src/GenFstWideInputTypes.java` builds two real on-heap FSTs via `FSTCompiler.Builder`'s public `INPUT_TYPE` parameter and `FSTCompiler.add(IntsRef, T)` (a genuinely wider-than-byte alphabet, unlike every other `GenFst*.java` generator here, which derives `IntsRef` labels from a `BytesRef`) -- one `BYTE2` FST with UTF-16-range labels (including combining-mark and CJK code points, up to `0xFFFF`) and one `BYTE4` FST with full-Unicode-range labels (including supplementary-plane code points up to `0x10FFFF`, well past `BYTE2`'s own ceiling). `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/fst_wide_input_types_fixtures.rs` opens both through this port's unmodified `Fst::read` and confirms `get_labels`/`seek_exact_labels` resolve every present key and reject absent ones, `iter_labels` enumerates every key in ascending order, `seek_ceil_labels`/`seek_floor_labels`/`seek_exact_labels` agree with the full enumeration, and the byte-keyed `get`/`iter` reject both fixtures outright. Hand-built unit tests in `fst.rs::tests` (`read_label_decodes_byte2_little_endian`, `read_label_decodes_byte2_legacy_big_endian`, `read_label_decodes_byte4_as_vint`) additionally pin down `read_label`'s exact byte-level encoding for each `INPUT_TYPE`/version combination in isolation, including the pre-`VERSION_LITTLE_ENDIAN` byte-swapped `BYTE2` case no real fixture from this Lucene version can exercise (current-version `FSTCompiler` only ever writes `VERSION_CURRENT`). **What's still not ported**: real Lucene's genuinely wider-alphabet `FSTCompiler`/`build_fst` construction for `BYTE2`/`BYTE4` (this port's own `build_fst`/`TrieNode` remain hardcoded to single-byte labels, so only the *read* side is widened) -- see `IntsRefFstEnum`'s own doc comment (below) for why building a genuinely wide-alphabet `Fst` from scratch here remains deferred. **FST construction (`build_fst`/`write_fst`, same file) is now ported, scoped to a simplified builder, not real `FSTCompiler`.** Real Lucene's `FSTCompiler` is an *incremental*, memory-bounded builder (a stack of `UnCompiledNode`s, a node hash table for suffix sharing/minimization, output pushing down shared prefixes) -- reproducing that algorithm exactly remains deferred, much larger future work. What's ported instead: `build_fst(&[(Vec<u8>, Vec<u8>)])` takes the *entire* sorted key/output sequence in memory, builds an ordinary trie, and serializes it bottom-up directly into the same list-encoded (variable-length arc) node/arc byte format `Fst::read`/`find_target_arc`/`read_arc` (above, unmodified) already parse -- explicit `vlong` targets everywhere (no `BIT_TARGET_NEXT` physical-adjacency compaction), each key's whole output placed on the single arc leading to its accepting node (no output-pushing down shared prefixes). **Suffix sharing / minimization is implemented**, though: `build_node` maintains a `NodeHash` (`HashMap<Vec<ArcSignature>, i64>`) keyed on each node's fully-resolved arc signature (labels, finality/final-outputs, child target addresses) and, before writing any node's bytes, checks whether a structurally-identical node has already been frozen elsewhere in the tree -- if so, its existing address is reused instead of writing a duplicate copy. This achieves the same *result* as real `FSTCompiler`'s incremental `NodeHash`-based freeze-and-dedup (two keys sharing a suffix, e.g. `"cat"`/`"bat"` sharing `"at"`, collapse to one shared node reachable from both `'c'` and `'b'`), just discovered by hash-consing the whole in-memory trie at once rather than incrementally as keys stream in -- the incremental/memory-bounded construction itself remains the deferred part, not the dedup algorithm. Proven with three tests in `fst.rs::tests`: `build_fst_shares_identical_suffix_node_across_two_prefixes` (`"bat"`/`"cat"`, asserting the node reached after `'b'` and after `'c'` are the literal same address), `build_fst_shares_classic_mop_pop_stop_top_suffix_node` (real Lucene's own canonical `FSTCompiler` suffix-sharing example -- `mop`/`moth`/`pop`/`star`/`stop`/`top` -- asserting the nodes after `"po"`/`"sto"`/`"to"` are all the same shared address while the node after `"mo"` is correctly distinct, plus full get/seek/enumerate regression over that now-shared-node FST), and `build_fst_dedup_keeps_compiled_size_sublinear_in_repeated_suffix_count` (8 distinct 2-byte prefixes sharing one 44-byte tail; asserts the compiled size is far below the naive no-sharing linear lower bound and that every prefix's node address is identical). `write_fst(&Fst)` serializes a built `Fst` back through the exact codec-header + `FSTMetadata.save` layout `Fst::read` parses, for a full round trip through the unmodified reader rather than only the in-memory `Fst` struct. **Verified against real Lucene, not just self-round-trip.** In addition to the self-round-trip unit tests in `crates/lucene-codecs/src/fst.rs::tests` (7-key set matching `fixtures/src/GenFst.java`'s shape, a single key, an empty key set, a key set including the empty-string key, a proper-prefix-of-another-key case, a 200-key set forcing multi-byte `vlong` targets, and unsorted/duplicate-key input rejection -- every case opens via the real unmodified `Fst::read` and confirms every present key resolves correctly and every absent key is rejected via `Fst::get`), the reverse direction is now covered too: `crates/lucene-codecs/examples/write_fst_fixture.rs` builds the same 7-key set via `build_fst`/`write_fst` and writes it to disk, and `fixtures/src/VerifyFst.java` opens that file through real Lucene's `FST.read(Path, ByteSequenceOutputs)` and looks up every key (7 present, 8 absent) via real `Util.get(FST, BytesRef)`. A second, larger fixture (`large/`, 200 keys) is also written and verified, forcing the same multi-byte-`vlong`-node-address-target encoding `build_fst_many_keys_forces_multi_byte_vlong_targets` stress-tests via self-round-trip -- previously never checked against a real Lucene reader, since the small 7-key set is too small to reach that path. Both ran and passed: `VerifyFst OK (<dir>): 7 present keys resolved, 8 absent keys rejected` and `VerifyFst OK (large): 200 present keys resolved, 3 absent keys rejected` -- concrete proof that `build_fst`'s simplified, non-minimizing, non-suffix-sharing construction is still a wire-format-valid FST that unmodified Lucene application code accepts (at both small and larger scale, with and without multi-byte node-address targets), not just bytes this port's own reader happens to tolerate. **Fixed-length-arc node decoding: `ARCS_FOR_BINARY_SEARCH` is now supported on read.** `Fst::find_target_arc` ports `FST.java`'s `ARCS_FOR_BINARY_SEARCH` branch verbatim: node header (`numArcs`/`bytesPerArc` vints), then a sparse binary search over fixed-size arc slots addressed as `posArcsStart - bytesPerArc * idx`; `read_arc`'s `BIT_TARGET_NEXT` branch also knows this encoding's "skip to before the arcs array" target rule (`Arc` grew `bytes_per_arc`/`num_arcs`/`pos_arcs_start` fields, defaulting to the list-node case). **Verified against a real Lucene-written fixture, not just a hand-built one**: `fixtures/src/GenFstBinarySearch.java` builds an `FST<BytesRef>` with `allowFixedLengthArcs(true)` and seven single-byte root labels spread widely enough (1, 40, 80, 120, 160, 200, 240) that real `FSTCompiler`'s own cost heuristic (`shouldExpandNodeWithDirectAddressing`) picks binary search over direct addressing for the root node -- the generator self-checks this by reading the root arc back and asserting `arc.toString()` contains `"(bs)"` before ever writing the fixture, so a future Lucene version quietly changing that heuristic and picking a different encoding would fail fixture generation loudly rather than silently testing the wrong thing. `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/fst_binary_search_fixtures.rs` opens that fixture through this port's unmodified `Fst::read`/`Fst::read_borrowed` and confirms all 7 present keys resolve and 8 absent keys (labels strictly between/outside the chosen ones) are rejected. Hand-built node tests (`fst.rs::tests::binary_search_node_finds_every_label`/`binary_search_node_rejects_absent_labels`) additionally pin down the byte-level field layout in isolation. **`ARCS_FOR_DIRECT_ADDRESSING` is now also supported on read.** `Fst::find_target_arc_direct_addressing` ports `FST.java`'s `ARCS_FOR_DIRECT_ADDRESSING` branch of `findTargetArc` verbatim: node header (label-range `numArcs`/`bytesPerArc` vints), a presence bit-table (`getNumPresenceBytes(labelRange)` bytes, one bit per label in the range, skipped rather than eagerly read -- matching `FST.readPresenceBytes`'s own "don't read them here" comment), then `firstLabel`, then a direct `labelToMatch - firstLabel` index into the range, rejected outright if out of bounds or (if in bounds) not actually present in the bit-table. `Arc` grew `node_flags`/`bit_table_start`/`first_label`/`presence_index` fields; `read_arc`'s label decode (implicit `first_label + arc_idx`, no on-disk label byte at all) and `BIT_TARGET_NEXT` target-skip arithmetic (skip past only the *present* arcs, i.e. the bit-table's set-bit count, not the full label range) both now dispatch on `node_flags` since two encodings share a non-zero `bytes_per_arc`. Four free functions (`bit_table_is_bit_set`/`bit_table_count_bits`/`bit_table_count_bits_up_to`/`bit_table_next_bit_set`) port `BitTableUtil`'s corresponding methods, byte-at-a-time rather than `BitTableUtil`'s own 8-bytes-at-a-time `readLong` fast path (a deliberate simplification, not a correctness gap -- see the `rust-performance` skill on not transliterating Java's perf tricks where a simpler equivalent suffices); `BitTableUtil.previousBitSet`/`FST.readLastArcByDirectAddressing` are now also ported (`bit_table_previous_bit_set`/`read_last_arc_by_direct_addressing`), needed once seek support (below) required "last arc of this node" access for `seek_floor`'s backtracking. **Verified against a real Lucene-written fixture, not just a hand-built one**: `fixtures/src/GenFstDirectAddressing.java` builds an `FST<BytesRef>` with `allowFixedLengthArcs(true)` and seven single-byte root labels chosen dense but not fully contiguous (`a`-`f` plus `h`, skipping `g`) so real `FSTCompiler`'s cost heuristic picks direct addressing over both binary search (too sparse a benefit) and `ARCS_FOR_CONTINUOUS` (which `FSTCompiler` always prefers instead once a label range has zero gaps) -- the generator self-checks this via `arc.toString()` containing `"(da)"` before ever writing the fixture. `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/fst_direct_addressing_fixtures.rs` opens that fixture through this port's unmodified `Fst::read`/`Fst::read_borrowed`/`Fst::iter` and confirms all 7 present keys resolve, 6 absent keys (including `g`, the one gap *inside* the range, specifically exercising the bit-table rejection path rather than just the range-bounds check) are rejected, and enumeration visits every present key in ascending order skipping the gap. Hand-built node tests (`fst.rs::tests::direct_addressing_node_finds_every_present_label`/`direct_addressing_node_rejects_absent_labels_in_and_around_range`/`direct_addressing_node_enumerates_every_present_label_in_ascending_order`) additionally pin down the byte-level field layout (presence bit-table, `first_label`, no per-arc label byte) in isolation. **`ARCS_FOR_CONTINUOUS` is now also supported on read.** `Fst::find_target_arc_continuous` ports `FST.java`'s `ARCS_FOR_CONTINUOUS` branch of `findTargetArc` verbatim: node header (`numArcs`/`bytesPerArc` vints), then `firstLabel` (no presence bit-table at all, unlike `ARCS_FOR_DIRECT_ADDRESSING` -- every label in `[firstLabel, firstLabel + numArcs)` is guaranteed present by construction), then a direct `labelToMatch - firstLabel` index into the range, rejected outright only if out of bounds, otherwise decoded via the same `read_next_real_arc` fixed-size-slot arithmetic `ARCS_FOR_BINARY_SEARCH` already established (`posArcsStart - bytesPerArc * arcIdx`, since both encodings share that addressing once a node header is parsed). `read_arc`'s label decode (implicit `first_label + arc_idx`, shared with `ARCS_FOR_DIRECT_ADDRESSING`) and `BIT_TARGET_NEXT` target-skip arithmetic (uses the full label range, `arc.num_arcs`, same as `ARCS_FOR_BINARY_SEARCH` -- there's no presence count to look up) both dispatch on `node_flags` accordingly. **Verified against a real Lucene-written fixture, not just a hand-built one**: `fixtures/src/GenFstContinuous.java` builds an `FST<BytesRef>` with `allowFixedLengthArcs(true)` and seven single-byte root labels that are fully contiguous (`a`-`g`, no gaps) -- once a label range has zero gaps, real `FSTCompiler`'s cost heuristic always prefers `ARCS_FOR_CONTINUOUS` over both direct addressing and binary search, since no presence bitset is needed at all -- the generator self-checks this via `arc.toString()` containing `"(cs)"` before ever writing the fixture. `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/fst_continuous_fixtures.rs` opens that fixture through this port's unmodified `Fst::read`/`Fst::read_borrowed`/`Fst::iter` and confirms all 7 present keys resolve, 6 absent keys (all strictly outside the label range, since `ARCS_FOR_CONTINUOUS` has no in-range gap to test) are rejected, and enumeration visits every key in ascending order. Hand-built node tests (`fst.rs::tests::continuous_node_finds_every_present_label`/`continuous_node_rejects_labels_outside_the_range`/`continuous_node_enumerates_every_label_in_ascending_order`) additionally pin down the byte-level field layout (no presence bit-table, no per-arc label byte, `first_label` plus direct indexing) in isolation. With this, all three of `FST.java`'s fixed-length-arc node encodings (`ARCS_FOR_BINARY_SEARCH`, `ARCS_FOR_DIRECT_ADDRESSING`, `ARCS_FOR_CONTINUOUS`) are now supported on read -- nothing in the fixed-length-arc node family remains `Error::Unsupported`. Real `FSTCompiler`'s incremental/memory-bounded construction and output-pushing down shared prefixes remain deferred (suffix sharing/minimization itself is now done, see above); and `IntsRefFSTEnum` (`IntsRef`-input enumeration) is also now ported, as `IntsRefFstEnum` -- but honestly scoped as a byte-keyed `BYTE1` `Fst` wearing an `IntsRef`-shaped API (each `i32` key element big-endian-encoded to 4 bytes at the API boundary via `encode_ints_key`/`decode_ints_key`, non-negative elements only), not real Lucene's genuinely wider-alphabet `IntsRefFSTEnum` over a `BYTE4`-keyed FST -- that would require a second, wider-label node/arc codec (`TrieNode`/`read_label`/`find_target_arc`'s direct-addressing and continuous arithmetic all hardcode single-byte labels today), out of scope here. `IntsRefFstEnum` wraps the existing `FstEnum` by composition (`build_fst_from_ints::<O>` delegates to `build_fst_typed`; `next`/`seek_ceil`/`seek_floor`/`seek_exact` are thin encode/decode wrappers around `FstEnum`'s own), so none of the traversal algorithm is duplicated. Tested in `fst.rs::tests` (`encode_decode_ints_key_round_trips`, `encode_ints_key_big_endian_preserves_numeric_order`, `ints_ref_fst_enum_over_empty_fst_yields_nothing`, `ints_ref_fst_enum_over_single_key_fst_yields_that_one_key`, `ints_ref_fst_enum_multi_key_shared_prefix_and_suffix_ascending_order`, `ints_ref_fst_enum_seek_ceil_floor_exact`, `encode_ints_key_rejects_a_negative_element_even_in_release_builds` -- the non-negative restriction is a real `assert!`, not `debug_assert!`, so it is not compiled out under `--release`). **Not yet consumed by any real caller**: `IntsRefFstEnum`/`build_fst_from_ints`/`encode_ints_key`/`decode_ints_key` have no production call site anywhere else in this workspace today, only their own unit tests -- this is new API surface, not wired into a synonym/suggest feature yet. **FST off-heap seek path validation (this task)**: investigated whether `seek_ceil`/`seek_floor`/`seek_exact` (`FstEnum`) and `Fst::iter` enumeration had ever been exercised over a `Fst` opened via `read_borrowed` (off-heap/zero-copy), as opposed to only `Fst::read` (owned).
