Found a real testing gap, not an implementation bug: `tests/fst_seek_fixtures.rs` and `fst.rs`'s own seek unit tests (`fst_seek_exact_on_present_and_absent_keys`, `fst_enum_seek_ceil_*`, `fst_enum_seek_floor_*`, etc.) exhaustively cover every node encoding and backtracking scenario, but every single one builds its `Fst` via `Fst::read`; conversely every existing `read_borrowed` test (`read_borrowed_matches_read_for_same_bytes`, `read_borrowed_over_a_real_mmap_directory_input`, `read_borrowed_body_is_a_slice_not_a_second_owned_buffer`) only ever called `get`/`get_typed`, never seek or `iter`. Added `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/fst_borrowed_seek_fixtures.rs`, which loads every existing fixture directory (list, binary search, direct addressing, continuous, non-root-array-node, and all three floor-backtrack fixtures) via both `Fst::read` and `Fst::read_borrowed` and asserts `seek_ceil`/`seek_floor`/`seek_exact`/`iter` produce byte-identical results from both, plus one test that opens a borrowed `Fst` over a real `MmapDirectory`-backed file and drives the full seek/enumeration surface (including a backtracking `seek_floor` call) against the mmap-backed slice. All new tests passed on the first run with no code changes needed to `fst.rs` itself: the borrowed path's node/arc reads all go through `SliceInput::slice(from, to)` (arbitrary positional access into the borrowed `&'a [u8]`), so backtracking to a previous arc or ascending to a parent node works identically to the owned path -- there was never a forward-only-access assumption to trip over.

**`PositiveIntOutputs`/`PairOutputs` are now ported, layered on top of the single `Vec<u8>` wire output type rather than threaded through `Fst`/`build_fst`/`build_node` as a generic parameter.** Since this builder never does real output-pushing (confirmed above -- each key's whole output already lives on one arc), combining two arcs' outputs when nodes are merged/shared never has to reconcile a partially-pushed prefix from one path with a different one from another: `build_node`'s existing `NodeHash` dedup already keys on each node's exact (encoded) final-output bytes, so structurally-identical subtrees with equal typed values still share correctly and subtrees with differing typed values never incorrectly merge. A new `Outputs` trait (`crates/lucene-codecs/src/fst.rs`) describes an `encode`/`decode`/`zero` codec to/from that `Vec<u8>`; `PositiveIntOutputs` (`i64`, `NO_OUTPUT = 0` encoding to zero bytes, matching real Lucene's sentinel), `ByteSequenceOutputs` (identity codec, the same type `Fst`/`build_fst` already use directly), and `PairOutputs<A, B>` (`Pair<A::Value, B::Value>`, length-prefixing the first component's encoded bytes so both components decode unambiguously; an all-zero pair encodes to zero bytes too) are implemented against it, plus `build_fst_typed::<O>`/`Fst::get_typed::<O>` thin wrappers around `build_fst`/`Fst::get`. Deliberately not ported: real Lucene's `Outputs.add`/`common`/`subtract` operations, since those exist solely to support output-pushing (finding/removing a shared output prefix to hoist onto a shared arc) and this builder has no output-pushing to support. Tested in `fst.rs::tests`: `positive_int_outputs_round_trips_values_including_zero`, `pair_outputs_round_trips_both_components_over_a_shared_prefix_key_set` (a mixed prefix/suffix-sharing key set, both components read back correctly per key), `pair_outputs_shared_suffix_nodes_keep_distinct_first_components` (the highest-risk case: `"bat"`/`"cat"` would share their tail node under plain byte outputs, but distinct per-key `Pair` values on that arc must -- and do -- prevent the node-hash dedup from merging them), and `pair_outputs_zero_value_encodes_to_no_extra_bytes`. **Ported**: `readFirstTargetArc`/`readFirstRealTargetArc`/`readNextRealArc`/`readNextArc` (`FST.java`'s enumeration primitives -- previously written, found to be dead code under the earlier `get`-only scope, and removed; reinstated once `iter`/`FstEnum` below needed them) plus `FstEnum` (`Fst::iter`, a port of `BytesRefFSTEnum`'s `next()`/`doNext`/`pushFirst`): full ascending-order enumeration of every `(key, output)` pair an FST accepts, over list-encoded and all three fixed-length-arc node encodings alike (mirroring `find_target_arc`'s own encoding support). **Seek support (`seekCeil`/`seekFloor`/`seekExact`) is now also ported**, over all four node encodings alike: `Fst::seek_exact` (a thin wrapper delegating to the already arc-by-arc-descending `Fst::get`, matching real `BytesRefFSTEnum.seekExact`'s own short-circuit-on-first-byte-mismatch semantics) plus `FstEnum::seek_ceil`/`seek_floor`/`seek_exact` (`FSTEnum.doSeekCeil`/`doSeekFloor`/`doSeekExact` ported field-for-field, including `rewindPrefix`'s shared-prefix reuse across successive seeks on the same enum, and the backtracking-with-output-accumulation logic for "target falls strictly between two sibling arcs"/"past the last arc of this node" cases -- `rollback_to_last_fork_then_push`/`backtrack_to_floor_arc`/`push_last`, the `seek_floor`-only mirror of the existing `push_first`). Verified both by hand-built-FST unit tests (`fst.rs::tests::fst_enum_seek_*`, including sequential forward-then-backward seeks on one enum and degenerate empty-FST/empty-key-set cases) and by a new differential test file, `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/fst_seek_fixtures.rs`, exercising all four real Lucene-written fixtures above (list, binary search, direct addressing, continuous) for exact hits, a ceil/floor landing strictly between two keys, before-the-first-key, and past-the-last-key cases, plus a fifth fixture, `fixtures/data/fst_seek_non_root_array_node/` (`fixtures/src/GenFstSeekNonRootArrayNode.java`), whose root stays list-encoded while each of the three fixed-length-arc encodings sits one level below it -- specifically exercising the backtrack-past-a-non-root-array-node code paths (`read_last_target_arc`'s array branch, `find_next_floor_arc_binary_search`/`_direct_addressing`/`_continuous`) that the four root-only fixtures above never reach. Fixture-verified against a real `FST<BytesRef>` built via real `FSTCompiler` (`allowFixedLengthArcs(false)`, so the fixture itself never emits the array-node encodings this slice doesn't support) with 7 keys sharing prefixes/suffixes (`app`/`apple`/`application`, `banana`/`band`/`bandana`, `z`) plus 8 deliberately-absent lookups (proper prefixes, over-extensions, a disjoint key) -- see `fixtures/src/GenFst.java` and `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/fst_fixtures.rs`, whose `iter_enumerates_all_keys_in_ascending_order` also confirms `Fst::iter` walks that same fixture in exactly its known sorted order. `find_target_arc`'s `ARCS_FOR_BINARY_SEARCH` decode path is likewise fixture-verified against a real binary-search-encoded root node (`fixtures/src/GenFstBinarySearch.java`, `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/fst_binary_search_fixtures.rs`), and that same fixture's `iter_enumerates_every_key_of_a_binary_search_root_node` proves `Fst::iter` enumerates a genuine fixed-length-arc node correctly, not just the hand-built one in `fst.rs`'s own unit tests. The same is now true for direct addressing: `find_target_arc_direct_addressing` is fixture-verified against a real direct-addressing-encoded root node (`fixtures/src/GenFstDirectAddressing.java`, `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/fst_direct_addressing_fixtures.rs`), and that fixture's `iter_enumerates_every_key_of_a_direct_addressing_root_node` proves `Fst::iter` enumerates a genuine direct-addressing node correctly, including skipping its one deliberate gap. A further fixture, `fixtures/data/fst_deep_trie/` (`fixtures/src/GenFstDeepTrie.java`, `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/fst_deep_trie_fixtures.rs`), closes the "shallow FST only" gap in the seek coverage above: its 9 keys (`abcaa`/`abcab`/`abcz`/`abda`/`abdz`/`acaa`/`aczz`/`baaa`/`bzzz`) share prefixes deeply enough that the path to `"abcaa"` crosses 5 distinct list-encoded trie levels, confirmed by the generator's own manual `readFirstTargetArc`/`readNextArc` walk before the fixture is written (mirroring the existing `"(bs)"`/`"(da)"`/`"(cs)"` self-checks) rather than assumed from "long strings." Every prior seek fixture's interesting structure sits at or one level below the root; this one forces `seekCeil`/`seekFloor`/`seekExact` to actually backtrack across 2-4 levels to resolve absent targets correctly (e.g. `"abcaz"` must fail past `"abca"`'s node and climb back up to the `"abc"` node to find `"abcz"`). Ground truth for all 17 seek targets comes from real Lucene's own `BytesRefFSTEnum.seekCeil`/`seekFloor`/`seekExact` against the reloaded FST, not hand-derived, matching this directory's established standard. |
| `codecs/lucene103/blocktree/Lucene103BlockTreeTermsReader`/`Writer`, `FieldReader`, `SegmentTermsEnum`/`Frame`, `TrieReader`/`TrieBuilder` (`.tim`/`.tip`/`.tmd` term dictionary + term index) | `lucene-codecs/src/blocktree.rs` | **ported, scoped to `seekExact` + `docFreq`/`totalTermFreq`, now covering multi-block fields (multi-child `.tip` tries and floor-split `.tim` blocks), not just single-block ones.** Correction to the row this replaces: the pinned Lucene version (10.5.0, `Lucene104PostingsFormat`) uses `Lucene103BlockTreeTermsReader`/`Writer` (package `lucene103.blocktree`), *not* `Lucene90BlockTreeTermsReader` -- that class lives in `backward-codecs` and is out of scope. This version's `.tip` term index is **not an FST** -- Lucene 10.x replaced it with a purpose-built binary trie (`TrieReader`/`TrieBuilder`); `fst.rs` (scoped to the older format) is not used here. Ported: opening a `.tim`/`.tip`/`.tmd` triple (header/footer/checksum framing, the embedded `Lucene104PostingsWriterTerms` sub-header + `BLOCK_SIZE` check, per-field `numTerms`/`sumTotalTermFreq`/`sumDocFreq`/`docCount`/`minTerm`/`maxTerm`), and now a **full trie decode** (all three node shapes -- `SIGN_NO_CHILDREN`, `SIGN_SINGLE_CHILD_WITH_OUTPUT`/`WITHOUT_OUTPUT`, `SIGN_MULTI_CHILDREN` with all three `ChildSaveStrategy` label encodings -- `BITS`/`ARRAY`/`REVERSE_ARRAY`) plus floor-block resolution (`LEAF_NODE_HAS_FLOOR`/`NON_LEAF_NODE_HAS_FLOOR`, the `numFollowFloorBlocks`/`(label, code)` byte layout). **Design**: rather than walking one root-to-leaf trie path per lookup (what real `SegmentTermsEnum.seekExact` does), `open()` recursively visits every reachable trie node, resolves every floor sub-block, decodes every resulting `.tim` block (re-attaching each block's own trie-path prefix, since a block only stores its suffix bytes), and merges everything into one sorted `Vec` -- the same shape the prior single-block slice used, just now fed by a full traversal instead of one root-node read. This eagerly decodes blocks a real `seekExact` for one term would never touch (acceptable for now: no enumeration/streaming consumer exists yet to notice, and correctness came first) -- see the module doc for the full tradeoff writeup. **Real bug this slice's fixture caught**: an interior trie node can have its own output block flagged `hasTerms=false` (a "pass-through" block that itself holds nothing but pointers to its own further-split children, produced by `Lucene103BlockTreeTermsWriter.writeBlocks` recursing to a deeper prefix instead of floor-splitting) -- the first implementation treated this as an unsupported non-leaf block and errored; the fix is to just skip that one physical block, since `PendingBlock.compileIndex` unconditionally merges every deeper recursion's own trie into the same trie this code already walks, so every term routed through the pointer-only block is independently reachable as a deeper node anyway. Caught by the new "many" field in `fixtures/src/GenBlockTree.java` (400 distinct terms, forcing real `Lucene103BlockTreeTermsWriter` past the default 25/48 min/maxItemsInBlock thresholds into both a multi-child trie and at least one floor split) -- every other fixture field stayed single-block and would never have hit this. **Still deferred**: automaton intersection (`IntersectTermsEnum`) -- pointer-only (`hasTerms=false`) blocks are skipped rather than opened (see above), and non-leaf `.tim` blocks are no longer in this list; see the "Multi-level blocktree" paragraph below, which superseded this claim once that support landed. **Suffix compression (read-side) is now supported**: `decode_block` dispatches on `code_l & 0x03` (`CompressionAlgorithm.NO_COMPRESSION`/`LOWERCASE_ASCII`/`LZ4`), reusing this port's own `lz4.rs` decompressor for LZ4 (a real, general-purpose decompressor, not a stub) and a small standalone port of `LowercaseAsciiCompression.decompress` for the other mode (`blocktree.rs::decompress_lowercase_ascii`); code `3` (never assigned to a `CompressionAlgorithm` constant) is rejected as `Error::Store(Corrupted)`, matching `CompressionAlgorithm.byCode`'s own `IllegalArgumentException`. This is purely read-side interop with real Lucene-written segments -- this port's own blocktree *writer* still only ever emits `NO_COMPRESSION`. **Verification, stated precisely**: LZ4 is verified against an actual `Lucene103BlockTreeTermsWriter`-produced fixture (200 terms sharing a long, highly repetitive-suffix common prefix, past the default min/maxItemsInBlock thresholds so the real writer chose LZ4 for several blocks) -- `fixtures/data/blocktree_compressed_index/`, `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/blocktree_compressed_fixture.rs` (`lz4_compressed_terms_match_real_lucene`, `lz4_compressed_enumeration_matches_real_lucene_terms_enum_next`). `LOWERCASE_ASCII` could **not** be forced out of a real `IndexWriter` in reasonable effort (the writer only takes that branch once LZ4 already failed to save 25% *and* the block's average suffix length still clears its own `prefixLength > 2`/`length > 2*numEntries` gates -- every term shape tried here landed on `NO_COMPRESSION` instead), so it's instead verified against a byte vector produced by directly invoking real Lucene's own `LowercaseAsciiCompression.compress` from the pinned 10.5.0 jar (real Lucene *bytes*, just not embedded in an on-disk segment) -- see `decompress_lowercase_ascii_matches_real_lucene_compress_output`/`decode_block_lowercase_ascii_compressed_suffixes` in `blocktree.rs`. A hand-built (this port's own `lz4::compress`-round-tripped) vector additionally covers the LZ4 dispatch path directly (`decode_block_lz4_compressed_suffixes`). **Ordered enumeration (`TermsEnum.next()`) and nearest-match seeking (`seekCeil()`) are now ported** -- `FieldTerms::iter()` returns a `TermsEnum` cursor (`next()`/`seek_ceil()`/`current()`) over the field's already-sorted `entries` `Vec`. **Design choice**: this is a thin index-bump/binary-search cursor over the Vec the prior slice already materializes, not a reimplementation of real `SegmentTermsEnum`/`SegmentTermsEnumFrame`'s stack-based lazy block-walk -- the eager-whole-field-materialization tradeoff was made by the prior slice, and once every term is already in one sorted Vec, replicating Java's per-frame FST/trie-path push/pop machinery on top of it would only reintroduce complexity this port deliberately avoided (see the `rust-performance` skill). Fixture-verified against the `many` field (400 terms, multi-block/floor-split) via real `TermsEnum.next()` -- the full 400-term ordered sequence (term bytes + docFreq/totalTermFreq) matches exactly, proving enumeration walks block/floor boundaries in the right order and not just within one block -- and `seekCeil()` against four real-Lucene-verified cases (exact match, a between-terms ceiling match, before-the-first-term, and after-the-last-term/`END`); no decode bug surfaced this time, matching on the first real-Lucene run (see `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/blocktree_fixtures.rs`). Unit tests cover cursor edge cases no real fixture reaches: an empty field, a single-term field, `seekCeil()` followed by `next()` continuing from the landed-on position, and `next()` called repeatedly past the end staying idempotent. Per-term postings-metadata bytes are decoded by `crate::postings::decode_term_metadata` per block (threaded across each block's own entries, `absolute` true only for each block's first entry -- blocks never share metadata state) and threaded into `FieldTerms`, which exposes `FieldTerms::postings(term, doc_in)`/`positions(...)` alongside `seek_exact`'s stats. Fixture-verified against a real `IndexWriter` (`fixtures/src/GenBlockTree.java`): "body"/"id"/"big"/"pos" (unchanged from the prior slice, all single-block) plus the new "many" field above, sampled across its range (first/last, several mid values spanning different trie branches and floor sub-blocks) and checked exhaustively (all 400 terms independently looked up) against real `TermsEnum.seekExact`/`docFreq`/`totalTermFreq`; see `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/blocktree_fixtures.rs`. Unit tests cover the new trie-decode primitives directly (hand-built single-child-with-output+floor, all three multi-children strategies incl. a `REVERSE_ARRAY` gap case, an end-to-end two-floor-block `open()` round trip, and corruption paths -- invalid strategy code, child-delta-exceeds-parent-fp, trie-nesting-depth guard) that no small real fixture reaches. **Wildcard/prefix automaton-shaped intersection is now ported, scoped to glob matching over the already-materialized `Vec`, not real `IntersectTermsEnum`/`CompiledAutomaton`.** `FieldTerms::intersect(&WildcardPattern) -> impl Iterator<Item = (&[u8], TermStats)>` (`crates/lucene-codecs/src/blocktree.rs`) narrows `entries` to the sorted sub-range starting with the pattern's literal prefix (two `partition_point` binary searches -- free, since `entries` is already sorted for `seek_exact`; see the new `prefix_upper_bound` helper) and then linearly filters that range against `crate::wildcard::WildcardPattern` (`crates/lucene-codecs/src/wildcard.rs`, new module), a from-scratch glob matcher (`*` = zero-or-more bytes, `?` = exactly one Unicode codepoint (1-4 UTF-8 bytes, falling back to 1 byte on invalid UTF-8), everything else literal) plus a `WildcardPattern::prefix()` constructor for pure `PrefixQuery` semantics. **Design tradeoff, stated plainly**: this is *not* `CompiledAutomaton`/`ByteRunAutomaton` DFA compilation and *not* real `IntersectTermsEnum` trie-block-skipping -- real Lucene can visit only the `.tip`/`.tim` blocks a compiled automaton's reachable states could lead to, potentially sub-linear in dictionary size; this port's `intersect` is `O(n)` in the field's term count once the literal-prefix range is applied, degrading to a full field scan for a pattern with no literal prefix (e.g. `*foo`); the per-candidate `WildcardPattern::matches` cost itself is *not* `O(1)` -- it's a backtracking matcher that is multiplicative (`O(term.len()^k)`), not additive, in the number of `*` tokens `k` (see `wildcard.rs`'s own doc comment), so a pattern with several `*`s against long terms is a genuine unguarded pathological case, not just a theoretical one. This mirrors the same "correctness first, honest about what's actually optimized" stance the postings work took (see the `postings.rs` row's lazy-cursor slices) rather than transliterating Java's per-frame automaton-driven stack machine on top of a representation (one eagerly sorted `Vec`) that no longer matches it -- reusing the existing `entries` `Vec`/binary-search idiom `seek_exact`/`TermsEnum` already established, not a new automaton-shaped subsystem. **Also deliberately out of scope this slice**: no regex (`RegexpQuery`) and no fuzzy/Levenshtein automaton (`FuzzyQuery`) -- both need a real automaton/edit-distance representation that's a materially larger scope than glob matching over a sorted `Vec`; (task #34 added `\`-escape support for a literal `*`/`?`/`\` byte, matching real `WildcardQuery.toAutomaton`'s `WILDCARD_ESCAPE` handling exactly -- see the task #34 row below). Fixture-verified against real `WildcardQuery`/`CompiledAutomaton.getTermsEnum` ground truth (`fixtures/src/GenBlockTree.java::appendWildcardIntersectManifest`, extended "many" field, 400 terms) for four patterns: an exact prefix run (`term037*`), a `*`-suffix pattern equivalent to a `PrefixQuery` (`term039*`), a `?` single-char wildcard (`term010?`), and a pattern matching zero terms (`zzz*`) -- `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/blocktree_fixtures.rs::many_field_wildcard_intersect_matches_real_lucene_wildcard_query`, matched on the first real-Lucene run. Unit tests (`wildcard.rs`) cover the matcher's own edge cases directly: empty pattern (matches only the empty term), pure `*` (matches everything including empty), literal-only pattern, `?` boundary cases (including on an empty term), `*` at the start/middle/end, adjacent `*`s collapsing to one, non-UTF-8 byte matching, and `literal_prefix()` extraction; `blocktree.rs` adds `intersect_prefix_and_wildcard_over_materialized_field` (prefix/`?`/mid-`*`/match-everything/match-nothing-in-range/match-nothing-out-of-range/exact-pattern/`WildcardPattern::prefix()` cases over a hand-built multi-term field) and `prefix_upper_bound_handles_ff_bytes_and_empty` (the `0xFF`-byte-run and empty-prefix corner cases the real fixture's ASCII terms never reach)  **Multi-level blocktree (`.tim` blocks that are themselves non-leaf) is now decoded, not just deferred.** Previously any block with `isLeafBlock == false` (some of its entries are in-block pointers to further-nested sub-blocks, rather than raw term suffixes -- real Lucene's mechanism for a prefix too wide to give every one of its sub-prefixes a separate `.tip` trie arc) was rejected with `Error::Unsupported`; every fixture this port had wasn't large/irregular enough to force real Lucene into writing one. `decode_block`/`decode_block_at_depth` now recurse into every sub-block entry (reattaching that entry's own key bytes as a prefix before merging its sub-entries in), confirmed against a new, dedicated fixture (`fixtures/src/GenBlockTreeMultilevel.java`, 8000 deterministic pseudo-random terms -- a sequential-numeric term set, even at 400+ terms, empirically never triggers a non-leaf block; real Lucene resolves that shape via floor blocks instead) that does reach one, checked structurally (not just "lookups still work") in `blocktree.rs::multilevel_fixture_reaches_a_genuine_non_leaf_block`. One real correctness bug surfaced and was fixed during this: a sub-block can be addressed **both** by its parent's in-block pointer **and** by its own independent `.tip` trie arc (real Lucene's `SegmentTermsEnum` only ever takes one path per lookup and never notices; this module's eager whole-field materialization visits every reachable block and was double-decoding such blocks until `open()` started passing `decode_block_at_depth` the full set of trie-collected top-level block fps, so a sub-block pointer whose target is already in that set is skipped rather than re-decoded). Differential test: `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/blocktree_multilevel_fixture.rs`. **All three `ChildSaveStrategy` label encodings (`BITS`/`ARRAY`/`REVERSE_ARRAY`) were already implemented and hand-built-unit-tested before this task (`multi_children_array_strategy`/`multi_children_bits_strategy`/`multi_children_reverse_array_strategy`/`multi_children_reverse_array_strategy_with_gap`) -- what was missing was a real-Lucene-fixture differential proof that each strategy is also chosen and decoded correctly against actual `TrieBuilder.ChildSaveStrategy.choose`-selected bytes, not just hand-assembled ones.** Auditing existing fixtures found `REVERSE_ARRAY` already forced for real: `blocktree_multilevel_index`'s "many" field (8000 random lowercase terms) makes the root trie node's children a fully dense `'a'..='z'` range, and `TrieBuilder.ChildSaveStrategy.choose`'s own cost formula (`needBytes`: `REVERSE_ARRAY` = 1, `ARRAY` = 25, `BITS` = 4) picks `REVERSE_ARRAY` -- `multilevel_fixture_reaches_a_genuine_non_leaf_block` now asserts `child_save_strategy == CHILD_STRATEGY_REVERSE_ARRAY` (previously unasserted, just implicitly exercised). `ARRAY` and `BITS`, however, were not forced anywhere: this task adds `fixtures/src/GenBlockTreeChildStrategies.java`, a new generator producing `fixtures/data/blocktree_child_strategies_index/`, whose two fields' leading-byte label sets were hand-picked so the same cost formula picks a distinct winner for each -- "arraystrat" (5 labels spanning printable-ASCII, distance 94: BITS=12, ARRAY=4, REVERSE_ARRAY=90 -> `ARRAY`) and "bitsstrat" (9 labels spaced 5 apart, distance 41: BITS=6, ARRAY=8, REVERSE_ARRAY=33 -> `BITS`) -- confirmed by decoding the real generated bytes before committing to this design (`root.child_save_strategy` matched the predicted code on the first real-Lucene run for both fields, no trial-and-error needed once the arithmetic was worked out from `TrieBuilder.java`'s own `needBytes` overrides). New differential test `child_strategies_fixture_forces_array_and_bits_strategies` (`blocktree.rs`) asserts each field's exact strategy code and `strategy_bytes`, then round-trips every term through the public `open`/`seek_exact` API against the manifest's ground-truth term list. No production code changes were needed -- this was purely closing a fixture-coverage gap for two already-correct code paths. | **Root-block-with-no-terms shape confirmed already handled, one incorrect rejection removed (this task).** `open()` previously errored with `Error::Unsupported("root block with no terms (all sub-blocks) ...")` whenever `collect_leaf_blocks`'s full trie traversal came back empty -- meant to guard the case where a field's root `.tip` trie node's own physical `.tim` block has `hasTerms == false` (holds nothing but sub-block pointers, e.g. because the field's very first terms already diverge enough on their leading byte that every top-level group hits `minItemsInBlock` before the root keeps any loose term of its own). Auditing `Lucene103BlockTreeTermsWriter.writeBlocks`/`PendingBlock.compileIndex` shows this guard's premise was wrong: the `.tip` trie always structurally mirrors the `.tim` block hierarchy, root included -- every sub-block pointer a block writes always gets a matching trie child merged in by `compileIndex`, regardless of nesting depth -- so `collect_leaf_blocks`'s existing unconditional recursion into a node's trie children (already relied on for the interior no-terms/pointer-only block case, see the paragraph above) already walks straight past a no-terms *root* into its real children with terms; `blocks` was never actually empty for this shape. The check is removed rather than specially handled; if `blocks` is ever empty for genuinely corrupt data, the existing `entries.len() as i64 != num_terms` check catches it with an accurate `Error::Store(Corrupted(...))` instead. Confirmed empirically, not just by source audit: `fixtures/src/GenBlockTreeChildStrategies.java`'s existing "arraystrat"/"bitsstrat" fields (5 and 9 leading-byte groups of 30 terms each) already force exactly this shape and were already passing through `open()` before this task -- the dead check simply never triggered on any fixture this port had. New test `open_field_with_no_terms_in_root_block_still_finds_every_term` (`blocktree.rs`) makes this explicit: asserts `root.has_terms == false` and `root.sign != SIGN_NO_CHILDREN` structurally for both fields (proving the shape, not assuming it), then round-trips every term through both `seek_exact` and full ordered `TermsEnum::next()` enumeration against the same existing fixture -- no new Java generator was needed.
| `codecs/lucene104/Lucene104PostingsWriter`, `codecs/lucene103/blocktree/Lucene103BlockTreeTermsWriter` (`.doc`/`.tim`/`.tip`/`.tmd` write side) | `lucene-codecs/src/postings_writer.rs::write_single_field` | **write path started, narrowly scoped to a single field, single `.tim` block, term-frequency-only postings.** Given one field's already-tokenized/inverted term dictionary (`FieldPostingsInput { field_number, index_options, doc_count, terms: &[TermPostings] }`, each `TermPostings` a term's bytes plus its `(doc_id, freq)` pairs sorted ascending by `doc_id`), produces `.doc`/`.tim`/`.tip`/`.tmd` bytes. **Exactly proven correct, no more**: (1) **single field per call** -- `numFields = 1` in `.tmd`; (2) **single `.tim` block, single trie node** -- every term must fit in one physical leaf block, and `.tip` is one root `SIGN_NO_CHILDREN` node with `hasTerms` set and no floor data (block-splitting, floor sub-blocks, and multi-level tries are not implemented -- a real writer would split once past `Lucene103BlockTreeTermsWriter`'s min/maxItemsInBlock thresholds, this one never does); (3) **`docFreq < BLOCK_SIZE` (256) for every term** -- only the group-varint "tail block" encoding is ever written (`Lucene104PostingsWriter`'s `flushDocBlock(true)` branch that never reaches `docBufferUpto == BLOCK_SIZE`); no full `ForUtil`/`PForUtil`-bit-packed blocks, no skip data, no impacts are ever produced, and a term at or above `BLOCK_SIZE` docs is rejected with `Error::DocFreqTooLarge` rather than silently producing wrong bytes; (4) **term frequency only, no positions/offsets/payloads** -- only `IndexOptions::Docs`/`DocsAndFreqs` are accepted (`Error::UnsupportedIndexOptions` otherwise), `.pos`/`.pay` are never written; (5) **`docFreq == 1` is pulsed into the term dictionary**, matching the real writer exactly -- no `.doc` bytes at all for a singleton term, `postings::singleton_postings` reads it back purely from the per-term metadata. The per-term postings-metadata bytes always take the bit-clear ("absolute-ish `docStartFP` delta") branch of `decodeTerm`'s encoding, never the zigzag-singleton-delta branch -- a correct but less compact simplification, since this writer has no need for that branch's extra savings. **Caller obligations, not re-validated beyond what's checked**: `terms` must already be sorted ascending by term bytes with no duplicates (checked, `Error::TermsNotSorted`), each term's `docs` must be sorted ascending by doc ID with no duplicates (checked, `Error::DocIdsNotSorted`) and every `freq >= 1` (checked, `Error::NonPositiveFreq`) -- `doc_count` itself (the field-level distinct-docs count written to `.tmd`) is taken as given from the caller, not cross-checked against `terms`. **Does not duplicate the read side's decode logic** -- it only emits bytes; correctness is proven entirely by round-tripping through the *existing, unmodified* `blocktree::open`/`postings::DocInput::open`/`postings::singleton_postings`, the same functions real Java-Lucene fixtures are opened with elsewhere in this port. Unit-tested in `postings_writer.rs` (mixed singleton/multi-doc terms; `IndexOptions::Docs`-only totalTermFreq aliasing; an all-singleton field needing no `.doc` file at all; the `doc_start_fp` delta-threading correctness across 20 terms/5 docs each; every validation-rejection path). **The required end-to-end proof lives in `lucene-search`** (this crate must not depend upward on `lucene-search`, see the `architecture` skill): `crates/lucene-search/tests/postings_writer_round_trip.rs::term_query_finds_correct_docs_over_freshly_written_postings` writes a 3-term field with a mix of singleton and multi-doc terms via `write_single_field`, opens it with the unmodified `blocktree::open`/`DocInput::open`, and runs the unmodified `lucene_search::search_term_query` (the same public query entry point real-fixture tests use) for every term plus a missing term, asserting the exact doc-ID sets Lucene's own `TermQuery`/`PostingsEnum` would return; a second test (`term_query_respects_live_docs_filter`) confirms the written postings compose correctly with a `.liv`-style deletion bitset. **Not verified against real Lucene bytes** -- unlike every read-side row in this table, there is no `fixtures/src/Gen*.java` generator for this writer (there is nothing for it to differentially test against: the point of a first write-side slice is proving this port's own writer and this port's own unmodified reader agree, not that this port's writer produces byte-identical output to `Lucene104PostingsWriter`/`Lucene103BlockTreeTermsWriter` -- those writers' actual on-wire choices, e.g. singleton run-length compression, real block-splitting thresholds, are known not to be replicated here, see above). **Explicitly deferred, not silently missing**: multi-block terms (`docFreq >= BLOCK_SIZE`, full `ForUtil`/`PForUtil` blocks, skip data, impacts), multi-block/floor-split/multi-child-trie term dictionaries (more than one field or more than one `.tim` block/`.tip` node), positions/offsets/payloads (`.pos`/`.pay`), suffix compression, and singleton run-length stat encoding -- all separate future slices. **Now wired into `IndexWriter::commit()`** (follow-up task, see PLAN.md): `IndexWriter::set_postings_field(Some(field_name))` (`crates/lucene-index/src/index_writer.rs`) opts a writer into calling this function for exactly one field of every segment `commit()` flushes, sourcing `TermPostings` from `crate::indexing_chain::invert_documents` over that field's `FieldValue::String` values -- the same one-field/single-`.tim`-block/`docFreq < BLOCK_SIZE`/term-frequency-only scope above, unchanged, now reachable from a real `IndexWriter::add_document`/`commit()` call rather than only from hand-built test input. A `docFreq >= BLOCK_SIZE` term in one commit's pending-doc batch makes the whole `commit()` fail atomically (nothing written), rather than silently truncating. **Now wired for more than one field per commit too (follow-up task):** `IndexWriter::add_postings_field(field_name)` opts a writer into additional postings fields on top of whatever `set_postings_field` already established (which keeps its original "replace, don't accumulate" semantics); `commit()` batches every configured field's `TermPostings` into exactly one `write_fields` call, so a commit with two or more distinct indexed text fields lands in one `.doc`/`.tim`/`.tip`/`.tmd` file set, matching how `merge_postings` in `merge.rs` already consumed `write_fields`. Proven end-to-end by `crates/lucene-search/tests/index_writer_postings_fixtures.rs::two_distinct_postings_fields_in_one_commit_are_both_searchable` (two fields, real term queries against both, asserting no cross-contamination). **Merge-policy interaction, fixed during review**: `execute_merge`/`merge_stored_only_segments` have no `.doc`/`.tim`/`.tip`/`.tmd` awareness at all, so a segment carrying postings could otherwise be silently merged away with no error the moment automatic merge triggering (task #71) fires -- `segment_stats()` now excludes any segment whose `.si` lists a `.doc` file from `find_merges`' candidate pool entirely, keeping it permanently un-mergeable rather than mergeable-with-silent-data-loss. Covered by `segments_with_postings_are_never_automatically_merged_away`, which enables both `set_postings_field` and `set_merge_policy`, crosses the merge threshold with postings-carrying commits, and asserts the segment count never drops and every `.tim` file survives. Required end-to-end proof: `crates/lucene-search/tests/index_writer_postings_fixtures.rs::documents_added_via_index_writer_are_searchable_by_term_query` adds documents via `IndexWriter::add_document`/`commit()` (not a hand-built fixture) and runs `lucene_search::search_term_query` against the result, plus a sibling test proving the `docFreq >= 256` commit is rejected. | **Positions write-side added (this task): `.pos` now supported, still term-frequency-scoped in every other way.** `write_single_field` accepts `IndexOptions::DocsAndFreqsAndPositions` in addition to `Docs`/`DocsAndFreqs` (`DocsAndFreqsAndPositionsAndOffsets` still rejected with `Error::UnsupportedIndexOptions` -- offsets/payloads remain unimplemented on the write side, a further deferred layer). `TermPostings` gained a `positions: Vec<Vec<i32>>` field, parallel to `docs`: each entry is a doc's absolute, ascending occurrence positions (e.g. `[0, 3, 4]`), required to have exactly `docs.len()` entries with `positions[i].len() == docs[i].1` (that doc's freq) whenever `index_options` indexes positions (`Error::MissingPositions`/`Error::PositionsFreqMismatch` otherwise); left empty for `Docs`/`DocsAndFreqs` fields. Scoped identically to the existing `.doc` tail-block restriction: **`total_term_freq < BLOCK_SIZE` (256) for every term with positions** -- only the vint-tail encoding (`refillLastPositionBlock`) is ever written, never a full `ForUtil`/`PForUtil`-encoded `.pos` block; a term at or above that bound is rejected with `Error::TotalTermFreqTooLarge`. A singleton term (`docFreq == 1`, pulsed out of `.doc`) still gets real `.pos` bytes when it indexes positions -- position data is independent of the `.doc` singleton optimization. Per-term metadata (`write_term_metadata`) now also threads a running `pos_start_fp` delta exactly like `doc_start_fp`, written whenever the field indexes positions. **Still not reimplementing the read side**: correctness is proven by round-tripping through the existing, unmodified `postings::read_positions`/`blocktree::FieldTerms::positions`. Unit-tested in `postings_writer.rs` (position round-trip via `read_positions` covering a singleton term with multiple occurrences and a multi-doc term with a position-accumulator reset between docs; every new rejection path). **The required phrase-query end-to-end proof lives in `lucene-search`**: `crates/lucene-search/tests/postings_writer_round_trip.rs::phrase_query_finds_correct_docs_over_freshly_written_positions` writes a 3-term field (`"fox"`/`"jumps"`/`"quick"`) across two docs that share every term but only align adjacently in one of them, opens it through the unmodified `blocktree::open`/`DocInput::open`/`PosInput::open`, and runs the unmodified `lucene_search::search_phrase_query` for `["quick", "fox"]`, `["fox", "jumps"]`, and `["quick", "jumps", "fox"]`, asserting the exact doc each phrase matches -- including the negative case where both docs contain every term but only one doc has them in that exact adjacent order, proving this isn't just a doc-ID conjunction. **`IndexWriter` wiring explicitly NOT touched by this task**: `IndexWriter::build_postings_output` (`crates/lucene-index/src/index_writer.rs`) still only ever builds term-frequency-only `TermPostings` (`positions: Vec::new()`, `set_postings_field` still only accepts `Docs`/`DocsAndFreqs`) -- a real `IndexWriter::add_document`/`commit()` session still cannot produce a `.pos` file yet; wiring positions into `IndexWriter` (sourcing per-doc position lists from `invert_documents`'s already-recorded `PostingEntry::positions`) is left for a follow-up task. **Multi-field support added (this task): `numFields > 1` in `.tmd` is now supported.** `write_single_field` is now a one-element-slice wrapper over the new `write_fields(inputs: &[FieldPostingsInput], segment_id, segment_suffix) -> Result<Output>`, which loops the same per-field write steps (unchanged) over every element of `inputs`, appending each field's `.doc`/`.pos` tail blocks and `.tim` block/`.tip` root node into the *same* shared byte buffers and writing one `.tmd` field record per field. **Per-field limits are exactly as before and apply independently to each field** -- every field is still capped at a single `.tim` block/root trie node, `docFreq < BLOCK_SIZE` (256), and (if it indexes positions) `total_term_freq < BLOCK_SIZE`; none of these bounds are shared or relaxed across fields, and a field violating its own bound still fails the whole call (`Error::DocFreqTooLarge`/`Error::TotalTermFreqTooLarge`) as before. Multi-block terms and multi-level tries remain out of scope (a separate, still-deferred slice). Unit-tested in `postings_writer.rs` (`write_fields_two_fields_share_one_tmd_and_stay_isolated`: two fields, one with positions, one without, opened via the unmodified `blocktree::open` and checked independently). **The required end-to-end proof lives in `lucene-search`**: `crates/lucene-search/tests/postings_writer_round_trip.rs::multi_field_segment_term_queries_are_isolated_per_field` writes a "title" field (`DocsAndFreqs`) and a "body" field (`DocsAndFreqsAndPositions`) in one `write_fields` call, where both fields index a term with the *same bytes* ("rust") but different postings, and runs the unmodified `lucene_search::search_term_query`/`search_phrase_query` against both fields in the same segment, asserting each field's results are correct and that neither field's postings leak into the other's lookups. **`IndexWriter` wiring NOT touched by this task**: `IndexWriter::set_postings_field` still only tracks one configured field per commit (unchanged) -- extending it to multiple fields is a separate follow-up, not attempted here. **Multi-block writer added (this task): a field's terms can now span more than one physical `.tim` block, addressed by a `SIGN_MULTI_CHILDREN` `.tip` root, not just one block/one `SIGN_NO_CHILDREN` root.** Splitting policy, deliberately the simplest one that stays correct without floor blocks or a second trie level: `write_fields` groups a field's (already-sorted) terms by their **first byte** (`group_terms_by_leading_byte`). A field with only one leading byte (or one term, or a term with zero bytes -- there's no leading byte to strip/route on) still gets the original single-block/single-`SIGN_NO_CHILDREN`-root shape, byte-for-byte unchanged (verified: none of the pre-existing single-block tests changed behavior, since their fixtures already exercise both shapes -- e.g. `mixed_singleton_and_multi_doc_terms_round_trip`'s "fox"/"quick"/"the" already has 3 distinct leading bytes and was already taking the multi-block path even before this task added a dedicated test for it). A field spanning 2..=33 distinct leading bytes gets one leaf `.tim` block per group (`write_tim_block`, parameterized by `strip_prefix_len` so the same function serves both the single-block case, prefix length 0, and each group, prefix length 1 -- a block only ever stores the bytes *after* its shared leading byte, matching `crate::blocktree::collect_leaf_blocks`'s "a block only stores its own suffix" contract on the read side), each addressed by its own `SIGN_NO_CHILDREN`/`hasTerms`/no-floor leaf node (`write_leaf_node`), with the field's `.tip` root being a single `SIGN_MULTI_CHILDREN` node with no output of its own (`write_multi_children_root`, always `ChildSaveStrategy::ARRAY` -- the simplest of the three label encodings `crate::blocktree::multi_children_labels_and_fps` supports on the read side; `BITS`/`REVERSE_ARRAY` are never emitted). Each block's per-term metadata delta-threading (`doc_start_fp`/`pos_start_fp`) resets fresh per block, matching `SegmentTermsEnumFrame`'s per-frame reset the read side (`decode_block`) already assumes -- blocks never share metadata state, whether split by floor (not implemented here) or by sibling leaf block (this task). **Explicitly still unimplemented, narrowed further than a first cut might suggest**: floor sub-blocks (a single leading-byte group with too many terms for one block -- this writer has no notion of a per-block term-count cap at all, so an enormous single-leading-byte group still produces one arbitrarily large block, not a floor split; audited again by a later "floor sub-blocks in blocktree writer" task, which confirmed this remains the only gap and that read-side floor support -- `blocktree.rs::expand_floor` -- already has solid real-Lucene fixture coverage including non-first floor sub-blocks, see PLAN.md); a second/deeper trie level (a field needing more than 33 distinct leading bytes is rejected outright with `Error::TooManyLeadingByteGroups` rather than silently misencoding the multi-children node's 5-bit `strategyBytes-1` header field, which can only address 2..=33 children); and the `BITS`/`REVERSE_ARRAY` label-encoding strategies. This is a deliberately narrower scope than "any field exceeding one block's term-count capacity splits automatically" -- the chosen policy (group by leading byte) is the simplest split that maps cleanly onto a *single-level* multi-child trie without floor data, at the cost of only working when a field's terms are naturally spread across enough distinct leading bytes (true of essentially any real natural-language field, false in principle for a pathological field where thousands of terms share one leading byte). **Proof, mirroring the single-block slice's own bar**: `postings_writer.rs::many_leading_byte_groups_force_multi_child_trie_root` (26 terms, one per lowercase letter -- 26 physical `.tim` blocks under one multi-child root, every term independently looked up through the unmodified `blocktree::open`, not just first/last), `rejects_field_needing_more_than_33_leading_byte_groups`, and `empty_term_falls_back_to_single_block_even_with_other_distinct_leading_bytes`. **The required end-to-end proof lives in `lucene-search`**: `crates/lucene-search/tests/postings_writer_round_trip.rs::term_query_finds_correct_docs_across_multiple_tim_blocks` writes the same 26-leading-byte-group field, opens it through the unmodified `blocktree::open`/`DocInput::open`, and runs the unmodified `lucene_search::search_term_query` for terms in the first, a middle, and the last physical block plus a missing term, proving every block is independently reachable and correctly decoded through the real query layer, not just that the writer's own bytes decode in isolation. **Not verified against real Lucene bytes**, same caveat as every other row segment above -- this proves the port's own writer and the port's own unmodified reader agree on a multi-block/multi-child-trie shape, not that it's byte-identical to what `Lucene103BlockTreeTermsWriter`'s real min/maxItemsInBlock-threshold-driven splitting would produce for the same input. **`IndexWriter` wiring NOT touched by this task**: `IndexWriter::build_postings_output`/`set_postings_field` are unchanged -- a real `IndexWriter::add_document`/`commit()` session still only ever produces single-field output via the (now multi-block-capable) `write_single_field`/`write_fields`, so this new splitting path already reaches `commit()` for whatever field is configured, but wiring a *second* configured field or otherwise changing `IndexWriter`'s own scope is a separate follow-up, not attempted here. **Full-block `.doc` doc-delta/freq emission added (this task): `docFreq >= BLOCK_SIZE` (256) is no longer rejected.** `write_full_block` (new) emits, for every complete 256-doc chunk of a term's postings, a level-0 skip header (`level0NumBytes` skip pointer -- any valid vlong, unused by the reader; `docDelta`/`blockLength` via new `write_vint15`/`write_vlong15` helpers, the exact write-side inverse of `postings::read_vint15`/`read_vlong15`) followed by the doc-delta/freq body, reusing `for_util::for_encode` (doc deltas) and `for_util::pfor_encode` (freqs) directly -- no bit-packing logic is reimplemented here, only called. **Encoding choices, stated plainly**: doc deltas always take the plain positive-`bitsPerValue` `ForUtil` shape; this writer never emits the `bitsPerValue == 0` ("all-256-consecutive") or `bitsPerValue < 0` (dense unary bit-set) alternate encodings the real writer picks for space efficiency (both already decode correctly on the read side, see the `postings.rs` row above, but this writer doesn't choose them) -- one correct, always-decodable shape was chosen over replicating every space-optimization the real writer has. Impacts are always an empty byte region (no competitive-impact computation at all); the reader accepts a zero-length impacts run and decodes it to an empty list, so this is valid, just not space- or query-optimized. The `docFreq % BLOCK_SIZE` remainder still uses the pre-existing group-varint tail-block path, with `prev_doc_id` now threaded from the last full block's last doc ID instead of always `-1`. **The per-term upper bound moved, not disappeared**: `validate_field` now rejects at `docFreq >= LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` (8192, `Error::DocFreqTooLarge`'s condition changed accordingly) rather than `>= BLOCK_SIZE`, since this writer still never emits the level-1 skip entries `postings.rs`'s reader expects to find interleaved above that threshold -- a term that large would round-trip incorrectly, so it is still rejected rather than silently misencoded. **Positions still explicitly out of scope for full blocks**: `total_term_freq >= BLOCK_SIZE` is still rejected with `Error::TotalTermFreqTooLarge`, unchanged -- a term reaching the new `.doc` full-block path can never also need a `.pos` full block in the same call regardless (`total_term_freq >= doc_freq` always), so this is a real, not merely theoretical, non-interaction, not an oversight. **Proof, mirroring the existing bar**: unit tests in `postings_writer.rs` cover `docFreq == BLOCK_SIZE` (one full block, no tail), `docFreq == BLOCK_SIZE + 1` (one full block plus a one-doc tail), `docFreq == 600` (two full blocks plus an 88-doc tail, exercising full-block-to-full-block `prev_doc_id` chaining, not just full-block-to-tail), a full block with `IndexOptions::Docs` (no freqs, no impacts field, no `pfor_encode` call), and small/full-block terms mixed in one field -- every one of these round-trips through the *existing, unmodified* `blocktree::open`/`DocInput::read_postings`, the same functions real Java-Lucene fixtures are opened with elsewhere in this port, asserting every decoded doc/freq exactly, not just "opened without erroring". **No new `fixtures/src/Gen*.java` generator was added for this task** -- deliberately: the existing "big"/"everywhere" fixture field (`docFreq == 300`) already forces the real Lucene *writer*'s own full-block path and fixture-verifies the *reader* side (`postings.rs`) against it; this task's job was proving this port's *own* new writer output is byte-compatible with this port's *own* already-fixture-verified reader, which is a Rust-only round-trip question (no new wire-format understanding is being claimed, unlike a decoder task) -- the same reasoning the original single-block writer slice gave for having no generator of its own (see this row's first paragraph). `for_util.rs`'s `for_encode`/`pfor_encode`/`bits_required` lost their `#[allow(dead_code)]` markers now that a real production caller exists. **Still explicitly deferred**: `.pos` full-block emission (`total_term_freq >= BLOCK_SIZE`, see above -- currently provably unreachable from this writer's own `.doc` full-block path, not merely unimplemented); real competitive-impact computation; the all-consecutive/dense-bitset alternate doc-delta encodings; `IndexWriter` wiring (`set_postings_field`/`build_postings_output`) is untouched by this task, so a real `add_document`/`commit()` session still cannot reach a `docFreq >= 256` term without separately tripping `flush_stored_only_segment`'s own pre-existing, unrelated `write_best_speed` `< 128`-docs-per-flush-chunk cap first -- see `crates/lucene-index/src/index_writer.rs`'s `commit_succeeds_below_the_doc_freq_boundary` test doc comment and `crates/lucene-search/tests/index_writer_postings_fixtures.rs`'s trailing comment for the full explanation of why no end-to-end `IndexWriter`-level test of the new boundary exists. **Level-1 skip-entry emission added (this task): `docFreq >= LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` (8192) is no longer rejected, and there is no further per-term docFreq ceiling.** `write_level1_span` (new) emits, before every complete span of `LEVEL1_FACTOR` (32) full level-0 blocks, a level-1 skip entry -- the exact write-side inverse of the existing, unmodified `postings::read_level1_entry`/`LazyDocsCursor::skip_level1_to`. The entry's vlong byte-length field is the one subtle part: `read_level1_entry` computes `doc_end_fp` as that field's value added to the reader's position measured *right after* the vlong itself, i.e. before the freq-gated `skip1EndFP`/`numImpactBytes` fields are read -- so the vlong must span every byte from there through the end of the whole entry plus its 32-block span, not just the span's own bytes (this writer's first draft got that wrong, undercounting by the 4 header bytes, caught by an `advance()` landing 33 docs off from the expected target). **Same encoding choices as level-0**: the level-1 entry's impacts region is always empty (`numImpactBytes = 0`, no competitive-impact computation at either level -- the reader accepts a zero-length impacts run); the `indexHasPos`-gated pos/pay sub-fields `read_level1_entry` supports are never written, because they're provably unreachable from this writer -- a term reaching `docFreq >= LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` has `total_term_freq >= LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS`, which would already have tripped `Error::TotalTermFreqTooLarge` had it indexed positions (the same non-interaction argument `write_full_block`'s own doc comment gives for its level-0 header). **`validate_field`'s docFreq bound is removed entirely, not merely raised**: `postings.rs`'s reader has no level-2 skip structure at all (`Lucene104` postings only ever have levels 0 and 1), so there is nothing left for a further ceiling to protect against -- a term spanning any number of level-1 spans plus a final partial span round-trips exactly like a sub-8192 term always did. **Proof, mirroring the level-0 bar**: unit tests in `postings_writer.rs` round-trip `docFreq == LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` (one span, no remainder), `LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS + 1` (one span plus a one-doc tail), and `2 * LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` (two spans back to back, exercising `level1_last_doc_id`/`prev_doc_id` threading across more than one span) through the existing, unmodified `blocktree::open`/`DocInput::read_postings`, asserting the exact doc/freq lists; the same three boundaries are re-proven through `LazyDocsCursor::advance` (`docfreq_at_level1_boundaries_advance_via_lazy_cursor`); and `writer_level1_span_advance_past_it_skips_corrupted_first_block_header` writes a real span, corrupts its first level-0 block's header bytes in place, and confirms `advance()` past the whole span still succeeds (never decoding the corruption) while `advance()` into the span surfaces it -- the write-side mirror of `postings.rs`'s own `lazy_cursor_advance_skips_whole_corrupted_level1_span_without_decoding_it` proof. **No new `fixtures/src/Gen*.java` generator**, same reasoning as the level-0 task: this is a Rust-only "writer and already-fixture-verified reader agree" question, not a new wire-format claim. **Still explicitly deferred**: real competitive-impact computation (both levels' impacts regions stay empty), the all-consecutive/dense-bitset alternate doc-delta encodings, `.pos` full-block emission, and `IndexWriter` wiring -- `set_postings_field`/`build_postings_output` are untouched by this task, and reaching `docFreq >= LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` via a real `add_document`/`commit()` session was already unreachable before this task (blocked by `flush_stored_only_segment`'s own unrelated `< 128`-docs-per-flush cap) and remains so. **Full-block `.pos` position emission added (this task), superseding the "positions still out of scope for full blocks" caveat above: `total_term_freq >= BLOCK_SIZE` is no longer rejected.** `write_position_tail` now buffers a term's position deltas into one flat, cross-doc sequence (resetting to each doc's absolute first position at that doc's first occurrence, exactly matching `read_positions`'s own flat-then-re-chop shape) and emits every complete 256-occurrence chunk as a full `PForUtil` block via the new `write_full_position_block`, reusing `for_util::pfor_encode` directly. Unlike `.doc` full blocks, a `.pos` full block has **no skip header at all** -- `crate::postings::read_positions`'s `num_full_blocks` loop calls a bare, unframed `for_util::pfor_decode`, so there was no level-0/level-1-equivalent skip-entry inverse to write here; the `total_term_freq % BLOCK_SIZE` remainder still uses the pre-existing vint-tail path. **The real, still-standing ceiling moved from `total_term_freq` to `docFreq`**: `validate_field` now rejects `docFreq >= BLOCK_SIZE` whenever a term indexes positions (`Error::DocFreqTooLargeForPositions`, replacing `Error::TotalTermFreqTooLarge`) -- not because of anything about `.pos` itself (which has no ceiling at all now), but because this writer's `.doc`-side `write_full_block` never emits the pos/pay skip sub-fields `read_full_block_header` expects on a full `.doc` block for a positions-indexing field; since `docFreq <= total_term_freq` always, a term can have arbitrarily large `total_term_freq` from a small number of high-freq docs and still round-trip correctly, as long as `docFreq` itself stays under `BLOCK_SIZE`. **Offsets are now supported too** (`IndexOptions::DocsAndFreqsAndPositionsAndOffsets`). A new `.pay` output stream is opened only when at least one field indexes offsets or payloads; per occurrence, an `offsetStartDelta`/`length` pair follows its position delta -- inlined in `.pos` (reusing the previous occurrence's length unless it changes) for the vint tail, or as two back-to-back bare `PForUtil` arrays in `.pay` for each full 256-occurrence block (`write_full_offset_block`), exactly like `read_positions`'s `has_offsets` branch already expects to decode. `payStartFP` is threaded through the per-term metadata the same running-delta way as `posStartFP`. Proof: `postings_writer.rs` unit tests cover a single position per doc with offsets, multiple positions per doc with offsets (confirming the intra-doc `startOffsetDelta` resets to 0 at each doc boundary), a `total_term_freq` spanning a full `PForUtil` block with offsets, and rejection tests for missing/mismatched/non-monotonic offsets -- all round-tripped through the existing, unmodified `postings::read_positions`/`blocktree::FieldTerms::positions`. **Payloads are now supported too** (`FieldInfo.hasPayloads()`, a per-field bool orthogonal to `IndexOptions` -- unlike offsets, not gated by a distinct `IndexOptions` variant). Payload fields are always written *before* offset fields at each occurrence (matching `Lucene104PostingsWriter`'s own field order), in both the vint tail (length re-written only when it changes since the previous occurrence *within the same term*, reset at `finishTerm`, mirroring the offsets length-suppression convention) and the full `PForUtil` block path (`write_full_payload_length_block`, which never suppresses -- every occurrence's length is written, matching the fixed-size block encoding). A payload is always present (possibly zero-length) for every occurrence once a field has payloads enabled -- there is no "absent payload" state distinct from "present with a zero-length payload". Proof: `postings_writer.rs` unit tests cover a single position per doc with payloads, multiple positions per doc with payloads (same-length-repeated, proving suppression, and varying-length), payloads combined with offsets on the same field (proving the interleaving order and a zero-length-payload case), a `total_term_freq` spanning a full `PForUtil` block with varying/empty payload lengths, and rejection tests for missing/mismatched payloads -- all round-tripped through the existing, unmodified reader with zero reader-side changes needed. **Proof, mirroring the `.doc` full-block bar**: unit tests in `postings_writer.rs` round-trip `total_term_freq == BLOCK_SIZE` (one full position block, no tail) and `total_term_freq == BLOCK_SIZE + 1` (one full block plus a one-occurrence tail), both using genuinely irregular (non-uniform) position deltas spread across several docs, through the existing, unmodified `postings::read_positions`/`blocktree::FieldTerms::positions`, asserting the exact per-doc position sequence, not just counts; a further test proves the previously-rejected "one doc, `freq == BLOCK_SIZE`" shape now round-trips exactly; and a replacement rejection test confirms `docFreq >= BLOCK_SIZE` while indexing positions is still rejected. **No new `fixtures/src/Gen*.java` generator**, same reasoning as every other writer-side task in this row: a Rust-only "writer and already-fixture-verified reader agree" question, not a new wire-format claim. **Still explicitly deferred**: payloads (any full block or tail), real competitive-impact computation, the all-consecutive/dense-bitset alternate `.doc` doc-delta encodings, and `IndexWriter` wiring (`set_postings_field`/`build_postings_output` are untouched by this task, and a real `add_document`/`commit()` session still cannot produce positions at all, per the earlier "IndexWriter wiring explicitly NOT touched" note above).

**Recommended next slice**: step back to a different Phase -- see below for why the wildcard/prefix intersection slice just landed is intentionally not followed by more work in this same subsystem. Glob-based wildcard/prefix term intersection (`FieldTerms::intersect`, `crate::wildcard::WildcardPattern`) landed this slice: a linear scan (narrowed by a literal-prefix binary-search range) over the already-materialized `entries` `Vec`, covering `PrefixQuery` exactly and `WildcardQuery`'s `*`/`?` glob subset, fixture-verified against real `WildcardQuery`/`CompiledAutomaton.getTermsEnum` output on the "many" field (see the `blocktree.rs` row above for the full writeup). This was explicitly scoped down from real `IntersectTermsEnum`/`CompiledAutomaton` automaton-driven trie-block-skipping (deferred, see that row) and does not include regex (`RegexpQuery`) or fuzzy/Levenshtein (`FuzzyQuery`) automata, both flagged as separate future slices requiring real automaton/edit-distance machinery rather than glob matching. Three reasonable next moves: (1) **regex or fuzzy automaton support**, building a real byte-level automaton/edit-distance representation now that glob/prefix has proven the `FieldTerms::intersect` shape works end-to-end against real Lucene; (2) **real `IntersectTermsEnum`-style trie-block-skipping**, replacing today's "scan the sorted `Vec`" approach with one that walks only the `.tip` trie nodes/`.tim` blocks an automaton's reachable states could lead to -- valuable once a field is large enough that `O(n)` scanning actually shows up in a profile, not before; (3) **step back to a different Phase entirely** -- this subsystem (`postings.rs`/`blocktree.rs`/`for_util.rs`/`wildcard.rs`) has now had a very long consecutive run of slices (level-0/level-1 skip data, positions, lazy cursors, enumeration, impacts, and now wildcard intersection), and PLAN.md's other Phase-1/2 read-path formats (points/BKD query execution, doc-values-backed sorting, or the actual `IndexSearcher`/`Weight`/`Scorer` plumbing that would let any of this get exercised end-to-end against a real query) are likely higher-value to de-risk before this subsystem's next increment -- this is the option this slice's own author recommends. Also still open but narrower: a real-fixture-verified full-`ForUtil`/`PForUtil`-block position path (`totalTermFreq >= BLOCK_SIZE`, currently only unit-tested).

## lucene-index

| Java | Rust | Status |
|---|---|---|
| `codecs/lucene99/Lucene99SegmentInfoFormat` (`.si` read + write) | `lucene-index/src/segment_info.rs::{parse, write}` | **both directions ported.** `write` is the exact byte-level inverse of `parse`, emits `numSortFields = 0` unless `SegmentInfo::index_sort` is set (single-field index sort, see below), and does not re-validate that `files` entries are segment-name-prefixed (callers are trusted, matching the parser's own stance) -- exercised via own-reader round-trip unit tests. **Verified against real Lucene in the writeŌåÆread direction** (unsorted case only, see below): `crates/lucene-index/examples/write_segment_info_fixture.rs` writes two `.si` files (`_0`: compound file, with minVersion, with diagnostics/files/attributes; `_1`: non-compound, with `hasBlocks`, no minVersion, everything else empty) and `fixtures/src/VerifySegmentInfo.java` opens them directly through `Lucene99SegmentInfoFormat.read` and confirms every property matches each segment's manifest -- passed on the first real-Lucene run |
| `index/SegmentInfo.indexSort` / `SortField`/`SortFieldProvider` (multi-field NUMERIC index sort, `.si` encoding) | `lucene-index/src/segment_info.rs::{IndexSortField, SortMissingValue, read_sort_field, write_sort_field}`, `SegmentInfo::index_sort: Option<Vec<IndexSortField>>` | **partial, NUMERIC-fields-only (any count).** Task #49 supported exactly one NUMERIC `SortField`; task #52 extended this to a real multi-field `Sort` -- `numSortFields` is written/read genuinely (0, or N priority-ordered `SortField` descriptors), matching real Lucene's `Sort` being an array of `SortField`s applied in order. Only NUMERIC fields are supported; any other `SortType` byte is rejected as `Error::UnknownSortFieldType` (arbitrary `SortFieldProvider` decoding would need either a matching plugin registry or a hard-coded allowlist this port doesn't have). **Byte-format status: NOT verified against real Lucene.** Real Lucene's index-sort `.si` bytes are written by pluggable `SortFieldProvider` Java classes and no real-Lucene-written sorted-segment `.si` fixture exists under `fixtures/` to derive the true byte layout from, for either a single-field or a multi-field sort -- the `SortField` encoding this port reads/writes (now repeated N times) is **this port's own internal format** (round-trip-correct against its own `parse`/`write`, confirmed by unit tests in `segment_info.rs` including 2- and 3-field round trips with mixed reverse/missing policies), not a byte-compatible port of `Lucene99SegmentInfoFormat`'s real encoding. A real Lucene reader would not be able to open a `.si` this port writes with an index sort set, and vice versa. Closing this gap needs either a real sorted-index `.si` fixture (to derive the true `SortFieldProvider` wire format) or accepting the divergence permanently and documenting it as this port's own extension. |
| `index/DocumentsWriterPerThread` sort-on-flush (physically reordering a flushed segment's documents by the index sort) | `lucene-index/src/segment_writer.rs::flush_sorted_stored_only_segment`, `SortKeySpec` | **partial.** Takes a non-empty, priority-ordered slice of `SortKeySpec`s (one per sort field, each with its own field name, in-memory `&[Option<i64>]` per-doc sort key, `reverse`, and `SortMissingValue`), stable-sorts the whole batch by comparing field 0 first and falling through to field 1, field 2, etc. only on a tie at every prior tier (ties/both-missing-at-every-tier keep original relative order), reorders stored fields accordingly, and records the full sort in the flushed `.si`. Each field's `reverse`/missing-value policy is applied independently at its own tier -- one field can be descending with missing-last while another is ascending with missing-first, matching real Lucene's per-`SortField` configuration. This port has no write-side doc-values format yet, so each field's sort keys can't be read back from an already-written file the way real Lucene's `DocValuesConsumer`-fed sort does -- they must already be in memory, parallel to `docs`. No query-side early-termination optimization either (irrelevant to correctness in this port regardless of index sort support). |
| `index/SegmentMerger` sort-preserving merge (k-way merge of already-sorted segments by the shared index sort) | `lucene-index/src/merge.rs::{merge_sorted_stored_only_segments, MergeSortKeySpec, compare_heads}` | **done, stored-fields-only scope (task #53, closing the gap task #49/#52 explicitly deferred).** Given `sort_fields` (one `MergeSortKeySpec` per priority tier, each carrying every source's per-doc sort key for that field, `reverse`, and `SortMissingValue`) and a list of `MergeSource`s, performs a genuine k-way merge: at each step it picks whichever source's current (undeleted) head doc has the smallest key across all tiers -- comparator logic reused, not reimplemented, via `crate::segment_writer::sort_key_rank` (made `pub(crate)` for exactly this reuse) -- and appends that doc, so the merged output is globally sorted across every source, not source A's docs followed by source B's. Field-number reconciliation and deleted-doc dropping work exactly as in `merge_stored_only_segments`. The merged `.si` correctly keeps `index_sort: Some(...)` (the concatenating `merge_stored_only_segments` still always writes `index_sort: None`, since it does not preserve sort order). **Precondition, not re-checked by this function:** every source must already be internally ordered by the same `sort_fields` key (true for anything written by `flush_sorted_stored_only_segment` or a previous call to this same function) and every source must share the same index sort as every other (real Lucene's hard "same sort or reject the merge" rule) -- the caller is responsible for having verified this (e.g. comparing each source's own `SegmentInfo.index_sort`); this function has no dependency on `SegmentInfo` and does not attempt to detect an out-of-order or mismatched source. **Scope: stored fields only**, matching this port's existing write-side limit -- doc values, norms, and term vectors attached to a `MergeSource` are silently ignored by this function (unaffected: still only reachable via `merge_stored_only_segments`'s concatenation-order merge). **No new Java fixture**: this is composition of two already-verified primitives (task #52's sort-key comparator, task #15/#37/#38's segment-writing path), following the precedent of prior composition tasks (#36-38, #47) -- unit-tested instead: two sources with interleaved keys where naive concatenation would visibly break sort order (confirmed the real merge doesn't), three sources, a primary-field tie broken by a secondary field, `.si` index-sort-descriptor preservation, deleted-doc dropping mid-merge, field-number reconciliation during the k-way walk, an empty-sources edge case, and a dedicated check that a multi-field document's content stays attached to the correct doc through reordering (not shuffled independently of its sort key). |
| `index/SegmentInfos` (`segments_N` read: header/footer, per-segment commit metadata, user data) | `lucene-index/src/segment_infos.rs` | ported (read-only), fixture-verified against a real 2-commit `IndexWriter` output |
| `index/DocumentsWriterPerThread`/`IndexingChain` (tokenize + build an in-memory inverted index from indexed field text) | `lucene-index/src/indexing_chain.rs::{InMemoryInvertedIndex, PostingEntry, invert_documents}` | **in-memory only, no persistence path (task #63) -- read this status carefully before assuming more.** `invert_documents` runs each `(doc_id, field, text)` triple through a `lucene_analysis::Analyzer` and groups the result into `InMemoryInvertedIndex { terms: BTreeMap<(field, term), Vec<PostingEntry>> }`, each `PostingEntry` holding a doc's `doc_id` plus its occurrences' resolved absolute positions and character offsets (`term_freq()` = occurrence count) -- the same per-term/per-doc grouping shape real Lucene's `TermsHashPerField`/`FreqProxTermsWriterPerField` build while indexing. `lucene-index/Cargo.toml` gained a `lucene-analysis` path dependency (clean downward edge, `lucene-analysis` has zero workspace deps). **This does NOT make documents indexed/searchable via analyzed text**: `segment_writer.rs` still has no write-side postings encoder (every flushed field remains `IndexOptions::None`, unchanged by this task, per that module's own "what this deliberately is not" section), so there is no code path from `InMemoryInvertedIndex` to any file on disk -- this structure cannot be persisted or read back until a postings writer exists (tracked separately, task #75). The output shape (doc-ID-sorted `Vec<PostingEntry>` per term, each with freq/positions/offsets) is chosen to match exactly what `Lucene104PostingsWriter`'s `.doc`/`.pos`/`.pay` encode needs as input, so that future writer can consume it directly. **Verified by unit tests only** (composition of task #61's already cross-engine-verified `Analyzer` plus this task's new grouping logic, same precedent as task #62's `query_parser.rs` wiring -- no new Java fixture): single doc/field exact shape, multiple docs sharing a term produce a doc-ID-sorted list, a repeated term's `term_freq`/positions are all recorded (not just the first occurrence), independent per-field entries for the same term text (no cross-field merging), and stopword-filtered text excludes the stopword while preserving surviving tokens' positions (reusing `StopFilter`'s position-increment-preservation guarantee). Coverage: `indexing_chain.rs` 100% lines. |
| `index/SegmentInfos.write` | `lucene-index/src/segment_infos.rs::write` | **ported.** Byte-level inverse of `parse`, always emits `VERSION_CURRENT` (so the SciId marker byte is always written, matching `parse`'s expectation for this format) and derives the `segments_N` file name from `generation` via the existing `lucene_store::directory::segments_file_name` helper rather than re-deriving the base-36 suffix a second time. Unlike `segment_info::write`/`field_infos::write` (which return `Vec<u8>` and let the caller route bytes through a `Directory`), this one takes a `&dyn Directory` directly and performs the write-then-sync itself: a `segments_N` file's correctness as a *commit* depends on being fsynced before it's durable, mirroring real `IndexWriter.commit()`'s write-then-`Directory.sync` sequencing rather than leaving that easy-to-forget step to the caller. Unit-tested by round-tripping through `parse` via a real `FsDirectory` (empty commit, single segment, multi-segment with SciId/del-counts/DV-update-files/user-data, generation-0 plain `segments` name, negative-generation rejection). **This is also the milestone verified by `crates/lucene-index/examples/write_segment_infos_fixture.rs` + `fixtures/src/VerifySegmentInfos.java`: a genuinely complete single-segment index (`.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm` + `.fnm` + `.si` + `segments_N`, reusing the already-verified `stored_fields::write_best_speed`/`field_infos::write`/`segment_info::write`) opened via real, high-level `DirectoryReader.open(FSDirectory.open(path))` -- not hand-built codec-level access -- succeeded on the first run, confirming doc count and stored field values through ordinary `IndexReader`/`StoredFields` calls.** The fixture's fields are deliberately stored-only (`IndexOptions::None`, no doc values/term vectors/points/vectors): `SegmentCoreReaders` (`org.apache.lucene.index.SegmentCoreReaders`) only opens a `FieldsProducer` when `FieldInfos.hasPostings()` is true, so a segment with zero indexed fields needs no `.tim`/`.tip`/`.doc` postings files at all -- this port has no postings/doc-values/points/vector *write* path yet (those remain read-only, see the rows above), so a fully-indexed segment (a real `TextField`, sorted doc values, etc.) is not yet achievable through `DirectoryReader.open`; only the stored-fields-only case was in scope for this milestone and is what's verified |
| `index/IndexWriter` (unifying add/update/delete/commit facade) | `lucene-index/src/index_writer.rs::IndexWriter` | **facade over already-built primitives, not a reimplementation of any of them.** `IndexWriter::open(dir, fields, codec_name, lucene_version)` resumes an existing commit (via `lucene_store::directory::last_commit_generation`, distinguishing "no commit yet" from "a commit file exists but is corrupt") or starts a fresh empty index; `add_document` buffers in memory; `commit()` flushes the buffer through the existing `segment_writer::flush_stored_only_segment` and writes the updated segment list via the existing `segment_infos::write`; `update_document`/`delete_documents` delegate straight to the existing `update_document::update_document`/`term_delete::resolve_and_apply_term_delete` + `deletes::apply_deletes`, unchanged; `apply_merge` folds an already-executed `merge::merge_stored_only_segments` result back into the writer's committed state. Every one of those underlying functions existed before this task -- this module's only new logic is the state threading (current `SegmentInfos`, buffered docs, segment-name counter) that previously had to be hand-carried by each caller/test across calls. Segment/commit ids are generated by hashing a monotonic counter with the current time (`DefaultHasher`, not a CSPRNG) since this workspace has no `rand` dependency and the only property a segment id needs here is uniqueness across a session, not statistical randomness. **Update (automatic merge triggering):** `IndexWriter::set_merge_policy(Some(config))` now opts a writer into automatic merging -- every subsequent `commit()`, right after writing its own `segments_N`, loops calling the existing `merge_policy::find_merges` against the writer's now-committed segments (stats built from each segment's `.si` via `segment_info::parse` + `merge_policy::segment_byte_size`, plus `del_count` already in memory) and, for each proposed group, executes it via the existing `merge::merge_stored_only_segments` and folds the result in via the existing `apply_merge`, repeating until `find_merges` proposes nothing further (guaranteed to terminate: every merge strictly shrinks the segment count). With no merge policy set (the default a freshly-opened writer starts with), `commit()` is byte-for-byte unchanged from before this feature, so none of the original tests needed updating. New tests: no-merge-policy commits never auto-merge; a commit sequence staying at/under `segments_per_tier` stays unmerged; a sequence crossing it merges down to fewer segments with every original document still readable; and 20 consecutive single-document commits under a tight policy converge without panicking or looping (segment count never exceeds commit count). **Explicitly deferred, not silently missing:** no merge-policy configurability from `open()` itself (only via the separate `set_merge_policy` setter), no concurrent/background merging, no multi-tier scheduling beyond one `merge_policy::find_merges` call, `update_document`/`delete_documents` do not trigger this check (only `commit()` does), no RAM-based flush triggering (only an explicit `commit()` flushes), no multi-threaded `DocumentsWriterPerThread`-style pooling, and `update_document`/`delete_documents` still only resolve against segments the caller supplies an opened `SegmentDeleteSource` for (inherited from `update_document.rs`/`term_delete.rs` -- no reader pool that opens every segment automatically). **No new Java fixture** (composition of already-verified primitives, same precedent as `update_document.rs`/`merge.rs`): unit tests cover opening a fresh directory, add+commit producing one readable segment (read back both through the returned struct and by re-reading `segments_N` off disk), a no-pending-documents commit still producing a valid next generation, multiple commits producing multiple independent, non-colliding segment names, resuming a writer against an already-committed directory without a segment-name collision, `update_document`/`delete_documents` against the same real-Lucene postings fixture `term_delete.rs`/`update_document.rs` already use (including a failing delete leaving the writer's in-memory state and on-disk `segments_N` untouched), and `apply_merge` folding a real `merge_stored_only_segments` result over two committed segments back into the writer. `SegmentInfos`/`SegmentCommitInfo` gained `PartialEq` (needed to assert a failed call left state byte-for-byte unchanged) -- a mechanical addition, no behavior change. **Update (postings/term-vectors/doc-values wiring):** `set_postings_field`, `set_term_vector_field`, and `set_doc_values_field` (NUMERIC only) each opt a writer into building and writing real postings/term vectors/doc values for one field per commit, respectively -- see this crate's/`lucene-codecs`'s own parity rows above for each feature's exact scope.
