All three can be configured at once, in the same or different fields, in one commit. `segment_stats()` excludes any segment carrying `.doc`/`.tvd`/`.dvd` files from automatic-merge candidacy, since `execute_merge` only merges stored fields. **Update (multiple postings/term-vector fields per commit):** `IndexWriter::add_postings_field`/`IndexWriter::add_term_vector_field` opt a writer into building postings/term vectors for *additional* fields on top of whatever `set_postings_field`/`set_term_vector_field` already established (which keep their original "replace, don't accumulate" semantics) -- `self.postings_fields`/`self.term_vector_fields` are now `Vec`s, not single `Option`s. `commit()` batches every entry in `postings_fields` into exactly **one** `lucene_codecs::postings_writer::write_fields` call (the same multi-field write primitive `merge_postings` in `merge.rs` already used), so a commit with, say, two distinct indexed text fields produces one `.doc`/`.tim`/`.tip`/`.tmd` file set covering both, not two separate file sets. Term vectors follow the same shape into `term_vectors::write_best_speed`, which already accepted multiple `TermVectorField` entries per `TermVectorsDocument` before this task -- the gap was purely on `IndexWriter`'s calling side (`build_term_vectors_output` only ever built a single-field `TermVectorField` per doc), now fixed to build one `TermVectorField` per configured field with content for that doc. New tests (`crates/lucene-index/src/index_writer.rs` unit tests plus `crates/lucene-search/tests/index_writer_postings_fixtures.rs::two_distinct_postings_fields_in_one_commit_are_both_searchable` and `crates/lucene-search/tests/index_writer_term_vectors_fixtures.rs::two_distinct_term_vector_fields_in_one_commit_are_both_readable`) prove two distinct fields committed together are both independently readable/searchable with no cross-contamination, on top of the existing single-field tests (unchanged, still passing byte-for-byte). **Still single-field-per-commit:** `set_doc_values_field` (no `add_doc_values_field` equivalent yet -- no per-field file-suffix machinery there to fan out to more than one field within a single segment); this is an intentional, undone gap, not an oversight. **Update (`rollback()`):** `IndexWriter::rollback(&mut self)` discards every document buffered by `add_document` since the last `commit()` -- a pure in-memory reset of `pending_docs` only, never touching `dir`/`segment_infos` (no `segment_infos::write` call). Writer configuration (`set_postings_field`/`set_term_vector_field`/`set_doc_values_field`/`set_merge_policy`) and any prior commit's segments both survive a rollback untouched, matching real Lucene's split between `IndexWriterConfig` (survives) and buffered documents (discarded). **Not replicated**: real `IndexWriter.rollback()` also closes the writer and releases its write lock permanently; this facade has no open/close lifecycle at all, so `rollback()` leaves the writer fully usable for further `add_document`/`commit()` calls. New tests: rollback discards pending docs so the next commit is empty of them; rollback with nothing pending is a safe no-op; rollback after a prior commit leaves that commit's segment untouched while discarding a second, uncommitted batch; and rollback preserves postings/term-vector/doc-values/merge-policy configuration for a later commit. **Update (two-phase commit, `prepare_commit()`/`finish_commit()`):** `commit()` is now `prepare_commit()` immediately followed by `finish_commit()`, kept as one call for backward compatibility -- every existing caller/test is unchanged. `prepare_commit()` does everything `commit()` used to do (flush `pending_docs` via `flush_stored_only_segment`, build/write postings/term-vectors/doc-values files) *except* the final `segment_infos::write` call, and stashes the resulting in-memory `SegmentInfos` in a new `prepared_commit: Option<SegmentInfos>` field; `finish_commit()` takes that stashed value and calls `segment_infos::write` (the one call that actually produces the next `segments_N`), then runs auto-merge exactly as `commit()` always has. **Honest scope, read before relying on this for anything crash-related**: real `IndexWriter.prepareCommit()`/`SegmentInfos.prepareCommit` write a `pending_segments_N` file plus enough on-disk state that a *new process* opening the index after a crash can discover a prepared-but-not-yet-committed generation and roll it forward or back. This port's `segment_infos::write` has no `pending_segments_N` equivalent and no `segments.gen` pointer file -- there is exactly one kind of `segments_N`, and "what's current" is simply "the highest-numbered `segments_N` that exists" (`lucene_store::directory::last_commit_generation`/`segment_infos::read_latest`). That does make the split genuinely meaningful, not cosmetic: after `prepare_commit()` returns, the new segment's data files are durably on disk and synced, but no `segments_N` references them yet, so a fresh `IndexWriter::open`/reader against the same directory still sees only the previous commit. But `prepared_commit` lives purely in the live `IndexWriter` value's memory -- if the process crashes (or the value is dropped) between `prepare_commit()` and `finish_commit()`, that prepared state is gone with no on-disk trace to recover, discover, or roll forward; the orphaned segment files are just inert bytes no `segments_N` ever points at. So: real caller-visible durability/visibility split, yes; crash-survivable two-phase commit or cross-process/cross-restart handoff, no. `finish_commit()` without a preceding `prepare_commit()` (or called a second time) returns `Error::NoPreparedCommit` rather than silently no-opping. New tests: `prepare_commit()` + `finish_commit()` produces byte-identical on-disk results to calling `commit()` directly (compared against two independent directories fed the same docs), including confirming the prepared generation is invisible to a fresh reader until `finish_commit()` runs; `prepare_commit()` alone (simulating a crash before activation) leaves the previous commit as the only one a fresh `read_latest`/reopened writer sees; `finish_commit()` with no prior `prepare_commit()`, and a second `finish_commit()` right after a successful one, both return `Error::NoPreparedCommit`; and a second `prepare_commit()` before `finish_commit()` replaces the pending prepared state rather than stacking. **Update (FFI exposure):** `open`/`add_document`/`commit`/`prepare_commit`/`finish_commit`/`rollback`/`set_merge_policy` are now reachable over the C ABI too -- see the `lucene-ffi/src/writer.rs` row below for the exact wire shape and what is not exposed. |
| `lucene-ffi` C-ABI wrapper over `IndexWriter` (IndexWriter commit/merge-policy/postings/term-vector/doc-values/update/delete FFI exposure) | `lucene-ffi/src/writer.rs::{ffi_open_writer, ffi_writer_add_document, ffi_writer_commit, ffi_writer_prepare_commit, ffi_writer_finish_commit, ffi_writer_rollback, ffi_writer_set_merge_policy, ffi_writer_set_postings_field, ffi_writer_set_term_vector_field, ffi_writer_set_doc_values_field, ffi_writer_update_document, ffi_writer_delete_documents, ffi_writer_segment_infos_len, ffi_writer_segment_info_name, ffi_writer_pending_doc_count, ffi_close_writer}` | Wraps seven `IndexWriter` methods behind a new opaque handle (`registry::WriterHandle`, `handle::RegistryTag::Writer`), same `guard`/`catch_unwind`/last-error/handle-validation conventions every other module in this crate already follows -- no write-side logic reimplemented. `ffi_open_writer` takes a filesystem path plus a caller's field list as five parallel arrays (name, number, `IndexOptions` ordinal, `DocValuesType` ordinal, store-term-vectors flag); `ffi_writer_add_document` takes one document's fields as four parallel arrays, with a `kind` byte per field selecting how its raw bytes decode (string/binary/i32/i64/f32/f64). Because `IndexWriter<'d>` borrows `&'d dyn Directory` and there is no owned/`'static` `IndexWriter` type, `WriterHandle` owns a heap-boxed `FsDirectory` alongside the writer and builds the writer's borrow against that stable heap address via one contained, documented `unsafe` block (`writer.rs::open_writer_handle`) -- sound because struct field declaration order guarantees the borrowing `writer` field drops before the owning `dir` field ever does. `WriterHandle` also needed explicit (documented) `unsafe impl Send/Sync`, since a bare `&dyn Directory` carries no auto-trait bound the compiler can see on its own, even though this crate's `Mutex`-guarded, one-thread-at-a-time access pattern makes both sound. `SlotMap::get_mut` -- previously `#[cfg(test)]`-only, since every earlier handle type was immutable once inserted -- is now a real (non-test) part of the crate's handle API, since a writer handle's whole point is in-place mutation across calls. **Update (postings/term-vector/doc-values FFI exposure):** `ffi_writer_set_postings_field`/`ffi_writer_set_term_vector_field`/`ffi_writer_set_doc_values_field` now wrap `IndexWriter::set_postings_field`/`set_term_vector_field`/`set_doc_values_field` too, one C function per setter, each taking an `enabled` flag (mirroring `ffi_writer_set_merge_policy`'s own `enabled == 0` -> `None` convention) plus a `(field_name, field_name_len)` pair decoded via this crate's existing `str_from_raw`; `enabled == 0` clears the setting (`None`), ignoring the name/length arguments. Caller-input errors these three can now surface (`UnknownPostingsField`/`UnsupportedPostingsIndexOptions`/`UnknownTermVectorField`/`UnsupportedTermVectorField`/`UnknownDocValuesField`/`UnsupportedDocValuesType`/`MissingDenseDocValue`/`NonNumericDocValue`/`NonBinaryDocValue`) all map to `FfiStatus::InvalidArgument`, extending `map_writer_error`'s existing status-mapping table. Tests: unknown-handle rejection and a disabled (`enabled == 0`) no-op for each of the three, an unknown-field-name rejection for each, and one real end-to-end test per setter (`set_postings_field_end_to_end_writes_readable_postings`, `set_term_vector_field_end_to_end_writes_readable_term_vectors`, `set_doc_values_field_end_to_end_writes_readable_numeric_values`) that opts a field in over FFI, adds documents and commits over FFI, then reads the resulting segment back Rust-side through this crate's own unmodified read side (`lucene_codecs::blocktree`/`postings`, `lucene_codecs::term_vectors::open`, `lucene_codecs::doc_values::parse_meta`/`numeric_value` respectively) to prove the field was genuinely written, not just that the FFI call returned `Ok`. **Update (update_document/delete_documents FFI exposure):** `ffi_writer_update_document`/`ffi_writer_delete_documents` now wrap `IndexWriter::update_document`/`delete_documents`. Both take `(field_name, field_name_len, term_ptr, term_len)` identifying the delete term as raw, already-analyzed bytes (no analysis happens at this FFI boundary, same stance as `query.rs`'s own raw-bytes terms); `ffi_writer_update_document` additionally takes the replacement document's fields via the same four parallel arrays/`kind` byte convention `ffi_writer_add_document` already uses. Neither is buffered -- both commit immediately on success, matching `IndexWriter::update_document`/`delete_documents`'s own atomicity. Since `SegmentDeleteSource` requires an opened `BlockTreeFields`/`DocInput` per segment (`update_document.rs`'s own scope: only segments the caller supplies an opened source for are considered), this FFI layer builds that itself: a new `writer.rs::open_all_segment_sources` reopens every one of the writer's currently-committed segments that has a `.tim` file on disk (i.e. was flushed with `ffi_writer_set_postings_field` enabled at that commit), plus its `.liv` if one exists; a segment with no `.tim` file is skipped, not errored, matching `SegmentDeleteSource`'s own "unlisted segment left untouched" contract. `IndexWriter` gained two small read-only accessors, `dir()`/`fields()`, so this FFI-side helper can reopen those files and know the field schema to decode postings against, without either becoming part of the writer's mutable surface. Tests: unknown-handle and null-field-name rejection for both, a real end-to-end `ffi_writer_update_document` test (add two docs with real postings on `id`, commit, update one by term over FFI, then read every live doc back through this crate's own unmodified `stored_fields`/`live_docs` read side to confirm the old doc is gone and the new one present), a real end-to-end `ffi_writer_delete_documents` test (same shape, proving only the matching doc is removed), and a no-postings-segment no-op test (deleting against a writer whose only segment was flushed stored-only leaves `del_count` at `0`, proving the "skip, don't error" contract). **Update (segment_infos/pending_doc_count introspection FFI exposure):** `ffi_writer_segment_infos_len`/`ffi_writer_segment_info_name` now wrap `IndexWriter::segment_infos` (length-then-per-index-name accessor, the same "length first" shape `results_fragments.rs`'s `ffi_fragment_results_len`/`ffi_fragment_result_text` already established), and `ffi_writer_pending_doc_count` wraps `IndexWriter::pending_doc_count`. Both are read-only, infallible aside from handle/index/buffer validation. Tests: unknown-handle rejection and null-out-pointer rejection for all three, an out-of-bounds segment index, a too-small name buffer (`BufferTooSmall`, nothing written), and one end-to-end test (`segment_infos_and_pending_doc_count_reflect_writer_state_across_commits`) confirming 0 segments/0 pending on a fresh writer, 2 pending after two buffered `add_document` calls with 0 segments before any commit, 1 segment named `_0`/0 pending right after the first commit, and 2 segments after a second commit. **Still deliberately not exposed, tracked here rather than silently missing:** `IndexWriter::apply_merge` has no FFI wrapper. `apply_merge` only makes sense once a caller has already run `merge::merge_stored_only_segments` to produce the `SegmentCommitInfo` it folds in, and this crate exposes no FFI surface to run that merge (merging today only ever happens automatically, inside `commit()`, via `ffi_writer_set_merge_policy`) -- wrapping `apply_merge` alone would be a bookkeeping-only call a JVM caller could never actually drive. Manual merge execution FFI (and `apply_merge` alongside it) is left as a separate, larger task. `ffi_open_writer`'s field-schema wire format is deliberately minimal: every `FieldInfo` flag beyond name/number/index-options/doc-values-type/store-term-vectors (`omit_norms`, `store_payloads`, `soft_deletes_field`, `parent_field`, points/vector dimensions) is fixed at its off/default value, since this task's field list only needs to support stored-fields-only documents. `ffi_writer_set_merge_policy` exposes the five knobs `lucene_index::merge_policy::MergePolicyConfig` has today (`max_merge_at_once`, `segments_per_tier`, `max_merged_segment_size`, `reclaim_weight`, and now `floor_segment_size`, real `floorSegmentMB`'s equivalent, default 16MB) -- `floor_segment_size` was added as a new trailing parameter, a direct signature break with all three in-repo call sites updated (no existing versioned-FFI-export convention in this crate to justify a defaulted overload instead). `forceMergeDeletesPctAllowed` is still not invented here, since this port's `find_forced_merges` has no deletion-percentage-aware `FORCE_MERGE_DELETES`-equivalent merge type for that knob to configure. Tests: null-pointer rejection (`open_writer_null_out_handle_is_null_pointer_error`, `open_writer_null_field_array_with_nonzero_count_is_null_pointer_error`, `add_document_null_array_with_nonzero_count_is_null_pointer_error`), invalid-UTF-8 path rejection, out-of-range enum-ordinal rejection, invalid/unknown-handle rejection for every one of the eight functions, double-close rejection, a cross-registry rejection (a directory handle passed to a writer function), and a real end-to-end test (`open_add_commit_end_to_end_produces_a_readable_segment`) that opens a writer over FFI, adds documents over FFI, commits over FFI, then reopens the same on-disk directory Rust-side (`segment_infos::read_latest` + `lucene_codecs::stored_fields::open`, bypassing the FFI writer handle entirely) and reads every document back to confirm the commit is genuinely valid and queryable, not just `Ok`-returning. Two more end-to-end tests cover the two-phase commit split and the merge-policy convergence behavior the same way. |

## lucene-search

| Java | Rust | Status |
|---|---|---|
| `search/TermQuery` (matching + BM25 scoring) | `lucene-search/src/query.rs::TermQuery`, `lucene-search/src/lib.rs::{search_term_query, search_term_query_scored}` | **ported.** Plain `{ field, term }` struct ŌĆö no `TermStates`/cross-segment stats attached (nothing to reuse them for yet). `search_term_query` (matching only) is unchanged; `search_term_query_scored` is its new scored sibling (task #13): same field/term/`live_docs` handling, additionally reading each matched doc's `freq` and computing a BM25 score via `similarity::score` (see that module's row for the norms/avg-field-length approximation every score here inherits) into a [`ScoringCollector`]. **Verified against real Lucene**: `crates/lucene-search/tests/scoring_fixtures.rs` scores the real `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` segment and asserts (a) the scored doc set exactly equals the already-fixture-verified unscored doc set, (b) `TopDocsCollector` output is correctly ordered (score descending, doc ID ascending on ties), and (c) every score matches a BM25 formula reimplemented independently in the test file from the segment's real `docFreq`/`doc_count`/per-doc `freq` ŌĆö not real-Lucene score equality (deferred, see the norms gap above), but full internal-consistency and formula-fidelity verification against real postings data. |
| `index/DocumentsWriterPerThread.flush` + `IndexWriter.commit` (minimal, no-merge multi-segment slice) | `lucene-index/src/segment_writer.rs::flush_stored_only_segment` | **ported, deliberately minimal.** `flush_stored_only_segment` takes an in-memory `Vec<Document>` + `Vec<FieldInfo>` and writes one brand-new stored-fields-only segment (`.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm`/`.fnm`/`.si`, all synced through a real `Directory`), returning the `SegmentCommitInfo` to push into `SegmentInfos::segments`. Calling it more than once against the same `Directory` with distinct segment names/ids and passing all the resulting `SegmentCommitInfo`s to one `segment_infos::write` call produces a single commit describing multiple, independently-flushed segments -- proven by `crates/lucene-index/examples/write_multi_segment_commit_fixture.rs` (two flushes, `_0` with 2 docs + `_1` with 3 docs, one `segments_N`) opened via real `DirectoryReader.open` + `fixtures/src/VerifySegmentInfos.java` (unchanged from the single-segment case -- it was already segment-count-agnostic, and passed first try: `DirectoryReader.open` correctly federates the two Rust-written segments into one 5-doc space). Note `segment_infos::write`/`parse` needed **no changes** for this: `SegmentInfos::segments` was already `Vec<SegmentCommitInfo>` with a plain loop on both the encode and decode side, so describing N segments in one commit was already mechanical; the actual gap this closes is the reusable "flush one batch of documents to one new segment" building block (previously hand-duplicated per fixture example -- `write_segment_infos_fixture.rs` now calls this same function instead of inlining its own copy). **Deliberately not implemented, out of scope for this slice** (see the module doc for the full list): no RAM accounting/automatic flush-triggering, no merging (`TieredMergePolicy`/`ConcurrentMergeScheduler`), no deletes/updates during indexing (`BufferedUpdates`), no NRT reopen, no concurrent `DocumentsWriterPerThread`-per-thread pooling, and -- same constraint as the single-segment fixture below -- every field is stored-only, since there is still no write-side postings/doc-values/points/vectors format. **Compound-file packing (task #38):** `flush_stored_only_segment` now takes a `use_compound_file: bool`. `false` (unchanged) writes the four files loose; `true` packs those same already-complete codec files through `compound_format::write` (task above) into `<name>.cfs`/`.cfe` instead and sets `SegmentInfo.is_compound_file: true` in the `.si`. Real Lucene's `IndexWriter` decides this per-flush via `TieredMergePolicy`'s size-based `noCFSRatio`/`maxCFSSegmentSizeMB` heuristic; this port has no merge policy or segment-size accounting at all yet (`PLAN.md` Phase 5 item 6), so rather than fake a heuristic with nothing real behind it, the caller decides directly with a plain boolean -- `update_document.rs` passes `false`, keeping its existing commits' on-disk shape unchanged. No new Java fixture needed since `compound_format`'s codec itself is already differentially verified (see its row above); this task is Rust-side composition, verified end-to-end by a unit test that flushes with `use_compound_file: true`, recovers the `.fnm`/`.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm` bytes *through* `compound_format::parse_entries`/`open_input` (not the original in-memory buffers), and confirms both `field_infos::parse` and `stored_fields::open`/`.document()` still work reading through those recovered slices, plus a regression test confirming `.si`/loose-file output for `use_compound_file: false` is unchanged (`.cfs`/`.cfe` files absent, `.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm`/`.fnm` present) |
| `index/SegmentMerger` | `lucene-index/src/merge.rs::merge_stored_only_segments` | **ported, scoped to exactly what's mergeable today.** Merges N already-flushed segments into one new segment: reads each source's `FieldInfos` (`field_infos::parse`) and `Document`s back out (`stored_fields::open` + `.document()`), drops non-live docs per an optional per-source `FixedBitSet` (`live_docs::parse`), reconciles field numbering across sources by field name (`reconcile_field_numbers`), renumbers surviving docs contiguously by concatenating sources in source order, and writes `.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm`/`.fnm`/`.si`. **Field-number reconciliation**: does the numbering half only (first-seen-across-sources order, one merged `FieldInfo` per distinct name using the first source's metadata) and skips real Lucene's `verifySameSchema` check. **Edge cases**: a source with no `live_docs` is treated as fully live; a fully-deleted source contributes zero docs (merged anyway rather than requiring the caller to pre-filter). Now also merges doc values (NUMERIC, BINARY, SORTED, SORTED_NUMERIC, and SORTED_SET), norms, term vectors, postings, and BKD points, if a caller supplies them per source (`MergeSource::numeric_doc_values`/`binary_doc_values`/`sorted_doc_values`/`sorted_numeric_doc_values`/`sorted_set_doc_values`/`norms`/`term_vectors`/`postings`/`points`, all optional): decodes each source's per-doc data via the existing read-side decoders (`doc_values::numeric_value`, `doc_values::binary_value`, `doc_values::sorted_ord` + `terms_dict::decode_all_terms`, `doc_values::sorted_numeric_values`, and (for SORTED_SET) the same per-value ordinal-to-bytes resolution generalized across `SortedSetKind::Single`/`Multi`, `norms::norm_value`, `term_vectors::TermVectorsReader::document`), drops non-live docs and renumbers contiguously the same way stored fields are, remaps field numbers through the same reconciliation, and re-encodes via the existing single-field write-side encoders (`doc_values::write_single_dense_numeric_field`, `doc_values::write_single_dense_binary_field`, `doc_values::write_single_dense_sorted_field`, `doc_values::write_single_dense_sorted_numeric_field`, `doc_values::write_single_dense_sorted_set_field`, `norms::write_single_dense_field`, `term_vectors::write_best_speed`), writing whichever of `.dvm`/`.dvd`/`.dvs`, `.nvm`/`.nvd`, `.tvd`/`.tvx`/`.tvm` result. **SORTED doc-values merging (`merge_sorted_doc_values`)**: unlike NUMERIC/BINARY, a SORTED field can't be merged by simple concatenation -- each source's term dictionary is built independently, so ordinal `N` in one source's dictionary is generally a *different term* than ordinal `N` in another's (real Lucene's `OrdinalMap` exists to solve exactly this). This port sidesteps building an explicit ordinal-remapping table: for each live doc it resolves that doc's own source's ordinal straight to term bytes (via that source's own `terms_dict::decode_all_terms`), then hands the merge's full per-doc *term-bytes* list to `doc_values::write_single_dense_sorted_field`, which rebuilds the merged, deduplicated, sorted dictionary itself -- so two sources' docs sharing a term land on the same merged dictionary entry purely because the merged dictionary is deduplicated by term bytes, not by ordinal. **SORTED_NUMERIC doc-values merging (`merge_sorted_numeric_doc_values`)**: no shared dictionary to reconcile at all -- each live doc simply contributes its own `Vec<i64>` of values (whatever order/count the source has), concatenated across sources exactly like `merge_numeric_doc_values` generalized from one value per doc to a list per doc. **SORTED_SET doc-values merging (`merge_sorted_set_doc_values`)**: multi-valued SORTED, so it reuses `merge_sorted_doc_values`'s exact resolve-to-bytes-and-let-the-writer-dedupe approach, per-value instead of per-doc -- each of a live doc's own source's ordinals (resolved uniformly whether that source's own entry collapsed to `SortedSetKind::Single` or stayed `Multi`) are turned into term bytes via that source's own dictionary, producing a `Vec<Vec<u8>>` per doc that `doc_values::write_single_dense_sorted_set_field` deduplicates into the merged dictionary itself, same no-remapping-table-to-get-wrong property as SORTED. **Scope of the doc-values/norms merge**: since the underlying write-side encoders only support one field per `.dvd`/`.nvd` file (no multi-field container yet), at most one numeric-doc-values field, at most one BINARY-doc-values field, at most one SORTED-doc-values field, at most one SORTED_NUMERIC-doc-values field, at most one SORTED_SET-doc-values field, and at most one norms field may be merged per call (`Error::TooManyNumericDocValuesFields`/`TooManyBinaryDocValuesFields`/`TooManySortedDocValuesFields`/`TooManySortedNumericDocValuesFields`/`TooManySortedSetDocValuesFields`/`TooManyNormsFields` otherwise) -- and since numeric, BINARY, SORTED, SORTED_NUMERIC, and SORTED_SET all land on the same `.dvm`/`.dvd`/`.dvs` extensions, merging more than one of those five doc-values types in the same call is also rejected (`Error::MultipleDocValuesTypesInOneMerge`); term vectors have no such per-call field-count limit, but do have a per-field content limit -- see below. **Sparse-across-sources rule**: a doc-values/norms field can only be merged if every source contributing at least one live doc supplies decodable, fully-dense data for that field (matches the write-side encoders' dense-only requirement) -- a source missing the field, or only sparsely populating it, is `Error::DocValuesFieldMissingInSource`/`BinaryDocValuesFieldMissingInSource`/`SortedDocValuesFieldMissingInSource`/`SortedNumericDocValuesFieldMissingInSource`/`SortedSetDocValuesFieldMissingInSource`/`NormsFieldMissingInSource` rather than a silent drop; for SORTED_NUMERIC/SORTED_SET this also covers a live doc whose resolved value list/set comes back empty, since the write-side encoders require every doc to have at least one value. Term vectors have no such constraint: a source with no term-vectors reader, or a doc with none, contributes an empty `TermVectorsDocument`. **Term-vectors content scope**: the read side (`TermVectorsReader::document`) fully decodes positions, offsets, and payloads when a source has them, and the write side (`term_vectors::write_best_speed`) now supports all three too (a later task lifted its earlier positions-only restriction -- see that row above). The remaining gap is entirely on the merge side: `merge_term_vectors`'s own field-combination logic across sources for offsets/payloads has not been reviewed for correctness, so it validates every source's term-vector fields up front and returns `Error::TermVectorOffsetsOrPayloadsNotSupported` for any field with offsets or payloads rather than merging data whose correctness hasn't been checked; positions-only term vectors (with or without positions at all) merge and round-trip correctly. **Postings merging (`merge_postings`)**: each source's term dictionary is independent (same reason SORTED doc values needs the ordinal-avoidance trick above), so this resolves each contributing source's own terms straight to bytes via that source's already-opened `blocktree::FieldTerms`, unions those bytes across sources into one sorted term set, and for each term concatenates every contributing source's `(mergedDocId, freq)` pairs in source order -- ascending overall for free, since merged doc ids occupy disjoint, increasing per-source ranges (`build_doc_id_maps`). Re-encoded via `postings_writer::write_fields`, which (unlike the doc-values/norms writers) already accepts any number of fields per call, so there is no single-field-per-merge-call limit for postings. Scoped to `IndexOptions::Docs`/`DocsAndFreqs` only -- a field whose merged `index_options` indexes positions is rejected with `Error::PostingsIndexOptionsNotSupported` rather than silently dropping positions/offsets/payloads data; merging those is a documented follow-up, not implemented here. Because field-number reconciliation only records the first-seen source's `FieldInfo` as the merged one and never checks agreement across sources sharing a field name, every other live-doc-contributing source's own `index_options` for that field is independently checked against the merged choice (`Error::PostingsIndexOptionsDisagreement`) -- otherwise a source with positions could have them silently dropped whenever an earlier, positions-free source happened to be picked as canonical. Same sparse-across-sources philosophy as doc values/norms applies at the field level (a source missing the postings field entirely while another live-doc-contributing source has it is `Error::PostingsFieldMissingInSource`) -- ordinary per-doc/per-term sparsity within a field is not an error, since that is exactly what a term dictionary already models. **Points merging (`merge_points`)**: a BKD points field has no shared dictionary to reconcile at all, unlike SORTED doc values or postings -- it's a flat, per-doc set of fixed-width packed values, closer in spirit to SORTED_NUMERIC doc values. This reads back every live doc's points via that source's own already-opened `points::PointsReader` (the *exact same* reader `lucene-search`'s `points_query::search_points_range` already uses -- no new BKD decode logic was written for this merge), drops non-live docs and remaps surviving doc ids to the merged id space via `build_doc_id_maps` (the same mechanism `merge_postings` uses), and concatenates the results across sources in source order; `points::write` rebuilds the merged BKD tree (leaf plan, packed index, bounding boxes) from that flat list itself, so there's no tree-merging logic to get wrong here. Like postings and unlike doc-values/norms, `points::write` already accepts any number of fields per call, so there is no single-field-per-merge-call limit for points. A merged field with points data in at least one live-doc-contributing source but not in every such source is `Error::PointsFieldMissingInSource`, matching the sparse-across-sources philosophy applied everywhere else -- but a field has no per-doc denseness requirement of its own here (a live doc contributing zero points for a field is not an error, and a field that ends up with zero points overall after the merge is simply omitted, matching `points::write`'s own `EmptyField` restriction and real Lucene's `finish()` returning `null` in that case). **Scope**: `points::write` supports `num_index_dims <= num_dims` (data-only, non-indexed trailing dimensions), and this merge preserves that -- every point's full `num_dims`-wide packed value round-trips through the merge unchanged. Because field-number reconciliation only records the first-seen source's `FieldInfo`, every other live-doc-contributing source's own BKD tree shape (`num_dims`/`bytes_per_dim`/`num_index_dims`, from that source's own `PointsField`) is independently checked against the merged field's declared shape and rejected with `Error::PointsShapeDisagreement` (for `num_dims`/`bytes_per_dim`) or `Error::PointsIndexDimsDisagreement` (for `num_index_dims`) on a mismatch. Multi-dimension points (e.g. `LatLonPoint`-shaped 2D fields) and multi-valued points (multiple points per doc for the same field) are both supported -- this is exactly what `points::write` already handles, and the concatenation this merge performs preserves both.

**Important caveat**: this port's only write-side path that produces a full segment, `segment_writer::flush_stored_only_segment`, still only ever writes stored-fields-only segments -- nothing in this port's normal flush path produces doc values/norms/term vectors/postings/points yet, so this merge logic is exercised only by its own unit/round-trip tests supplying synthetic per-source data, not by a real "flush two segments, then merge them" scenario. Unit-tested: field-number reconciliation in isolation; stored-fields merging (two segments no deletions, some docs deleted in each, a fully-deleted source, mismatched field numbers reconciled end-to-end through a re-parsed `.fnm`, zero sources, a real `.liv` round trip); numeric doc values, BINARY doc values, SORTED doc values, SORTED_NUMERIC doc values, SORTED_SET doc values, norms, and term vectors each merged in isolation (two sources, deletions, a source missing the field/reader entirely); a hand-built term-vectors source with POSITIONS+OFFSETS+PAYLOADS being rejected with `Error::TermVectorOffsetsOrPayloadsNotSupported` instead of reaching `write_best_speed`'s assert; SORTED-specific correctness tests -- overlapping term dictionaries across sources dedupe into one shared dictionary entry (not two), disjoint term dictionaries produce a merged dictionary containing every term from both sources, and every doc's merged term is resolved back through the unmodified reader stack (`parse_meta` + `sorted_ord` + `terms_dict::decode_all_terms`) and checked against the actual expected term bytes, not just "some valid ordinal"; SORTED_NUMERIC-specific: a multi-value doc keeps both its values (not just one) after merge; SORTED_SET-specific: the same overlapping-dictionary and disjoint-dictionary correctness tests as SORTED, but per multi-valued doc (a doc in one source with `["red","blue"]` and a doc in another with `["red","green"]` dedupe into a 3-entry shared dictionary, with each doc's full resolved value *set* checked, not just dictionary size); the too-many-fields and missing-in-a-live-source error paths for all five doc-values types, plus the multiple-doc-values-types-at-once error path for the numeric+BINARY and SORTED_NUMERIC+SORTED_SET pairs specifically (not all ~10 possible pairs); postings-specific: two sources with no deletions merging correctly (verified by reopening the merged `.tim`/`.tip`/`.tmd`/`.doc` through the unmodified `blocktree`/`postings::DocInput` reader and checking actual doc ids/freqs, not just "some valid output"), a term shared by both sources merging its postings in ascending merged-doc-id order, deletions dropping a doc's terms from the merge, a fully-deleted source contributing nothing, the missing-in-a-live-source error, the positions-indexed-field-rejected-as-out-of-scope error, and a source disagreeing with the merged field's `index_options` (positions vs. Docs/DocsAndFreqs) being rejected rather than silently dropped; points-specific: two sources with no deletions merging correctly (verified by reopening the merged `.kdm`/`.kdi`/`.kdd` through the unmodified `points::PointsReader` and checking actual doc ids/packed values, plus a full round trip through the unmodified `points_delete::resolve_points_range_doc_ids` range resolver), deletions dropping non-live docs from the merged points, a fully-deleted source contributing nothing, the missing-in-a-live-source error, a cross-source BKD-shape-disagreement error (one source's own points data using a different `bytes_per_dim` than the merged field's declared shape), two sources with consistent `num_index_dims < num_dims` (a `LatLonShape`-style bounding box shape) merging correctly with every point's full packed value -- including the non-indexed trailing dimension -- preserved, and a cross-source `num_index_dims` disagreement (same `num_dims`/`bytes_per_dim`, different `num_index_dims`) being rejected with `Error::PointsIndexDimsDisagreement`; and full round-trip tests -- stored fields + NUMERIC doc values + norms + term vectors, stored fields + BINARY doc values + norms + term vectors, and stored fields + SORTED doc values (with an overlapping term across sources) + norms + term vectors, each together in one call -- via real `Directory` I/O, verified by reading back every format through this port's own readers, including checking the `.si` file lists every written file. **Deliberately not implemented**: no merge *policy* (`TieredMergePolicy`-style "which segments, when" -- the caller picks sources), no background/concurrent merging, no merge-time codec upgrade, no multi-field `.dvd`/`.nvd` support, and no offsets/payloads-term-vectors merging (rejected explicitly with `Error::TermVectorOffsetsOrPayloadsNotSupported` -- see the term-vectors paragraph above), and postings merging is scoped to `IndexOptions::Docs`/`DocsAndFreqs` only (no positions/offsets/payloads -- see the postings paragraph above), and points merging supports `num_index_dims <= num_dims` but requires it to be consistent across all merged sources (see the points paragraph above) |
| `index/TieredMergePolicy.findMerges`/`findForcedMerges` (merge-set decision, not execution/scheduling) | `lucene-index/src/merge_policy.rs::{find_merges, find_forced_merges}` | **ported (task #47), a simplified but real-shaped scoring/selection algorithm, not naive size-only bin-packing and not a byte-for-byte port of real Lucene's own (considerably more complex) algorithm.** Decides which currently-existing segments should merge next; execution stays `merge.rs`'s job (its own doc comment already flagged "not a merge policy" as out of scope -- this closes that gap), and background/concurrent scheduling (`MergeScheduler`) remains untouched. **New `SegmentStat` type, not `SegmentCommitInfo` directly**: `SegmentCommitInfo` (`segments_N`) carries `del_count` but not doc count or byte size -- those live in the separate per-segment `.si` file (`segment_info::SegmentInfo`); `SegmentStat` (name/doc_count/del_count/size_bytes) is the minimal shape the algorithm needs, built from either. **Size-unit decision**: real `TieredMergePolicy` sizes segments by on-disk byte size (`segBytes`); this port provides `segment_byte_size(dir, info)`, which sums real file lengths for a segment's `.si`-listed files through the existing `Directory` trait (no new trait method needed) for the honest, byte-accurate case, and `SegmentStat::from_segment_info` as a documented doc-count approximation for callers without a `Directory` handy -- the algorithm itself is unit-agnostic, it only needs a monotonic comparable size. **Kept real-shaped**: already-oversized segments (>= `max_merged_segment_size`) excluded from further merge input; a reclaim-weighted score (`size * (1 - reclaim_weight * del_count/doc_count)`) so a heavily-deleted segment is preferred over an equally-sized clean one, matching real Lucene's intent of favoring merges that reclaim deleted space; a `segments_per_tier` target suppressing merges once segment count is already at/below it; a `max_merge_at_once` cap no proposed group ever exceeds; smaller/more-deleted segments preferred by sorting before grouping. **Simplified/dropped, explicitly**: real Lucene's exact `MergeScore` (log-based skew penalty, floor/ceiling tier smoothing, iterative multi-candidate search with rollback) replaced by one simpler score; one greedy grouping pass instead of an iterative multi-merge search; no compound-file awareness; `find_forced_merges` merges the excess down to a target count in a single group rather than real Lucene's own chunked multi-pass forced-merge walk. `MergePolicyConfig` defaults mirror real `TieredMergePolicy`'s (`maxMergeAtOnce=10`, `segmentsPerTier=10`, `maxMergedSegmentMB=5000`, and now `floorSegmentMB=16`). **`floorSegmentMB` (follow-up)**: `MergePolicyConfig.floor_segment_size` now ports real Lucene's `floorSegmentBytes`/`setFloorSegmentMB` (default `16 * 1024 * 1024`) -- wired into `find_merges`' scoring at the same point real Lucene's own `floorSize(bytes)` helper (`Math.max(floorSegmentBytes, bytes)`) is called, clamping a segment's size up (for scoring only, not eligibility or real merge byte accounting) before the reclaim discount is applied, so a pile of genuinely tiny segments isn't scored as disproportionately "cheap" relative to one another. **`forceMergeDeletesPctAllowed` (follow-up)**: now ported too, alongside a new `find_forced_delete_merges` function -- real Lucene's `TieredMergePolicy.findForcedDeletesMerges`-equivalent, the deletion-percentage-aware merge type the earlier `floorSegmentMB` task noted this port didn't yet have anywhere to plug that knob into. Unlike `find_merges`/`find_forced_merges`, it selects segments purely by `pctDeletes = 100.0 * del_count / doc_count` exceeding `MergePolicyConfig.force_merge_deletes_pct_allowed` (default `10.0`, matching Java's `TieredMergePolicy.forceMergeDeletesPctAllowed`) -- strictly greater, matching Java's own `pctDeletes <= forceMergeDeletesPctAllowed` skip condition inverted; a lone qualifying segment is still returned as its own group of size 1 (real Lucene rewrites even a single heavily-deleted segment to reclaim space), unlike the size-`>= 2` grouping `find_merges`/`find_forced_merges` use. Tested: mixed over/under-threshold segments, an exact-boundary segment (excluded, not included), zero-deletions (selects nothing), a single qualifying segment among clean ones, and the default value itself. **Not wired into `IndexWriter`** -- `find_forced_merges` itself isn't wired there either, so this stayed scoped to the policy primitive, consistent with that precedent. **Closing the loop with `merge.rs`**: `lucene-index/tests/merge_policy_to_merge_integration.rs` flushes three real stored-fields-only segments, has `find_merges` pick all three, and feeds that exact chosen name group into `merge::merge_stored_only_segments` (re-reading each segment's files off disk by name), confirming the merged segment holds all six docs -- proves the decide/execute handoff has no shape mismatch, without building a full automatic merge-triggering pipeline (real `IndexWriter`/`MergeScheduler` integration remains out of scope). This is a pure heuristic decision function, not new byte-format decoding, so no Java fixture applies -- correctness here means matching the documented simplified rules, verified by direct unit tests (many-small-segments proposes a merge, oversized segment excluded, high-del-ratio preferred over equal-size low-del-ratio, already-optimal segment count proposes nothing, `max_merge_at_once` cap respected, and, for the floor: `floor_segment_size_changes_selection_among_many_tiny_segments` and `floor_segment_size_does_not_affect_oversized_segment_exclusion`). |
| `index/IndexWriter` deletes (doc-ID-level mechanics, plus single-segment delete-by-term resolution) | `lucene-index/src/deletes.rs::{mark_deleted, apply_deletes}`, `lucene-index/src/term_delete.rs::{resolve_term_doc_ids, resolve_and_apply_term_delete}` | **ported: doc-ID-level apply mechanics (task #16) plus single-segment delete-by-term resolution (task #27).** Real Lucene's delete path is two halves: (1) `BufferedUpdates`/`ReaderPool` resolve *which* doc IDs a `deleteDocuments(Term/Query)` call names, per segment, by running the query against that segment's live postings/doc-values reader; (2) `ReadersAndUpdates.writeLiveDocs` takes the resolved doc IDs and turns them into an updated live-docs bitset, a new `.liv` file, and a bumped `delGen`/`delCount`. `deletes.rs` is half (2): `mark_deleted` clears the given doc IDs out of a `FixedBitSet` (starting from "all live" when the segment has no deletions yet, i.e. `del_gen == -1`, or from an existing bitset otherwise), returning the updated bitset plus a count of *newly* deleted docs (already-deleted doc IDs are idempotent, not double-counted); `apply_deletes` wraps that around a `SegmentCommitInfo`, writing the result via the existing `live_docs::write` to a **newly established filename convention** (`liv_file_name`: `_<segment>_<delGen in base36>.liv`, matching real Lucene's `IndexFileNames.fileNameFromGeneration(segment, "liv", delGen)`) and returning a new `SegmentCommitInfo` with `del_gen` incremented (`-1` -> `1` on first delete, else `+1`, matching `SegmentCommitInfo.getNextDelGen()`) and `del_count` increased by the newly-deleted count. Out-of-range doc IDs are a hard `Err`, never a silent no-op or a panic. `term_delete.rs` is (part of) half (1), **scoped to exactly one already-opened segment**: `resolve_term_doc_ids` takes that segment's `BlockTreeFields` + opened `.doc` file + a `(field, term)` pair and returns the matching live doc IDs ascending -- an unknown field or an absent term yields an empty `Vec`, not an error, matching `TermQuery.createWeight`'s `null`-`Scorer` "no matches" outcome. This reimplements the same lookup `lucene-search::term_doc_ids` already does (`field.postings(term, doc_in)` filtered by `live_docs`) directly against `lucene-codecs` primitives (`BlockTreeFields`, `DocInput`) rather than depending on `lucene-search` from `lucene-index`: the intended dependency graph is `util ŌåÉ store ŌåÉ codecs ŌåÉ index ŌåÉ search ŌåÉ core ŌåÉ ffi`, and `lucene-search` already depends on `lucene-index`, so the reverse edge would invert it into a cycle -- since every primitive the lookup needs already lives in `lucene-codecs`, which `lucene-index` depends on directly, reimplementing the handful of lines there avoids both the cycle and a speculative new shared-primitive extraction in `lucene-codecs`. `resolve_and_apply_term_delete` composes `resolve_term_doc_ids` with `apply_deletes` for the full per-segment resolve-then-apply flow, finally closing the "here's a term to delete" -> "here's the actual `mark_deleted`/`apply_deletes` call" gap for one segment. **Deliberately not implemented**: true multi-segment *resolution* (a real `IndexWriter`'s `BufferedUpdates`/`ReaderPool` opens and searches every currently-open segment's live postings reader itself; this port has no reader pool, so a caller of `update_document` ŌĆö see the row below ŌĆö still has to hand it whichever segments' `BlockTreeFields` it already has open) and delete-by-query beyond a single exact term. `updateDocument` itself is now implemented as an atomic wrapper ŌĆö see `lucene-index/src/update_document.rs` below ŌĆö fanning the per-segment delete-by-term resolution here out across a whole `SegmentInfos`'s segment list and committing it together with a new segment in one `segments_N` write. Unit-tested (`deletes.rs`): `mark_deleted` from an all-live (`None`) state, from an existing partially-deleted bitset, idempotent re-deletion of an already-deleted doc, boundary doc IDs (`0`, `max_doc-1`), out-of-range and negative doc IDs (both `Err`), empty doc-ID batch, plus full round-trip tests via a real `FsDirectory` (first delete round, second round incrementing `del_gen` and unioning with the first, re-deleting the same doc not double-counting, an out-of-range doc ID erroring without writing a file). 99.51% line coverage. Unit-tested (`term_delete.rs`), reusing the checked-in real-Lucene `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` fixture: `resolve_term_doc_ids` for a multi-doc term, a singleton term needing no `.doc` file, a missing term, a missing field, and `live_docs` filtering out an already-deleted doc; `resolve_and_apply_term_delete` end to end against a real `FsDirectory` (`del_gen`/`del_count`/`.liv` bytes all correct for the term's actual matching docs), deleting the same term twice across two rounds confirming `del_gen` increments without double-counting already-deleted docs, and a term with no matches producing a no-op round that still bumps `del_gen`. 98.78% line coverage. |
| `index/IndexWriter` delete-by-point-range resolution (BKD, single segment) | `lucene-index/src/points_delete.rs::{resolve_points_range_doc_ids, resolve_and_apply_points_range_delete}` | **ported (task #36).** The BKD-range analog of task #27's `term_delete.rs`, same two-halves split: `resolve_points_range_doc_ids` is (part of) half (1), scoped to one already-opened segment's `lucene_codecs::points::PointsReader` + one `field_number` + an inclusive `[min_packed, max_packed]` packed-byte range (`PointRangeQuery`'s own default `newRangeQuery` semantics) ŌĆö decodes every point via the existing `PointsReader::decode_all_points`, keeps only points where **every** dimension's slice independently satisfies `min[dim] <= value[dim] <= max[dim]` (unsigned byte-wise, matching `Arrays.compareUnsigned` and `PointRangeQuery.matches`), filters by `live_docs`, and returns the matching doc IDs ascending and deduplicated (a multi-valued point field can put more than one matching value on the same doc). An unknown `field_number` yields an empty `Vec`, not an error, same "no matches, not a caller bug" convention `term_delete` uses. `resolve_and_apply_points_range_delete` composes that with `deletes::apply_deletes`, the same resolve-then-apply shape as `resolve_and_apply_term_delete`. **Reused vs. newly written, stated plainly**: unlike delete-by-term, where `lucene-search::term_doc_ids` already existed and `term_delete.rs` just reimplemented its handful of lines locally (to avoid `lucene-index` depending back on `lucene-search` ŌĆö confirmed again here by reading both `Cargo.toml`s: `lucene-search` depends on `lucene-index`, not the reverse), **no BKD range-query matcher existed anywhere in the workspace to reuse**: `lucene-search`'s only range-shaped queries (`search_numeric_range`/`search_sorted_ord_range`/`search_multi_valued_range` in `doc_value_query.rs`) walk doc-values data, the "slow" `SortedNumericDocValuesField.newSlowRangeQuery` fallback path real Lucene uses when no BKD index exists ŌĆö not the BKD tree at all; and `lucene_codecs::points` has no intersection/pruning logic either, only the already-existing `PointsReader::decode_all_points` (decodes every point in a field unconditionally, see `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/points_fixtures.rs`). So this module's range-matching logic (`packed_value_in_range`) is genuinely new, reusing only `decode_all_points` as its data source ŌĆö a real, honest gap against real `BKDReader.intersect`'s tree-pruning traversal (which can skip whole leaves/subtrees the packed index proves are entirely in/out of range): this port's approach is `O(field's total point count)` per call, not sublinear, tracked here rather than hidden. **Cross-engine verification approach**: no new checked-in real-Lucene fixture ŌĆö the existing `fixtures/data/points_index/` fixture (task #18/#22, `GenPoints.java`) is single-dimension only, and this module's own tests need a hand-built 2D (`LatLonPoint`-shaped) fixture anyway to exercise the "every dimension independently in range" semantics that fixture can't reach; extending it with a new `Append*Manifest.java` would add Java-side machinery without covering anything the in-memory fixture (built via the existing, already real-Lucene-verified `points::write`/`points::open` round trip from task #18/#22) doesn't already cover byte-for-byte. Unit-tested: exact range match, inclusive boundaries on both ends, a zero-match range (no-op, empty `Vec`), a range matching every doc, an unknown field number, `live_docs` filtering an already-deleted doc out of the match set, a 2D multi-dimension field where one dimension alone would over-match but the AND-across-dimensions rule correctly excludes it, and end-to-end `resolve_and_apply_points_range_delete` against a real `FsDirectory` (`del_gen`/`del_count`/`.liv` bytes correct, plus a zero-match round still bumping `del_gen`). 99.38% line coverage. **Deliberately not implemented**: multi-segment resolution and delete-by-query beyond a single field's point range, same scope limits as `term_delete.rs`. |

| `index/IndexWriter.updateDocument(Term, doc)` | `lucene-index/src/update_document.rs::update_document` | **ported (task #37).** The atomic delete-by-term + add-document composition real Lucene defines `updateDocument` as, built entirely by wiring together already-verified primitives rather than new byte-format work: task #27's `term_delete::resolve_and_apply_term_delete` (delete half, fanned out over every segment in the caller's `SegmentInfos` that it supplies an opened [`SegmentDeleteSource`] for ŌĆö segments with no supplied source are left untouched, not silently dropped) and task #11's `segment_writer::flush_stored_only_segment` (add half ŌĆö a brand-new segment for the replacement document). Both halves are applied to an in-memory copy of the segment list; the **only** durable state transition is one `segment_infos::write` call at the very end, after every fallible step has already succeeded ŌĆö so a reader opening any `segments_N` this port writes either sees the fully-old state (previous generation, if `update_document` errored before its final write) or the fully-new one (old segments with bumped `del_gen`s + the one new segment, all in the next generation's single fsync'd file), never a half-applied mix. This is a state-machine/ordering guarantee, not a new decoder, so no new byte format needed cross-engine fixture verification (same reasoning as task #36's points-delete "reused vs. newly written" note) ŌĆö what *is* verified against the checked-in real-Lucene `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` fixture (the same one `term_delete.rs`'s own tests use) is that the delete half's resolution is correct within this composition, not just in isolation. **Free function, not a method on a stateful writer**: this port has no long-lived `IndexWriter`-equivalent struct (task #11's "minimal multi-segment writer" is itself a free function, `flush_stored_only_segment`, operating on `Directory` state the caller owns) ŌĆö `update_document` follows that same style rather than introducing a new stateful abstraction unprompted. **Known, inherited limitation, not new to this task**: this port's only write path (`flush_stored_only_segment`) writes stored-fields-only segments (no write-side postings format exists yet, `PLAN.md` Phase 5 item 2), so a delete-by-term issued against *only* a segment this port wrote itself can never actually match anything ŌĆö there is nothing to resolve against. Also confirms the new commit round-trips through `segment_infos::parse`. 99.25% line coverage. |

| `search/TopScoreDocCollector` | `lucene-search/src/collector.rs::TopDocsCollector` | **ported (task #13).** Keeps the top `n` `(doc_id, score)` hits, tie-broken by lower doc ID on an exact score tie ŌĆö verified against `HitQueue.lessThan` (`org.apache.lucene.search.HitQueue`), not assumed. No `TotalHits`/`TotalHits.Relation` tracking (nothing here does early termination yet ŌĆö every `collect` call is a fully evaluated hit). Unit-tested for fewer-than-`n`, exactly-`n`, more-than-`n` (eviction), tie-break (both on initial fill and on eviction), and empty-input cases. |
| `search/similarities/Similarity`/`BM25Similarity` (formula only) | `lucene-search/src/similarity.rs` | **ported: the pure BM25 scoring formula, plus real per-doc/avg norms decoding (this task).** Formula verified against `BM25Similarity.java`/`BM25Scorer.doScore` (Lucene 10.5.0) ŌĆö `idf(docFreq, docCount) = ln(1 + (docCount - docFreq + 0.5) / (docFreq + 0.5))`, `tfNorm(freq, fieldLength, avgFieldLength, k1, b) = freq / (freq + k1*(1-b+b*fieldLength/avgFieldLength))`, `score = idf * tfNorm`, defaults `k1 = 1.2`, `b = 0.75` (`BM25Similarity()`'s no-arg constructor). **Correctness fix (task #32)**: `tfNorm` previously carried a spurious `(k1+1)` numerator factor (the textbook Robertson/Sparck-Jones BM25 term, not real Lucene 10.5.0's actual formula, which folds no such factor into `BM25Scorer.doScore`'s `weight - weight / (1 + freq * normInverse)`); every self-consistency test in this crate had independently reimplemented the same wrong factor, so none of them could catch it. It was caught by `DisjunctionMaxQuery`'s (task #32) new cross-engine test comparing an absolute score against real `IndexSearcher.explain()` output for the first time in this port, rather than a hand-rederivation of this module's own formula ŌĆö fixed in `similarity::tf_norm`, with `scoring_fixtures.rs`'s/`phrase_query_fixtures.rs`'s hand-computed expected values updated to match; every dependent test (`scoring_fixtures.rs`, `phrase_query_fixtures.rs`, `boolean_query_fixtures.rs`, `dismax_query_fixtures.rs`) still passes since they only assert relative/self-consistent properties, except the one new test that now checks the literal real-Lucene-comparable magnitude. No query-time boost is folded in (none exists in this port). **The norms gap, previously stated here as open, is now closed**: `crates/lucene-codecs/src/norms.rs`'s read side (`norm_value`) is fixture-verified and complete (see that row above); real Lucene's default `Similarity.computeNorm` encodes a field's token-count length via `SmallFloat.intToByte4` (a lossy 4-bit-mantissa byte encoding), and `BM25Similarity.LENGTH_TABLE`/`SimScorer.score` decode it back with `SmallFloat.byte4ToInt` ŌĆö this port now has that exact decode (`lucene_util::small_float::byte4_to_int`, wrapped by `similarity::decode_norm`), verified against hand-derived known byteŌåölength values from `SmallFloat.java`'s algorithm. `lucene-search/src/field_norms.rs::FieldNorms::open` computes `avgFieldLength` once per field per query (summing every live doc's decoded length, not recomputed per scored doc ŌĆö see the `rust-performance` skill), and `search_term_query_scored`/`search_boolean_query_scored` take an optional `FieldNorms`/`HashMap<String, FieldNorms>`, using it for real per-doc/avg field length when present. **The one remaining, explicitly-scoped gap**: passing `None` (a field with no opened norms ŌĆö norms disabled for that field, or a caller that hasn't wired norms opening up yet) still falls back to the constant `1.0`/`1.0` substitution (`similarity::UNNORMED_FIELD_LENGTH`) ŌĆö a documented, deliberate fallback for that one case, not a blanket approximation anymore. Also still open: no cross-engine Java-side BM25-score fixture generator exists, so a full query's *final* score hasn't been diffed byte-for-byte against real Lucene's own output (only the length-normalization term's liveness and the decoded lengths themselves are differentially verified) ŌĆö deferred. Differential-verified in `crates/lucene-search/tests/scoring_fixtures.rs` against the real `_0.nvm`/`_0.nvd` this fixture's `IndexWriter` wrote: decoded per-doc lengths match hand-derived values from the fixture's own known per-term postings frequencies (a doc's BM25 length is the sum of its terms' frequencies), `avgFieldLength` is their mean, and real-norms scores differ from the constant-fallback scores for the same query/term. Unit-tested with independently hand-computed expected values (not just asserting the implementation's own output) for `idf`/`tf_norm`/`score`/`decode_norm`, plus monotonicity properties (more common term ŌåÆ lower idf, longer field ŌåÆ lower tf_norm, higher freq ŌåÆ higher score, real length ratio ŌåÆ correctly ordered scores). |
| `util/SmallFloat` (`intToByte4`/`byte4ToInt` only) | `lucene-util/src/small_float.rs` | **ported**, scoped to exactly the pair BM25 norms need (not the general `byteToFloat`/`floatToByte` 24-bit-mantissa pair used elsewhere in Lucene for unrelated float encodings). Verified byte-for-byte against `SmallFloat.java` (Lucene 10.5.0): `longToInt4`/`int4ToLong`'s "top 4 significant bits plus a biased shift" scheme, `NUM_FREE_VALUES = 255 - longToInt4(Integer.MAX_VALUE) = 24` (asserted as a concrete value, not just trusted from the derivation). Unit-tested: subnormal range (bytes 0-23) decodes exactly, hand-derived known byteŌåÆlength values, monotonicity (SmallFloat's whole purpose ŌĆö larger byte never decodes to a smaller length), and encodeŌåÆdecodeŌåÆre-encode fixed-point round trips for both subnormal and lossy normal-range values. |
| `util/BytesRefHash` (term/byte-sequence interning pool) | `lucene-util/src/term_interner.rs::{TermInterner, TermId}` | **new standalone primitive (task #67), not a byte-for-byte port of `BytesRefHash.java` and NOT yet wired into any indexing or query path.** Real `BytesRefHash` is tied to Lucene's `ByteBlockPool` allocation strategy and exposes sort/compact/rehash machinery for the indexing chain's per-field term dictionaries; this module has none of that. It only carries the core value proposition -- deduplicating recurring byte sequences into a stable, cheap-to-copy handle -- as a from-scratch `HashMap`-backed pool: `TermInterner::intern(&[u8]) -> TermId` returns the same `TermId` for byte-identical input and a fresh one otherwise, `TermInterner::get(TermId) -> Option<&[u8]>` looks the bytes back up, `TermId` is a plain `Copy` `u32` wrapper. No `unsafe` (workspace only permits it in `lucene-util`/`lucene-store`/`lucene-ffi`, and this module doesn't need it). Unit-tested: repeated identical bytes intern to the same ID, distinct bytes get distinct IDs, IDŌåÆbytes round trip, the empty byte string as a valid distinct term, lookup of an unrecognized/out-of-range `TermId` returns `None` rather than panicking, and a stress case interning 20,000 calls over a 50-word vocabulary that confirms `TermInterner::len()` collapses to exactly 50 stored entries (dedup actually happening, not just returning arbitrary IDs), plus a separate 5,000-all-distinct-terms case. **Explicitly deferred**: wiring this into `lucene-index`'s indexing chain or `lucene-search`'s query terms (future task), `ByteBlockPool`-style bulk/arena allocation, sorting/compaction, and any on-disk format tie-in -- this is purely an in-memory helper. |
| `search/Weight`, `search/Scorer`, `search/BulkScorer` (as a trait hierarchy) | ŌĆö | **deferred, not started.** This port's scoring is wired directly into `search_term_query_scored`/`search_boolean_query_scored` as plain functions (see the `TermQuery`/`BooleanQuery` rows below), not through a `Weight`/`Scorer` class hierarchy ŌĆö same "no speculative polymorphism with a single implementation" reasoning `lib.rs`'s module doc already applies to unscored matching. Revisit once a second query type or multi-segment federation gives the hierarchy a real second caller. |
| `search/BooleanQuery` (matching + BM25 scoring, `minimumNumberShouldMatch`, nested `BooleanQuery` clauses, `PhraseQuery` clauses) | `lucene-search/src/query.rs::{BooleanQuery, Clause}`, `lucene-search/src/lib.rs::{search_boolean_query, search_boolean_query_scored, matched_boolean_docs, resolve_clause_docs, clause_scores, should_match_counts}` | **ported**, including `minimumNumberShouldMatch` (task #24), nested `BooleanQuery` clauses (task #25), and `PhraseQuery` clauses (task #29, closing the gap this row previously noted as deferred). `must`/`should`/`must_not` are `Vec<Clause>` plus `minimum_should_match: usize`; `Clause` is a closed **three**-variant enum ŌĆö `Clause::Term(TermQuery)`, `Clause::Phrase(PhraseQuery)`, or `Clause::Boolean(Box<BooleanQuery>)`, recursively (an enum, not a `Weight`/`Scorer`-style trait object, since exactly three query shapes need to nest here today ŌĆö see the `rust-performance` skill's "enums where the closed set allows" guidance). `BooleanQuery::with_must`/`with_should`/`with_must_not` take `impl Into<Clause>` items ŌĆö `Clause`'s `From<TermQuery>`/`From<PhraseQuery>`/`From<BooleanQuery>` impls kept every existing call site compiling unchanged. Matching semantics verified against real `BooleanQuery.rewrite()`/`BooleanWeight.scorer`/`bulkScorer`/`explain` source, not guessed: no `must`/`should` clauses at all (with or without `must_not`) matches **nothing** ŌĆö real Lucene rewrites both "empty clause list" and "only `MUST_NOT` clauses" ("pure negative BooleanQuery") to `MatchNoDocsQuery`; a pure-exclusion query is *not* "every doc except the excluded ones". `minimum_should_match` gates `should` **regardless of whether `must` is also non-empty** ŌĆö verified against `BooleanWeight` source specifically because this is the one place the pre-#24 rule ("`should` is score-only once `must` exists") is easy to get backwards: that rule only holds at `minimum_should_match == 0`; for `minimum_should_match > 0`, a doc drawn from `must`'s conjunction (or, when `must` is empty, `should`'s disjunction) is only kept if it also matches at least `minimum_should_match` of the `should` clauses ŌĆö a genuine behavior change gated purely on `minimum_should_match > 0`. The counting mechanism ([`should_match_counts`]) is a `HashMap<i32, usize>` tally of how many `should` clauses' doc-ID lists contain each candidate doc ŌĆö needed because a plain `Disjunction` only reports "in the union", not "how many clauses agreed". `minimum_should_match` exceeding `should.len()` needs no special-case branch: real `BooleanQuery.rewrite()` turns that into an explicit `MatchNoDocsQuery` at query-construction time, but no doc's should-match count can ever reach an unreachable threshold either way, so the same threshold comparison already yields the identical "matches nothing" result. `search_boolean_query`/`search_boolean_query_scored`'s previously-duplicated matched-doc-set computation is unified in one shared `matched_boolean_docs` helper. **Nested clauses**: [`resolve_clause_docs`] recursively resolves a `Clause::Boolean` clause via a fresh `matched_boolean_docs` call on the nested query ŌĆö respecting *that* query's own `must`/`should`/`must_not`/`minimum_should_match` completely independently of the parent's, with no hardcoded nesting-depth limit (verified with 2ŌĆō3 levels of nesting, not just one extra level). [`clause_scores`] is the scoring sibling: a nested `BooleanQuery`'s own score contribution is the sum of *its own* matching `must`/`should` sub-clauses' scores, restricted to the doc set the nested query itself actually matched ŌĆö mirroring real Lucene's additive `BooleanScorer` recursion, so a should-clause hit the nested query's own `must_not`/`minimum_should_match` excludes can't leak a score contribution into the parent. **`Clause::Phrase` (task #29)**: `resolve_clause_docs` delegates matching straight to `search_phrase_query` (collected via a local `VecCollector`), and `clause_scores` delegates scoring straight to `search_phrase_query_scored` (collected via a tiny inline `ScoringCollector`) ŌĆö both reusing the standalone phrase-query functions' logic rather than duplicating it. Because a `Clause::Phrase` needs the segment's opened `.pos`/`.pay` files, `search_boolean_query`/`search_boolean_query_scored` (and every internal helper in the recursive chain ŌĆö `matched_boolean_docs`, `resolve_clause_docs`, `clause_scores`) now additionally take `pos_in: Option<&PosInput>`/`pay_in: Option<&PayInput>` (a breaking signature change from the pre-task-#29 four/six-argument shape; every call site in this crate and `lucene-ffi` was updated to pass `None`/`None` where no phrase clause is used) ŌĆö `None` is fine for a query with no multi-term `Clause::Phrase` at any nesting depth, surfacing `Error::MissingPosInput` only if one turns out to need it, same convention `search_phrase_query` already established. **Verified against real Lucene**: `crates/lucene-search/tests/boolean_query_fixtures.rs` computes expected conjunction/disjunction/difference from `manifest.properties`' real `PostingsEnum`-derived doc sets and asserts `search_boolean_query` matches exactly, including a `minimum_should_match`-with-`must`-present case, a nested-`must`-clause case, and a three-level-deep nesting case. **`search_boolean_query_scored`** (task #13) computes the identical matched-doc set, then reports each doc's score as the sum of its BM25 score across every `must`/`should` clause it satisfies (mirroring real Lucene's additive `BooleanScorer`; `must_not` never contributes, matching `Occur.MUST_NOT`'s filter-only contract) ŌĆö verified in `crates/lucene-search/tests/scoring_fixtures.rs` against the real segment, including a dedicated test that a `must_not` clause never changes the score, a test (task #24) proving `minimum_should_match` gates matching only, not the score sum, a test (task #25) proving a nested `must` clause's own score sums correctly into the parent's additive total, and a test (task #29) proving a `Clause::Phrase`'s own score sums correctly alongside a sibling `Clause::Term`, against the `pos` field's real alpha/beta postings. Unit tests in `lib.rs`/`query.rs` additionally confirm a nested clause's own `minimum_should_match` and the parent's are fully independent settings (no cross-contamination in either direction), plus a `Clause::Phrase` nested inside a `Clause::Boolean` resolves both matching and scoring correctly. **Still deferred**: `lucene-ffi`'s `ffi_search_boolean_query` still only ever constructs flat `Clause::Term` clauses from its four-parallel-array C-ABI wire format ŌĆö exposing `Clause::Phrase`/`Clause::Boolean` *construction* over that wire format remains a separate, deferred FFI design question (alongside the already-deferred `_scored` FFI wrappers). **Edge cases (task #60)**: six real Lucene `BooleanQuery`/`BooleanWeight` corner cases were individually verified against this port's actual `matched_boolean_docs`/`should_match_counts`/`clause_scores` code (not assumed) and found already correct, locked in with new regression tests rather than requiring a fix: a pure `must_not`-only query matches nothing (confirmed *before* `must_not` ever enters the merge, not via an "everything except excluded" shortcut); `minimum_should_match > 0` with zero `should` clauses at all (a nonsensical-but-configurable combination) correctly matches nothing, not "trivially satisfied"; `minimum_should_match` exceeding `should.len()` has no distinct code path from the ordinary case, so no off-by-one is possible at or past the boundary; a nested `Clause::Boolean`'s own `must_not` never leaks into or is leaked into by an outer level's `must_not` (each nesting level gets a fresh `matched_boolean_docs` call); and ŌĆö deliberately **not** a bug ŌĆö a literal duplicate `should` clause (the same `TermQuery` twice) double-counts toward `minimum_should_match` and double-scores, matching real `BooleanQuery`'s own documented non-deduping behavior (duplicating a clause is itself a known, intentional way to boost it in real Lucene), not something this port needed to special-case away. **Rewrite pass (task #79)**: `BooleanQuery::rewrite`/`Clause::rewrite` add a pure, standalone, **opt-in** simplification pass -- never called by `search_boolean_query`/`search_boolean_query_scored` themselves, so existing execution is unchanged. Implements exactly three rules: (1) a single-clause query with no `must_not` collapses to that clause, but only in the two cases proven not to change matching -- `must.len() == 1` with `should` empty and `minimum_should_match == 0`, or `should.len() == 1` with `must` empty and `minimum_should_match <= 1` (both boundary cases where a positive `minimum_should_match` would otherwise turn "matches nothing" into a false positive are deliberately excluded); (2) zero-clause/`must_not`-only "matches nothing" is a documented no-op, since `matched_boolean_docs` already produces that result with no `MatchNoDocsQuery`-equivalent `Clause` to rewrite to; (3) every clause is rewritten recursively, bottom-up, including through nested `DisjunctionMax`/`ConstantScore`/`Boost`. **Duplicate-clause deduplication, resolved precisely (re-audited against `BooleanQuery.java`'s actual `rewrite()` source, not the earlier task #60 assumption)**: real `BooleanQuery.rewrite()` does two genuinely different things here, and this port now matches one and deliberately not the other. (a) **`MUST_NOT`/`FILTER` dedup** is unconditional set-membership dedup (`MUST_NOT`/`FILTER` are stored in a `HashSet`) with no scoring implication, since neither ever contributes to score -- `MUST_NOT` only excludes docs matched by `must`/`should`. **Rule 4, now implemented**: `Clause::rewrite` removes exact duplicate `must_not` clauses (order-preserving, keeps the first occurrence); this port has no separate `FILTER` occur type yet (see this row's `Clause` shape above), so only the `MUST_NOT` half of real Lucene's rule applies today. Proven safe against this port's own executor, not assumed: `matched_boolean_docs` only ever folds `must_not` into a `Disjunction` used purely for exclusion, and `clause_scores` never iterates `must_not` at all (only `must.iter().chain(should.iter())`) -- so a repeated `must_not` clause changes neither the matched-doc set nor any score. (b) **`MUST`/`SHOULD` dedup is correctly left unimplemented, but the earlier justification for that ("real Lucene doesn't dedup these either, duplicating a clause is itself an intentional way to boost it") was wrong** -- real `BooleanQuery.rewrite()`'s `deduplicateClauses` *does* fold duplicate `MUST`/`SHOULD` clauses, replacing every occurrence with **one** copy carrying a recombined boost from `IndexSearcher.getSimilarity().computeQueryTermWeight(count)` for the common unweighted-duplicate case, falling back to a linear boost sum only when explicit per-clause boosts are already present. That `computeQueryTermWeight` call is `Similarity`-specific and is *not* equivalent to "sum each clause's score `count` times" -- it approximates what one token at `count`-times term frequency would have scored. This port's `Clause::rewrite` has **no `IndexSearcher`/`Similarity` in scope** (it runs before any index is opened), so there is no way to reproduce real Lucene's actual `MUST`/`SHOULD` dedup faithfully; a naive alternative (drop the duplicate, or sum boosts unconditionally) would silently produce *different* scores than both this port's current (correct, additive) behavior *and* real Lucene's actual rewritten behavior -- a correctness regression, not a simplification. Left unimplemented until a future task threads a term-weight function into the rewrite path. This is why `clause_scores`'s existing additive-per-clause behavior (a duplicate `should`/`must` clause doubles its score contribution, confirmed against this port's own executor by task #60) is still exactly right for the *unrewritten* query -- it matches real Lucene's own pre-rewrite `BooleanWeight` scoring, which is what this port's non-rewriting `search_boolean_query_scored` always uses. Proven scoring-equivalent, not just structurally simplified: `crates/lucene-search/tests/boolean_query_fixtures.rs`'s `rewrite_produces_identical_scored_results_for_single_must_clause`/`_for_single_should_clause`/`_for_nested_single_clause_boolean`/`_for_duplicate_must_not_clauses` run the same query pre- and post-`rewrite()` through `search_boolean_query_scored` against the real fixture segment and assert identical `TopDocsCollector` output (doc IDs and scores both); `query.rs`'s `rewrite_removes_exact_duplicate_must_not_clauses`/`rewrite_keeps_distinct_must_not_clauses_and_preserves_order`/`rewrite_does_not_deduplicate_must_not_clauses_inside_a_nested_boolean_clause`/`rewrite_deliberately_does_not_deduplicate_duplicate_must_clauses` cover the structural rule and its documented scope boundary. |
| `search/PhraseQuery`/`ExactPhraseScorer`/`SloppyPhraseMatcher` (in-order sloppy matching, no reordering; BM25 scoring) | `lucene-search/src/query.rs::PhraseQuery`, `lucene-search/src/lib.rs::{search_phrase_query, search_phrase_query_scored, phrase_matches_in_doc, phrase_matches_in_doc_sloppy, phrase_freq_exact}` | **ported: exact adjacent-position matching (`slop == 0`, task #19), in-order sloppy matching (`slop > 0`, task #28), and BM25 scoring (task #29, closing that gap) -- term reordering within the slop budget, and graduated sloppy match-quality scoring, are not supported, see below.** `PhraseQuery { field: String, terms: Vec<Vec<u8>>, slop: u32 }` implicitly places `terms[i]` at query-relative position `i` (still no `PhraseQuery.Builder.add(Term, int position)`-style arbitrary/non-adjacent positions -- `slop` widens how far apart the implicitly-numbered terms may drift at match time, it doesn't let a caller assign arbitrary per-term positions). `slop` defaults to `0` (matching real `PhraseQuery.Builder`'s default); `PhraseQuery::with_slop` is the builder method. **Exact alignment algorithm** (`phrase_matches_in_doc`, unchanged from task #19): every position in the first term's list is a candidate base `p`, checked against every other term's sorted position list via `binary_search` for `p+i`. **Sloppy alignment algorithm** (`phrase_matches_in_doc_sloppy`, task #28's addition): for a candidate base position `p_0` (every occurrence in the first term's list), a doc matches at slop `s` iff there exists a strictly-increasing, in-order alignment `p_0 < p_1 < ... < p_{n-1}` (one position per term, `p_i` drawn from `term_positions[i]`) whose total "moves" -- `sum_{i=1}^{n-1} (p_i - p_{i-1} - 1)`, which telescopes to `(p_{n-1} - p_0) - (n-1)` -- is at most `s`; for a fixed `p_0` the minimum such total is found by a greedy scan picking, at each step, the smallest position in the next term's list that's strictly greater than the previous chosen position (provably optimal since the total telescopes to a function of only `p_0` and the final position). This formula is derived from real `PhraseQuery`'s own Javadoc description of slop ("the number of positions all words need to move ... to line up in order"), cited in `phrase_matches_in_doc_sloppy`'s doc comment. **Scoped subset, stated precisely**: this is an **in-order-only** implementation -- it requires the chosen positions to be strictly increasing in phrase order.
