Real Lucene's general `SloppyPhraseMatcher` (`org.apache.lucene.search.SloppyPhraseMatcher`) additionally allows term **reordering** within the slop budget (e.g. "quick fox" matching "fox ... quick" at a high enough slop) via a priority-queue-based edit-distance computation over `PhrasePositions`/repeats -- that general algorithm was not implemented here: this task could not confidently re-derive and verify its exact edit-distance formula against real Lucene's source within scope, so reordering support is deliberately left out rather than guessed at (a correctness-first, honestly-scoped subset, per this port's established practice -- see BKD's split-heuristic and term_vectors' scoped write side for the same call). `search_phrase_query` computes the doc-level conjunction across every term's live-filtered doc-ID list first (reusing `docid_set::Conjunction`, since phrase match implies term match), then dispatches per candidate doc to `phrase_matches_in_doc` (unchanged fast path) when `query.slop == 0`, or `phrase_matches_in_doc_sloppy` otherwise. **Edge cases** (both paths): an empty `terms` list matches nothing (mirrors real `PhraseQuery.Builder.build()`'s `MatchNoDocsQuery` result for zero added terms); a single-term "phrase" degenerates to a plain `search_term_query` call regardless of `slop` (trivially aligned wherever the lone term occurs, never needs an opened `.pos` file); a term missing from the field matches nothing, not an error; a repeated term (e.g. "the the") is handled without special-casing. **BM25 scoring (task #29's addition)**: `search_phrase_query_scored` mirrors `search_phrase_query`'s matching exactly, additionally computing each matched doc's **phrase frequency** (in place of a single term's `freq`) and feeding it through the same BM25 machinery `search_term_query_scored` uses (`similarity::tf_norm`, real per-doc/avg norms via the same `FieldNorms` contract). The phrase's overall `idf` is the **sum of each constituent term's own `idf(docFreq, docCount)`** -- verified against `BM25Similarity.idf(CollectionStatistics, TermStatistics[])`'s real source, which sums per-term idf across a multi-term statistics array rather than inventing a single combined docFreq; this is not this port's own invention. **Exact phrase frequency** (`phrase_freq_exact`): counts every valid base position `p0` in the first term's own (sorted, deduplicated) position list for which the rest of the phrase aligns -- one match per distinct starting position of the phrase's first word, matching `ExactPhraseScorer`'s own per-start-position counting granularity (does not suppress overlapping matches, e.g. "the the the" counts 2 matches for phrase "the the"). **Sloppy phrase frequency**: **deliberately simplified** to `1` if any valid alignment exists (via `phrase_matches_in_doc_sloppy`), `0` otherwise -- real Lucene's `SloppyPhraseMatcher` instead accumulates a graduated per-match contribution of `1.0 / (matchLength + 1)` (tighter alignments score higher) summed across every alignment its priority-queue-based algorithm finds; this port could not confidently re-derive/verify that exact per-match weighting formula (on top of the alignment-enumeration algorithm already scoped down to in-order-only, see above) within this task's scope, so **graduated sloppy match-quality scoring is deliberately deferred**, tracked here, in favor of the simpler matches-or-not boolean signal -- consistent with this port's "scope down honestly rather than guess at unverified Lucene internals" practice (BKD's split heuristic, `phrase_matches_in_doc_sloppy` itself). **Verified against real Lucene**: `crates/lucene-search/tests/phrase_query_fixtures.rs` (task #19) reuses the existing `pos` field checked into `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` for the exact-matching (`slop == 0`) path (doc 8555: "alpha"@0, "beta"@1, adjacent; doc 8556: "alpha"@0 and @1, no "beta" at all); `two_term_phrase_scored_matches_hand_computed_bm25_score` (task #29) hand-derives the expected BM25 score from the manifest's real `docFreq` values and asserts `search_phrase_query_scored` matches, independently of `similarity::score`'s own unit tests. **The sloppy path's cross-engine gap is now closed**: `GenBlockTree.java` was extended with doc7 ("pos" field: "alpha"@0, "beta"@3, a real, known, non-adjacent gap requiring `(3-0)-(2-1) = 2` moves), and at fixture-generation time it *actually runs* real `IndexSearcher.search` with a real `PhraseQuery.Builder().add(alpha).add(beta).setSlop(n)` against that doc for `n` in `{0, 1, 2, 3, 5}`, recording each verdict in `manifest.properties` (`field.pos.sloppyGap.realLuceneSlopResults=0:false,1:false,2:true,3:true,5:true`). `crates/lucene-search/tests/phrase_query_fixtures.rs::sloppy_phrase_gap_matches_real_lucenes_phrase_query_set_slop_at_every_tested_value` reads that manifest key back and asserts `search_phrase_query`'s own sloppy-path verdict agrees with real Lucene's at every one of those five slop values -- confirmed passing, i.e. this port's `phrase_matches_in_doc_sloppy` formula is now cross-engine verified against actual `SloppyPhraseMatcher`/`PhraseQuery.setSlop(n)` behavior for a known non-adjacent gap, not just self-consistent unit tests. (The formula's own internal correctness was already covered by the hand-computed unit tests in `lib.rs` listed previously; this closes the gap those tests alone couldn't: agreement with real Lucene's actual output.) Term **reordering** within the slop budget remains unimplemented and unverified (see the scoped-subset note above) -- only in-order sloppy matching has cross-engine proof. |
| `search/DisjunctionMaxQuery`/`DisjunctionMaxScorer` (matching + BM25 scoring, nested `Clause` disjuncts) | `lucene-search/src/query.rs::{DisjunctionMaxQuery, Clause::DisjunctionMax}`, `lucene-search/src/lib.rs::{search_disjunction_max_query, search_disjunction_max_query_scored, resolve_dismax_docs, dismax_scores}` | **ported (task #32).** `DisjunctionMaxQuery { disjuncts: Vec<Clause>, tie_breaker: f32 }`; `Clause` grows a fourth variant, `Clause::DisjunctionMax(Box<DisjunctionMaxQuery>)`, nesting the same way `Clause::Boolean` already does (arbitrary depth, and a `DisjunctionMaxQuery` disjunct may itself be a `Term`/`Phrase`/`Boolean`/`DisjunctionMax`). Matching is a pure union (`resolve_dismax_docs`, built on the same `Disjunction` merge combinator `BooleanQuery`'s `should`-only case uses) ŌĆö unlike `BooleanQuery.should`, there is no `minimum_should_match`-style gate; a `DisjunctionMaxQuery` with zero disjuncts matches nothing, mirroring `BooleanQuery`'s own empty-clause-list rule. Scoring (`dismax_scores`) implements real `DisjunctionMaxScorer`'s exact formula, not an approximation: a matching doc's score is `max(disjunct scores) + tie_breaker * sum(every other matching disjunct's score)`, computed via the same recursive per-clause `clause_scores` a `Clause::Boolean` disjunct already uses (so a nested `Boolean`/`DisjunctionMax` disjunct scores correctly to arbitrary depth). `tie_breaker == 0.0` (real `DisjunctionMaxQuery(Collection<Query>)`'s single-arg constructor default) degenerates to pure max-of-disjuncts scoring. **Verified against real Lucene**: `crates/lucene-search/tests/dismax_query_fixtures.rs` reuses the checked-in `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` fixture and its already-fixture-verified `body` postings (`cat`={0,2}, `dog`={0,1}, `bird`={1,4}), plus a genuine `IndexSearcher.search(new DisjunctionMaxQuery(...), 10)` run against that exact on-disk segment (`fixtures/src/AppendDismaxManifest.java`, appended to `manifest.properties` as `dismax.*` keys without perturbing the segment's already-committed random ID) asserting doc-for-doc, score-for-score agreement with real Lucene's own recorded `TopDocs` output ŌĆö true cross-engine verification of the tie-breaker formula, not just self-consistency. Unit tests in `lib.rs` additionally cover: empty-disjunct-list, a missing-term disjunct contributing nothing, exact tie-breaker arithmetic, a doc matching only one disjunct getting exactly that disjunct's score, and nesting in both directions (`DisjunctionMax` inside `Boolean`, `Boolean` inside `DisjunctionMax`, `DisjunctionMax` inside `DisjunctionMax`). **Deferred, same as `BooleanQuery`**: `lucene-ffi` C-ABI construction of a `Clause::DisjunctionMax` disjunct (the FFI wire format still only builds flat `Clause::Term` clauses). |
| `search/ConstantScoreQuery`/`BoostQuery` (matching + scoring, nested `Clause` composition) | `lucene-search/src/query.rs::{ConstantScoreQuery, BoostQuery, Clause::ConstantScore, Clause::Boost}`, `lucene-search/src/lib.rs::{resolve_clause_docs, clause_scores}` | **ported (task #33).** `ConstantScoreQuery { inner: Box<Clause>, score: f32 }` and `BoostQuery { inner: Box<Clause>, boost: f32 }` each wrap any other `Clause`; `Clause` grows two more variants, `ConstantScore(Box<ConstantScoreQuery>)` and `Boost(Box<BoostQuery>)`, nesting the same way `Boolean`/`DisjunctionMax` already do (either direction, arbitrary depth ŌĆö a `ConstantScoreQuery`/`BoostQuery` can wrap a `Boolean`/`DisjunctionMax`/each other, and a `BooleanQuery`/`DisjunctionMaxQuery` clause can be a `ConstantScore`/`Boost`). Matching for both is exactly the wrapped clause's own matching set (`resolve_clause_docs`'s `ConstantScore`/`Boost` arms recurse straight into the inner clause, no narrowing). Scoring (`clause_scores`): `ConstantScoreQuery` discards the inner clause's own score entirely and reports `score` for every doc the inner clause matched (real `ConstantScoreWeight`/`ConstantScoreScorer`'s behavior ŌĆö the wrapped query's score never surfaces); `BoostQuery` multiplies the inner clause's own score by `boost` (real `BoostQuery.BoostWeight`'s exact behavior ŌĆö a pure rescale, not a replacement). **Cross-engine verification scope**: no new Java fixture generator was added ŌĆö both wrappers are a trivial arithmetic composition (a literal constant; one `f32` multiply) over an inner clause whose own scoring is already cross-engine-verified against real `IndexSearcher`/`TopDocs` output (task #30's `scoring_fixtures.rs`, task #32's `dismax_query_fixtures.rs`), so there was no Lucene-specific formula or wire format left to get wrong that a new fixture could catch. Instead, `lib.rs`'s unit tests use `search_term_query_scored`'s already-real BM25 score for `body:cat`/`body:dog` at specific docs (from the checked-in `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` fixture) as the known-real inner score, and assert the wrapped score is exactly that constant, or exactly that real score times the boost ŌĆö verifying this task's arithmetic against a real inner score without a second fixture generator. Unit tests cover: matching-set-equals-inner for both wrappers, a missing-inner-term matching nothing, the constant score exactly overriding two different real inner scores, boost multiplying a real inner score, both wrappers composing inside a `BooleanQuery` alongside a sibling clause (additive total), `BoostQuery` nested inside a `DisjunctionMaxQuery` disjunct, `ConstantScoreQuery` wrapping a nested `DisjunctionMaxQuery`, and `BoostQuery` wrapping a nested `ConstantScoreQuery` (confirming the two compose as `inner_constant * boost`, not independently). **Deferred, same as `BooleanQuery`/`DisjunctionMaxQuery`**: `lucene-ffi` C-ABI construction of a `Clause::ConstantScore`/`Clause::Boost` clause (the FFI wire format still only builds flat `Clause::Term` clauses; `ffi_search_boolean_query_scored`'s field-name-extraction match treats both new variants like `Phrase`/`Boolean`/`DisjunctionMax`, contributing no field name). |
| `search/MatchAllDocsQuery`/`MatchNoDocsQuery` (matching + scoring, `Clause` composition) | `lucene-search/src/query.rs::{MatchAllDocsQuery, MatchNoDocsQuery, Clause::MatchAllDocs, Clause::MatchNoDocs}`, `lucene-search/src/lib.rs::{match_all_doc_ids, resolve_clause_docs, clause_scores}` | **ported.** `MatchAllDocsQuery { max_doc: i32 }` matches every **live** doc in `0..max_doc`, scored flat `1.0` (real `MatchAllDocsQuery`'s `ConstantScoreScorer` always scores `boost`, `1.0` unless wrapped in a `BoostQuery`/`Clause::Boost` ŌĆö matching this crate's existing `ConstantScoreQuery`/`WildcardQuery`/etc "flat constant, compose a wrapper for anything else" convention). `MatchNoDocsQuery { reason: String }` matches nothing, ever ŌĆö `resolve_clause_docs`'s `Clause::MatchNoDocs` arm returns an empty `Vec` directly, no segment lookup at all (`reason` is purely informational, mirroring real `MatchNoDocsQuery(String reason)`'s documented rewrite-provenance string; nothing in this crate inspects it). **Why `max_doc` lives on the query struct, not threaded as a new parameter through `resolve_clause_docs`/`clause_scores`/`search_boolean_query` and the rest of that call graph**: every other leaf `Clause` variant resolves its matched-doc set from a term dictionary lookup (a term's own postings already enumerate exactly the docs it needs) ŌĆö `MatchAllDocsQuery` is the first clause with nothing to seek into, so rather than a wide, mechanical signature change across every function in `resolve_clause_docs`'s call graph (touching call sites in other crates' tests too) for a value only this one variant needs, the caller supplies `max_doc` once at construction time, the same way it already knows and passes `live_docs` per search call. `match_all_doc_ids` (the shared `0..max_doc` sweep both `resolve_clause_docs` and `clause_scores` call) is the same shape as `doc_value_query::search_numeric_range`'s own `[0, max_doc)` sweep ŌĆö no dictionary, so a full sweep is the only correct option. `Clause` grows two more leaf variants, `MatchAllDocs(MatchAllDocsQuery)` and `MatchNoDocs(MatchNoDocsQuery)`, usable anywhere a `Clause` is, including nested inside `BooleanQuery`/`DisjunctionMaxQuery`/`ConstantScoreQuery`/`BoostQuery`. **Tests**: `crates/lucene-search/tests/match_all_no_docs_fixtures.rs` reuses the real `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` segment (via `boolean_query_fixtures.rs`'s own manifest-driven open helper) and a hand-built `live_docs` bitset (the checked-in fixture itself has no deletions) to prove: `MatchAllDocsQuery` returns exactly the live doc set with some docs marked deleted (not the deleted ones), and every doc with no deletions; `MatchNoDocsQuery` always returns empty regardless of deletions; `MatchAllDocsQuery` as a `must` clause alongside a real `TermQuery` behaves identically to that `TermQuery` alone; `MatchNoDocsQuery` as a `must` clause makes the whole `BooleanQuery` match nothing; and both compose correctly through `search_boolean_query_scored`/`TopDocsCollector` (`MatchAllDocsQuery` scores every live doc flat `1.0`, `MatchNoDocsQuery` produces zero hits). Plus `query.rs` unit tests for construction/`Clause::from`/builder methods. **Deferred, same as every other `Clause` variant since task #29**: `lucene-ffi` C-ABI construction of a `Clause::MatchAllDocs`/`Clause::MatchNoDocs` clause. |
| `search/TermInSetQuery` (matching + scoring, `Clause` composition) | `lucene-search/src/query.rs::{TermInSetQuery, Clause::TermInSet}`, `lucene-search/src/lib.rs::term_in_set_doc_ids` | **ported.** `TermInSetQuery { field: String, terms: Vec<Vec<u8>> }` matches a doc if it contains ANY of the given same-field terms ŌĆö implemented as a union over each term's existing single-`TermQuery` postings resolution (`field_terms.postings(term, doc_in)` per term, deduplicated/sorted), not a new low-level postings walk. **Scoring, verified against the actual Java `Scorer` code, not just the class javadoc**: real `TermInSetQuery`'s default rewrite (`CONSTANT_SCORE_BLENDED_REWRITE`) builds a `ConstantScoreScorer` whose score is always the fixed boost (`1.0` unless wrapped in a `Clause::Boost`) regardless of how many of the terms a doc actually matched ŌĆö NOT the max score across matched terms, and NOT a summed `BooleanQuery`-OR score, even though the matching semantics are exactly that of a same-field disjunction. This crate's `clause_scores` arm for `Clause::TermInSet` matches: flat `1.0` per matching doc. An absent term contributes nothing (no error); every term absent, or an empty `terms` list, correctly matches nothing (the union of zero/empty sets is empty, no special-casing needed). **Tests**: `crates/lucene-search/tests/term_in_set_query_fixtures.rs` (9 tests) against the real `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` fixture ŌĆö any-not-all matching, a 3-term union, absent-term/all-absent-terms/empty-term-set/missing-field (all correctly empty, no error), composition as both a `must` and `should` `BooleanQuery` clause, and a scoring test explicitly proving a doc matching two of the given terms still scores `1.0`, not `2.0` (disproving the summed-should hypothesis). **Deferred, same as `MatchAllDocsQuery`/`MatchNoDocsQuery` above**: `lucene-ffi` C-ABI construction of a `Clause::TermInSet` clause (the two exhaustive field-name-extraction matches in `lucene-ffi/src/{explain.rs,query.rs}` were extended to treat it as fieldless, same no-op treatment those files already give `MatchAllDocs`/`MatchNoDocs`). |
| `search/WildcardQuery` (matching + constant scoring, `Clause` composition) | `lucene-codecs/src/wildcard.rs::WildcardPattern` (escape support), `lucene-search/src/query.rs::{WildcardQuery, Clause::Wildcard}`, `lucene-search/src/lib.rs::{wildcard_doc_ids, resolve_clause_docs, clause_scores}` | **ported (task #34).** `WildcardQuery { field: String, pattern: Vec<u8> }` is a leaf `Clause::Wildcard(WildcardQuery)`, matching every doc that has at least one term (for `query.field`) `lucene_codecs::wildcard::WildcardPattern` accepts, **union**ed across every matching term (`wildcard_doc_ids`: `FieldTerms::intersect(&pattern)` enumerates matching terms ŌĆö reusing task #1's `WildcardPattern`/`intersect` machinery unchanged rather than building a parallel matcher ŌĆö then every matching term's postings' doc IDs are collected, sorted, and deduplicated, since a multi-valued field can have more than one matching term in the same doc). Scoring (`clause_scores`'s `Clause::Wildcard` arm): a flat, unscored `1.0` per matching doc ŌĆö real Lucene's `MultiTermQuery` has no single term's frequency/idf to score a multi-term match against by default; a caller wanting a different constant or a rescale already has `ConstantScoreQuery`/`BoostQuery` (task #33) to compose on top, same as real Lucene's own default rewrite chain. **This task also closed a gap task #1 explicitly deferred**: `WildcardPattern::new` now supports `\`-escaping (`\*`/`\?`/`\\` match a literal `*`/`?`/`\`; a trailing unpaired `\` falls back to matching a literal `\`), matching real `WildcardQuery.toAutomaton`'s `WILDCARD_ESCAPE` handling exactly ŌĆö escaping any other byte is a harmless no-op, same as real Lucene's `default` fallthrough. `Clause` grows a sixth variant, `Wildcard(WildcardQuery)` (a leaf, not a wrapper ŌĆö it does not nest another `Clause` the way `Boolean`/`DisjunctionMax`/`ConstantScore`/`Boost` do), usable anywhere a `Clause` is (a `BooleanQuery`/`DisjunctionMaxQuery` clause, or wrapped in `ConstantScoreQuery`/`BoostQuery`). **Verified against real Lucene**: `fixtures/src/AppendWildcardManifest.java` (same append-only pattern as `AppendDismaxManifest.java` ŌĆö opens the already-committed `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` directory read-only, no segment regeneration/ID perturbation) runs eight real `org.apache.lucene.search.WildcardQuery`s against `body`'s real terms/postings (`cat`={0,2}, `dog`={0,1}, `bird`={1,4}) ŌĆö a literal, a trailing `*`, a `?`, a bare `*` (matches every term), a no-match pattern, an escaped `*` (no term contains a literal `*`, so it matches nothing), an escaped non-special byte (`do\g`, a no-op escape, matches `dog`), and a `?` landing on `bird`'s last byte (`bir?`) ŌĆö recording real Lucene's own matched doc IDs into `manifest.properties`' `wildcard.*` keys. `crates/lucene-search/tests/wildcard_query_fixtures.rs` re-runs the equivalent `Clause::Wildcard` query for every recorded case and asserts doc-for-doc agreement, the actual cross-engine proof (not a self-consistency check) ŌĆö all eight cases matched real Lucene's output on the first run. Additional unit tests (in the same file) cover an empty pattern (matches nothing, since `body` has no empty term), pure-wildcard patterns (`**`/`?`), a missing field, and composing `Clause::Wildcard` inside a `BooleanQuery`'s `must` alongside a plain `Clause::Term`. New escape-specific unit tests in `wildcard.rs` cover `\*`/`\?`/`\\`, a trailing unpaired `\`, and escaping a non-special byte. **Deferred, same as every other `Clause` variant since task #29**: `lucene-ffi` C-ABI construction of a `Clause::Wildcard` clause (the FFI wire format still only builds flat `Clause::Term` clauses; `ffi_search_boolean_query_scored`'s field-name-extraction match now also treats `Wildcard` like `Phrase`/`Boolean`/`DisjunctionMax`/`ConstantScore`/`Boost`, contributing no field name). No real `IntersectTermsEnum`/`CompiledAutomaton` trie-block-skipping (unchanged from task #1 ŌĆö `intersect` is still an `O(n)`-in-field-term-count scan narrowed by a literal-prefix range); no regex/`FuzzyQuery` (still need real automaton/edit-distance machinery, unchanged scope from task #1). |
| `search/PrefixQuery` (matching + constant scoring, `Clause` composition) | `lucene-codecs/src/wildcard.rs::WildcardPattern::prefix`, `lucene-search/src/query.rs::{PrefixQuery, Clause::Prefix}`, `lucene-search/src/lib.rs::{prefix_doc_ids, resolve_clause_docs, clause_scores}` | **ported (task #35).** `PrefixQuery { field: String, prefix: Vec<u8> }` is a leaf `Clause::Prefix(PrefixQuery)`, matching every doc that has at least one term (for `query.field`) starting with `prefix`'s literal bytes, **union**ed across every matching term (`prefix_doc_ids`, structurally identical to task #34's `wildcard_doc_ids` ŌĆö `FieldTerms::intersect` enumerates matching terms, then every matching term's postings' doc IDs are collected, sorted, and deduplicated). Scoring (`clause_scores`'s `Clause::Prefix` arm): the same flat, unscored `1.0` per matching doc as `Clause::Wildcard`, for the same reason (no single term's frequency/idf to score a multi-term match against; `ConstantScoreQuery`/`BoostQuery` compose on top if a caller wants otherwise). **Design decision, made explicitly rather than defaulted to**: real `PrefixQuery` is functionally "match every term starting with X," which could be built as (a) a thin wrapper constructing a `WildcardQuery` pattern by escaping `prefix`'s bytes and appending an unescaped trailing `*`, reusing `WildcardPattern::new`'s glob parser, or (b) a direct prefix match bypassing glob syntax entirely. This port takes (b): `PrefixQuery` calls `lucene_codecs::wildcard::WildcardPattern::prefix` directly ŌĆö a constructor that already existed (task #1, for exactly this purpose) and builds its token list straight from `prefix`'s raw bytes as `Literal` tokens plus a trailing `AnyMany`, **never invoking `WildcardPattern::new`'s escape/glob-parsing loop**. Option (a) was rejected because it would require re-escaping `prefix` byte-by-byte before matching, which is exactly the kind of edge case this task's own scoping called out: a prefix like `a*b` must match every term starting with the 3 literal bytes `a`, `*`, `b`, not be reinterpreted as "`a`, then anything, then `b`" ŌĆö building on `WildcardPattern::prefix` sidesteps that risk entirely (there is no escaping step to get wrong) rather than mitigating it with careful escaping. **Verified against real Lucene**: `fixtures/src/AppendPrefixManifest.java` (same append-only pattern as `AppendWildcardManifest.java` ŌĆö opens the already-committed `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` directory read-only, no segment regeneration/ID perturbation) runs six real `org.apache.lucene.search.PrefixQuery`s against `body`'s real terms/postings (`cat`={0,2}, `dog`={0,1}, `bird`={1,4}) ŌĆö a prefix matching one term (`ca` ŌåÆ `cat`), a prefix matching several (`b` ŌåÆ `bird`), the empty prefix (matches every term in the field), a prefix equal to a full existing term (`cat`, must still match, plus any longer terms sharing it ŌĆö none exist in this fixture, but the case pins the boundary), a no-match prefix (`zzz`), and a prefix containing literal `*`/`?` bytes (`a*b?c`, no term contains these bytes, so it's a no-match case, but it proves the bytes are matched literally rather than panicking or being glob-reinterpreted) ŌĆö recording real Lucene's own matched doc IDs into `manifest.properties`' `prefix.*` keys. `crates/lucene-search/tests/prefix_query_fixtures.rs` re-runs the equivalent `Clause::Prefix` query for every recorded case and asserts doc-for-doc agreement, the actual cross-engine proof (not a self-consistency check) ŌĆö all six cases matched real Lucene's output on the first run. Additional unit tests (in the same file) cover a missing field, a prefix containing literal `*`/`?`/`\` bytes confirmed not glob-interpreted (including a bare trailing `\`, which would trigger `WildcardPattern::new`'s trailing-unpaired-escape fallback if this query mistakenly routed through it), and composing `Clause::Prefix` inside a `BooleanQuery`'s `must` alongside a plain `Clause::Term`. Unit tests in `query.rs` cover `PrefixQuery::new`, equality, the `Clause::From` conversion, and `BooleanQuery::with_must` accepting a bare `PrefixQuery`. **Deferred, same as every other `Clause` variant since task #29**: `lucene-ffi` C-ABI construction of a `Clause::Prefix` clause (the FFI wire format still only builds flat `Clause::Term` clauses; `ffi_search_boolean_query_scored`'s field-name-extraction match now also treats `Prefix` like `Wildcard`/`Phrase`/`Boolean`/`DisjunctionMax`/`ConstantScore`/`Boost`, contributing no field name). No real `IntersectTermsEnum`/`CompiledAutomaton` trie-block-skipping (unchanged from task #1); no regex/`FuzzyQuery` (unchanged scope from task #1). |
| `search/FuzzyQuery` (matching + constant scoring, `Clause` composition) | `lucene-codecs/src/fuzzy.rs::{edit_distance, FuzzyMatch}`, `lucene-codecs/src/blocktree.rs::FieldTerms::fuzzy_intersect`, `lucene-search/src/query.rs::{FuzzyQuery, Clause::Fuzzy}`, `lucene-search/src/lib.rs::{fuzzy_doc_ids, resolve_clause_docs, clause_scores}` | **ported (task #42).** `FuzzyQuery { field: String, term: Vec<u8>, max_edits: u8, prefix_length: usize, transpositions: bool }` is a leaf `Clause::Fuzzy(FuzzyQuery)`, matching every doc that has at least one term (for `query.field`) within `max_edits` edit distance of `term`, restricted to terms sharing `term`'s first `prefix_length` bytes exactly, **union**ed across every matching term (`fuzzy_doc_ids`, structurally identical to task #34/#35's `wildcard_doc_ids`/`prefix_doc_ids` ŌĆö `FieldTerms::fuzzy_intersect` enumerates matching terms, then every matching term's postings' doc IDs are collected, sorted, and deduplicated). Defaults mirror real `FuzzyQuery` exactly: `max_edits = 2` (`FuzzyQuery.defaultMaxEdits`/`LevenshteinAutomata.MAXIMUM_SUPPORTED_DISTANCE`), `prefix_length = 0`, `transpositions = true`. Scoring (`clause_scores`'s `Clause::Fuzzy` arm): the same flat, unscored `1.0` per matching doc as `Clause::Wildcard`/`Clause::Prefix`, for the same reason. **No `LevenshteinAutomata`/`CompiledAutomaton`/`IntersectTermsEnum` machinery** ŌĆö this port instead computes edit distance directly with a plain `O(n*m)` DP (`fuzzy::edit_distance`) each time a candidate term is tested (narrowed first to the sorted range starting with `term`'s `prefix_length`-byte literal prefix, the same binary-search-then-linear-filter shape `FieldTerms::intersect` already established for `WildcardQuery`/`PrefixQuery`), closing `wildcard.rs`'s last remaining explicitly-deferred gap from task #1. **Damerau-Levenshtein-with-transpositions, verified against real Lucene's actual default, not assumed**: `edit_distance(a, b, transpositions: bool)` implements the "restricted"/"optimal string alignment" variant ŌĆö substitution/insertion/deletion/adjacent-transposition each cost 1 edit when `transpositions = true` (real `FuzzyQuery`'s own default), degrading to plain Levenshtein (an adjacent swap costs 2, not 1) when `transpositions = false`. `prefix_length` is an exact-match requirement on the candidate's leading bytes, held entirely outside the edit-distance budget (real `FuzzyQuery`'s `prefixLength` semantics), not a "free" edit region within it. **Byte-vs-codepoint scope decision, stated explicitly**: real Lucene's `LevenshteinAutomata` operates on UTF-32 codepoints (`FuzzyQuery` decodes the target term via `UnicodeUtil.codePointAt`/`codePointCount` before building the automaton, so a multi-byte character costs one edit unit, not 2-4), but this port's `edit_distance` operates on raw bytes ŌĆö a deliberate shortcut, not an oversight, since this port's terms are `Vec<u8>` with no guaranteed UTF-8 validity and every fixture/test term is ASCII (where one byte and one codepoint coincide, so byte-level distance is pragmatically equivalent here); full codepoint decoding (mirroring `wildcard.rs`'s `utf8_codepoint_len` approach) is deferred as a documented gap for non-ASCII terms, see `fuzzy.rs`'s module doc for the full writeup. **Verified against real Lucene**: `fixtures/src/AppendFuzzyManifest.java` (same append-only pattern as `AppendWildcardManifest.java`/`AppendPrefixManifest.java` ŌĆö opens the already-committed `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` directory read-only, no segment regeneration/ID perturbation) runs eleven real `org.apache.lucene.search.FuzzyQuery`s against `body`'s real terms/postings (`cat`={0,2}, `dog`={0,1}, `bird`={1,4}) ŌĆö exact match, single substitution/insertion/deletion, **the single most important case**: a transposition (`"cta"` vs. target `"cat"`, `maxEdits=1`) matching with `transpositions=true` and *not* matching with `transpositions=false` (confirmed against real Lucene: it does, and it doesn't, exactly as this port's own `edit_distance` predicts), `prefix_length` excluding an otherwise-in-range candidate, and `max_edits` exactly-at-vs-one-over the boundary ŌĆö recording real Lucene's own matched doc IDs into `manifest.properties`' `fuzzy.*` keys. `crates/lucene-search/tests/fuzzy_query_fixtures.rs` re-runs the equivalent `Clause::Fuzzy` query for every recorded case and asserts doc-for-doc agreement, the actual cross-engine proof (not a self-consistency check) ŌĆö all eleven cases matched real Lucene's output on the first run, including the transposition case in both directions. Additional unit tests (in the same file) cover a missing field, an exact-match case against the real fixture, and composing `Clause::Fuzzy` inside a `BooleanQuery`'s `must` alongside a plain `Clause::Term`. `fuzzy.rs`'s own unit tests cover `edit_distance` directly (identical strings, single substitution/insertion/deletion, the transposition-with-vs-without case, multiple transpositions, a multi-edit case (`"kitten"`/`"sitting"`, distance 3)) and `FuzzyMatch` (max-edits boundary, prefix-length exclusion and zero-requirement cases, a candidate shorter than `prefix_length`, exact match, `literal_prefix` extraction including the longer-than-term clamp case). Unit tests in `query.rs` cover `FuzzyQuery::new`'s defaults, the builder methods, the `Clause::From` conversion, and `BooleanQuery::with_must` accepting a bare `FuzzyQuery`. **Deferred, same as every other `Clause` variant since task #29**: `lucene-ffi` C-ABI construction of a `Clause::Fuzzy` clause (the FFI wire format still only builds flat `Clause::Term` clauses; `ffi_search_boolean_query_scored`'s field-name-extraction match now also treats `Fuzzy` like `Wildcard`/`Prefix`/`Phrase`/`Boolean`/`DisjunctionMax`/`ConstantScore`/`Boost`, contributing no field name). No real `IntersectTermsEnum`/`CompiledAutomaton`/`LevenshteinAutomata` trie-block-skipping (unchanged scope from task #1/#34/#35 ŌĆö `fuzzy_intersect` is an `O(n)`-in-field-term-count scan, narrowed by the `prefix_length` literal-prefix range, with an `O(n*m)` DP per candidate); full Unicode-codepoint edit distance for non-ASCII terms (see the byte-vs-codepoint scope decision above). `RegexpQuery` is now ported too ŌĆö see the next row. |
| `search/RegexpQuery` (matching + constant scoring, `Clause` composition) | `lucene-codecs/src/regexp.rs::{RegexpPattern, RegexpError}`, `lucene-codecs/src/blocktree.rs::FieldTerms::regexp_intersect`, `lucene-search/src/query.rs::{RegexpQuery, Clause::Regexp}`, `lucene-search/src/lib.rs::{regexp_doc_ids, resolve_clause_docs, clause_scores, Error::Regexp}` | **ported (task #43), scoped to a restricted Lucene-regexp syntax subset, not real `o.a.l.util.automaton.RegExp`/`CompiledAutomaton`.** `RegexpQuery { field: String, pattern: String }` is a leaf `Clause::Regexp(RegexpQuery)`, matching every doc that has at least one term (for `query.field`) the compiled `pattern` accepts **in full** (real `RegexpQuery`'s whole-term-match convention ŌĆö a pattern like `ca` does *not* match indexed term `cat` as a substring), **union**ed across every matching term (`regexp_doc_ids`, structurally identical to task #34/#35/#42's `wildcard_doc_ids`/`prefix_doc_ids`/`fuzzy_doc_ids` ŌĆö `FieldTerms::regexp_intersect` enumerates matching terms, then every matching term's postings' doc IDs are collected, sorted, and deduplicated). Scoring (`clause_scores`'s `Clause::Regexp` arm): the same flat, unscored `1.0` per matching doc as `Clause::Wildcard`/`Clause::Prefix`/`Clause::Fuzzy`, for the same reason. **Scope decision, made explicitly rather than defaulted to**: no crate in this workspace depends on the `regex` crate (checked ŌĆö no `Cargo.toml` reference anywhere), so this task had a real choice between (a) a hand-built parser/matcher for Lucene's own restricted `RegExp` syntax, or (b) pulling in `regex` and translating/restricting its semantics to Lucene's conventions. **(a) was chosen**: real Lucene's `RegExp` is deliberately not PCRE/Perl regex (no anchors as zero-width assertions, no lookahead/backreferences, and its own `~`/`&` operators standard `regex` doesn't have), so reusing `regex` directly risked either silently accepting syntax Lucene rejects or needing a translation/validation layer nearly as large as writing a purpose-built parser ŌĆö continuing the `fuzzy.rs`/`wildcard.rs` "hand-build a small, honestly-scoped matcher" precedent instead of reaching for an off-the-shelf crate. **Exact syntax subset supported**: literal bytes (with `\`-escaping of any byte, mirroring `WildcardPattern::new`'s escape convention), `.` (any single byte), `*`/`+`/`?` postfix quantifiers on the immediately preceding atom, **`{n}`/`{n,}`/`{n,m}` bounded repetition** (also postfix, mutually exclusive with `*`/`+`/`?` on the same atom ŌĆö added in a follow-up slice after task #43 shipped the rest of this subset; `{0,0}` legally matches zero occurrences, `m < n` or a non-numeric/missing bound is `RegexpError::MalformedRepeat`), `[...]` character classes (literal bytes and/or `a-z`-style ranges, optional leading `^` negation, a trailing unescaped `-` before `]` treated as a literal dash), `(...)` grouping (precedence/quantifier-scope only, no capture), `|` alternation. **Exact subset deliberately NOT supported, rejected with a `RegexpError` parse error rather than silently mis-parsed**: `~` (complement) and `&` (intersection) ŌĆö Lucene-specific operators that would need real automaton complementation/intersection, materially beyond this slice's backtracking-matcher scope (see the follow-up task's investigation note below) ŌĆö and named classes (`\d`, `\w`, POSIX `[:alpha:]`). Anchors `^`/`$` are not special-cased at all outside `[^...]`'s negation position (irrelevant given whole-term matching is already always in effect, matching real Lucene's own treatment of `^`/`$` as ordinary literals in `RegExp`). **Implementation**: `Parser` (recursive-descent, grammar in `regexp.rs`'s doc comment) builds a small AST (`Literal`/`AnyByte`/`Class`/`Concat`/`Star`/`Plus`/`Ques`/`Repeat`/`Alt`); `RegexpPattern::matches` is a continuation-passing backtracking matcher (`node_match`/`concat_match`/`star_match`/`repeat_match`) enforcing whole-term matching by only succeeding when the candidate is consumed to its exact end ŌĆö same "match predicate over already-materialized `FieldTerms`" shape as `fuzzy.rs`/`wildcard.rs`, not a `CompiledAutomaton`/`ByteRunAutomaton` DFA. `RegexpPattern::literal_prefix()` extracts the pattern's guaranteed leading literal byte run (only from a `Concat` root, stopping at the first non-`Literal` node) for `FieldTerms::regexp_intersect`'s binary-search-then-linear-filter narrowing (same trick `wildcard.rs`/`fuzzy.rs` already use); an alternation or a pattern starting with `.`/a class/a quantifier conservatively returns an empty prefix, falling back to a full-field scan ŌĆö always *correct*, just not optimized, the same documented tradeoff `wildcard.rs`'s own `literal_prefix` makes for `*foo`-shaped patterns. **Byte-vs-codepoint scope decision, stated explicitly**: same tradeoff `fuzzy.rs` already documents for edit distance ŌĆö real Lucene's `RegExp`/`Automaton` machinery is codepoint-wide, this module's `.`/class matching is byte-wide, a deliberate shortcut since every fixture/test term and pattern is ASCII (one byte == one codepoint); a multi-byte UTF-8 character under `.` would consume only its first byte here. **Verified against real Lucene**: `fixtures/src/AppendRegexpManifest.java` (same append-only pattern as `AppendFuzzyManifest.java`/`AppendWildcardManifest.java` ŌĆö opens the already-committed `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` directory read-only, no segment regeneration/ID perturbation) runs real `org.apache.lucene.search.RegexpQuery`s against `body`'s real terms/postings (`cat`={0,2}, `dog`={0,1}, `bird`={1,4}) ŌĆö exact literal, **the single most important case**: the whole-term-match convention (`ca` against `cat`, confirmed against real Lucene: no match, exactly as this port's own whole-term-match design predicts), a `.` wildcard matching only 3-byte terms, `*`/`+`/`?` quantifiers, a `[...]` class, two-way and three-way alternation, a no-match case, a missing-field case, and (**follow-up slice**) four `{n,m}` bounded-repetition cases ŌĆö `{n}` exact count (`do{1}g`), `{n,}` unbounded max (`bi{1,}rd`), `{n,m}` both bounds (`ca{1,2}t`), and `{0,1}` behaving like `?` (`do{0,1}g`) ŌĆö recording real Lucene's own matched doc IDs into `manifest.properties`' `regexp.*` keys. `crates/lucene-search/tests/regexp_query_fixtures.rs` re-runs the equivalent `Clause::Regexp` query for every recorded case and asserts doc-for-doc agreement, the actual cross-engine proof (not a self-consistency check) ŌĆö every case matched real Lucene's output. Additional tests in the same file cover a missing field standalone, the whole-term-match convention standalone, composing `Clause::Regexp` inside a `BooleanQuery`'s `must` alongside a plain `Clause::Term`, and a malformed pattern (`a~b`, the `~` complement operator ŌĆö updated from an earlier `{n,m}` example now that bounded repetition is supported) surfacing as `Err(Error::Regexp(_))` rather than panicking. `regexp.rs`'s own unit tests cover every supported construct directly (literal, whole-term-match, `.`, `*`/`+`/`?`, `{n}`/`{n,}`/`{n,m}` bounded repetition incl. exact-count/unbounded-min/both-bounds/zero-min/`{0,0}`/composition with other operators/repeat-on-a-group, classes incl. ranges/negation/trailing-dash-literal, alternation, nested grouping, escapes incl. inside a class) plus every parse-error case (unmatched paren/bracket, empty class, dangling quantifier, malformed repeat ŌĆö missing close brace, non-numeric bound, empty braces, `max < min`, dangling `{` with no preceding atom, each unsupported operator) and `literal_prefix` extraction (pure literal, stops at first non-literal, stops at a bounded repeat, alternation is empty, leading wildcard/class is empty, empty pattern). `blocktree.rs` adds `regexp_intersect_over_materialized_field` (literal-prefix-narrowed range, no-useful-prefix alternation, whole-term-match no-substring case, out-of-range no-match) over the same hand-built multi-term field `intersect_prefix_and_wildcard_over_materialized_field` already uses. **Deferred, same as every other `Clause` variant since task #29**: `lucene-ffi` C-ABI construction of a `Clause::Regexp` clause (the FFI wire format still only builds flat `Clause::Term` clauses; `ffi_search_boolean_query_scored`'s field-name-extraction match now also treats `Regexp` like `Fuzzy`/`Wildcard`/`Prefix`/`Phrase`/`Boolean`/`DisjunctionMax`/`ConstantScore`/`Boost`, contributing no field name). No real `IntersectTermsEnum`/`CompiledAutomaton` trie-block-skipping (unchanged scope from task #1/#34/#35/#42 ŌĆö `regexp_intersect` is an `O(n)`-in-field-term-count scan, narrowed by the literal-prefix range, with a backtracking match per candidate); full Unicode-codepoint matching for non-ASCII terms/patterns (see the scope section above). **`~`/`&` explicitly investigated and deferred, not silently skipped**: real Lucene's `RegExp` builds these via `Automaton` complement/intersection over the *entire* language `Operations.complement`/`Operations.intersection` operate on (a full DFA construction, including determinization/minimization for complement ŌĆö `Operations.complement` explicitly builds a *total* automaton over the whole alphabet before subtracting), which has no cheap backtracking-matcher analogue: this module's matcher only ever asks "can some path consume the input," a question with no natural encoding of "and no other pattern could also consume it" (`&`) or, far worse, "match everything this pattern does NOT match" (`~`, which requires enumerating/complementing over the whole byte alphabet at every position, not just refusing a match). A subtly-wrong hand-rolled complement (e.g. one that only complements at the top level, or one that mishandles a class/group boundary) would be worse than an honest, typed `RegexpError::UnsupportedOperator` ŌĆö so `~`/`&` remain rejected at parse time pending an actual automaton-based engine, which is a materially larger undertaking (full NFA/DFA construction + determinization) than this module's scope. **Bounded-repeat nesting DoS mitigation**: adding `{n,m}` introduced a new pathological case a backtracking matcher over the prior operator set never had -- small, ordinary-looking nested bounds (e.g. `(a{1,15}){1,15}`) can combine multiplicatively and hang on a long failing input, confirmed by reproduction (a 40-byte all-`a` term against that pattern hung before this fix). `Pattern::matches` now runs every match under a fixed `MATCH_STEP_BUDGET` (1,000,000 node visits, charged in `node_match` itself so it bounds total work regardless of which node shape drives the blowup) and reports "no match" rather than hanging once exhausted -- the same fail-fast direction real Lucene's automaton construction takes (rejecting a pathological pattern up front) rather than exploring it at query time. Regression-tested directly (`nested_bounded_repeat_does_not_hang_on_a_failing_match`). |
| `queries/spans/SpanTermQuery`/`SpanNearQuery`/`SpanOrQuery` (matching + flat scoring, `Clause` composition) | `lucene-search/src/query.rs::{SpanQuery, Clause::Span}`, `lucene-search/src/lib.rs::{span_matches_in_doc, span_near_matches, combine_span_clauses, collect_span_leaves, span_doc_ids, search_span_query}` | **ported (task #55), scoped to direct in-memory span computation over a doc's already-decoded position lists, not real Lucene's lazy `Spans` iterator API (`nextStartPosition`/`nextDoc`/`advance`, buffered `NearSpansOrdered`/`NearSpansUnordered` merge state) -- see below for the exact scope decision.** `SpanQuery` is a closed three-variant enum -- `SpanTerm { field, term }` (a leaf matching a single term's every occurrence, real `SpanTermQuery`'s exact semantics: each occurrence becomes its own `(position, position + 1)` span, not just "does it occur"), `SpanNear { clauses: Vec<SpanQuery>, slop: u32, in_order: bool }` (real `SpanNearQuery`'s equivalent), and `SpanOr { clauses: Vec<SpanQuery> }` (real `SpanOrQuery`'s equivalent, a pure union) -- wired into a new `Clause::Span(SpanQuery)` variant, resolved via `resolve_clause_docs`/`clause_scores` following the exact `Wildcard`/`Prefix`/`Fuzzy`/`Regexp` precedent: flat, unscored `1.0` per matching doc (real span-aware scoring, `SpanWeight`/`SpanScorer`, is a separate, unscoped problem). **This is a genuinely different query family from `PhraseQuery`** (task #19/#28): a span query's result is the actual matching **span ranges** (`[start, end)` position pairs), not just a doc match/no-match, and those ranges compose (a `SpanNear` of `SpanNear`s, etc). **Scope decision, made explicitly**: rather than porting the lazy `Spans` iterator machinery, `span_matches_in_doc` computes every matching span directly against a doc's already-decoded per-leaf position lists -- the same "compute matches directly against decoded data" shape `phrase_matches_in_doc`/`phrase_matches_in_doc_sloppy` already use for `PhraseQuery` -- an honestly-scoped MVP: does a doc contain a valid span for this query, and what are its matching span ranges, computed eagerly rather than via a lazy iterator with buffered merge state. `SpanTerm` returns every occurrence as its own span; `SpanOr` returns the sorted, deduplicated union of every sub-query's own spans; `SpanNear` (`span_near_matches`/`combine_span_clauses`) evaluates every combination of one span per sub-clause (a cartesian product -- acceptable for this scope, not the sub-linear early termination a real lazy `NearSpans` iterator gets, same "correctness first, profile before optimizing" call this crate's other multi-term matchers already make) and accepts a combination iff its arranged spans are non-overlapping and increasing with total slack (`sum(next.start - prev.end)` over adjacent arranged spans, generalizing `phrase_matches_in_doc_sloppy`'s single-position "moves needed" formula to `[start, end)` span ranges) at most `slop`. **The `in_order` differentiator, this task's key new capability vs `PhraseQuery`**: `in_order == true` requires the chosen sub-spans non-overlapping and increasing in the query's own clause order (real `SpanNearQuery(clauses, slop, true)`); `in_order == false` instead sorts the chosen sub-spans by **start position** (not clause order) before the same check, accepting **any** relative order among the clauses provided the spans still fit within the slop budget (real `SpanNearQuery(clauses, slop, false)`) -- a capability `PhraseQuery`'s own sloppy matching (task #28) deliberately does not have (that was explicitly scoped to in-order-only; see that row above). `span_doc_ids` (the `Clause::Span` doc-ID resolver) collects every distinct leaf `SpanTerm`'s `(field, term)` pair `query` touches (`collect_span_leaves`), fetches each one's live-filtered position-list map via the same `term_doc_positions` helper `search_phrase_query` uses, and takes the **union of every leaf's own doc list** as a safe, simple over-approximation of the true candidate set (rather than a tighter, per-variant candidate computation, e.g. a `SpanNear`'s candidates could be the conjunction of its sub-clauses' doc lists) -- `span_matches_in_doc` itself already correctly reports "no match" for a candidate doc that doesn't actually satisfy a stricter requirement, so the wider set only costs some wasted lookups, never an incorrect result. Requires `pos_in` whenever `query` has at least one leaf (an `Err(Error::MissingPosInput)` otherwise) -- unlike `PhraseQuery`, even a single-leaf `SpanTerm` needs real per-occurrence positions, so there is no single-term fast path skipping positions the way a length-1 `PhraseQuery` has. **Verified against real Lucene**: `fixtures/src/GenBlockTree.java` gained doc8 (`"pos"` field: `"delta"@0`, `"gamma"@1` -- occurrence order deliberately reversed relative to a `SpanNearQuery` built with clauses in `[gamma, delta]` order) plus `field.pos.span.*` manifest keys, recorded by *actually running* real `org.apache.lucene.queries.spans.SpanNearQuery`/`SpanOrQuery` (the `lucene-queries` module, not `lucene-core` -- these classes are not in `lucene-core-10.5.0.jar`) against this fixture at generation time: real Lucene's own verdict is `SpanNearQuery([gamma, delta], slop=0, inOrder=true)` does NOT match doc8 while `SpanNearQuery([gamma, delta], slop=0, inOrder=false)` DOES -- exactly the `in_order` differentiator this task's own scoping flagged as most likely to be subtly wrong if hand-derived without checking real Lucene, and `crates/lucene-search/tests/span_query_fixtures.rs::span_near_in_order_and_out_of_order_agree_with_real_lucene` confirms this port's implementation agrees with both real-Lucene verdicts (plus a `SpanTerm` sanity check and a `SpanOrQuery` cross-engine check in the same file). Unit tests (`lucene-search/src/lib.rs`) additionally cover: `SpanTerm` matching every occurrence in a multi-occurrence doc; `SpanNear` in-order matching an ordered adjacent pair and rejecting a reversed one; `SpanNear` slop-boundary exactness (exactly-at-limit matches, one-over doesn't); `SpanOr` union semantics (either/neither/both sub-spans matching); nested `SpanNear`-of-`SpanNear` composition (including the no-match-when-inner-fails-to-align case); empty-clauses and missing-leaf edge cases. **Deferred, same as every other `Clause` variant since task #29**: `lucene-ffi` C-ABI construction of a `Clause::Span` clause (the FFI wire format still only builds flat `Clause::Term` clauses; `ffi_search_boolean_query_scored`'s field-name-extraction match now also treats `Span` like `Regexp`/`Fuzzy`/`Wildcard`/`Prefix`/`Phrase`/`Boolean`/`DisjunctionMax`/`ConstantScore`/`Boost`, contributing no field name). A lazy `Spans` iterator API, real span-aware scoring (`SpanWeight`/`SpanScorer`), and the other real span query subclasses this port doesn't cover (`SpanNotQuery`, `SpanContainingQuery`/`SpanWithinQuery`, `SpanFirstQuery`/`SpanPositionRangeQuery`, `SpanMultiTermQueryWrapper`) are all out of scope, tracked here rather than half-implemented. |
| `search/SortedNumericDocValuesField.newSlowRangeQuery`/`SortedSetDocValuesField.newSlowRangeQuery` (single- and multi-valued), `search/SortField.Type.LONG` (single-key sort), `search/SortedNumericSelector`/`SortedSetSelector` (MIN/MAX) | `lucene-search/src/doc_value_query.rs::{search_numeric_range, search_numeric_range_with_skip_index, search_sorted_ord_range, sort_by_numeric_doc_value, ValueSelector, search_multi_valued_range, sort_by_multi_valued_doc_value}` | **Single-valued NUMERIC/SORTED ported (task #21); multi-valued SORTED_NUMERIC/SORTED_SET range+sort ported (task #31, closing the gap task #21 deferred); skip-index-driven NUMERIC range scan ported (this task, closing task #21/#31's remaining "full sweep only" gap for NUMERIC).** `search_numeric_range` sweeps every live doc in `[0, max_doc)` and reports one matching a `[min, max]` inclusive range on `doc_values::numeric_value` to a `Collector` ŌĆö the correct fallback for a field with no skip index (this port parses no BKD point index for range queries either, so a full sweep is the only option in that case). **`search_numeric_range_with_skip_index`** is the skip-index-driven sibling: given an already-decoded `doc_values::DocValuesSkipIndex` (`doc_values::parse_skip_index`, task #185), it walks the index's intervals in doc-ID order and skips a whole interval's doc range without decoding a single value whenever that interval's finest-level `[min_value, max_value]` summary can't intersect the query's `[min, max]` (mirrors real Lucene's `PointRangeQuery`-style block-skipping, just over doc-values blocks instead of BKD leaves); only intervals that might match get scanned doc-by-doc. Returns the number of values actually decoded (for callers/tests that want to confirm real skipping happened, not just "didn't crash"). A doc with no value (`numeric_value` returns `None`, legitimate for a sparse field) never matches, including an all-`i64` range, in both functions. `search_sorted_ord_range` is the same shape over a single-valued SORTED field's ordinal (`sorted_ord`); `min_ord == max_ord` is an equality predicate ŌĆö resolving a term to its ordinal is left to the caller (`terms_dict`). `sort_by_numeric_doc_value` is a standalone post-processing function (not a `Collector` variant ŌĆö see its doc comment for why: sorting needs the whole candidate set in hand before producing the first output pair, unlike `Collector`'s per-doc streaming callback or `TopDocsCollector`'s incremental top-`N` heap) that takes an already-collected candidate doc-ID list (e.g. `search_term_query`'s output) and returns `(doc_id, value)` pairs ascending by value, ties broken by ascending doc ID (same convention `TopDocsCollector` documents for a score tie); a candidate doc missing a value is either dropped (`MissingValue::Exclude`) or given a caller-supplied substitute (`MissingValue::Default`), both explicit, documented policies. **Task #31's multi-valued addition**: `ValueSelector` (`Min`/`Max`) reduces a doc's multiple values to one comparable value, real Lucene's `SortedNumericSelector.Type`/`SortedSetSelector.Type` equivalent scoped to MIN/MAX only (`MIDDLE_MIN`/`MIDDLE_MAX` are deferred ŌĆö a niche median-ish reduction with no numeric-field equivalent, documented as a small follow-up in the module doc). `search_multi_valued_range`/`sort_by_multi_valued_doc_value` are the multi-valued siblings of the two single-valued functions above, built directly on the already-read-side-complete `doc_values::sorted_numeric_values` (confirmed to genuinely decode a doc's *entire* multi-valued list, not just one value, making this task tractable without further codec work); both take a `SortedNumericEntry`, which ŌĆö since `sorted_numeric_values` already reads SORTED_NUMERIC values and a multi-valued `SortedSetKind::Multi` field's ordinals identically ŌĆö means these two functions serve **both** SORTED_NUMERIC and SORTED_SET's multi-valued case with no separate sorted-set-specific code path (pass the `Multi` variant's `ords` entry for SORTED_SET; a single-valued `SortedSetKind::Single` field still uses `search_sorted_ord_range`, no reduction needed). **Deliberately deferred**: MIDDLE_MIN/MIDDLE_MAX selectors, descending sort/multiple sort fields (single ascending key only), and skip-index-driven range pruning for `search_sorted_ord_range`/`search_multi_valued_range` (SORTED/SORTED_NUMERIC/SORTED_SET ŌĆö only the NUMERIC path has a skip index to consult today). **Verified against real Lucene**: single-valued functions reuse the already-checked-in `fixtures/data/doc_values_index/` (`varying`/`sparse` fields) and `fixtures/data/sorted_dv_index/` (`sorted` field) fixtures already opened by `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/{doc_values,sorted_doc_values}_fixtures.rs`. **`search_numeric_range_with_skip_index` reuses `fixtures/data/doc_values_skip_index/`** (task #185's fixture, `fixtures/src/GenDocValuesSkipIndex.java`: 36,000 docs, strictly-increasing NUMERIC values, a genuinely 2-level skip index) ŌĆö differential tests prove it returns byte-for-byte the same matched-doc set as `search_numeric_range` across a narrow single-doc range, a range spanning one base interval, an unbounded match-everything range, and an out-of-domain match-nothing range, plus `live_docs` filtering; separate assertions on the returned decoded-value count prove real interval skipping happens (zero decodes for the match-nothing range, far fewer than 36,000 for the narrow ranges, all 36,000 only for the unbounded range) rather than merely "doesn't crash". The multi-valued functions reuse `fixtures/data/multi_valued_dv_index/` (real `IndexWriter`-written via `fixtures/src/GenMultiValuedDocValues.java`, already checked in and already opened by `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/multi_valued_doc_values_fixtures.rs` for read-side verification, so no new Java generator was needed): a SORTED_NUMERIC `nums` field (values `[5,10],NONE,[7],[1,2,3],NONE` across 5 docs) and a SORTED_SET `tags` field (ords `[0,2],NONE,[1],[0],[1,2]` over 3 terms), both exercising the sparse (`IndexedDISI`) and multi-value (`DirectMonotonicReader` address-range) paths. Fixture-driven tests confirm boundary inclusivity, `live_docs` filtering, missing-doc exclusion under an unbounded range, and ŌĆö the key selector-specific case ŌĆö that a doc's MIN falling in range while its MAX doesn't (and vice versa) is decided by the selector alone, not both values; the same range/sort functions are additionally exercised directly against the SORTED_SET `tags` ordinals to confirm they generalize. Also unit-tested in isolation: `ValueSelector::reduce` (MIN/MAX correctness, empty-values case), tie-break-by-ascending-doc-ID, both `MissingValue` policies, empty-candidates, and decode-error propagation. |
| `facet/sortedset/SortedSetDocValuesFacetCounts` (basic per-ordinal facet counting only, not the `lucene-facet` module's reader-state/taxonomy machinery) | `lucene-search/src/facets.rs::{facet_counts, resolve_labels, top_n_facets, FacetCount}` | **ported (task #50), single-segment, query-scoped, both scope decisions documented explicitly below.** `facet_counts` takes an already-opened SORTED_SET field's `SortedNumericEntry` (the ordinal-array half ŌĆö the same shape `doc_value_query.rs`'s multi-valued functions already take for the `Multi` variant of `SortedSetKind`) plus a caller-supplied matching-doc-ID slice, and increments a counter for **every** ordinal of every matching doc (`sorted_numeric_values`, already-decoded ŌĆö no new format decoding needed, exactly the "thin aggregation layer" this task's brief called for), so a multi-valued doc correctly increments more than one counter, not just a "primary" value. `resolve_labels` turns per-ordinal counts into `FacetCount { ord, label, count }` via `terms_dict::decode_all_terms` (the already-existing `lookupOrd`-equivalent this port built for task #4/#21/#31). `top_n_facets` sorts descending by count, ties broken by ascending ordinal (this crate's usual determinism convention, e.g. `sort_by_numeric_doc_value`'s ascending-doc-ID tie-break), then truncates ŌĆö real Lucene's `Facets.getTopChildren` convention. **Scope decision 1 ŌĆö single-segment only, not index-wide**: real Lucene's faceting is index-wide because `SortedSetDocValuesReaderState` builds one *merged* ordinal map across every segment's terms dictionary up front; this port has no such merged map, and each segment's SORTED_SET terms dictionary independently assigns its own ordinals (`terms_dict.rs`), so summing raw per-ordinal counts across segments would silently conflate unrelated terms that happen to share an ordinal number in different segments. `facet_counts` therefore operates on one already-opened segment only; a multi-segment caller must merge per-segment results **by resolved string label** (via `resolve_labels`), not by raw ordinal ŌĆö a straightforward follow-up once per-segment counting is proven correct (which it now is), not implemented here. **Scope decision 2 ŌĆö query-scoped counting is the only mode**: real Lucene's `FacetsCollector` has no separate "count the whole index" API distinct from running a query that matches everything; `facet_counts` mirrors that by taking an explicit matching-doc-ID slice with no separate all-docs code path ŌĆö a caller wanting "every doc in the segment" passes every live doc ID as that slice. **Empty-matching-set convention, documented rather than left ambiguous**: an empty matching-doc-ID slice returns a result with every ordinal present at count `0` (a `Vec<u64>` sized to the full terms-dictionary count), not an empty `Vec` ŌĆö keeps the result's ordinal set always equal to "every term in the dictionary" regardless of match count, so callers never special-case resolving labels for an empty match set. **Verified against real Lucene**: reuses the already-checked-in `fixtures/data/multi_valued_dv_index/` fixture (task #31, `fixtures/src/GenMultiValuedDocValues.java`) ŌĆö no new Java generator was needed because its manifest already records real ground truth computed via a straightforward per-doc `SortedSetDocValues.nextOrd()`/`lookupOrd()` iteration (`field.tags.ords`/`field.tags.terms` keys), a genuine real-Lucene-computed cross-check without depending on the `lucene-facet` module (not a project dependency) ŌĆö matching this task's own documented reasoning for why a manual per-doc iteration is an honest substitute. Tests confirm: counts match the manifest's real per-ordinal ground truth exactly (`facet_counts_match_real_lucene_ground_truth`); a multi-valued doc (`tags` = `[red, blue]`) increments both ordinals, not just the first (`multi_valued_doc_increments_every_ordinal_not_just_first`); excluding a doc from the matching set drops exactly its contribution and nothing else (`doc_not_in_matching_set_contributes_nothing`); an empty matching set yields all-zero counts sized to the full term count (`empty_matching_set_yields_all_zero_counts`); `top_n_facets` sorts descending, truncates, and breaks ties by ascending ordinal (three dedicated tests) plus the `n`-larger-than-available and empty-input edge cases; and decode-error propagation from `sorted_numeric_values` surfaces as `Err`, not a panic. `facets.rs` line coverage: 98.74%. **Deferred, matching the two scope decisions above**: index-wide/multi-segment aggregation (label-keyed merge across segments), and any `lucene-facet`-module concept beyond basic per-ordinal counting (hierarchical/taxonomy facets, drill-down/drill-sideways, range facets) ŌĆö none of which this port has any other supporting machinery for yet either. ~~No `lucene-ffi` exposure~~ ŌĆö closed by the Faceted search FFI exposure task: see the `lucene-ffi` section's `facets.rs`/`results_facets.rs` row for `ffi_facet_counts_sorted_set`. |
| `search/TopFieldCollector` (search-time sort-by-field, numeric single-key only) | `lucene-search/src/collector.rs::{SortDirection, FieldValueDoc, TopFieldCollector}`, `lucene-search/src/doc_value_query.rs::{sort_top_n_by_numeric_doc_value, search_numeric_range_sorted_by_field}` | **ported (task #80).** The first general SEARCH-time "sort matched query results by a doc-value field" collector, distinct from the earlier segment-level index-sort helpers (`sort_by_numeric_doc_value`/`sort_by_multi_valued_doc_value`, task #21/#31, still ascending-only, unchanged by this task). `TopFieldCollector` mirrors `TopDocsCollector`'s exact bounded, always-sorted-`Vec` design (same `O(n)`-per-insert tradeoff), ranking `(doc_id, value: i64)` pairs by `SortDirection::Ascending`/`Descending` instead of `TopDocsCollector`'s score-descending-only order, ties broken by ascending doc ID (same convention). It is deliberately **not** a `Collector`/`ScoringCollector` impl ŌĆö reading a doc's sort value from doc-values is fallible (`doc_values::Error`), and neither trait's `collect` signature carries a `Result` ŌĆö so `TopFieldCollector::offer(doc_id, value)` takes an already-decoded, infallible `i64`; callers do the fallible decode themselves. `sort_top_n_by_numeric_doc_value` is the reusable composition point: given any already-collected candidate doc-ID slice (the same contract `sort_by_numeric_doc_value` already has ŌĆö output of `search_term_query`/`search_boolean_query`/any doc-value range query in this module), a `NumericEntry`, a `SortDirection`, a `MissingValue` policy, and a `top_n` bound, it decodes each candidate via the existing `doc_values::numeric_value` (no new decode logic) and returns the top-`n` `FieldValueDoc`s. `search_numeric_range_sorted_by_field` is a concrete end-to-end wiring of that composition point onto an existing query path: runs `search_numeric_range` into a `VecCollector`, then sorts the matches by a (possibly different) numeric field. **Scope, stated precisely**: numeric doc-value fields only (`SortField.Type.LONG`/`INT` ŌĆö no `DOUBLE` bit-reinterpretation, no String/`SortedDocValues`-based sort); single sort key only, no secondary `Sort` composition; ties always broken by ascending doc ID, matching every other tie-break convention in this crate. **Missing-value handling**: the same `MissingValue::Exclude`/`Default(i64)` policy `sort_by_numeric_doc_value` already established ŌĆö `Exclude` drops a candidate with no value from consideration entirely, `Default(v)` substitutes `v` and lets it compete for a rank normally. **Standalone, not wired into every existing scored-search caller**: `search_term_query`/`search_boolean_query`/`search_term_query_scored`/`search_boolean_query_scored` are unchanged; every existing scored-search entry point still returns relevance order only, and a caller wanting field-sorted results calls one of the two new functions above explicitly. **Verified**: 8 new unit tests in `collector.rs` (empty/zero-`top_n`, ascending order, descending order, top-N truncation in both directions, ascending-doc-ID tie-break, `field_rank_order` direct check) plus 8 new unit tests in `doc_value_query.rs` reusing the real, already-checked-in `fixtures/data/doc_values_index/` fixture's `varying`/`gcd`/`sparse` fields ŌĆö `search_numeric_range_sorted_by_field_end_to_end_real_fixture` queries `gcd in [1000, 1100]` (real values 1000/1025/1075/1200/1050 across docs 0-4, matching docs 0, 1, 2, 4), sorts those matches by the `varying` field (real values -100/7/42/1000/-3), and asserts the exact hand-computed doc-ID order both ascending (`[(0,-100),(4,-3),(1,7),(2,42)]`) and descending (the reverse), plus a top-2-truncated descending case ŌĆö not just "sorted somehow". A hand-built constant-value case separately confirms the ascending-doc-ID tie-break holds under both directions. `sort_top_n_missing_doc_excluded_by_default_policy`/`_gets_default_value` reuse the `sparse` field (5/NONE/15/NONE/25) to confirm both `MissingValue` policies. `cargo test -p lucene-search`: 442 lib tests pass. `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean. **Deferred**: `DOUBLE`/String-field sort keys, multi-key `Sort` composition. ~~`lucene-ffi` C-ABI exposure~~ ŌĆö closed by the TopFieldCollector FFI exposure task: `lucene-ffi/src/range_sort.rs::{ffi_search_numeric_range_sorted_by_field, ffi_search_numeric_range_sorted_by_field_multi_segment}` (see the `range_sort.rs` row below). **Follow-up (task #88): wired into multi-segment search** ŌĆö `lucene-search/src/multi_segment.rs::{merge_multi_segment_by_field, search_numeric_range_sorted_by_field_multi_segment, DocValueSegment}` is the sort-by-field analogue of `merge_multi_segment_scored`: runs the existing, unmodified `search_numeric_range_sorted_by_field` independently per already-opened segment, translates local doc IDs to global via `doc_base`, and merges through `TopFieldCollector` a second time, reusing its ascending-doc-ID tie-break rather than reimplementing it. Sequential only ŌĆö no `rayon`-concurrent sibling yet (unlike the scored path's `merge_multi_segment_scored_concurrent`); adding one without a motivating caller/test would be untested surface, so it's a further follow-up, not silently dropped. Scope otherwise unchanged from `TopFieldCollector` itself (numeric fields, single sort key). Verified by `multi_segment::tests::sort_by_field_multi_segment_translates_doc_ids_across_segments` (two segments with different doc bases, both directions asserted against hand-computed global values) and `sort_by_field_multi_segment_tie_break_is_global_ascending_doc_id` (three equal-valued docs spanning two segments, proving the tie-break survives cross-segment translation). |
| `grouping/CollapsingTopDocsCollector` (field-collapse: keep only the highest-scoring doc per distinct collapse-key value, NUMERIC key only) | `lucene-search/src/collector.rs::{CollapsingCollector}` | **ported, scoped down from real Lucene/Solr's `CollapsingQParserPlugin` collector.** Single-pass algorithm matching real `CollapsingTopDocsCollector` (not two-phase collect-then-rerank): `offer(doc_id, score, key: Option<i64>)` keeps a `HashMap<i64, ScoreDoc>` of one current best-scoring doc per collapse-key value, replacing a group's winner only when a candidate outranks it (reusing `TopDocsCollector`'s own `rank_order` ŌĆö score descending, lower doc ID wins a tie). `top_docs()` does the final top-`n` reduction over just the group winners. **Scope, stated precisely**: NUMERIC doc-values collapse key only (an already-decoded `i64`), not real Lucene's more common SORTED-field ordinal key ŌĆö a SORTED key needs an extra ordinal-to-value resolution step (via the field's terms dictionary, as `facets.rs::resolve_labels` already does for a different purpose) not added here; real `CollapsingTopDocsCollector` itself special-cases NUMERIC vs SORTED internally, so this isn't an invented split. Like `TopFieldCollector`, deliberately **not** a `Collector`/`ScoringCollector` impl (the collapse key is a fallible doc-value decode) ŌĆö callers decode each candidate's key themselves and call `offer` with the already-decoded `Option<i64>`. **Missing collapse-key value (`key: None`)**: kept, not discarded, and **not** collapsed together with other missing-key docs ŌĆö each survives as its own singleton group, i.e. this port implements Solr's `nullPolicy=EXPAND` (a real, documented policy value), not the `IGNORE` default; chosen as the simpler single case (no separate "drop" path needed alongside "keep, uncollapsed"). **Verified**: 8 new unit tests in `collector.rs` ŌĆö empty input, `top_n == 0`, multiple docs sharing one key (only the highest score survives), distinct keys all appearing subject to top-N truncation, missing-key docs each surviving independently, group-winner replacement on a better candidate, and the ascending-doc-ID tie-break within a group. `cargo test --workspace` passes; `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean. **Deferred**: SORTED/ordinal-keyed collapsing, `nullPolicy=IGNORE`/other Solr null policies, multi-segment wiring (collector-level only, following the same "collector lands first, multi-segment wiring is a documented follow-up" pattern `TopFieldCollector`'s own row above records), `lucene-ffi` C-ABI exposure. |
| `facet/range/LongRangeFacetCounts`/`DoubleRangeFacetCounts` (bucket counting only, not the `lucene-facet` module's reader-state machinery) | `lucene-search/src/facets.rs::{NumericRange, range_facet_counts}` | **ported (task #58), same module and conventions as task #50's SortedSet facet counting above, not a parallel implementation.** `range_facet_counts` takes an already-opened NUMERIC field's `doc_values::NumericEntry`, a caller-supplied `&[NumericRange]` (each with a `label` and independently inclusive/exclusive `min`/`max` bounds), and a matching-doc-ID slice, and returns `(label, count)` pairs in the **same order as the input `ranges` slice** ŌĆö real Lucene's `FacetResult.labelValues` preserves caller-specified range order, not sorted by count (unlike `top_n_facets`'s deliberate sort for the string-facet case). Reuses `doc_values::numeric_value` (task #21/#31's decode) directly for each doc's value ŌĆö no new decoding. **Ranges may overlap by design, not by oversight**: real Lucene never requires ranges to partition the value space, so `range_facet_counts` checks every range independently per doc and increments each one whose bounds the doc's value satisfies ŌĆö a doc matching two overlapping ranges is counted in both, not assigned to a single "winning" bucket. **Missing-value rule matches `doc_value_query.rs`'s existing convention exactly**: a doc with no value for the field (`numeric_value` returns `None`) contributes to no range, including an unbounded-looking one like `i64::MIN..=i64::MAX` on both ends. **Empty-matching-set convention matches task #50's `facet_counts`**: an empty `matching_docs` slice returns every range present at count 0, not an empty `Vec`. **Boundary handling** (`NumericRange::contains`) applies `min_inclusive`/`max_inclusive` independently (`>=`/`>` and `<=`/`<`), so all four combinations are representable. **Verified against real Lucene**: reuses the already-checked-in `fixtures/data/doc_values_index/` fixture (task #21/#31, `varying` field: -100/7/42/1000/-3 across docs 0-4, `sparse` field: 5/NONE/15/NONE/25) ŌĆö no new Java generator needed, since bucket assignment is hand-verified directly against those already-differentially-verified recorded values rather than re-deriving decode correctness. Tests cover: non-overlapping ranges partitioning the 5 docs correctly; an overlapping-ranges case where doc 2 (value 42) is counted in two overlapping ranges; all four inclusive/exclusive boundary combinations tested precisely at the boundary value 42 itself (`[42,42]` matches, `[42,42)` and `(42,42]` both exclude it, `(7,1000)` still matches 42 while excluding the endpoint docs); the `sparse` field's missing docs never counting under an unbounded range; a doc excluded from `matching_docs` contributing nothing; an empty `matching_docs` yielding all-zero counts; caller-specified range order preserved regardless of count; and decode-error propagation surfacing as `Err`. `facets.rs` line coverage: 99.10% (up from 98.74% pre-task). **Deferred, same scope boundary as task #50**: index-wide/multi-segment range aggregation, and any `lucene-facet`-module concept beyond basic bucket counting (hierarchical/taxonomy facets, drill-down/drill-sideways). ~~No `lucene-ffi` exposure~~ ŌĆö closed by the Faceted search FFI exposure task: see the `lucene-ffi` section's `facets.rs`/`results_facets.rs` row for `ffi_range_facet_counts`. |
| `search/ConjunctionDISI`, `DisjunctionDISIApproximation` (merge algorithms only, not the full `DocIdSetIterator`/`TwoPhaseIterator` class hierarchy) | `lucene-search/src/docid_set.rs::{Conjunction, Disjunction, Excluding}` | **ported as plain `Iterator<Item = i32>` adapters**, not a bespoke `next_doc`/`advance` trait ŌĆö see the module's doc comment for why `std::iter::Peekable` already covers what real Lucene's `DocIdSetIterator` needs here. `Conjunction` is leapfrog (advance-to-current-max, repeat until all agree), `Disjunction` is a simple per-step min-scan (not a min-heap ŌĆö acceptable first cut per `rust-performance`'s "correctness first, profile before optimizing", revisit if clause counts grow), `Excluding` is the `must_not` AND-NOT filter. Boxed (`Box<dyn Iterator<Item = i32>>`) rather than monomorphized, since clause count is runtime-determined (`Vec<TermQuery>`) ŌĆö no closed set of shapes to monomorphize over the way a fixed-arity merge would allow. No `TwoPhaseIterator`/approximation-then-confirm split exists yet (nothing needs it: every clause here is an already-fully-decoded `TermQuery` doc list, not an expensive-to-confirm match). Unit-tested directly (no fixture needed ŌĆö pure merge logic over synthetic doc-ID lists) for no-overlap/full-overlap/partial-overlap/empty-clause/single-clause/no-clauses cases on both `Conjunction` and `Disjunction`, plus `Excluding`'s exclude-nothing/exclude-everything/exclude-disjoint-from-base/empty-base cases. |
| `search/WANDScorer`, `ImpactsDISI`, `MaxScoreCache` | `lucene-search/src/lib.rs::{search_term_query_scored_maxscore, search_boolean_query_scored_maxscore}` | **partially ported, scoped narrowly on both the single-term and `BooleanQuery` sides ŌĆö no full multi-way WAND pivot selection.** `search_term_query_scored`/`search_boolean_query_scored` (the plain scored paths) remain exactly as before: eagerly materializing every matching doc's score with no competitive-score threshold at all. Two separate, narrowly-scoped MAXSCORE-pruned siblings now exist alongside them: <br>- **`search_term_query_scored_maxscore`** (single `TermQuery`, `lucene_codecs::postings::LazyDocsCursor`-backed): once `collector::TopDocsCollector` is holding a full top-`n`, a level-0 block whose `similarity::max_score_for_impacts` upper bound can't beat the collector's current worst kept score is skipped whole (`advance()`d past its last doc, never decoded). Falls back to `search_term_query_scored` verbatim when `doc_in` is `None`, `docFreq <= 1`, or an index option `LazyDocsCursor` doesn't support. <br>- **`search_boolean_query_scored_maxscore`** (BooleanQuery WAND/MAXSCORE dynamic pruning task): a pure SHOULD-disjunction `BooleanQuery` (`must`/`must_not` both empty, `minimum_should_match <= 1`) of plain `Clause::Term` clauses only (no nested `Boolean`/`Phrase`/`DisjunctionMax`/wildcard-family/points clause), each clause's term with `docFreq > 1`. Implements a **simplified two-tier essential/non-essential-style skip, not full multi-way WAND pivot selection** ŌĆö an explicit, documented scope narrowing (see that function's own doc comment for the full algorithm): each clause gets its own `LazyDocsCursor`, merged by taking the minimum current doc ID across active cursors; before each round, a clause still positioned in a real (non-tail) level-0 block has its own current-block bound (`similarity::max_score_for_impacts`) compared against `threshold - sum(every OTHER active clause's per-clause global bound)`, where a clause's global bound (`idf(doc_freq, doc_count)`, always valid since BM25's `tf_norm` component is strictly `< 1.0` for any finite `freq`) stands in for that other clause's true contribution rather than that other clause's own (potentially block-stale) current bound ŌĆö strictly more conservative than a fully-refreshed multi-way WAND, never incorrect. Falls back to `search_boolean_query_scored` verbatim the moment any precondition above doesn't hold, or a clause's term doesn't exist/its field doesn't support `lazy_postings`. Both functions share one thread-local skip counter (`test_only_maxscore_block_skip_counter`, `#[cfg(any(test, feature = "test-support"))]`-gated) proving real per-clause block decode is skipped, not just that results match the eager path. **Not yet ported**: `ImpactsDISI`/`MaxScoreCache`-equivalent shared machinery, full multi-way WAND pivot selection for `BooleanQuery` (more than two tiers, continuously-refreshed per-clause block bounds for every clause rather than a global stand-in for "other" clauses), and any dynamic pruning for `PhraseQuery`/`DisjunctionMaxQuery`/nested-`Boolean` scored search. |
| `search/IndexSearcher.search` fan-out + `TopDocs.merge` (matching/scoring fan-out and global merge, no `DirectoryReader` abstraction) | `lucene-search/src/multi_segment.rs::{OpenSegment, merge_multi_segment_scored, search_term_query_multi_segment, search_boolean_query_multi_segment}` | **ported (task #41), scoped precisely below.** Real `IndexSearcher.search` iterates every `LeafReaderContext`, scores/collects each one locally using that segment's own `docBase` to translate local doc IDs to global ones, then merges per-segment `TopDocs` (`TopDocs.merge`/`HitQueue` tie-break: score descending, lower doc ID wins a tie). This port has no `LeafReaderContext`/`DirectoryReader` object to iterate ŌĆö callers instead pass a plain `&[OpenSegment]` (each entry bundling one already-opened segment's `fields`/`doc_in`/`pos_in`/`pay_in`/`live_docs` plus a caller-computed `doc_base`, the sum of every earlier segment's `maxDoc`). **One shared generic fan-out+merge core** (`merge_multi_segment_scored`), not one copy per query type: every scored query function in this crate already reduces to the same `Vec<ScoreDoc>` shape via `TopDocsCollector`, so the merge step (translate by `doc_base`, re-rank, truncate to `top_n`) needs nothing query-type-specific ŌĆö `search_term_query_multi_segment`/`search_boolean_query_multi_segment` are thin wrappers around that one core, calling `search_term_query_scored`/`search_boolean_query_scored` per segment; a third query type's multi-segment entry point is another equally thin wrapper, not a second merge implementation.
