Each segment is collected into its own bounded `TopDocsCollector::new(top_n)` before the cross-segment merge (matching real per-leaf `TopFieldCollector` behavior, and provably lossless: a global top-`top_n` can never need more than `top_n` hits from one segment). The merge itself reuses `TopDocsCollector`'s own comparator a second time (feeding every segment's already-ranked, doc-base-translated hits through one more fresh collector) rather than reimplementing the tie-break rule. **Explicit idf/scoring-parity scope decision ŌĆö read carefully**: real `BM25Similarity`'s `idf` is computed from `CollectionStatistics`/`TermStatistics` gathered **index-wide** across every segment (`IndexSearcher.termStatistics`/`collectionStatistics`), not per-segment. This port's existing scored query functions (`term_doc_scores`, `lib.rs`, unchanged by this task) compute `idf` from **that one segment's own** `docFreq`/`docCount` (`blocktree::FieldTerms`/`TermStats`) ŌĆö there is no index-wide statistics aggregation anywhere in this port, and this task does not add one (that would need a `DirectoryReader`-level aggregation step across every segment's term dictionary before scoring starts, out of scope here). Consequently: **this task claims "correct matching + correct per-segment-relative BM25 scoring + correct global merge order," not "byte-for-byte parity with real multi-segment Lucene's BM25 scores"** ŌĆö whenever a term's `docFreq`/`docCount` genuinely differ across segments (the common case for a >1-segment index), a per-segment idf and an index-wide idf diverge, and this port computes the former. **Verified**: unit tests in `multi_segment.rs` isolate the merge core with synthetic per-segment scores (interleaved/overlapping scores across 2-3 segments, truncation to `top_n`, a zero-match segment, cross-segment tie-break by ascending global doc ID, `top_n == 0`, zero segments, a single segment with nonzero `doc_base`), plus end-to-end calls through both public wrappers against the real `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` segment. **Cross-engine verification** (`tests/multi_segment_fixtures.rs`): no genuine 2+-segment real-Lucene fixture exists in this repo yet, so ŌĆö per this task's documented next-best alternative ŌĆö the same real, `IndexWriter`-produced `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` segment is opened **twice** (as "segment 0" at `doc_base=0` and "segment 1" at `doc_base=` that segment's own real `maxDoc`), modeling a genuine two-segment index; each "segment"'s real BM25 scores (already fixture-proven by `scoring_fixtures.rs`) are independently concatenated/translated/sorted by this test itself (not by calling the code under test twice) and asserted equal, doc-for-doc and score-for-score, to `search_term_query_multi_segment`'s actual output ŌĆö proving the merge/doc-base-translation/tie-break logic against real recorded scores, the highest-risk "looks locally correct per-segment, wrong globally" bug class this task's brief specifically calls out. **Still deferred**: real index-wide `CollectionStatistics`-based idf (above); a genuine multi-segment Java fixture generator; multi-segment support for `PhraseQuery`/`DisjunctionMaxQuery`/`ConstantScoreQuery`/`BoostQuery`/`WildcardQuery`/`PrefixQuery` (each would be another thin wrapper around `merge_multi_segment_scored`, not yet added). `lucene-ffi` C-ABI exposure is now closed by task #51 (see its own row below). **`doc_base` computation and per-file segment opening are no longer manual** -- see the `DirectoryReader`/`SegmentReader` row directly below (task #45). |
| `index/DirectoryReader.open(Directory)` + `SegmentReader` (federated segment-opening only, not `MultiTerms`/a unified leaf abstraction) | `lucene-search/src/directory_reader.rs::{DirectoryReader, SegmentReader, OpenedSegments}` | **ported (task #45), scoped precisely below.** `DirectoryReader::open(dir)` finds the latest `segments_N` (new `lucene_index::segment_infos::read_latest`, a thin wrapper over the already-existing `lucene_store::directory::read_latest_commit` + `parse`), opens one `SegmentReader` per listed segment, and computes each segment's `doc_base` as the running sum of every earlier segment's `maxDoc` -- the two things the task #41 row above flags as still manual. Per segment, only the files that segment actually has get opened, checked against `SegmentInfo.files` rather than assumed: `.tim`/`.tip`/`.tmd`/`.doc`/`.pos`/`.pay` are opened together or not at all (a segment with none of them -- e.g. this port's stored-fields-only fixtures, see `segment_writer.rs`'s doc comment -- gets an empty `blocktree::BlockTreeFields::empty()`, a small new constructor added alongside this task); `.liv` is opened only when `del_gen != -1`, reusing `lucene_index::deletes::liv_file_name` rather than re-deriving that filename convention. **Crate placement, worked out explicitly**: this lives in `lucene-search`, not `lucene-index`, because it has to hand back `lucene_search::multi_segment::OpenSegment` values and `lucene-index` cannot depend on `lucene-search` (same downward-dependency constraint already hit by tasks #27/#36). **Two-call API, not one**: `DirectoryReader::open_segments()` returns an `OpenedSegments` that owns the freshly-opened `DocInput`/`PosInput`/`PayInput` values (borrowing from each `SegmentReader`'s own byte buffers), and `OpenedSegments::as_open_segments()` returns the final `Vec<OpenSegment>` borrowing from that -- two calls because `OpenSegment` holds `&'a DocInput<'a>` (a reference to an already-constructed value, not owned bytes), and storing that value directly inside `SegmentReader` would be self-referential, which is illegal without `unsafe` (`lucene-search` is `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]`). **Compound-file segments (`.cfs`/`.cfe`) are now wired in (task #76)**: this is read-path wiring of two *already-existing* primitives, not new codec work -- `SegmentReader::open` checks `SegmentInfo.is_compound_file` and, if set, opens the segment's `.cfs`/`.cfe` pair once (new `CompoundArchive`, `directory_reader.rs`) via `lucene_codecs::compound_format::{parse_entries, check_data_header_footer, open_input}` (unchanged, called exactly as `segment_writer.rs`'s own compound test already does), instead of returning `Error::CompoundFileUnsupported`. Every sub-file lookup (`.fnm`, `.tim`, `.tip`, `.tmd`, `.doc`, `.pos`, `.pay`) now goes through one shared helper, `open_segment_file` (plus `find_segment_file_name` for the name-only lookup `.tim`'s codec-suffix derivation needs), so there is exactly one branch point ("compound: read out of the archive by extension suffix; loose: `dir.open` the `SegmentInfo.files` entry ending in that extension, as before") rather than duplicated ad-hoc logic per file type -- non-compound segments are provably unaffected (same code path, same tests passing). **Verified against a real Java-written compound segment, not just this port's own writer**: `fixtures/data/compound_index/` (`GenCompoundFormat.java`, real `IndexWriter` with `useCompoundFile=true`, 5 docs, a real `.tim`/`.tip`/`.tmd`/`.doc` postings quad packed alongside `.fnm`/stored-fields/doc-values files inside one `.cfs`) now opens successfully through `DirectoryReader::open` and answers a real term query correctly (`compound_file_segment_opens_and_is_queryable`, replacing the old rejection test) -- this is what proves postings-in-a-compound-file also works, not just `.fnm`. A second unit test flushes the same documents through this port's own `segment_writer::flush_stored_only_segment` twice, once loose and once with `use_compound_file: true`, and confirms the compound segment opens with fields/doc-count matching the loose one, with no loose `.fnm` present on disk to fall back to (`compound_flushed_segment_opens_with_field_infos_matching_non_compound_flush`). All prior tests (real single/live-docs fixtures, stored-fields-only, missing-`.fnm`, partial-blocktree, `open_if_changed` reuse/reopen) still pass unchanged. **Still not compound-aware, honestly**: doc-values, norms, and term-vector readers elsewhere in this crate (`doc_value_query.rs`, `field_norms.rs`, `term_vectors_query.rs`, `soft_deletes.rs`) each open their own files directly off the outer `Directory` by name, independent of `DirectoryReader`/`SegmentReader` -- none of them consult `SegmentInfo.is_compound_file` or this task's new `open_segment_file`/`CompoundArchive`, so a compound segment that also had doc-values/norms/term-vectors packed into its `.cfs` would still fail to open through *those* call sites (this port's own write side doesn't yet produce such a segment, so nothing exercises the gap today, but it is real and unclosed). A `MultiTerms`/unified multi-segment `Terms` iteration abstraction and real index-wide `CollectionStatistics`-based idf (task #41's own gaps) remain unchanged by this task. `lucene-ffi` C-ABI exposure of this reader is closed by task #51 (see its own row below). NRT/reopen is closed by task #46 -- see the next row. Soft-delete visibility is closed by task #48 -- see the row below. |
| `index/IndexWriterConfig.setSoftDeletesField` + soft-delete **visibility** (`SoftDeletesDirectoryReaderWrapper`/`PendingSoftDeletes`'s read-side check only, not `IndexWriter.softUpdateDocument`'s write side) | `lucene-search/src/soft_deletes.rs::{SoftDeletesField, is_soft_deleted, is_live, effective_live_docs}` | **ported (task #48), read-side (visibility) only -- see the honest write-side scope call below.** Real Lucene's soft-delete rule is exactly a `DocValuesFieldExistsQuery` over the configured soft-deletes field: a doc is soft-deleted if that field has *any* value for it (presence, not a specific sentinel value). `is_soft_deleted`/`is_live`/`effective_live_docs` implement that same presence-based OR-with-hard-deletes rule against an already-opened `lucene_codecs::doc_values::NumericEntry` (the read side task #4/#21 already built): a doc is invisible if its `.liv` bit is cleared (hard-deleted) **or** its soft-deletes-field doc-values value is present (soft-deleted) -- both conditions independently sufficient, and a doc hit by both stays invisible, not double-counted or contradictory. **Integration point, chosen deliberately**: rather than growing every scored-query function in `lib.rs`/`multi_segment.rs` an extra "and also check this doc-values field" parameter, `effective_live_docs` computes one combined `FixedBitSet` (hard-live AND NOT soft-deleted) that a caller passes straight into any existing `live_docs: Option<&FixedBitSet>` parameter unchanged -- every pre-existing single-hard-delete-only call site is completely unaffected, since nothing forces it to call the new function at all. **Write-side scope decision, now partially closed by task #54**: real Lucene's soft-delete *write* path (`IndexWriter.softUpdateDocument`) relies on `NumericDocValuesFieldUpdates`, which appends a small delta record to an existing segment's doc-values generation rather than rewriting the whole `.dvm`/`.dvd`/`.dvs` triple. At the time this task (#48) was written, this port had no incremental doc-values update format/codec at all -- the only doc-values write primitive (`lucene_codecs::doc_values::write_single_dense_numeric_field`) always wrote a brand-new, complete, single-dense-field triple from scratch, so this task deliberately did not fake a "cheap incremental marking" shim on top of it. **Task #54 has since built exactly that missing incremental-update primitive** (`lucene_codecs::doc_values_updates`, a single-generation sparse `(docId, value)` overlay file, read-through-overlay decode) and wired it into this module as `mark_soft_deleted_via_overlay`/`is_soft_deleted_with_overlay`/`effective_live_docs_with_overlay`: marking one doc soft-deleted no longer requires touching the base `.dvd`/`.dvm` bytes at all. This closes the write-side gap for **one overlay round** -- it does not implement real Lucene's full multi-generation `docValuesGen` lifecycle (many sequential update rounds, newest-generation-wins across rounds) or `SegmentCommitInfo`/`.si` generation-metadata wiring; see `doc_values_updates.rs`'s own doc comment for that scope statement. **Verified**: unit tests cover all four hard/soft-delete combinations (hard-only invisible, soft-only invisible, neither live, both invisible-not-contradictory) plus `effective_live_docs`'s OR-composition (no-soft-deletes-field passthrough, all-live-state, combined-with-existing-hard-deletes, same-doc-both-mechanisms) -- all against the real checked-in `fixtures/data/doc_values_index/` fixture's genuinely sparse (`IndexedDISI`) `sparse` numeric field (task #4/#21's own real-Lucene-written bytes: docs 0/2/4 present, 1/3 absent), not a hand-built or dense-encoded stand-in (a dense field can't represent "no value at all" for any doc, so it can't stand in for a real soft-deletes field's presence semantics). An end-to-end composition test additionally reuses the real `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` fixture (`body`/`bird` -> docs `[1, 4]`) together with that same real sparse doc-values field to confirm `effective_live_docs`'s output composes correctly with `search_term_query`: doc 4 (soft-deleted per the real doc-values fixture) is excluded from the real term-query match, leaving only doc 1, and additionally hard-deleting doc 1 leaves nothing live at all -- proving the OR-composition against real decoded bytes end-to-end, not just self-consistently. **Deliberately out of scope beyond the write-side gap above**: cross-segment orchestration (like `directory_reader.rs`, this operates on one already-opened segment at a time; a caller wires it in per segment) and `lucene-ffi` C-ABI exposure. |
| `index/NumericDocValuesFieldUpdates` + `IndexWriter.updateNumericDocValue` (multi-generation incremental numeric doc-values update chain; `SegmentCommitInfo.docValuesGen` metadata wiring still not implemented) | `lucene-codecs/src/doc_values_updates.rs::{write_numeric_updates, read_numeric_updates, numeric_value_with_updates, numeric_value_with_generations}`, wired into `lucene-search/src/soft_deletes.rs::{mark_soft_deleted_via_overlay, is_soft_deleted_with_overlay, effective_live_docs_with_overlay}` | **ported (task #54, extended to N generations in a follow-up pass) -- unblocks task #48's documented write-side gap.** Real Lucene marks a doc's doc-values field with a new value without rewriting the whole segment's `.dvd`/`.dvm` triple by appending a small "generation" file of sparse `(docId, value)` deltas (`NumericDocValuesFieldUpdates`/`FieldUpdatesWriter`), applied as an overlay over the base doc-values at read time, with `SegmentCommitInfo.docValuesGen` tracking which generations exist and newest-generation-wins when the same doc is touched across many rounds. This port implements the core mechanism for **any number** of sequential overlay rounds: `write_numeric_updates` encodes a sparse `(docId -> newValue)` map (sorted, de-duplicated keeping the last write per doc) into a small standalone file per generation, reusing this crate's `codec_util` header/footer/CRC conventions for structural integrity; `read_numeric_updates` decodes each generation's file back to a `HashMap<i32, i64>`, validating strictly-ascending doc ids; `numeric_value_with_updates` composes a single already-decoded overlay map with the existing base `doc_values::numeric_value` decode (overlay winning when present), and `numeric_value_with_generations` generalizes that to a whole ordered chain of overlay maps (oldest-to-newest, matching `SegmentCommitInfo.docValuesGen`'s own counter order), checking newest-to-oldest so a later generation's write always overrides an earlier one for the same doc, falling through past generations that didn't touch a given doc, and finally falling back to the base decode. **Byte format is this port's own invention, not a real-Lucene port**: there is no checked-in fixture for `NumericDocValuesFieldUpdates`' actual on-disk generation-file bytes (same honest situation as task #49/#52's index-sort format), and there's no plan to derive one either -- only the header/footer/CRC shell reuses `codec_util`, the field layout in between is invented for this task and documented as such in the module's own doc comment; layering multiple generations reuses that same per-generation format unchanged, one file per generation, composed only at read time. **Scope decision, still explicit**: `SegmentCommitInfo`/`.si` `docValuesGen` metadata wiring (tracking which generation number each file corresponds to, and `IndexWriter` actually writing a new generation against a committed segment) is deliberately deferred -- this is "the update-overlay mechanism itself works and is correct across arbitrarily many chained rounds", not the full commit-lifecycle integration; callers are responsible for keeping the slice of decoded overlay maps passed to `numeric_value_with_generations` in ascending-generation order themselves. **Wired into task #48's soft-deletes flow**: `mark_soft_deleted_via_overlay` marks a doc soft-deleted by writing *only* an overlay file (any value, per task #48's presence-based semantics) with zero base-file I/O; `is_soft_deleted_with_overlay`/`effective_live_docs_with_overlay` extend task #48's existing presence check and combined-bitset computation to consult the overlay first, falling back to the base decode -- the concrete, real "incremental update without full rewrite" property task #48's own write-side gap called for (still single-generation at this integration point; not yet upgraded to consume a generation chain). **Verified**: unit tests cover overlay round-trip (including unsorted input and duplicate-doc last-write-wins), an empty overlay round-tripping to an empty map, wrong-segment-id and truncated-file rejection, and a hand-built out-of-order-doc-ids rejection (exercising the validation path no honest writer output can reach); overlay-vs-base composition tests cover overlay-overrides-base, base-fallback-when-absent-from-overlay, and empty-overlay-is-a-no-op, all against a base numeric field built through the real `write_single_dense_numeric_field`/`parse_meta` round trip (not hand-rolled bytes). Multi-generation layering is covered by dedicated unit tests: three chained generations all touching the same doc (newest wins), overlapping-but-distinct doc sets across three generations (each doc resolves to its own newest write), a doc untouched by any generation (falls back to base), an empty generation chain (degenerates to plain base decode), a doc whose newest-touching generation isn't the chain's last entry (falls through past an unrelated later generation to an earlier one), and a test proving the chain composes with the *unmodified* `write_numeric_updates`/`read_numeric_updates` per-generation I/O (each generation really is its own standalone file). The soft-deletes integration is verified against the real checked-in `fixtures/data/doc_values_index/` sparse fixture (task #4/#21/#48's own real-Lucene-written bytes, docs 0/2/4 soft-deleted in the base, 1/3 not): marking doc 3 soft-deleted via `mark_soft_deleted_via_overlay` alone (no base rewrite) makes `is_soft_deleted_with_overlay`/`effective_live_docs_with_overlay` correctly exclude it while the plain base-only `is_soft_deleted` still (correctly) reports it as not soft-deleted, proving the base bytes were genuinely untouched; additional tests cover the empty-overlay-matches-plain-version case and the no-base-soft-deletes-field-but-overlay-present case. **Merge-awareness audit (follow-up task)**: investigated whether this overlay composes correctly with `merge.rs`'s doc-values-aware segment merging. Finding: **there is no production code path to compose in the first place** -- `doc_values_updates` has exactly one consumer today, `lucene-search/src/soft_deletes.rs`'s query-time overlay-aware live-docs check, which never touches `merge.rs`; `IndexWriter` has no `update_numeric_doc_value`-style method that writes an overlay against a committed segment (`SegmentCommitInfo::doc_values_gen` is set to `-1` everywhere and never wired up); and `merge.rs`'s `MergeSource`/`SourceNumericDocValues` (and the sibling BINARY/SORTED/SORTED_NUMERIC/SORTED_SET source structs) carry no overlay field at all -- the merge's numeric-field code path calls `doc_values::numeric_value` directly on each source's base `data`/`entry`, so there is no parameter a caller could even use to plug an overlay in. A new regression test, `merge::tests::numeric_doc_values_update_overlay_does_not_survive_a_merge_today` (`crates/lucene-index/src/merge.rs`), proves this concretely through both features' real public APIs: it writes a real overlay marking doc 0 with a new value, confirms `numeric_value_with_updates` genuinely sees it, then runs an actual `merge_stored_only_segments` call over that same source (necessarily using only the base data, since that's all `SourceNumericDocValues` can express) and confirms the merged segment keeps the **stale** pre-update value -- i.e. if a future task ever wires an overlay-writing update method into `IndexWriter` without also teaching whichever call site assembles `MergeSource`s to resolve each source's "effective" (overlay-folded) values first, updates would be silently dropped by any subsequent merge. **Scope conclusion**: this is not a bug to fix in the current codebase -- there is no real caller today that both writes an overlay against a committed segment and later merges it, so "does merge see the overlay" isn't yet a well-formed question against production code. It is documented here as the explicit boundary any future `IndexWriter`-level update-write API must account for: fold overlays into base values before constructing `MergeSource`s, keeping `merge.rs` itself unaware of update generations. |
| `index/DirectoryReader.openIfChanged(DirectoryReader)` (NRT reopen against an already-committed `Directory`, not the `ReaderPool`-backed writer overload) | `lucene-search/src/directory_reader.rs::DirectoryReader::open_if_changed` | **ported (task #46), scoped precisely below.** `reader.open_if_changed(dir)` reads `dir`'s latest `segments_N` and compares its generation to the one `reader` was opened from: identical generation returns `Ok(None)`, matching real `openIfChanged`'s "nothing changed" convention (callers keep using their existing reader rather than rebuild it). A changed generation builds a new `DirectoryReader` through a shared helper, `open_at_reusing`, which for each segment in the new commit looks for an already-open `SegmentReader` in `reader`'s own segment list matching on segment name **and** segment id **and** `del_gen`, reusing it in-memory (`SegmentReader::clone_reader`, a plain struct clone -- `BlockTreeFields`/`FixedBitSet` are already `Clone` -- no file I/O) only when all three match, and opening fresh from disk otherwise (`SegmentReader::open`, the same path `DirectoryReader::open_at` already used). `del_gen` is now tracked on `SegmentReader` (a new private field, populated from the owning commit at open time) precisely so a delete-only change on an otherwise-unchanged segment -- same name/id, bumped `del_gen` -- is never mistaken for "safe to reuse": that segment's `.liv`/`live_docs` genuinely differ under the new commit, and serving it from the old reader would silently show deleted documents as live. A merged-away or replaced segment always falls into "open fresh," since its replacement has a different name/id. **Verified**: `open_if_changed_returns_none_when_generation_unchanged` (no writes since open -> `None`); `open_if_changed_reuses_unchanged_segment_and_opens_new_one` (a second `flush_stored_only_segment` call adds segment `_1` under a new `segments_N` -- the reopened reader has both segments with correct `doc_base`s, and genuine reuse of segment `_0` is proven, not assumed, by deleting `_0`'s on-disk `.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm`/`.fnm` files before calling `open_if_changed`: a fresh open of `_0` would then fail with a file-not-found error, so the call succeeding is only possible if the original in-memory reader was reused); `open_if_changed_reopens_segment_whose_del_gen_changed` (the correctness-critical case -- `deletes::apply_deletes` bumps segment `_0`'s `del_gen` with no new segment added, and the reopened reader's `live_docs` reflects the new deletion rather than the original "no deletions" state). **Deliberately scoped down from real Lucene's actual `openIfChanged`**: this is one reader reopening itself, not the `ReaderPool`-wide sharing real `IndexWriter`/`StandardDirectoryReader` provide (there, *every* open `DirectoryReader` in a process benefits from another reader's already-open segments, not just the one being reopened); no `SearcherFactory`/`ReaderManager` warm-up-listener hook runs on newly-opened sub-readers before they're handed back; and there is still no `openIfChanged(IndexWriter)` overload (reading uncommitted flushed segments directly from an in-memory writer rather than a committed `segments_N` on disk) -- that remains PLAN.md ┬¦2 item 7's larger, writer-integrated NRT scope, unaddressed here. **Doc-values audit ("NRT reopen after sparse doc-values commits"): found and fixed a real gap.** `SegmentReader::open` never opened a segment's `.dvm`/`.dvd` at all before this audit -- confirmed by reading it end to end and by this module's own prior doc comment, which said doc-values were "deliberately excluded... irrelevant here." Fixed: `SegmentReader` now opens `.dvm`/`.dvd` (present together or not at all, same contract as `.tim`/`.tip`/`.tmd`, transparently through a `.cfs`/`.cfe` archive when compound), parsed via the unchanged `doc_values::parse_meta`, exposed via new `SegmentReader::field_infos`/`doc_values_meta`/`doc_values_data` accessors that feed directly into the existing dense/sparse-agnostic `doc_values::{numeric_value, binary_value, sorted_ord, sorted_numeric_values}` readers -- no new low-level codec logic. Because these live on `SegmentReader` alongside every other per-segment file `open_if_changed` already reopens-or-reuses, NRT reopen refreshes them for free. One genuine bug found and fixed while wiring this in: the doc-values codec suffix must be derived from the actual `.dvm` file name (like `.tim`'s already is), not hardcoded to `""` -- a real Lucene-written segment (`fixtures/data/compound_index/`) gives doc values their own codec suffix (`Lucene90_<n>`) independent of the postings suffix, and the first cut broke that fixture's existing `compound_file_segment_opens_and_is_queryable` test with a suffix-mismatch error before the fix. **Verified end-to-end through the real `IndexWriter` -> commit -> NRT reopen -> read-back path**: two new tests, `directory_reader.rs::tests::sparse_doc_values_nrt::{nrt_reader_reads_sparse_numeric_field_after_first_commit, nrt_reopen_reads_new_segments_sparse_numeric_values_correctly}` -- the first commits a sparse NUMERIC field (present/absent/present) and reads it back through a freshly opened `DirectoryReader`; the second adds a second commit with a brand-new, differently-sparse second segment and confirms `open_if_changed` correctly serves both the reused first segment's original values and the newly opened second segment's own sparse values, with correct `doc_base`s. **Not yet consumed by existing doc-values query code**: `doc_value_query.rs`/`facets.rs` still take raw, separately-hand-loaded `.dvm`/`.dvd` bytes exactly as before this audit -- neither was changed to call the new `SegmentReader::field_infos`/`doc_values_meta`/`doc_values_data` accessors, so today those accessors have no production consumer, only the two new tests above use them directly. NRT-reopen-correctness for doc-values is proven at the `SegmentReader` level; wiring the query-side readers to actually go through it is a separate, still-open follow-up. |
| `index/IndexReader.getTermVector(int doc, String field)` (query-facing read API over term vectors) | `lucene-search/src/term_vectors_query.rs::{term_vector_for_doc, matched_term_offsets}` | **ported (task #39), a thin adapter -- no new byte-format decoding.** `term_vector_for_doc` resolves a `(doc, field name)` pair to `crates/lucene-codecs/src/term_vectors.rs`'s `(doc, field number)` shape via `FieldInfos` and returns that already-decoded `TermVectorField` (every term with its frequency, and whichever of positions/offsets/payloads that field had turned on at index time -- all already fully decodable per task #3/#26's work, nothing new added here). Mirrors real `IndexReader.getTermVector`'s `null`-return convention: `Ok(None)` for an unknown field name, a doc with no term vectors at all, or a doc missing that particular field; `Err` only propagates straight from `TermVectorsReader::document` (doc ID out of range, or a corrupt `.tvd`/`.tvx` region), the same passthrough convention every other `lucene-search` query function already uses for its codec reader. **Highlighting primitive, precisely scoped**: `matched_term_offsets` computes `(term, start_offset, end_offset)` spans for a set of matched terms in one field -- exactly what a `Highlighter`/`UnifiedHighlighter` needs to slice source text at match boundaries -- but only this one primitive; there is no fragment selection, snippet assembly, or `PassageFormatter`-equivalent, and it returns `None` outright (not a fabricated guess) when the field wasn't indexed with offsets (`has_offsets == false`), since this port never decoded any to begin with. Positions and payloads are equally already-decodable but aren't surfaced through a dedicated function here -- callers read them straight off the `TermVectorField`/`TermVectorTerm` `term_vector_for_doc` returns. **No new fixture generated**: per the `differential-testing` skill's precedent for composition/wiring tasks (#36-38), this task's logic (field-name resolution, error passthrough, span computation) touches no new byte format, so its tests reuse the real, already cross-engine-verified `fixtures/data/term_vectors_index/` fixture (task #3's) rather than generating new Java output. Unit-tested: field resolved by name with real offsets returned; unmatched term yields no spans; unknown field name, a field known in `FieldInfos` but not stored for that doc, and a doc with no term vectors at all all return `None`; an out-of-range doc ID surfaces as `Err`; a field without offsets makes `matched_term_offsets` return `None`. **Deliberately out of scope**: multi-segment federation (this function still takes one already-opened segment's `TermVectorsReader` directly; task #45's `DirectoryReader` doesn't open term-vectors files at all -- `OpenSegment` has no term-vectors field, see that row above). The write side's offsets/payloads gap this row used to note here has since been closed by a later task (`write_best_speed` now supports all three) -- unrelated to this read-side task either way, tracked in the write-side row above. **Fragment selection/snippet assembly, the one thing this row's own note above deferred, is now addressed by task #56 -- see the next row.** |
| `search/uhighlight/UnifiedHighlighter` + `PassageFormatter` (fragment assembly / text-snippet highlighting; not `BreakIterator`-based sentence detection or term-density passage scoring) | `lucene-search/src/highlighter.rs::{Fragment, FragmentConfig, assemble_fragments}` | **ported (task #56), a real but honestly-scoped MVP -- simplified passage-boundary heuristic, not `BreakIterator`.** Given the original field text and a set of task #39's `TermOffsetSpan`s, `assemble_fragments` slices out fixed-size (`window_chars`-configurable) character windows around each match (or cluster of nearby matches), wraps matches in caller-configurable `pre`/`post` markers (default `<b>`/`</b>`, real Lucene's `PassageFormatter` default), and merges overlapping/abutting windows into one fragment rather than emitting duplicates -- capped at `max_fragments`. **Passage-boundary heuristic, documented as a simplification, not silently pretended sentence-aware**: window edges are snapped outward to the nearest whitespace boundary so a fragment doesn't start/end mid-word, but there is no term-density scoring; fragments are simply emitted in left-to-right document order and truncated at `max_fragments`. **Sentence-boundary snapping, opt-in via `FragmentConfig::snap_to_sentence` (default `false`, prior behavior unchanged)**: when set, a fragment's rendered edges snap to the sentence(s) containing its match(es) instead of the fixed window -- a real but deliberately narrow terminator rule (`.`/`!`/`?` followed, after skipping whitespace, by an uppercase letter or the text's end), **not** ICU/`BreakIterator`-grade Unicode sentence segmentation: no locale rules, no comprehensive abbreviation dictionary. **Extended (still not ICU-grade)**: a small hardcoded English-only abbreviation list (`ABBREVIATIONS` -- "mr"/"mrs"/"ms"/"dr"/"jr"/"sr"/"vs"/"etc"/"inc"/"st"/"prof"/"capt"/"co"/"ltd"/"gen") now suppresses a sentence break after these specific words' trailing `.`, closing the previously-documented "Mr. Smith" false positive (re-tested by `sentence_snap_abbreviation_list_closes_mr_smith_false_positive`, now asserting no break); any abbreviation not on this short fixed list still produces the old false positive (`sentence_snap_unlisted_abbreviation_still_breaks`, using "Cmdr."), so this is a targeted fix, not universal period-suppression. **Found in review**: "st" on the list (for "St." as in a street name) would otherwise also swallow the sentence break after any ordinal number ending in "st" (21st., 1st., 91st., ...) -- e.g. "He finished 21st. She started next." incorrectly merging into one fragment. Fixed by excluding an alphabetic run directly preceded by a digit from the abbreviation check (an ordinal suffix, not a real abbreviation), covered by `sentence_snap_ordinal_number_is_not_mistaken_for_st_abbreviation`. A terminator immediately followed by a closing quote (`"`/`'`/U+201D/U+2019) or paren/bracket (`)`/`]`/`}`) before any whitespace is now recognized as a sentence end too (the closing punctuation is skipped before the whitespace+uppercase check) -- previously e.g. `He said "Stop." Then left.` wasn't recognized as a break at all, since the character right after `.` wasn't whitespace (`sentence_snap_closing_quote_after_terminator_is_recognized`, `sentence_snap_closing_paren_after_terminator_is_recognized`). Decimal numbers ("3.5", "$5.00") were already handled correctly by the base terminator rule and needed no change. **Marker-insertion correctness for multi-match fragments**: `render_cluster` inserts `pre`/`post` around each match within a merged fragment working from the last match backward, so an earlier (leftward) insertion's byte offsets are never invalidated by a later one -- the one part of this logic genuinely easy to get subtly wrong, and covered by a dedicated test with two nearby matches merging into one fragment with both terms highlighted and neither original word corrupted. **Offset-unit finding**: term-vector offsets are decoded verbatim by task #3/#39 and never reinterpreted, carrying whatever unit real Lucene's `Analyzer` wrote at index time (UTF-16 code units in real Lucene); this port's checked-in fixture is ASCII-only so byte/UTF-16/scalar counts are indistinguishable there. `highlighter.rs` treats incoming offsets as Unicode-scalar (`char`) counts (equivalent to UTF-16 for the entire Basic Multilingual Plane) and converts to UTF-8 byte offsets via `char_indices()` before any slicing, so a match spanning a multi-byte UTF-8 character cannot panic even on out-of-range/mis-unitted input (offsets are clamped to the text's char count first). **No new Java fixture needed for the fragment-assembly logic itself** (there is no "real Lucene bytes" to check string-slicing/highlighting against -- correctness here means "produces a sensible readable snippet," checked by direct unit tests), but one test composes task #39/#3's real, cross-engine-verified fixture offsets (`fixtures/data/term_vectors_index/`, doc 0's "text" field: "cat"/"car"/"cat" at char offsets 0..3/4..7/8..11) with the real text those exact offsets denote (`"cat car cat"`, per `fixtures/src/GenTermVectors.java`'s `CannedTokenStream` token list), not a made-up string. Unit-tested: single match windowed/highlighted correctly; two nearby matches merge into one fragment with both terms highlighted; two far-apart matches stay separate; window clamping at text start/end without panicking; `max_fragments` truncation; a multi-byte UTF-8 match; out-of-range/invalid spans (negative, end-before-start, past text end) dropped defensively rather than panicking. **Deliberately out of scope**: term-density passage scoring/ranking, and full ICU/`BreakIterator`-grade Unicode sentence segmentation (locale rules, abbreviation dictionaries) even though a real, scoped-down sentence-boundary heuristic is now implemented (see above) -- real, substantial follow-on work, not silently skipped. ~~`lucene-ffi` C-ABI exposure~~ -- closed by the Highlighter FFI exposure task: see the `lucene-ffi` section's `highlighter.rs`/`results_fragments.rs` row for `ffi_assemble_fragments`. |
| `index/CheckIndex` (standalone segment-consistency verifier, self-check only -- not the differential-testing harness) | `lucene-index/src/check_index.rs::{Check, CheckResult, check_segment, check_directory}` | **ported (task #57), scoped to the cross-file/cross-structure checks this port's current write-side scope makes valuable -- not full `CheckIndex`.** Deliberately *not* built on top of `lucene-search`'s `DirectoryReader`/`SegmentReader` (task #45): those types expose only the curated subset of state a query needs and hide exactly what a self-check must cross-reference (`SegmentInfo.files`, per-field flags, raw `.si`/`.fnm`/stored-fields bytes). Lives in `lucene-index` (not `lucene-search`, which it has no actual dependency on -- every type it composes is already available here), and reuses `crate::segment_infos::read_latest` for the shared "find the latest commit, list its segments" step, then opens each segment's files directly through the same lower-level decoders `lucene-search`'s `directory_reader.rs` itself calls. Each check reports independently as a named pass/fail (`Check { name, passed, message }`), matching real `CheckIndex`'s own per-check `Status` reporting style rather than a single boolean. **Implemented**: every file `.si` lists opens and has a structurally valid codec footer (`codec_util::retrieve_checksum` -- doubles as a "forgot to write/list a file" check); `.si` doc_count vs `.liv`'s byte-size-implied word count, derived independently of `si.doc_count` (not by passing it into the decode call, which would make the check vacuous by construction); `live_docs` cardinality vs `SegmentCommitInfo.del_count` (surfaced through `live_docs::parse`'s own `DelCountMismatch`, since that cross-check is already enforced at decode time -- this module reports it under its own named check rather than re-deriving the same arithmetic); `.fnm`'s per-field flags (doc values, norms, term vectors, postings via `index_options != None`) cross-checked in both directions against which of `.dvd`/`.dvm`/`.nvd`/`.nvm`/`.tvd`/`.tvx`/`.tvm`/`.tim`/`.tip`/`.tmd` the segment's file list actually includes (a field claiming a feature with no matching files is flagged, and so is a file group present with no field claiming it); stored-fields reader's own `max_doc()` vs `.si`'s declared `doc_count`; **postings term-by-term re-derivation (revisited from a prior deferral -- see below)**: for every field with postings and every term in its dictionary, walks the term's actual postings via `blocktree::BlockTreeFields::iter_fields` (added by this task) and `DocInput::read_postings`/`postings::singleton_postings` -- the same read-side API `lucene-search`'s query path already uses -- and independently recomputes `totalTermFreq` (sum of decoded per-doc freqs), cross-checking it against the term dictionary's own recorded `TermStats`; each decoded doc ID is also checked for being in-range and strictly increasing (`postings.doc_ids_valid:<field>`), the meaningful proxy for `docFreq` corruption given this decode API's structure (see below for why a plain `docFreq` recount would be vacuous). A `.si` that fails to open/parse short-circuits every other check for that segment (nothing else can be trusted without a valid file list) and reports a single `si.open` failure. **Revisited scope decision**: task #57 originally deferred postings re-derivation with the stated reason "requires walking per-format internals this port's read-side decoders expose in different shapes per format -- genuinely a separate, large task." Re-examined this task: that blocker no longer holds for postings specifically -- `blocktree::FieldTerms::iter()` already yields every `(term, TermStats)` pair, `DocInput::read_postings`/`postings::singleton_postings` already fully materialize a term's `(docID, freq)` pairs (both already exercised by `lucene-search`'s query path, task #45), so only a one-line accessor (`iter_fields`) was missing; no new decode logic was needed. Investigating the decode API surfaced a genuine structural finding, not just a rediscovery: `read_postings`/`singleton_postings` are *parameterized by* the claimed `docFreq` (same as real Lucene's own `PostingsEnum.reset`/`TermState.docFreq`), so `postings.docs.len()` is always exactly equal to the claimed `docFreq` whenever decoding succeeds at all -- a plain recount can never disagree, so it isn't implemented as one; a wrong claimed `docFreq` instead surfaces as an out-of-range/non-monotonic decoded doc ID (`postings.doc_ids_valid`) or an outright decode error (`postings.open`), which is what the implemented checks actually catch. A `docFreq == 1` singleton term stores no per-doc freq on disk at all (`singleton_postings` reconstructs it from the term dictionary's own recorded `total_term_freq`), so `totalTermFreq` re-derivation is honestly vacuous for singletons -- a real format fact, not a port-specific gap. The same vacuity extends to any `IndexOptions::Docs` (freq-less) field with `docFreq > 1`, for a related-but-distinct reason: `blocktree.rs`'s meta parsing sets `total_term_freq = doc_freq` for such fields (no independent stat is ever written) and the postings decoder synthesizes freq `1` for every doc when a field stores no freqs at all, so the comparison there is also always `doc_freq == doc_freq` -- `postings.doc_ids_valid` remains meaningful for these fields regardless, since it depends only on decoded doc IDs, not freqs. **Still deliberately deferred** (unchanged from before, real substantial follow-on work per format): doc-values value-range sanity, points-tree structural invariants, and vectors-graph structural invariants; each needs its own per-format traversal (points-tree traversal, HNSW graph traversal), not a natural extension of this module's cross-file bookkeeping. **No new Java fixture generated**: this is self-consistency logic layered over already-differentially-verified decoders, not new byte-format decoding, so direct unit tests (including deliberately-corrupted inputs) are the right verification method, per the `differential-testing` skill's precedent -- the postings re-derivation negative test builds its corruption via the existing `postings_writer::write_single_field` API (swapping in a term dictionary that claims a different `totalTermFreq` than the real `.doc` bytes it's paired with actually sum to), not raw byte mutation. Unit-tested: the real `blocktree_index` and `live_docs_index` fixtures pass every check cleanly (including the new postings checks); deliberately corrupted cases confirm each failure mode reports clearly rather than panicking or false-passing -- a hand-mutated `SegmentCommitInfo.del_count`, a truncated `.liv` file, a `.si` listing a nonexistent file, a `.si` that won't parse at all, a `.liv` whose byte size disagrees with `si.doc_count`, a file with a corrupted footer, a partial `.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm` file set, a `si.doc_count` that disagrees with a real stored-fields reader's `max_doc()`, a term dictionary whose recorded `totalTermFreq` disagrees with its actual postings' summed freqs, a term dictionary whose real postings decode to an out-of-range/non-monotonic doc ID while `totalTermFreq` still agrees (proving `postings.doc_ids_valid` is independently exercised, not just piggybacking on the `totalTermFreq` check), and a segment with postings but no `.doc` file. Coverage: `lucene-index/src/check_index.rs`, `cargo llvm-cov --fail-under-lines 95` passing workspace-wide. |
| `search/LRUQueryCache` (per-segment matching-docs bitset cache) | `lucene-search/src/query_cache.rs::QueryCache`, `query_cache.rs::search_term_query_cached` | **new standalone primitive, not a byte-for-byte port of `LRUQueryCache.java`, now wired into one real search entry point (`TermQuery` only) via an opt-in cached wrapper -- the underlying `search_term_query`/`QueryCache::get_or_compute` logic itself is unchanged.** Real `LRUQueryCache` tracks per-segment `IndexReader.CacheKey` identity via weak references, bounds itself by both entry count and estimated RAM usage, and applies a `shouldCache` heuristic to skip caching queries that aren't worth it; none of that is implemented. This module keeps only the core value proposition: given a `(segment, query)` pair, hand back a previously computed `FixedBitSet` of matching doc IDs instead of recomputing it. `QueryCache<S, Q>` is generic over any segment identifier `S: Eq + Hash + Clone` (this port has no `IndexReader.CacheKey`-style segment identity object yet, so a caller-supplied key such as a segment name or generation number stands in) and any query representation `Q: Eq + Hash + Clone`; `query::TermQuery` picked up an additive `Hash` derive (alongside its existing `PartialEq + Eq`) so it can be used directly as `Q`. API: `QueryCache::new(max_entries)`, `get_or_compute(segment, query, || -> FixedBitSet)`, `invalidate_segment(&segment) -> usize`, `remove(&segment, &query) -> bool`, `clear()`, `len()`/`is_empty()`. Eviction is bounded by entry count only (no RAM-based sizing), least-recently-used-first, tracked via a monotonic access counter rather than an external LRU-list crate. No `unsafe` (`lucene-search` is `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]`). Unit-tested (`QueryCache` itself): cache miss computes and stores; cache hit reuses the stored bitset without recomputing (verified via a call counter); distinct queries against the same segment get distinct entries; the same query against different segments get distinct entries; inserting past `max_entries` evicts the correct least-recently-used entry; `invalidate_segment` removes only that segment's entries, leaving other segments untouched; a `max_entries == 0` cache never actually retains anything; `clear()` empties every entry; `TermQuery` used end-to-end as a concrete `Q`. **Wired entry point**: `search_term_query_cached(cache, segment, fields, doc_in, live_docs, num_docs, query, collector) -> Result<()>` composes `QueryCache::get_or_compute` with the existing, unchanged `search_term_query` -- opt-in, `search_term_query` itself and every existing caller of it are unaffected. Real-fixture-tested (`blocktree_index`, not synthetic data): the same query run twice against the same segment returns identical, correct doc IDs on both calls, with the second call proven to be a genuine cache hit (not a silent recompute) by omitting `.doc` input on the second call -- both fixture terms tested (`docFreq == 2`) require `.doc` input to actually execute, so a real recompute without it fails with `Error::BlockTree`, making an `Ok` result on the second call proof the cache path was taken; a different query against the same segment key, and the same query against a different segment key, are each proven to be genuine fresh misses the same way; `invalidate_segment` is proven to force a real recompute on the next call for that segment, also the same way. **Explicitly deferred**: RAM-based cache sizing, automatic per-segment invalidation hooks tied to real segment open/close/merge lifecycle events (`invalidate_segment` exists and is correct, but nothing in this port calls it automatically yet -- a caller of `search_term_query_cached` still invokes it manually), cache-worthiness heuristics like real `LRUQueryCache.shouldCache`, and wiring any query type other than `TermQuery` (in particular `BooleanQuery`, blocked on its `Clause::DisjunctionMax` variant embedding a non-`Eq`/`Hash` `f32 tie_breaker`) into a cached entry point. |

## lucene-ffi

| Java file/class | Rust module | Status/notes |
|---|---|---|
| ŌĆö (no direct Java equivalent; this is the JNI/C-ABI boundary itself, task #20) | `lucene-ffi/src/directory.rs::{ffi_open_directory, ffi_close_directory}` | **new.** Opens/closes a real `lucene_store::directory::FsDirectory` at a caller-given filesystem path, behind an opaque `u64` handle (`lucene-ffi/src/handle.rs::SlotMap`, a hand-rolled generation-tagged slotmap ŌĆö see that module's doc comment for why it isn't reused from elsewhere in the workspace). Each handle also carries an 8-bit registry-type tag (`RegistryTag::{Directory,Segment,Results,ScoredResults,SortedResults,DirectoryReader,FacetResults}`, the last one added by the Faceted search FFI exposure task) alongside its index/generation bits, so a handle from one of this crate's seven registries is rejected outright by another registry's `get`/`remove` on a tag mismatch, rather than only being caught if its index/generation also happens to miss. |
| ŌĆö | `lucene-ffi/src/segment.rs::{ffi_open_segment, ffi_close_segment}` | **new, partial.** Opens one segment's `.fnm`/`.tim`/`.tip`/`.tmd` term dictionary (`lucene_codecs::blocktree::open`) plus, optionally, its `.doc`/`.pos` postings files, from already-known file names/segment ID/suffix/`maxDoc` (a real caller is expected to have already parsed `segments_N`/`.si` to discover these ŌĆö see that module's doc comment for why this doesn't parse `.si` itself). **Task #30**: `ffi_open_segment` grew optional `nvm_name`/`nvd_name` parameters, opening the segment's `.nvm`/`.nvd` norms pair (`lucene_codecs::norms::{parse_meta, check_data_header_footer}`, always validated against the empty codec suffix ŌĆö real Lucene's norms format has none, unlike `.tim`/`.doc`/etc) so `ffi_search_*_query_scored` can use real per-doc/avg field lengths instead of always falling back to `similarity::UNNORMED_FIELD_LENGTH`; `SegmentHandle` now also carries the parsed `field_infos` (needed to map a scored query's field *name* to the field *number* `NormsEntry`/`Norms` are keyed by ŌĆö `BlockTreeFields` has no such mapping of its own). **No `.pay` (payload) parameter yet** ŌĆö `search_phrase_query`/`search_phrase_query_scored` are always called with `pay_in: None` from `query.rs`. **Task #40**: `ffi_open_segment` grew optional `dvm_name`/`dvd_name`/`dv_suffix` parameters, opening the segment's `.dvm`/`.dvd` doc-values pair (`lucene_codecs::doc_values::{parse_meta, check_data_header_footer}`) so `ffi_sort_by_doc_value`/`ffi_sort_by_multi_valued_doc_value` (see below) have real doc-values bytes to sort by; unlike `.nvm`/`.nvd`, `.dvm`/`.dvd` carry their own per-field codec-suffix component in their index header, so `dv_suffix` is a separate parameter from `segment_suffix` rather than reusing it. `SegmentHandle` grew matching `dv_data`/`dv_meta` fields, both `None` when the segment was opened without doc values (the two sort entry points then return `FfiStatus::InvalidArgument` ŌĆö unlike norms, there's no meaningful constant fallback for "nothing to sort by"). **Points range query FFI exposure task**: `ffi_open_segment` grew optional `kdm_name`/`kdi_name`/`kdd_name` parameters, opening the segment's `.kdm`/`.kdi`/`.kdd` BKD points meta/index/data files (`lucene_codecs::points::open`, validated once at open time then stored as owned bytes on a new `SegmentHandle::points_data` field) so `ffi_search_points_range` (see below) has points data to search; like `.nvm`/`.nvd`, always validated against the empty codec suffix (`""`), not `segment_suffix`/`dv_suffix` ŌĆö real Lucene's points format has no per-field codec-suffix component in its index header either. A segment opened without them can't serve `ffi_search_points_range` (`FfiStatus::InvalidArgument`, same "no sensible fallback" story as doc values' absence). |
| `search/SortField.Type.LONG`/`INT`/`SortedNumericSortField`/`SortedSetSortField` (single-key ascending doc-value sort, C-ABI wrapper) | `lucene-ffi/src/sort.rs::{ffi_sort_by_doc_value, ffi_sort_by_multi_valued_doc_value}` | **new, task #40.** Thin `catch_unwind`-guarded wrappers around `lucene_search::{sort_by_numeric_doc_value, doc_value_query::sort_by_multi_valued_doc_value}`, following task #30's exact FFI shape: resolve a field name to a NUMERIC/SORTED_NUMERIC `.dvm` entry via the segment's `field_infos` (same name -> number lookup `open_field_norms` already does for norms), run the sort over a caller-given candidate doc-ID list, and store the resulting ascending `(doc_id, value)` pairs under a new `SortedResultsHandle`. The missing-value policy (`lucene_search::MissingValue::Exclude`/`Default(i64)`) crosses the wire as `missing_is_default: bool` + `missing_default: i64` (ignored when the bool is `false`) rather than a tagged union; `ffi_sort_by_multi_valued_doc_value`'s `ValueSelector` (MIN/MAX) crosses as an `i32` (`0`/`1`, anything else is `FfiStatus::InvalidArgument`). Same "also serves SORTED_SET" reuse `doc_value_query.rs` documents for the multi-valued function applies here too ŌĆö passing a SORTED_SET field's ordinal-array entry works unchanged. **Ascending-only, single-sort-key-only** (see the deferred row below) ŌĆö matches `doc_value_query.rs`'s own documented scope; a `descending` flag isn't exposed since the wrapped Rust functions don't support it and a reverse-then-relabel hack wouldn't be real Lucene sort semantics. |
| `index/NumericDocValues.advanceExact`/`.longValue` (single-doc "does this doc have a value, and what is it" read ŌĆö C-ABI wrapper) | `lucene-ffi/src/sort.rs::ffi_numeric_doc_value_for_doc` | **new, FFI exposure audit for sparse doc-values reading.** Before this, every doc-values FFI entry point (`ffi_sort_by_doc_value`/`ffi_sort_by_multi_valued_doc_value` above, `range_sort.rs`'s range-sort pair, `facets.rs`'s facet counters) operated over a *set* of docs and already correctly threaded the sparse "no value" case through as an aggregate policy (`MissingValue::Exclude` drops the doc from the output, `MissingValue::Default` substitutes a caller-given value) ŌĆö but none of them let a caller ask "does *this one* doc have a value for this field" and get back a real present/absent distinction; a caller wanting that had to sort a one-doc candidate list and infer presence from whether the result set came back empty, which is indirect and doesn't work at all for a field with `MissingValue::Default` baked in. `ffi_numeric_doc_value_for_doc` closes that specific gap: a thin `catch_unwind`-guarded wrapper directly around `lucene_codecs::doc_values::numeric_value` (already `Result<Option<i64>>`-shaped ŌĆö `Ok(None)` means "doc legitimately has no value", already distinct from `Ok(Some(0))` at the Rust level), reusing `sort.rs`'s existing `numeric_entry_for` field lookup. Crosses the wire as two out-parameters: `out_has_value: *mut bool` and `out_value: *mut i64`, the latter left untouched (not zeroed) whenever `*out_has_value` comes back `false`, so a caller can never mistake "no value" for a stored `0` (or any other sentinel) ŌĆö verified by a test that deliberately pre-poisons `*out_value` with a non-zero sentinel before the call and confirms it's still there after a "no value" result. Same field-lookup/entry-kind-validation and error-status conventions as `ffi_sort_by_doc_value` (unknown field/wrong entry kind/segment without doc values ŌåÆ `InvalidArgument`). **Review-confirmed bug fixed before landing**: `lucene_codecs::doc_values::numeric_value`'s own `DocOutOfRange` check only bounds-checks `doc` for DENSE entries -- a sparse entry has no `max_doc` of its own, so a doc ID far past the segment's real document count silently fell through the docs-with-field bitset lookup and came back as `has_value == false` instead of an error. Fixed by checking `doc < 0 || doc >= segment.max_doc` directly against the segment's own `max_doc` inside this FFI function, uniformly for dense and sparse entries, before ever calling into the codec -- proven by a dedicated test (`numeric_doc_value_for_doc_out_of_range_positive_doc_on_sparse_field_is_invalid_argument`) against the same sparse fixture with a doc ID far past its real document count. Any other decode error still maps to `FfiStatus::Decode`. **NUMERIC fields only** ŌĆö BINARY/SORTED/SORTED_NUMERIC/SORTED_SET per-doc "does this doc have a value" lookups are not exposed through FFI yet (genuine, explicitly out-of-scope gap for a follow-up task; the underlying `lucene_codecs::doc_values::{binary_value, sorted_ord, sorted_numeric_values}` functions already exist and are equally `Option`-shaped, so closing that gap is "more of the same wiring", not new design). Tested against the same real-Lucene `fixtures/data/doc_values_index/`'s `sparse` field (5, *no value*, 15, *no value*, 25 across docs 0..4) already used by `sort_by_doc_value_missing_default_policy_real_fixture`: a present-value doc, a missing-value doc (confirming `out_value` is left untouched), a dense field's present value, plus the usual unknown-field/wrong-entry-kind/negative-doc/unknown-handle/null-out-param/decode-error status-code paths. |
| `search/TopFieldCollector` + `PointRangeQuery`/`SortedNumericDocValuesField.newSlowRangeQuery` (numeric range query, ranked by a doc-value field, ascending or descending ŌĆö C-ABI wrapper, single- and multi-segment) | `lucene-ffi/src/range_sort.rs::{ffi_search_numeric_range_sorted_by_field, ffi_search_numeric_range_sorted_by_field_multi_segment}` | **new, TopFieldCollector FFI exposure task.** Thin `catch_unwind`-guarded wrappers around `lucene_search::doc_value_query::search_numeric_range_sorted_by_field` (single segment, task #80) and `lucene_search::multi_segment::search_numeric_range_sorted_by_field_multi_segment` (multi-segment fan-out/merge, task #88) ŌĆö no range-matching, sorting, or doc-ID-translation logic reimplemented, only C-ABI marshaling. **Result-handle shape reuses the existing `SortedResultsHandle`/`registry::sorted_results()` (task #40)**, not a new handle type: both wrapped functions return `Vec<FieldValueDoc>`, i.e. exactly the same `(doc_id: i32, value: i64)` wire shape `SortedResultsHandle` already carries for `ffi_sort_by_doc_value`/`ffi_sort_by_multi_valued_doc_value` ŌĆö read back via the existing `ffi_sorted_results_len`/`ffi_sorted_results_copy`/`ffi_close_sorted_results` trio, no new accessor functions needed. `direction` crosses the wire as an `i32` (`0` = `SortDirection::Ascending`, `1` = `SortDirection::Descending`, anything else is `FfiStatus::InvalidArgument`), the same `0`/`1`-selector convention `ffi_sort_by_multi_valued_doc_value`'s `ValueSelector` already established; `range_field`/`sort_field` are looked up via the existing `sort.rs::numeric_entry_for` helper (now `pub(crate)`, reused rather than duplicated), and `missing_is_default`/`missing_default` reuse `sort.rs::missing_value` unchanged. **Multi-segment wire format is a flat array of already-open segment handles plus a parallel caller-supplied `doc_base` array, not a `DirectoryReaderHandle`**: task #51's `DirectoryReaderHandle` carries no `.dvm`/`.dvd` doc-values data per segment at all, so there is nothing for a reader-handle-based entry point to read a doc-value from ŌĆö each already-opened `ffi_open_segment` handle already carries its own `dv_data`/`dv_meta` (task #40), so this function instead looks up each handle in the existing `segments()` registry and builds the exact `lucene_search::multi_segment::DocValueSegment` list that function already expects, with the caller supplying each segment's `doc_base` explicitly (a segment has no way to know its own position in a larger commit on its own). `live_docs` is always `None`, the same documented "no `.liv` FFI surface yet" behavior every other query entry point in this crate already has. **Verified**: differential test asserting the FFI wrapper's output matches calling `search_numeric_range_sorted_by_field` directly against the same real `fixtures/data/doc_values_index/` fixture bytes; both sort directions and top-`n` truncation; the missing-value default policy; multi-segment doc-ID translation and tie-break (the same fixture segment opened twice with different `doc_base`s, mirroring `multi_segment.rs`'s own cross-segment tests); and the usual null-pointer/unknown-handle/decode-error/invalid-direction/invalid-field/segment-without-doc-values error paths for both entry points. No new Java fixture generator needed ŌĆö this is FFI wiring around already cross-engine-verified `lucene-search` logic (tasks #80/#88), not new correctness surface. Coverage: `range_sort.rs` 99.33% lines, 99.03% regions. |
| `search/PointRangeQuery` (search-side, single already-opened segment ŌĆö C-ABI wrapper) | `lucene-ffi/src/points_query.rs::ffi_search_points_range` | **new, Points range query FFI exposure task.** Thin `catch_unwind`-guarded wrapper around `lucene_search::points_query::search_points_range` (task #81) ŌĆö no BKD read/traversal or packed-value comparison logic reimplemented, only C-ABI marshaling: resolve `field` (a caller-supplied name) to a field *number* via the segment's `field_infos` (same `find(|f| f.name == field)` pattern `sort.rs::numeric_entry_for`/`query.rs::open_field_norms` already use ŌĆö an unknown name is `FfiStatus::InvalidArgument`, distinct from `search_points_range`'s own "unknown field *number* matches nothing" convention, which only applies once a valid number is already in hand), reconstruct a `PointsReader` from the segment's stored `.kdm`/`.kdi`/`.kdd` bytes (see the segment-open row above for the new `kdm_name`/`kdi_name`/`kdd_name` parameters), and collect matches into a new `ResultsHandle`. **Result-handle shape reuses the existing `ResultsHandle`/`registry::results()` (task #20's original unscored FFI work), no new handle type**: `search_points_range` collects through this crate's plain `Collector` trait into a flat, ascending `Vec<i32>` of matched doc IDs ŌĆö exactly the same shape `query.rs`'s `ffi_search_term_query`/`ffi_search_boolean_query`/`ffi_search_phrase_query` already collect into `ResultsHandle`; | ŌĆö | `lucene-ffi/src/results.rs::{ffi_results_len, ffi_results_copy, ffi_close_results}`, `lucene-ffi/src/results_scored.rs::{ffi_scored_results_len, ffi_scored_results_copy, ffi_close_scored_results}` (task #30), `lucene-ffi/src/results_sorted.rs::{ffi_sorted_results_len, ffi_sorted_results_copy, ffi_close_sorted_results}` (task #40) | **new.** Reads a results handle's collected doc IDs back out via a caller-allocated buffer (`ffi_results_len` sizes it, `ffi_results_copy` bulk-copies ŌĆö chosen over a per-index accessor since a JNI caller almost always wants the whole array at once, see that module's doc comment), then releases the handle. No Rust-side-allocated memory ever crosses the boundary in this slice ŌĆö `ffi_results_copy`/`ffi_scored_results_copy`/`ffi_sorted_results_copy` only ever write into a buffer the caller already allocated. **`ffi_scored_results_copy` (task #30)** writes into two caller-allocated *parallel* buffers (`out_doc_ids: *mut i32`, `out_scores: *mut f32`, same `buf_len`) rather than one interleaved buffer ŌĆö see `results_scored.rs`'s module doc for why; backed by a new `ScoredResultsHandle`/`registry::scored_results()` registry (a separate `RegistryTag`, not a widened `ResultsHandle`) so a results handle from the wrong search flavor is rejected by the handle-tag check rather than misread. **`ffi_sorted_results_copy` (task #40)** is the same parallel-buffers shape again (`out_doc_ids: *mut i32`, `out_values: *mut i64`), backed by yet another separate `SortedResultsHandle`/`registry::sorted_results()` registry ŌĆö a sort's second element is an arbitrary doc-value, not a BM25 score, so it gets its own handle type rather than being folded into `ScoredResultsHandle`. |
| ŌĆö | `lucene-ffi/src/error.rs::{FfiStatus, guard, ffi_get_last_error_message}` | **new.** Every exported function's body runs inside `guard`, which wraps `std::panic::catch_unwind` and converts a caught panic into a stable `FfiStatus::Panic` status code plus a thread-local last-error message (readable via `ffi_get_last_error_message`) instead of letting the unwind cross into the JVM. **Notable implementation detail**: the panic message is captured via a process-wide panic hook (installed once, active only while the calling thread is inside `guard`) rather than by downcasting `catch_unwind`'s `Box<dyn Any + Send>` payload to `&str`/`String` ŌĆö the ordinary downcast approach was tried first and found to intermittently fail to match either type in this environment even though the same payload's type is correctly observable from a hook at panic time; see `error.rs`'s `install_panic_hook` doc comment for the full investigation. Every handle-taking function validates its handle(s) against the relevant `SlotMap` before doing anything else, returning `FfiStatus::InvalidHandle` on a miss (stale/closed/unknown handles never dereference freed state). Every call site locks its registry's `Mutex` via `registry::lock_recovering` (`.lock().unwrap_or_else(|poisoned| poisoned.into_inner())`) rather than a bare `.lock().unwrap()` ŌĆö a panic caught by `guard` while a registry lock was held would otherwise poison that `Mutex` permanently, making every later `.lock().unwrap()` on it panic again forever (turning one bad call into a permanently broken registry); recovering the poisoned guard is sound here since every `SlotMap` mutation is a single non-panicking sequence with no possibility of a torn write. **Task #30's regression test for the scored path** (`registry_mutex_recovers_from_poisoning_after_a_panic_mid_scored_query`) uses a `thread_local!`-scoped panic-injection switch rather than reusing task #20's process-wide `AtomicBool` one (`PANIC_ON_NEXT_TERM_QUERY`) ŌĆö `cargo test`'s default parallel execution means a process-wide flag armed by one test can fire inside a different, concurrently-running test's call to the same function, a real (if narrow) flakiness source task #29's review flagged in the pre-existing unscored-path test; the new thread-local flag is immune to that race by construction (arming and firing always happen on the same test's own thread). The pre-existing `PANIC_ON_NEXT_TERM_QUERY` itself was not changed by this task ŌĆö fixing it is tracked as a separate follow-up. |
| `index/DirectoryReader.open(Directory)` + `IndexSearcher.search` fan-out, sequential and concurrent (C-ABI wrapper) | `lucene-ffi/src/directory_reader.rs::{ffi_open_directory_reader, ffi_close_directory_reader, ffi_search_term_query_multi_segment, ffi_search_boolean_query_multi_segment, ffi_search_term_query_multi_segment_concurrent, ffi_search_boolean_query_multi_segment_concurrent}` | **new, task #51.** Exposes task #45's `lucene_search::directory_reader::DirectoryReader` and task #41's multi-segment fan-out/merge over the C ABI, following tasks #20/#30/#40's exact FFI pattern (opaque `u64` handles, `catch_unwind`-guarded `extern "C" fn`s via `guard`, `lock_recovering` registry-mutex access, bounds-checked out-buffers). A new `RegistryTag::DirectoryReader`/`registry::directory_readers()` registry backs a `DirectoryReaderHandle`; `ffi_open_directory_reader` takes a filesystem path directly (not an already-open `ffi_open_directory` handle -- a `DirectoryReader` copies every segment's bytes into its own owned buffers at open time and needs the directory for no longer than that one call, unlike `ffi_open_segment`'s directory-handle-reuse case). `ffi_search_term_query_multi_segment`/`ffi_search_boolean_query_multi_segment` reuse task #30's existing `ScoredResultsHandle`/`ffi_scored_results_len`/`ffi_scored_results_copy`/`ffi_close_scored_results` trio rather than inventing a new results type, since multi-segment search returns the exact same `Vec<ScoreDoc>` shape single-segment scored search already does. Every per-segment norms slot passed to the wrapped `lucene_search` functions is `None` -- task #45's `DirectoryReader` carries no `.nvm`/`.nvd` data, so every multi-segment scored query here falls back to `similarity::UNNORMED_FIELD_LENGTH`, the same documented fallback single-segment scored queries already use for a bare `None`. **Avoiding task #29's flakiness pattern**: the new poison-recovery regression test arms a **thread-local** `Cell<bool>` switch (`PANIC_ON_NEXT_MULTI_SEGMENT_QUERY`), following `query.rs`'s post-task-#29 `PANIC_ON_NEXT_SCORED_TERM_QUERY` precedent rather than task #20's older process-wide `AtomicBool`, since `cargo test`'s parallel thread pool can otherwise let one test's armed flag fire inside a different, concurrently-running test's call to the same function. **Verified**: happy-path multi-segment term and boolean search against the real `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` fixture; wrong-tag handle rejection in both directions (a `ScoredResultsHandle` id passed as a reader handle, and a `DirectoryReader` handle passed to `ffi_scored_results_len`); null-pointer/unknown-handle/double-close cases for every new entry point; the poison-recovery regression test above. No new Java fixture needed -- this is FFI wiring around already cross-engine-verified `lucene-search` logic (tasks #41/#45), not new correctness surface. Coverage: `directory_reader.rs` 96.04% lines.

**Progress (Concurrent segment search FFI exposure):** `ffi_search_term_query_multi_segment_concurrent`/`ffi_search_boolean_query_multi_segment_concurrent` expose task #68's `search_term_query_multi_segment_concurrent`/`search_boolean_query_multi_segment_concurrent` (`lucene-search/src/multi_segment.rs`, the `rayon`-based sibling row above) over the identical wire format, handle validation, and `ScoredResultsHandle` readback the sequential wrappers above already use -- no search/merge logic reimplemented at this layer, only the fan-out function called differs (`_concurrent` instead of the sequential one). **Verified**, including the critical byte-for-byte proof at the FFI boundary itself: `term_query_multi_segment_concurrent_matches_sequential_ffi_wrapper`/`boolean_query_multi_segment_concurrent_matches_sequential_ffi_wrapper` each open two independent `DirectoryReader` handles against the same real `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` fixture, run the sequential wrapper through one handle and the concurrent wrapper through the other, and assert the read-back `(doc_id, score)` vectors are equal -- confirming the identical-output property already proven for the underlying Rust functions still holds with the FFI marshaling/handle/registry layer in the loop. Plus the same real-fixture-happy-path/unknown-reader-handle/null-out-handle coverage every other entry point in this crate carries. `cargo test -p lucene-ffi`: 269 tests pass (up from 261). Coverage: `directory_reader.rs` 95.81% lines. |
