| `queryparser/classic/QueryParser`, `queryparser/flexible/standard/StandardQueryParser` | `lucene-search/src/query_parser.rs::{parse_query, parse_query_with_analyzer, ParseError}` | **a minimal parser inspired by classic `QueryParser`'s syntax (task #44), not a port of `QueryParser.java`/`StandardQueryParser` themselves.** Both real classes are large grammars (JavaCC-generated in the classic case) covering range queries, configurable boolean-operator precedence, per-field analyzers, fractional fuzzy similarity, and a great deal of escaping-edge-case handling; this module is a from-scratch, hand-written recursive-descent parser (same "small, honestly-scoped hand-built parser" precedent `wildcard.rs`/`regexp.rs`/`fuzzy.rs` already established) turning a deliberately small syntax subset directly into this port's existing `Clause` tree ŌĆö `parse_query(input: &str, default_field: Option<&str>) -> Result<Clause, ParseError>` reuses every already-ported constructor (`TermQuery`/`PhraseQuery`/`BooleanQuery`/`WildcardQuery`/`PrefixQuery`/`FuzzyQuery`/`RegexpQuery`/`BoostQuery`), adding no new query representation. **Boolean-operator style, a deliberate single-style choice**: real classic `QueryParser` supports *both* `+`/`-` prefixes *and* `AND`/`OR`/`NOT` operators simultaneously, with configurable default-operator precedence ŌĆö exactly the "half-supported mix" this task's scoping explicitly called out to avoid. This parser supports **only** `+`/`-`/bare-is-SHOULD (`+term` = `Occur::MUST`, `-term` = `Occur::MUST_NOT`, bare = `Occur::SHOULD`, mapped straight onto `BooleanQuery`'s existing `must`/`should`/`must_not` buckets with no translation layer); `AND`/`OR`/`NOT` tokens parse as ordinary bare terms, never as operators ŌĆö unambiguous to parse (every clause's role comes from its own leading character, never from what's between clauses), so no precedence table is needed at all. **Supported grammar**: `field:term` and bare terms (`default_field: Option<&str>`; `None` plus a bare term is a clean `ParseError::MissingField`, never a silent "search every field" guess), quoted `"phrase terms"` ŌåÆ `PhraseQuery`, `field:term~`/`field:term~N` (`N` in `0..=2`, matching `FuzzyQuery`'s own `LevenshteinAutomata.MAXIMUM_SUPPORTED_DISTANCE` range) ŌåÆ `FuzzyQuery`, `field:prefix*` (a single trailing unescaped `*` and no other wildcard char) ŌåÆ `PrefixQuery` vs. `field:c?t`/any other `*`/`?` combination ŌåÆ `WildcardQuery` (mirroring real `QueryParser`'s own `PrefixQuery`-vs-`WildcardQuery` split), `field:/pattern/` (Lucene's own regexp delimiter convention, `\/` escaping a literal slash without ending the pattern) ŌåÆ `RegexpQuery`, `(...)` grouping recursing to arbitrary depth (not just one level ŌĆö "one grouping construct" was the scoping ask, not a depth cap), and a `^boost` suffix on any atom (term, phrase, group, wildcard, etc.) ŌåÆ `BoostQuery`. Escaping: inside a bareword, `\` followed by any byte inserts that byte literally, stripped from the resulting term ŌĆö the same convention `wildcard.rs::WildcardPattern::new` already documents. **Deferred explicitly, rejected with a `ParseError` rather than silently mis-parsed**: `AND`/`OR`/`NOT` as real operators with precedence rules (not implemented at all), fractional-similarity fuzzy (`term~0.8`, the `StandardQueryParser` float-similarity convention ŌĆö only a bare `~` or `~` plus a plain `0..=2` integer is accepted), and any escaping edge case beyond the single `\`-then-any-byte rule (e.g. `\uXXXX` Unicode escapes). **Verification**: no cross-engine Java fixture applies here (there's no "real Lucene bytes" for query-string *syntax* to decode ŌĆö the correctness question is "does this string parse to the `Clause` a human would expect," per this task's own scoping note) ŌĆö unit tests in `query_parser.rs` cover every supported grammar construct (single term, `field:term`, phrase, `+`/`-` combination, wildcard, prefix, fuzzy with/without explicit edit distance, regexp with/without escaping, one level and nested parenthesized groups, boost on a term and on a group) plus every malformed-input case (unclosed quote/paren/regexp, including after a trailing escape; unmatched close paren; missing field; invalid/non-finite boost; invalid fuzziness including out-of-range and fractional; unsupported range syntax; empty/whitespace-only input; empty group) confirming a clean `Err`, never a panic. `crates/lucene-search/tests/query_parser_fixtures.rs` is the honest substitute for a Java fixture: it parses queries against the real `IndexWriter`-produced `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` segment `term_query_fixtures.rs`/`boolean_query_fixtures.rs` already validate, executes them via `search_boolean_query`, and confirms the result matches the equivalent hand-built `Clause` (`TermQuery`/`PhraseQuery`/nested `BooleanQuery`) executed the same way ŌĆö proving the parser's output is not just structurally right but genuinely executes to the same doc set as the already-differentially-verified query layer. **Deferred, same as every other `Clause`-producing task**: no `lucene-ffi` C-ABI entry point accepts a query string yet (the FFI wire format still only builds flat `Clause::Term` clauses); no query-string support for `Clause::DisjunctionMax`/`Clause::ConstantScore` (real classic `QueryParser` has no direct syntax for either anyway ŌĆö both are Java-API-only constructs). **Analyzer wiring (task #62)**: closes the gap the `lucene-analysis` row above previously flagged (nothing wired an `Analyzer` into this module). `parse_query` is unchanged and now delegates to a new additive entry point, `parse_query_with_analyzer(input, default_field, analyzer: Option<&lucene_analysis::Analyzer>)` ŌĆö `None` reproduces every prior literal-term behavior exactly (all 41 pre-existing tests pass unmodified, plus a new test directly comparing `parse_query`'s and `parse_query_with_analyzer(.., None)`'s output). When an analyzer is supplied it runs over a bareword's text before `Clause::Term`, and over each whitespace-separated word of a quoted phrase before `Clause::Phrase` (real `QueryParser` analyzes phrase text word-by-word, not as one blob), but **never** over wildcard/prefix/fuzzy/regexp pattern text ŌĆö matching real classic `QueryParser`, which doesn't analyze pattern syntax either, since tokenizing/lowercasing/stopword-filtering a glob or regex would corrupt it (verified with pattern text containing uppercase letters and a stopword-shaped substring that must survive untouched). Zero/one/multi-token-per-word handling (a deliberately simplified subset of real `QueryParserBase.newFieldQuery`'s fuller handling, which can also build position-aware `SynonymQuery`s ŌĆö out of scope): one token ŌåÆ `Clause::Term`/one phrase position; zero tokens (the word analyzed away entirely, e.g. it was itself a stopword) ŌåÆ an empty `BooleanQuery` (no `must`/`should`/`must_not`), already this crate's established "matches nothing" shape per `matched_boolean_docs`'s own doc comment, so no new `Clause` variant was needed; more than one token ŌåÆ `Clause::Phrase` in order (bareword) or spliced into the phrase's term list (one phrase word). No new Java fixture ŌĆö this composes two already independently cross-engine-verified pieces (this row's own parser grammar, the `lucene-analysis` row's analyzer chain); the added zero/one/multi-token control flow is new Rust-level logic covered directly by unit tests, not new byte-format decoding. **Numeric range syntax (`PointRangeQuery`'s classic-`QueryParser` grammar)**: `field:[min TO max]` parses into a leaf `crate::query::Clause::PointsRange(PointsRangeQuery)` carrying `field`/`min: i64`/`max: i64`. **Exclusive bounds now supported (follow-on task)**: `[`/`]` and `{`/`}` are recognized independently per side, matching real classic `QueryParser` exactly ŌĆö `[a TO b]` (inclusive/inclusive), `{a TO b}` (exclusive/exclusive), `[a TO b}` and `{a TO b]` (mixed) all parse; only a genuinely mismatched/missing closing delimiter (anything other than `]`/`}`) is a `ParseError::InvalidRangeBound`. Since `PointsRangeQuery` still only stores one inclusive `[min, max]` pair (no separate min/max-inclusive flags), an exclusive *literal* bound is converted to the equivalent inclusive one at parse time in `Parser::parse_range` ŌĆö stepped one value toward the other bound (`min + 1`/`max - 1`, saturating so a bound already at `i64::MIN`/`i64::MAX` can't overflow) ŌĆö mirroring real Lucene's own `QueryParserBase.getRangeQuery`, which performs the identical adjustment before constructing its inclusive-only `PointRangeQuery`. An exclusive `*` (open-ended) bound is left unstepped, since `*` denotes "no bound" rather than a literal value (`{* TO 100}` is still fully open on the low end). Either bound may be `*` (mapped to `i64::MIN`/`i64::MAX`, real Lucene's own open-end convention) or a plain, optionally-negative decimal integer; a non-numeric bound, a missing/misspelled `TO`, or a missing/mismatched closing delimiter is a `ParseError::InvalidRangeBound` rather than a panic or a silently-wrong clause. Only `i64` bounds are supported ŌĆö string/date range queries (non-numeric bounds, real `TermRangeQuery`'s territory) are also `ParseError::InvalidRangeBound`, not a fallback to lexicographic comparison. **Execution now wired (task #199), resolving the previously-tracked gap.** `resolve_clause_docs`/`clause_scores` in `lucene-search/src/lib.rs` both gained a real `Clause::PointsRange` arm (a shared `points_range_doc_ids` helper): given an optional new `points: Option<&points_query::PointsInput<'_>>` parameter ŌĆö threaded through `search_boolean_query`/`search_boolean_query_scored`/`search_disjunction_max_query`/`search_disjunction_max_query_scored` and every internal helper between them (`matched_boolean_docs`/`resolve_dismax_docs`/`dismax_scores`), the same "new optional input, `None` fine until a clause needs it" precedent `pos_in`/`pay_in` already established ŌĆö a `Clause::PointsRange` looks its field's number up from `PointsInput::field_infos` (mirroring `lucene-ffi/src/points_query.rs::field_number_for`'s existing name-to-number lookup, one layer down from the C ABI), packs the query's `i64` `min`/`max` via a new `points_query::pack_i64` helper (real `LongPoint`'s sign-bit-flipped big-endian encoding, previously only hand-rolled in test code), and delegates straight to the already-existing, already-tested `points_query::search_points_range` ŌĆö no BKD traversal or packed-value comparison logic duplicated. `points: None` for a query that turns out to contain a `Clause::PointsRange` is `Error::MissingPointsInput(field)` (renamed from `Error::UnexecutablePointsRange` now that the clause genuinely is executable given the right input ŌĆö same "caller didn't open a resource this call needed" shape as `Error::MissingPosInput`); an unknown field name (present in `points.field_infos`? no) matches nothing, not an error, same convention every other clause follows. `explain::explain_clause` has no `PointsInput` parameter (out of scope for this task) and so always surfaces `Error::MissingPointsInput` for a `Clause::PointsRange` ŌĆö an existing, documented limit, not a regression. Multi-segment federation (`multi_segment.rs`) passes `points: None` at its two `search_boolean_query_scored` call sites, unchanged ŌĆö same "single already-opened segment" scope this whole module already documents. **End-to-end proof**: `lib.rs`'s `points_range_query_string_matches_real_segment_end_to_end` test parses a real query *string* (`"price:[20 TO 40]"`, `"price:{20 TO 40}"` exercising task #195's exclusive syntax, and an unknown-field case) via `query_parser::parse_query`, builds a real `PointsInput` from `lucene_codecs::points::write`/`open` plus a hand-built `FieldInfos`, and confirms `search_boolean_query`/`search_boolean_query_scored` return the correct doc set (and constant `1.0` score) against a small indexed fixture (docs valued 10/20/30/40/50) ŌĆö the full query-string-to-results path, not just a direct `search_points_range` call. Covered by unit tests in `query_parser.rs` as before (all four inclusive/exclusive combinations, negative bounds, `*` on either/both ends, saturating exclusive bounds, bare default-field range, boosted range, every malformed shape), plus the pre-existing `exclusive_bound_excludes_boundary_value_end_to_end` test, plus `lib.rs`/`explain.rs` unit tests pinning the (renamed) `Error::MissingPointsInput` path for a `None` `points` input. |

| `search/IndexSearcher` constructed with an `ExecutorService` (concurrent per-leaf search) | `lucene-search/src/multi_segment.rs::{merge_multi_segment_scored_concurrent, search_term_query_multi_segment_concurrent, search_boolean_query_multi_segment_concurrent}` | **ported (task #68), a `rayon`-based parallel sibling of the existing sequential fan-out/merge core ŌĆö not a port of real `IndexSearcher`'s `Executor`/`LeafSlice` machinery itself.** Real Lucene's `IndexSearcher(IndexReader, Executor)` constructor searches each `LeafReaderContext` (or `LeafSlice` group of leaves) on the supplied `Executor`, then merges the partial `TopDocs` once every leaf finishes. This port has no thread-pool abstraction of its own, and `rayon` is already a workspace dependency used elsewhere in this crate, so `merge_multi_segment_scored_concurrent` uses `rayon::prelude::*`'s `par_iter` over segments in place of an `Executor`: each segment's `TopDocsCollector`, per-segment search call, and doc-base translation run independently inside the parallel closure (no shared mutable state between segments, so no locking needed), producing one `Vec<ScoreDoc>` per segment. Those per-segment vectors are then merged **sequentially**, through the identical `TopDocsCollector` type [`merge_multi_segment_scored`] (the pre-existing sequential core, unchanged by this task) already uses for its own merge step ŌĆö the same merge logic, not a second implementation of it, and `rayon`'s `.collect()` preserving input order regardless of which worker thread computed which element is what makes the two paths' outputs provably identical rather than merely usually-the-same. `search_term_query_multi_segment_concurrent`/`search_boolean_query_multi_segment_concurrent` are thin wrappers mirroring the existing `search_term_query_multi_segment`/`search_boolean_query_multi_segment` exactly, differing only in which core they call. **Additive only**: the pre-existing sequential functions (`merge_multi_segment_scored`, `search_term_query_multi_segment`, `search_boolean_query_multi_segment`) and all of their tests are unchanged. **Verified**: sequential and concurrent results are asserted byte-for-byte identical (same doc IDs, same order, same scores ŌĆö `assert_eq!`, not an epsilon compare) for the same input across an empty index (zero segments), a single segment, 16 synthetic segments (enough for rayon's global pool to plausibly run more than one in parallel), a `top_n`-truncation case, a case where every segment ties on score at the same local doc ID (exercising the cross-segment tie-break through the concurrent path too), and both real end-to-end query types (term, boolean) against the real `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` fixture. **Explicitly deferred**: any thread-pool configuration/sizing knob (real Lucene's `Executor` lets a caller supply an arbitrarily sized/shaped pool; this always uses rayon's process-global pool, with no equivalent knob exposed), work-stealing tuning beyond what that global pool already provides out of the box, and any I/O-bound async concern ŌĆö this is CPU-parallel per-segment scorer evaluation only. ~~No `lucene-ffi` C-ABI entry point exposes the concurrent path yet~~ ŌĆö closed by the Concurrent segment search FFI exposure task: `lucene-ffi/src/directory_reader.rs::{ffi_search_term_query_multi_segment_concurrent, ffi_search_boolean_query_multi_segment_concurrent}` (see the `directory_reader.rs` row below for that FFI wiring's own details). **Deadline/timeout support (follow-up, additive only)**: `merge_multi_segment_scored_with_deadline`/`merge_multi_segment_scored_concurrent_with_deadline` (same file) are new sibling functions -- not modifications to the two functions above, which stay byte-for-byte unchanged and untouched by any existing caller -- taking an `Option<Instant>` deadline checked once per segment (sequential) or once per `rayon` closure, before that segment's own `per_segment_search` call. This port has no `TotalHits`/exact-vs-partial relation type, so expiry is signaled by a plain `timed_out: bool` rather than inventing new hit-count-relation API surface. Best-effort, not preemptive, matching real `TimeLimitingBulkScorer`'s own granularity: an expired deadline stops FURTHER segments from starting, it does not abort one already in flight. `deadline: None` degrades to byte-for-byte the same code path as the non-deadline siblings. **Not yet wired into any query-level entry point** (`search_term_query_multi_segment`/`search_boolean_query_multi_segment`/their FFI exposures all still call the non-deadline core) -- these are additive fan-out-loop primitives only, a caller must opt in explicitly; no `lucene-ffi` exposure yet either. |

| `search/IndexSearcher.explain(Query, int)` + `search/Explanation` | `lucene-search/src/explain.rs::{Explanation, explain_clause}` | **ported (task #59), introspection only ŌĆö does not change any scoring behavior.** `Explanation { matched, value, description, details }` mirrors real `Explanation` exactly (`matched` stands in for `isMatch()`; `Explanation::match_(value, description)`/`.with_details(vec)` and `Explanation::no_match(description)` mirror the real `Explanation.match(...)`/`Explanation.noMatch(...)` factory split). `explain_clause(fields, doc_in, pos_in, pay_in, live_docs, clause, doc, norms)` recomputes each node's `value` via the *exact same* `similarity::idf`/`similarity::tf_norm` calls (and the same `term_doc_freqs`/`term_doc_positions`/`phrase_freq_exact`/`matched_boolean_docs`/`resolve_clause_docs` helpers) `search_term_query_scored`/`search_boolean_query_scored`/`search_phrase_query_scored`/`search_disjunction_max_query_scored` already call ŌĆö its top-level `value` is bit-for-bit identical to those functions' own output for the same doc, verified directly (`assert_eq!`, not an epsilon compare) in this module's own unit tests rather than re-derived independently. **Detailed explanations** (weight ŌåÆ score ŌåÆ idf/tfNorm sub-trees, or the query's own composition formula): `Clause::Term` (idf with `docFreq`/`docCount` leaf details, tfNorm with `freq`/`k1`/`b`/`fieldLength`/`avgFieldLength` leaf details), `Clause::Phrase` (same shape, phrase idf = sum of each term's own idf, tfNorm keyed on phrase frequency), `Clause::Boolean` (sum of matching `must`/`should` sub-clause explanations, `no_match` when a `must` clause fails, `minimum_should_match` isn't met, or the query has no `must`/`should` clauses at all), `Clause::DisjunctionMax` (real `max + tie_breaker * sum(rest)` formula over matching disjuncts' own explanations), `Clause::ConstantScore` (matches iff the wrapped clause matches, always reports the constant, discarding the wrapped clause's own score), `Clause::Boost` (wrapped clause's own explanation value multiplied by `boost`). **Flat explanations** ("1.0 = matches, unscored constant score" or a clean `no_match`, no per-term breakdown): `Clause::Wildcard`/`Clause::Prefix`/`Clause::Fuzzy`/`Clause::Regexp`/`Clause::Span` ŌĆö same "no single term's frequency/idf to score against" rationale each query type's own `query.rs` doc comment already gives for why they score a flat `1.0`. No new Java fixture generator needed (per the `differential-testing` skill's precedent for presentation-layer logic over already-differentially-verified scoring ŌĆö there's no "real Lucene bytes" to check a description string against, only the numeric equality this task's tests assert directly against this crate's own already-verified ground truth). Coverage: `lucene-search/src/explain.rs` 97.82% lines (workspace total 97.28% lines, `cargo llvm-cov --fail-under-lines 95` passing). |
